The Thread Of Fate

by Paravato

Summary

“There’s no need to be nervous Miss Vidal, you’ve already challenged me in a lecture. This meeting should be easy for you.” Agatha’s eyes flicked up and briefly met hers before returning to the laptop screen.
Rio felt the heat creeping into her cheeks. ‘Amazing first impression acquired.’ She thought. “Yeah, I jumped the gun on that one. I apologise, Professor.”
“No need to apologise. It’s nice to know at least one person in that class has prior knowledge of the subject being discussed. I just ask that, if you’re going to challenge me, you have the confidence to do so immediately and don’t need it coaxing out of you.”

OR: Rio is a PhD student, Agatha is her supervisor and some lines become blurred.

Notes

It's been a literal decade since I wrote a fic, but these two have me in such a damn chokehold.
I'm trying out a thing where each chapter will be from a different characters' perspective so please let me know if it's working or not!

Rio

Rio sat at her kitchen counter sipping a mug of coffee and looking at the flat she had chosen in England; Cambridge to be exact. The place she would be moving to in six months time to begin her PhD. She was loath to be moving from the house that she owned in Virginia to a rent controlled apartment that would inevitably be a money vacuum, but it was a sacrifice she needed to make if she wanted to re-enter the world of academia this September. Her lease didn’t start for another 3 months which gave her time to pack as much of her life as she could possibly need, to move to another country for at least three years. She had chosen a spacious two-bedroom flat in Eddington, just a five minute drive from the university. Though it had only just occurred to her that she wouldn't actually have her car with her. ‘Damn it,’ she thought. ‘I guess walking won’t kill me.’

Her place at Cambridge university was secured and her accommodation was waiting for her, the only thing she needed to sort out now was her PhD supervisor. Was she cutting it incredibly fine by waiting this long to email prospective supervisors? Absolutely. Did she care? Absolutely not. She had confidence in her academic CV to grab the attention of the people she had chosen to email.

With her emails already written and saved as drafts, she set her alarm for 2:45am to make sure she was able to send them at exactly 8am UK time. She had two supervisors in mind, both specialising in ancient history, and tried to tailor the two separate emails to them specifically. The research topic she had chosen was ancient Greece – specifically the portrayal of ancient Greece in modern media – and she hoped it would appeal to them.

The first email was sent to Wanda Maximoff, a senior lecturer who had coached many PhD students to a pass. Her reputation spoke for itself, as did the past students Rio had spoken to on various message boards whilst making her choice on which university she was going to attend. She would be in extremely good hands if Wanda agreed to be her supervisor.
But her second email was sent to her first choice, Professor Agatha Harkness. Agatha’s name had been the first to come up when Rio had googled Cambridge university and, throughout her research on the various lecturers and professors that worked there, her searches had always found a way back to Agatha.
She had a reputation much like Wanda’s. Plenty of PhD students under her belt with an incredibly high pass rate. In fact, Rio couldn’t find any suggestion that any of Agatha’s students had failed. Though she believed that there was no way not a single student had failed, this had intrigued her. 

The message boards had confirmed that Agatha’s PhD students always left with a pass. Some people joked that her title should be changed from Professor Harkness to Professional Ball-breaker as she also had a reputation for taking no nonsense and pushing her students a little too far to achieve the results she believed they should be getting. This didn’t phase Rio though, she was confident that she could take whatever Agatha threw at her. She wasn’t one to break easily and didn’t back down from a challenge. If anything, she thrived when people pushed her, applied pressure and raised the stakes. Yes she was happy with her choices for supervisors and now just had to hope they’d choose her. 

Rio paced around her house for the next half an hour, not wanting to go straight back to bed after sending the emails and risk missing a reply, but she could feel her tiredness winning her over. She was about to shut her laptop down and go back to sleep when her email notification pinged. She clicked it as quickly as she could and read the response: 

Dear Miss Vidal,

I thank you for expressing your interest in my being your supervisor for your PhD. I would like to request a meeting with you in person on the 15th of September at 11:30am in my office to discuss the matter further. I look forward to meeting you.

Sincerely
Professor Harkness

Rio’s heart was pounding, maybe she wasn’t as confident as she originally thought. But Agatha Harkness had asked for a meeting so she was definitely happy. She sent a reply expressing her gratitude and agreeing to the meeting. She waited for another fifteen minutes in case Wanda replied to her as well but when she didn’t receive one, she decided to go to bed. The slight excitement made it so that drifting off posed a challenge but she eventually managed a restful night's sleep.

__________


The following three months were spent surrounded by her family helping her pack her life into as few cases as possible. Her parents flew out with her, taking some of her luggage as their own so that she didn’t have to do multiple trips, and spend a silly amount of money, in order to get all of her things into her flat.
“You did a good job picking this place, kiddo.” Her father said as he moved from room to room taking it all in. “Thanks dad, I learned from the best.” Rio said with a chuckle.
“Damn right you did!” He popped his head around a door frame with a smug smile on his face. 

“Yes you definitely inherited your fathers expensive tastes, mija.” Her mother stood grinning at the two of them, “it’s going to be a change going from your house to an apartment though, and no car. Are you sure you’re going to be alright?” Rio had heard her mothers concerns many times since she told her parents that she’d be moving to England. She knew her mom was proud of her and supportive of all of her choices, but she was a natural born worrier and couldn’t help showing it. “I’ll be fine mom, I’ve thought it all through.” Rio said, her voice calm.
“And she’s got her old man’s smarts.” Her dad added as he walked to his wife’s side.
“That doesn't fill me with the confidence you think it does.” Her mom replied jokingly.

They spent the next few days getting Rio’s things unpacked and in some semblance of order. The flat was already partially furnished so there wasn’t much that Rio needed to source on her own, but they did have the foresight to order some things to the apartment building such as: a TV, some flat-packed furniture and some pots and pans to get her started.
When her parents were satisfied that they’d moved her in well enough, they said their goodbyes – a teary one on her mothers end – and headed off back to the States. 

Rio now had the next three months to get her bearings around the area. Finding the good bars, the best places to get food and familiarising herself with the walk to and from the uni. Her meeting with Agatha was always in the back of her mind attached to a small shred of uncertainty. What if she rejects her? Would she still be able to try and appeal to Wanda? Why did Wanda not reply to her email? This wasn’t normal for her, she didn’t usually panic about things. She was always so controlled and collected, but then again this was a pretty big thing. 

In what felt like the blink of an eye, the start of the semester rolled around. Rio decided to attend some of the freshers week events to get her bearings around the university campus and maybe start making some friends. She was on her own here after all, having some people she enjoyed spending time with wouldn’t be a bad thing. She went to some of the introduction events for the ancient history courses hoping to meet some like-minded undergraduates, and they didn’t disappoint. Rio didn’t consider herself a ‘social butterfly’ by any stretch of the imagination, but if she could find common ground with someone, that was enough of a start.

A boy with bouncy, dark hair approached her and offered his hand. “Hi I’m Billy,” he enthusiastically said. “Are you studying ancient history too?”
Rio shook his hand. “Nice to meet you, I’m Rio, and I’m here to get my PhD but I figured it couldn’t hurt to check out the department and meet some people.” She gave him a small smile. He was wearing a pair of black, ripped jeans, a knitted jumper and a dark hoodie. His style reminded her of her own at his age and the fond memories came back to her. The freedom she felt when she first painted her nails black and shaved the slit in her eyebrow, her parents encouraging smiles and words of encouragement. “You look great, mija. It really suits you!”  

Billy gestured over his shoulder, “my friend Alice is over there, we’re kind of on our own at the moment, but if you’re wanting to expand your social circle you’re more than welcome to spend the day with us.” His smile was so genuine that Rio couldn’t resist following him over to Alice. Her main colour scheme was red and black, even in her hair. She wore a leather jacket and big black boots. “I’m glad to see that the goth and emo looks are coming back in. It’s really validating for my younger self.” Rio said with a small chuckle and extended her hand towards Alice. “I’m Rio, nice to meet you.” Alice accepted her hand shake and introduced herself in turn and, just like that, Rio had found some people that she could see herself spending some more time with. 

The three of them spent the day touring the department and ended it in the campus bar. “You undergrads don’t know how good you’ve got it, you know.” Rio said, starting her second pint. “You won’t find alcohol this cheap anywhere else.”
“Is that why you’re doing your PhD? Because paying adult prices for beer was too much for you?” Alice asked with a smirk.
Rio snorted. “Yes, exactly. I’m paying north of $30,000 a year so that I can have cheaper beer. It’s a decent trade if you think about it.” The three of them laughed, another round was bought in and the conversation flowed. 

Rio was happy with how easy it had been to connect with these two – even if they were teenagers. But then again, when she was doing her masters, she found herself spending more time with the undergrads than she did her fellow masters students. She liked the idea of being able to help them the way the post-graduate students had done for her. Paying it forward, as it were.
Billy’s voice brought her out of her thoughts. “So since you’re getting your PhD, does that mean we can give our coursework to you?”
Alice nudged him playfully. “He means to read it over before we submit it, not write it for us. He wouldn’t dream of being that cheeky, right Billy?” Billy just shrugged with a lopsided smile and Rio laughed. “I guess I could proofread your work. Not for free though.” She gave a show of pretending to think, “I’ll take payment in the form of alcohol.”
Alice smiled, “I’m sure we can arrange that.” 

Over the course of the week Rio, Billy and Alice met up for drinks a few more times and then Monday the 15th of September arrived. Rio’s meeting with Agatha was today. She had taken the liberty to check Agatha’s lecture schedule and decided to attend her first lecture of the semester to get a feel for her style of teaching.
That morning Rio found herself agonising over what clothes to wear, it felt juvenile. She wanted to make a good impression on Agatha but also didn’t want to appear like she was trying too hard – and her limited outfit choices weren’t helping. After what felt like hours, she finally decided on a plain, white shirt, black jeans and a dark-green leather jacket, finishing by throwing on her cleanest pair of Converse and headed to the university. 

She found herself a seat in the back corner of the lecture hall and Alice and Billy settled in next to her. “I didn’t think PhD students needed to attend lectures.” Billy said, giving her a confused look.
“Oh we don’t, but I have a meeting with Professor Harkness today about her being my supervisor so I thought I’d sit in.”
“Agatha Harkness is your supervisor?” Alice asked, her eyes widening. “You’re a brave woman.”
Rio was about to respond when a woman strode into the room, closing the door behind her. All she did was walk towards the desk in the centre of the room, but she had the attention of every single person in there. Rio recognised her from her picture, this was Professor Agatha Harkness. 

When Agatha spoke her voice was low and controlled, echoing around the hall. She had a transatlantic accent which made her very easy to listen to. “Welcome to your first lecture of the semester. I am Professor Harkness and you will address me as such.” She adjusted the cuff on her blazer before speaking again. “You will be expected to turn in a 3,500 word essay at the end of each semester and the word count is non-negotiable. You will lose ten percent for every hundred words you come under, but you will not get any extra for going over. I don’t like teachers' pets.” Her gaze swept over the crowd of wide-eyed, baby-faced first year students before her, and Rio swore Agatha’s eyes lingered in her direction for a fraction of a second longer than they did anywhere else. “Does everyone understand?” The question was met with a quiet murmur of agreement and Agatha moved around the desk to the laptop in the centre of it. “Excellent. Let’s begin.” The lights dimmed and the projector came to life as she fired up the PowerPoint. 

The lecture was much like all of the other introductory lectures Rio had sat through in her academic career. An outline of the module and the things that would be covered – each semester would cover either Ancient Greece, Ancient Rome or Ancient Egypt – and a reiteration of the coursework that was expected. Even when talking about such mundane things, Agatha commanded the room. Everyone’s eyes were on her, taking in every word she spoke like they were the most important words they’d ever hear. Rio suddenly understood why Agatha had such a good pass record, you couldn’t help but listen to her and let every word sink in. 

The rest of the lecture was an introduction to Ancient Greece, covering the main twelve Olympian gods and some of their more notable children. “As we all know, Disney’s Hercules is the most accurate re-telling of the story.“ Agatha said as a still from the movie was projected on the screen. A chuckle made its way around the room from the students, “but something that people don’t know too much about is that Heracles – the Greek pronunciation – was originally given the name Alcides by his parents.” She let the statement sit and watched the students scribble the information down before she continued. “It was only later that he became known as Heracles as a way to honour Hera, the Queen of the gods.”
Rio couldn’t help the way that she scoffed, it was almost like she didn’t have control over it. She knew the statement was incorrect and thought, ‘well that’s not true.’
It was only when she noticed everyone’s eyes trained on her that she realised she’d said it out loud. She looked at Billy and Alice who were staring at her wide eyed, mouths slightly open in surprise, like they couldn’t believe that she’d dared speak when Professor Harkness was teaching – never mind had the gaul to tell her that she was incorrect. ‘Fuck. She thought. What a great first impression.’

The silence in the room was heavy before Agatha filled it. “I sense somebody disagrees with me.” She levelled her gaze directly at Rio. “Don't be shy, speak your mind.”
Rio shuffled in her seat, changing her slouched position to a straight one, and cleared her throat. “Well you said that Heracles’ name was changed to honour Hera.” She paused, choosing her words carefully and Agatha gestured at her to continue. “But he was renamed Heracles in an unsuccessful attempt to mollify Hera, with Heracles meaning Hera's ‘pride’ or ‘glory.’” Rio looked around, uncomfortably aware that Agatha hadn’t stopped looking at her. She hadn’t even blinked. But Rio swore that, even from this distance, she could see a faint look of amusement cross Agatha’s face. “What is your name please?”
‘Absolutely fantastic. I haven't even had my meeting with her yet and she already has a negative opinion of me. Well done, Rio.’
“Rio Vidal.” 

Agatha picked up a piece of paper from the desk and studied it for a second. “Miss Vidal, I don't recall seeing your name on the list of students taking this module.”
“I'm here to get my PhD and thought this module would be a good one to sit in on.” Rio spoke before she could overthink, although thinking in any capacity would really benefit her right now.
Agatha hummed quietly in acknowledgment and went back to teaching, flicking the PowerPoint to the next slide. Rio’s face burned with embarrassment as the words “This is not true!” were shining bright for everyone to see. “Well the surprise of this slide has been ruined, but the point remains the same. There are many different ways that Greek myths are told and portrayed, all we can do is find the consistencies between them and hold those in higher regard.”

The rest of the lecture passed without incident and Rio practically ran out of the room when it ended. She didn’t dare spare a glance in Agatha’s direction and waited for Billy and Alice to catch up. “Well you’re brave, I’ll give you that.” Billy said.
Rio snorted, “stupid is what I am. I never could keep my mouth shut.” She looked between Alice and Billy before saying, “come on, I need a coffee.” She had half an hour before she had to be face-to-face with Agatha and, no doubt, pay for what she’d just done. Alcohol was her instinct, but coffee was the better choice. “You’re gonna have fun with Agatha as your supervisor after that stellar first impression.” Alice joked, “although Billy is grateful that you took some of the heat off of him.” She finished as she playfully nudged him but Billy just levelled her with a glare. Rio raised her eyebrow in intrigue but didn’t press for more information, she checked the time and decided it was time to go face her fate. “It’s been fun kids but I have to go. I’ll see you on the other side.” She gave them a mock salute before heading off in the direction of Agatha’s office.

Rio had never found a door intimidating before, but no other door had ‘Professor Harkness’ written on a plaque attached to it. She checked the time, 11:30 exactly, took a deep breath and knocked on the door. A few seconds passed before “you may enter” was heard from the other side. Rio did as instructed and entered the room. The office was smaller than she was expecting, the far wall was lined with bookcases which were full – possibly dangerously so with the way the books were stacked – the other walls were bare save for an A3 canvas of a forest bathed in moonlight hanging above a desk that was tucked into the corner. Agatha sat at the desk, a pair of glasses perched on her nose, typing on a laptop. Without looking up she said, “please, take a seat.” In the centre of the room were two arm chairs with a coffee table between them, Rio took off her bag and uncomfortably perched on one of them. 

It felt like an hour passed before Agatha spoke again. “Miss Vidal, wonderful to finally meet you.” She still didn’t look up from her laptop. Rio tried to respond but the words got stuck, she tried to disguise it as clearing her throat. “It’s wonderful to finally meet you as well, Professor Harkness.” She saw the corners of Agatha’s mouth lift slightly and realised that she definitely hadn’t been able to disguise it as clearing her throat. “There’s no need to be nervous Miss Vidal, you’ve already challenged me in a lecture. This meeting should be easy for you.” Agatha’s eyes flicked up and briefly met hers before returning to the laptop screen. Rio felt the heat creeping into her cheeks. ‘Amazing first impression acquired.’ She thought. “Yeah, I jumped the gun on that one. I apologise, Professor.”
“No need to apologise. It’s nice to know at least one person in that class has prior knowledge of the subject being discussed. I just ask that, if you’re going to challenge me, you have the confidence to do so immediately and don’t need it coaxing out of you.” She gave another brief look in Rio’s direction. “I have to ask, why did you wait until six months before starting your PhD to inquire about me being your supervisor?”
“I figured you'd have lots of requests to sift through so I decided to wait on the off chance you'd be able to give my inquiry your full attention.” Agatha had asked for confidence and Rio was going to show it. 

She was focussed on Agatha, searching for any signs of approval but she was still looking at her laptop. “What subject do you have in mind for your thesis?” The question took Rio by surprise. Her email to Agatha had included the details about her thesis, surely she wouldn’t have requested an in person meeting if she hadn’t read the full email. But she answered anyway. “The portrayal of Greek Mythology in modern media.” 

Agatha hummed in thought, still not giving Rio her full attention. “Not the strongest of titles.” Rio was about to respond when she spoke again, “and why should I be interested in being your supervisor?”
‘Is she being fucking serious?’ “Because you specialise in Ancient Greece.” Rio stated as if it were the most obvious thing in the world. “I did my research, you're the most wanted PhD supervisor in the field.” She was starting to get annoyed, what gave Agatha the right to speak to people like that? “Hmm. So you googled me.” There was no inflection of a question, it was an observation. Rio was trying her best to keep it together. “I googled the university and you came up.” But the fact that Agatha had barely bothered to look at her since she walked into the room was grating on her. “Are you going to pay any attention to me during this meeting, or is your laptop more interesting?”
Agatha’s gaze remained trained on her laptop but her eyebrow lifted slightly. “When you give me something to devote my full attention to, Miss Vidal, you shall have it.”

Rio’s resolve snapped. She would not be spoken to in this manner and she was going to make Agatha regret asking for confidence. “So you don't deem me asking you specifically to be my supervisor worth your time? I came to this university for your reputation, for you . But you know what? I'm good actually, I always have a backup plan. I also emailed Ms. Maximoff about being my supervisor and she was rather enthusiastic about the idea. She also seems like someone who can actually be bothered to drag herself away from her laptop for two seconds to have a conversation with me.” She wasn’t sure why she’d lied about getting a response from Wanda as it was sure to come back and bite her in the arse in about thirty seconds, but the look on Agatha’s face was worth it. She was finally looking at Rio, her attention wasn’t anywhere else. There was definitely surprise in her look and something else that Rio couldn’t currently place. Was it anger? Hurt? Or just incredulity at her sudden outburst? Either way she felt pride swell in her chest. 

Agatha removed her glasses, definitely uncomfortable in the tension Rio’s words had created. “I really thought it would take you longer to break than that. You don't seem that,” she gestured lazily, “easily flustered.” ‘She’s trying to get control back.’ Rio thought. But before she could respond, Agatha continued. “But I have to admit, the passion you just showed is intriguing. Bring me your proposal on Wednesday, I'll give it a look over and make my decision.”
Rio was stunned. What had just happened? How had she had two opportunities to make a good impression on Agatha, fucked both of them, and still managed to come out with a win? Agatha’s voice shook her from her thoughts. “This is where you agree, thank me and leave.”

“I- Yes I'll bring my proposal to you, thank you.” Her brain had switched off and she was on autopilot as she made her way to the door. “Miss Vidal?” Agatha called after her. She stopped and looked over her shoulder. “Try not to get so easily wound up in future, or this will not work out.” Agatha put her glasses back on and turned her attention back to her laptop as if she had never moved in the first place, and Rio left the office.

The door clicked shut behind her and she leaned against it, sighing heavily. “How the fuck am I going to survive this?” She checked the time, 12pm. Had it really only been half an hour? It felt like years. Was it too early to get a drink? ‘ Fuck it, it’s five o’clock somewhere,’ she thought. She opened a group chat with Alice and Billy as she started walking.

Rio: Either of you two fancy a drink?

Alice: Can’t, we've got lectures all day

Billy: Also it’s only 12. I know time moves differently at your age but damn!

Rio: Losers 

She chuckled because she knew they were right, it was probably too early to start drinking on a Monday and she needed to go home and rethink her thesis title. The combination of being on her phone and thinking about Agatha’s harsh comments meant that she didn’t see the other person coming towards her until it was too late. 

Their bodies collided and the other person was knocked off balance, throwing the stack of papers they were carrying into the air. Rio instinctively grabbed the other person to stop them from falling, grabbing both their arm and waist pulling them close to her. It took a second for the papers to settle on the ground and for both of them to realise that they were practically hugging. They awkwardly broke apart saying overlapping apologies.
“Oh my god I am so sorry!”
“No, no it’s fine. It was my fault!”
“Here let me help you pick these up.” Rio crouched down and started scooping up the papers scattered around them. The other person joined her and Rio handed them her pile, their fingers brushing lightly and they took it. It was only then that Rio noticed the red waves of hair and the striking green eyes. She recognised this woman but through the jumble of the last 30 seconds, couldn’t place her face. They both stood back up and the other woman spoke first. “Thank you for your help and for stopping me from ending up like these papers.” She chuckled and extended her hand. “I’m Wanda,” she cleared her throat. “Ms. Maximoff.” ‘Wanda of course.’ Rio remembered her from her picture on the university website. She took her hand and shook it. “I’m Rio, Rio Vidal.” Wanda raised her eyebrows slightly in recognition.
“PhD student right? Sorry for not responding to your email, I’m unfortunately not taking any more students this year.” She seemed to realise that they were still shaking hands and pulled hers away. “I hope you managed to find someone, I thought your proposal was excellent.” She spoke like it was a speech she'd been rehearsing for a play. Rio found her tone of voice slightly odd but didn’t read into it. “Yes I did! Professor Harkness is my supervisor.” Wanda cast a shy glance in the direction of Agatha’s office.
“Well good luck with that one. You’re gonna need it.” She smirked and walked away leaving Rio standing there.

Maybe Monday afternoon was the best time for a drink after all. 

Agatha

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha had spent the last six months sifting through emails from PhD students requesting her as their supervisor, and this evening was no different. She was used to this, knowing that she was so coveted did wonders for her ego, but the pickings for this upcoming academic year were more slim than the last. “Does no one have an original idea any more?” She asked to her empty living room as she read yet another proposal on the fall of the Roman Empire. She didn’t need to take on any PhD students this year, it wouldn’t kill her to have a year without doing it. But the truth was that she enjoyed it. She liked being a mentor and shaping people into the best they could be – even if her methods did get some complaints – so she felt that a part of her would be missing if she didn’t take on a student this year.

Her phone buzzed on the table next to her, a message from her colleague, Jen Kale.

Jen: Any joy picking a student yet?

Agatha: I’m this close to just putting their names in a hat and letting fate decide.

Jen: Let’s not get too extreme just yet. You still have 6 months, you might be surprised.

Agatha: I’ll give one more student a chance. If the next request I get doesn’t immediately grab my attention, I’m calling it for the year.

Jen: I’m glad my advice is being taken and extreme behaviour is being avoided.

Agatha rolled her eyes and shut her laptop down, deciding on an early night.   

She woke the next morning an hour earlier than usual, she groaned when she checked the time and saw 7:30, but dragged herself out of bed anyway. Immediately offended by the lack of caffeine in her system, her first port of call was the kitchen turning her laptop on as she waited for her coffee to brew.
She leant against the kitchen counter letting the coffee work its magic and running through the list of errands she had for the day, when her email notification pinged on her laptop. Reluctantly she moved to sit in front of it – definitely not awake enough to deal with whatever this was – and groaned when she saw the subject line, “PhD Supervisor Request” at the top of her inbox. She had really hoped that people had given up. It was so rare that people would wait this long to request a supervisor. But, if she was being honest with herself, the fact that it had been left this long was intriguing. That’s why she’d been so quick to read the other five she’d received this past week, and she’d be ready to give the same rush to this one had the others not been so bad.

She allowed herself a few minutes of annoyance before she opened the email. It had the same basic structure she’d grown accustomed to: polite and formal wording, a little bit of smoke being blown up her arse and an attached academic CV and PhD proposal outline. Remembering her message to Jen the night before, she said, “hmm, let’s see what you’ve got Rio Vidal.” She opened the CV first. A three year undergraduate degree in Archaeology followed by a gap year and a part-time masters in Ancient History, graduating both with a first. This wasn’t a surprise to Agatha as it was rare for students to request her when they had less than a first.

So far the email was exactly like the rest of them but something made her want to take extra time to read the proposal. She wasn’t sure what it was, but she just had a feeling that this one wouldn’t be bad. She opened the proposal and quirked an eyebrow as she read the title: The Portrayal Of Greek Mythology In Modern Media. ‘Not the strongest title, but I can work with this.’ She thought as she scanned the rest of the document. All in all it was a very well put together proposal, it actually held her attention as she read it. The fact that she’d stopped skimming it and had actually gone back to the start to read every word properly took her by surprise. She never did that. “Well Miss Vidal,” she said to her empty kitchen, “you have my attention.”

She was about to start typing her response when her phone buzzed, the screen lighting up with a name she was less than enthusiastic about seeing.

Maximoff: Have you also received a supervisor request from Rio Vidal?

Of course Rio Vidal would also request her. The only student that had actually managed to interest her was making her work for it.

Agatha: I have. I want her.

There was no chance that Agatha was letting Wanda have this one. Was it rooted slightly in pettiness? Yes, yes it was. Wanda had hurt her and Agatha loved to hold a grudge.

Maximoff: Of course you do, she’s the only student with a decent proposal.

‘Astute as ever.’ She thought

Agatha: I have sent plenty of other requests your way.

Maximoff: Only because you don’t want them, that’s hardly fair Agatha. My pass rate is just as good as yours is, I deserve to be able to pick my own students.

Agatha let out an exasperated sigh. She hated when Wanda remembered that she had a spine and now she was going to have to resort to asking nicely. But she was not begging. That was entirely different.

Agatha: Wanda, please. Let me have this one and I’ll let you have the next one.

The seconds waiting for the reply turned into minutes and it made Agatha wonder if Wanda was finally going to stand up for herself, put her in her place and take Rio Vidal on as her student.

Maximoff: Okay. I will not respond to her email, but we can’t keep going on like this Agatha. We are going to have to talk properly at some point.

Agatha: Thank you.

She refused to acknowledge the last part of Wanda’s message. They had an agreement to only speak about work related matters and Agatha didn’t break agreements.
She returned her focus to her email to Rio Vidal. She was fairly sure that she wanted to take her on this year, but wanted to meet her in person first. First impressions can make all the difference.

__________

 

Agatha used freshers week as her final prep time, choosing to go into the university and sit in her office to avoid distractions. That lasted all of about thirty seconds before there was a knock at her door. She sighed and said, “you may enter.” The first word had barely been spoken before the door was flung open and two women barged in. Agatha rolled her eyes. “Good morning Lilia, Jen,” she started, looking between them. “What can I do for you on this fine Monday morning?” Lilia and Jen were also lecturers at Cambridge university and, much to her chagrin, Agatha’s best friends. “Can’t we just want to spend some time with you, Harkness?” Lilia asked and she flopped into one of the armchairs. Jen, ever the prim-and-proper one, delicately perched herself in the other armchair before adding, “for once we’re ahead on our lecture prep but I can see now that you’re uncharacteristically behind.” She furrowed her brow in confusion as she craned her neck to try and see the notes on Agatha’s desk.
Agatha, not liking being called out, quickly gathered up the papers covering her desk and placed them face down. “I know I’m very behind right now, but I’m sorting it out. Or I was before you two came bumbling into my office.”
Lilia leaned forward in her seat. “Well now we simply need to know what could have been distracting the great Professor Agatha Harkness this much.” Her smile was mischievous and Jen picked up her train of thought. “Could there be a new woman in your life?” She feigned a shocked expression but Agatha quickly shut her down. “No. There are no new women in my life, nor will there ever be. I am enjoying my time being single.”
Lilia snorted. “Tell that to Agatha from a two and a half years.”
“We really don’t need to be bringing that up.” Any hint of joking had been removed from Agatha’s voice, letting Lilia and Jen know that they’d taken it too far. They both quickly apologised and Agatha said, “now if you two don’t mind, I really need to get this finished.” Her tone was lighter but there was still some hurt lingering beneath it. Her two friends agreed and left her in peace. 

She obviously knew what had been distracting her, she just didn’t want to admit it. The truth was that she’d spent the last month agonising over seeing the kid again. They’d been so close before she left. No. Before she was forced to leave. But now, two and a half years later, who knows where they stood with each other. She was absolutely capable of putting the past behind her and treating him like any other student but she’d be lying if she said that receiving the text from Wanda a month ago hadn’t spun her head.

The text had read: “I’m letting you know this because I don’t think it’ll be good for either of you if it’s a surprise. Billy is in your class this semester. Please try to be nice to him. I’m not asking for me because I know that will only achieve the opposite result, I’m asking for him.”
At first Agatha had been angry. That was her immediate reaction. How dare that woman insinuate that she’d be anything other than kind to Billy? When had she ever shown any inkling of ill will towards him? But then she’d seen the guilt trip that Wanda had embedded in the message. “I’m not asking for me, I’m asking for him.” Agatha had read out loud and the anger had been shunted in a new direction. She was no longer angry at Wanda, she was angry for Billy. How on earth could she use her child in that way? What kind of mother would use her son to guilt trip her ex? Billy wasn’t a part of this, he hadn’t done anything wrong. This was between the two adults.

It had taken Agatha nearly two days to calm down enough to reply to Wanda’s message, not that she deserved a reply, and she’d spent the next month cycling through emotions about the upcoming semester.
That was why she was behind on her lecture prep. She’d let Wanda get into her head and was overthinking every possible upcoming interaction she could have with Billy.

 

__________


Monday the 15th of September arrived entirely too quickly, Agatha only just got her lecture notes for the first semester sorted in time. But with everything done and ready it was time to begin the first lecture of the semester. On the first day she always made sure she was the last to enter the room. She enjoyed the control it gave her to be able to walk in and know that everyone’s eyes were on her. All she did was walk to the desk, but she knew every single person in that room was waiting for her to speak.

She revelled in the fact that this was a room of fresh faced students with minds that were hers to mould. There was a reason that she took up teaching as a profession. She liked the feeling she got when a student's face lit up upon hearing a new piece of information. She liked knowing that she’d changed someone's negative opinion on something. But more than anything she loved getting to talk about subjects that interested her. In this lecture hall, speaking to these students, she wasn’t just the ‘weird kid’ who knew a bit too much about the Greek gods. They were all there to hear her speak about exactly that. They were paying to hear her speak about it, and that feeling was unparalleled.

She began the way that she always did, by introducing herself and giving a brief outline on the essays that she expected from them. She looked across the crowd of faces before her, taking them all in, lingering ever so slightly on the back corner. She knew that he was in her class but was still surprised to see him, for some reason. It was almost like she’d been refusing to believe it until she saw it, but there he was clear as day. He’d dyed his hair black but his features remained the same. Billy Maximoff. She had a faint feeling of guilt watching the way he shuffled in his seat under her gaze.

Needing to bring herself back into the room, she let her gaze wander back to the centre and asked, “does everyone understand?” A murmur of agreement came in response and she made a mental note to bring them all out of their shells and help them find their voices. “Excellent. Let’s begin.”

She opened up the PowerPoint and began the introduction to the module. She could practically feel her students hanging on her every word as she moved on to the lecture proper. Even she wasn’t able to tell that she’d finished prepping this mere days ago. She felt so at ease standing front and centre of the room watching people rush to write down what she was saying, eager to remember every word. 
She was ramping up to the first plot twist of the lecture. “As we all know, Disney’s Hercules is the most accurate re-telling of the story.“ She said, accompanying it with a still from the movie being projected on the screen, and allowing herself to share in the chuckle that made its way around the room. “But something that people don’t know too much about is that Heracles – the Greek pronunciation – was originally given the name Alcides by his parents.” She allowed the students time to write the fact down. “It was only later that he became known as Heracles as a way to honour Hera, the Queen of the gods.”

Her finger was hovering over the button, waiting to change to the next slide when she heard a scoff from the back corner. ‘Surely that’s not him.’ She thought as her gaze snapped in the direction she’d heard it. But it was followed by a mumble that wasn’t in his voice. “Well that’s not true.” Agatha watched as all the heads in the room turned in the direction the voice came from. A woman with dark hair tucked into the far corner of the seating bank who now looked very uncomfortable. Interesting.

“I sense somebody disagrees with me. Don't be shy, speak your mind.” The woman suddenly seemed to become aware that Agatha was looking at her and she shuffled in her seat, clearing her throat to – Agatha assumed – buy herself some time to compose her thoughts. “Well you said that Heracles’ name was changed to honour Hera.” She paused and Agatha gestured for her to continue. “But he was renamed Heracles in an unsuccessful attempt to mollify Hera, with Heracles meaning Hera's ‘pride’ or ‘glory.’” Agatha didn’t let her gaze drop. ‘Impressive, she knows her stuff. Very interesting.’ She couldn’t hide the amusement that crept into her expression, and she didn’t care to. “What is your name please?” she asked as she made her way to the desk. “Rio Vidal.” Agatha felt an involuntary look of surprise appear on her face, but she hid it by looking at the list of names she’d printed out. “Miss Vidal, I don't recall seeing your name on the list of students taking this module.” Obviously she knew why that was but she couldn’t let Rio know that could she? Wait, why couldn’t she? Why did she have the sudden urge to appear aloof to this woman?

“I'm here to get my PhD and thought this module would be a good one to sit in on.” Rio’s voice broke her from her thoughts but said thoughts had shaken her slightly and she needed to get them back on teaching. All she gave in response was a non-committal “hmm” and returned her attention to her lecture, quickly flicking to the next slide. In truth she had forgotten what the next slide was, but as soon as she saw it, it brought her right back to where she needed to be.

She got through the remainder of the lecture with no further hiccups and watched with slight amusement as Rio practically ran from the room. But then her attention was quickly drawn back to Billy. Should she try to talk to him? Should she ask him to wait behind until everyone was gone so that she could reassure him that she wouldn’t make his life hell? Should she let him know that she misses him and that she wished he didn’t have to be caught up in the shit between her and his mother?
His eyes met hers as he walked past her but she couldn’t read his expression. She tried to speak to him but the words got stuck in her throat, probably for the best since she didn’t actually know what she would say to him, and he hurried out of the door.
This was not going to be easy.

Having been knocked off balance during the lecture, Agatha went straight to her office. She needed some silence to be able to sort her head out.
She practically threw herself into the nearest chair and held her face in her hands. How was she going to go a whole semester having Billy in her class? She definitely needed to talk to him, on that she was certain, and it was for purely selfish reasons. Of course she wanted to make sure that he was okay, she still cared for him, but she needed to do it for her own peace of mind. She needed to know where they stood and how to conduct herself going forward.

And then there was Rio, the other person occupying her mind. She would be in Agatha’s office in approximately fifteen minutes for a meeting that Agatha had not prepared for in any way, shape or form. Billy had been taking up so many of her thoughts and she really didn’t think this PhD student would immediately be fighting for space, and yet here she was. She’d taken it upon herself to attend the first lecture of the semester – no doubt an attempt to make a good first impression – and had shown that she wasn’t afraid to speak out, even if she did need a little prompting. Agatha was always impressed when students found the nerve to question her, she enjoyed engaging in debates and discussions, and when the debate was good, she didn’t mind it derailing her lecture. As long as there was still something to be learned, she couldn’t be mad. But she wasn’t used to being challenged in the very first lecture, students typically found their voices in the second week, so she was instantly intrigued.
But why was she intrigued? Agatha recalled the way Rio had spoken with certainty. Despite her nervous tone, she still spoke as if she knew what she was saying was the ultimate truth. She didn’t say, “I read that…” or “I’ve heard that…” she simply just spoke like it was plain and simple. Agatha respected that. Respect, that was it! That’s what she felt.

A knock at her door broke her from her thoughts and she checked her watch, 11:30. Fuck .
She scrambled to her desk and sat before saying “you may enter.” Agatha watched as Rio Vidal entered her office and immediately started scanning the room and turned her gaze to her laptop when Rio found the canvas above her head. She opened a blank document typing bullet points to try and structure the meeting that had already begun – before telling Rio to take a seat.

  • Introduction
  • Ask why she waited so long
  • Subject of thesis?
  • Why should I be interested?

When she was happy with her list she started working through the points. “Miss Vidal, wonderful to finally meet you.” Check.
Rio’s seemed to choke on her response and Agatha couldn’t help the small smile that crossed her lips. ‘She’s as nervous as I am.’ she thought, letting the revelation calm her down a fraction.
“There’s no need to be nervous Miss Vidal,” Agatha began, though she wasn’t sure where it was coming from, “you’ve already challenged me in a lecture. This meeting should be easy for you.” She allowed herself to briefly look at Rio, finding her eyes immediately. Such a nice shade of brown. ’Wait, what? No, I wasn’t focussing on that.’ She battled with her own thoughts as Rio spoke again, but Agatha only tuned in to the last few words. “I apologise, Professor.” What was she apologising for again? Oh the lecture, right. “No need to apologise. It’s nice to know at least one person in that class has prior knowledge of the subject being discussed. I just ask that, if you’re going to challenge me, you have the confidence to do so immediately and don’t need it coaxing out of you.” Some part of her brain must have been prepared for this because it’s like she was running on autopilot. It was dangerous though so she brought herself back to her list but not before her eyes wandered back to Rio’s face for a second.

“I have to ask, why did you wait until six months before starting your PhD to inquire about me being your supervisor?” Check. It wasn’t relevant to anything but it was something that had puzzled her, so why not find out? She barely heard Rio’s answer though as she was so focussed on getting through her list and ending this meeting as quickly as she could. “What subject do you have in mind for your thesis?” ‘Wait, I know this. At least I should know this. What was it?’
“The portrayal of Greek Mythology in modern media.” That was it! She hummed as she remembered reading it months ago. “Not the strongest of titles.” ‘Shit was that out loud? That was out loud. Fucking hell just move on.’ “And why should I be interested in being your supervisor?” Check. All of her points had been hit, now she just needed to wrap it up. Rio’s response was much like her email had been, just in a less formal wording. “Hmm. So you Googled me.” Agatha deadpanned. It was meant to be a question but she was just trying so hard to get this meeting to end that her tone came out wrong.
“I googled the university and you came up. Are you going to pay any attention to me during this meeting, or is your laptop more interesting?” It seemed Rio was responding to the harsh tone of Agatha’s last comment, and she couldn’t blame her. She had been wholly unprofessional throughout this entire thing. But there was no point trying to backpedal, the best she could do was lean into it and try to own it. Still not daring to look at Rio she said, “when you give me something to devote my full attention to, Miss Vidal, you shall have it.”

Agatha knew as soon as she’d said it that it wasn’t the right thing to say at all and Rio’s response drove that point home. “So you don't deem me asking you specifically to be my supervisor worth your time?” It was the opposite actually, but it was too late to say that now. “I came to this university for your reputation, for you . But you know what? I'm good actually, I always have a backup plan.” A backup plan? What backup plan? How had she managed to royally fuck this up? This wasn’t how she usually was! “I also emailed Ms. Maximoff about being my supervisor and she was rather enthusiastic about the idea. She also seems like someone who can actually be bothered to drag herself away from her laptop for two seconds to have a conversation with me.” Wanda’s name ripped her from her thoughts. She had said that she wouldn’t respond to Rio’s email, why had she lied? Agatha couldn’t believe the audacity that woman possessed. There was no way in hell that she was going to let Wanda take this student away from her. She had to claw this back. She was searching Rio’s face for any hint that she was lying about Wanda responding to her but she couldn’t find one. All she saw was a look of determination.

Agatha took off her glasses in an attempt to appear casual before saying, “I really thought it would take you longer to break than that. You don't seem that easily flustered.” Was it working? She could see the response forming in Rio’s mind and spoke before she could. “But I have to admit, the passion you just showed is intriguing. Bring me your proposal on Wednesday, I'll give it a look over and make my decision.”
Rio was just staring at her, her mouth hanging open slightly. ‘Please can this just end now? I need this to be over.’ “This is where you agree, thank me and leave.” Rio stuttered out her reply and started to make her exit. This absolute travesty of a meeting was so nearly over, so why was she calling Rio’s name again? “Try not to get so easily wound up in future, or this will not work out.” She didn’t look at Rio for her response. She just put her glasses back on and stared blankly at her screen until she heard the door shut.

What the actual fuck was that?

Agatha checked her watch, 12pm. How had it only been thirty minutes? It felt like an age. She leant forward, resting her head on her desk and groaned. Today was not her day. Thankfully she only had the one lecture to do today as it was the first day of classes and she always kept the rest of the day free for meetings with PhD students. She thanked every god she could think of that the rest of them had been so lack-lustre this year that she’d only taken one on, even if that one was already causing her some issues.

She sat back up and promptly deleted those useless bullet points, instead replacing them with an actual plan to supervise Rio through her PhD. She opened up her proposal and started making notes on it. ‘Fuck me, did I ask her to bring me her proposal on Wednesday?’ She was literally annotating Rio’s proposal now. Why had she asked her to bring it to the next meeting? ‘She is absolutely going to think I’m crazy. Maybe she should go to Wanda instead.’ As soon as the thought entered her head she chastised herself for thinking it. ‘Absolutely not! Get your shit together, Harkness!’ She wasn’t sure how long she’d been working on it, but her head was starting to spin. So she closed her laptop and left her office.
She couldn’t decide what she needed more, some fresh air or a drink. Muscle memory seemed to take over and she found herself outside Jen’s office.

Agatha knocked on the door and, upon Jen’s approval, entered the room.
She sighed heavily, and dramatically flopped into one of the arm chairs. “Okay, how bad is it?” Jen asked, knowing exactly what Agatha needed.
“The cupboard under your desk kind of bad.”
“Oh damn.” Jen reached down, retrieving a bottle of whiskey and two glasses from the cupboard. She gave them both a healthy pour and sat in the chair opposite Agatha. “Should I text Lilia?”
Agatha sighed again. “No, I’ll tell her later. She always puts more into the first day than we do.”
Jen laughed. “She puts us to shame really.”
“Ha. Yep.” Agatha raised her glass to Jen before taking a sip. The whiskey warmed her throat as it went down. If she thought about it too long she’d say that she and Jen had made a little too much of a habit out of midday drinks in their offices, which is why she wasn’t thinking about it. “So go on, tell me what you needed the comfort of the cupboard for.” Jen said as she sat back in her seat.
“I just had my first meeting with that PhD student I told you about.” She took another sip. “It went… well, it went.” She chuckled dryly.
“Oh, was she not what you thought? Did she catfish you with her proposal?”
“The opposite.” Agatha said, turning her attention to the liquid in her glass. “She’s actually more than I thought she would be.” She wasn’t entirely sure what she meant by that, so she took another sip. “She attended my lecture actually.”
Jen raised an eyebrow, taking a sip herself. “Oh wow, she was really trying to make an impression then. And it sounds like it worked?”
“It did.”
Jen leant forwards, putting her glass on the table between them. “Agatha, if I may, I don’t think this is the student you came here to talk about.” She paused and Agatha knew she was waiting for her to meet her gaze. “The Maximoff boy is taking your module this semester isn’t he?” Agatha let her eyes drop again – more looking through Jen than looking at her – but she didn’t respond. She really didn’t know what to do about Billy.

“Agatha?” Jen brought her back into the room. “We don’t have to talk about it if you don’t want to, but it’s clearly messing with your head.”
Agatha took another sip before saying, “He’s the reason I was so behind on my lecture prep for the semester. Wanda messaged me to let me know that he would be in my class for the semester. Because she’s thoughtful that way. ” She said the last few words in a whinier tone.
“You spoke to Wanda?” Jen’s voice was sharp with concern and an edge of surprise.
“We made an agreement to only speak about work. Since we work in the same department we figured that we couldn’t just avoid speaking entirely, so this was the compromise we found. And now, since Billy is one of my students, he counts as work.” She let out one short laugh before continuing. “You know she implied that I’d treat him harshly? ‘Please try to be nice to him,’ she’d said. As if I’d ever treat him badly. I mean how could she actually think that?” She’d started and now she couldn’t stop. It all just came pouring out. “Oh and the cherry on top was that she said ‘I’m not asking for me, I’m asking for him.’ I mean what right does she have to ask me for anything? How the fuck did she think using Billy to guilt trip me was a good idea? I should have taken him with me instead of leaving him with his manipulative bitch of a mother. He doesn’t deserve this. He did nothing wrong.” When her rant finally ended she was breathing heavily. She hadn't even realised how angry she’d gotten until she was sat in the silence after the fact.

Jen had just sat, quietly listening to her vent, clearly aware that she needed to get this off of her chest. Agatha took a deep breath and slowly released it. “I think I needed that. Thanks.”
“Literally any time.” They both took a long sip of their whiskey. “Are you going to talk to him before your next lecture?” 
“I honestly have no idea. I don’t even know how to begin a conversation with him any more. Do I request a meeting with him?”
Jen thought for a second. “You could ask him to meet you in an empty classroom. That way you get privacy to have a conversation and you’re both free to leave whenever you want.”
“That’s a pretty decent idea actually, Jen.”
“I do have them occasionally.”
They both laughed and then let a comfortable silence settle around them for a moment.

“I am disappointed that you don’t have a new woman though. You’re getting boring in your old age.” Jen smirked.
“Shut the fuck up Jen.”

Chapter End Notes

Please let me know if having multiple perspectives is working!

Rio

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

There was something about the way Wanda had spoken that bothered Rio, but she couldn’t quite place it. Was it just the awkwardness of them literally running into each other and that being their first conversation? Did Wanda feel embarrassed about the fact that she never replied to Rio’s email? Why did she appear almost nervous when Agatha was mentioned?
Rio had so many questions that she knew she wasn’t going to get the answers to any time soon, so she put her headphones on and walked back to her flat. The mild September air and the music playing in her ears helped to ground her as her mind was still racing.

Her thoughts wandered back to her meeting with Agatha. She wasn’t going crazy, that was a strange meeting right? Had Agatha truly not read her proposal? Had she forgotten to attach it to her email? Or was this Agatha’s weird way of punishing her for speaking out in her lecture, for ruining a twist she was trying to give the first years?

Rio arrived at her flat and turned on the TV for background noise, doing basic tasks to keep herself busy and to try and pass some time. She was starting to miss home, her parents, her friends. Sure she’d called them in the past few months that she’d been in England, but it wasn’t the same as physically being with them or actually spending time with them.

She was pacing around the living room, restless, unsure what to do with her time. It was early afternoon – and she’d already decided that she wasn’t the kind of lonely woman who drinks alone on a Monday afternoon – so she did the next best thing. She went out, bought some snacks, changed into comfy clothes and settled herself in for a Lord Of The Rings marathon. It had been a good few years since she’d treated herself to twelve hours of the best cinema ever made and she knew that it would take her mind off of, well, everything.

The next morning she woke up still on her sofa, having fallen asleep at some point during the last half of Return Of The King, with a sharp pain in her neck and shoulder. “Ah, fuck.” She hissed when she tried to sit up properly. “Note to self, do not fall asleep on this sofa again.” She tried her best to massage it to a point where she could move her neck again and shuffled into her room to freshen herself up for the day.

She stood in the shower letting the warm water cascade over her, getting lost in the feeling for a moment. When she finally managed to drag herself out of the shower she checked her phone for the first time and saw messages in her chat with Alice and Billy.

Billy: Are you coming in today or did Agatha scare you too much yesterday?

Billy: I’ll take your silence as an admission of fear

Alice: Leave her alone, she’s an important PhD student you know. 😘

Rio chuckled and checked the time: 10:12am. It was too late for her to go now even if she wanted to.

Rio: Nah I’ve got some actual work to do for my important PhD haha

She got dressed and took her laptop to the sofa, opening up her proposal to make her edits. She read and re-read the title as Agatha’s words replayed in her mind. “Not the strongest of titles.”
She sighed as she erased the words before typing it back out exactly word for word. “‘Not the strongest’ what the fuck does that mean?” she asked out loud. “What does she want me to change it to?” What did Agatha want her to do to any of the proposal? She hadn’t been specific, she’d just asked for it to be brought to her. ‘She’s getting it emailed.’ Rio thought. ‘I’m not wasting paper for her.’  

 She opened up her original email to Agatha and checked that the proposal had actually been attached, which it had, so what did she actually want her to do? Was this all just some weird mind game to see if Rio would do anything she asked without questioning it? 
She thought about going into the university to ask Agatha what she wanted her to do but then decided going in was stupid when she could just email her. But what would she say? “I’m terribly sorry but this basic task you’ve set me has proven too difficult.” No, of course she couldn't say that. Would asking for clarification give Agatha more ammo to use against her? “Miss Vidal, not only have you attempted to embarrass me in a lecture, but you have also failed to perform the most mundane task I could have asked you to do.” Rio could hear her voice clear as day saying the words in her head. She huffed and threw her head backwards against the couch, staring at the ceiling before her eyes began to wander around her strikingly bare apartment.

She thought about her house back in Virginia and how she had a plant or a painting in every room to add colour and character. She was renting this flat so she knew she couldn’t start putting canvases on the walls, but there was nothing stopping her from getting a few plants. She closed her proposal and started googling garden centres nearby, within an hour she was walking down the aisles carefully choosing plants.
She didn’t want anything too high maintenance in case she managed to find herself a social life at some point, but she got a few indoor plants and a couple of outdoor ones to put on her balconette.
Happy with her choices, she went back to her flat and got to work finding places for them. She liked working with her hands, feeling the soil shift through her fingers, it reminded her of working at her parents' vineyard when she was a child. She fondly remembered chasing her cousins through the vines and sneaking handfuls of grapes when the adults weren’t paying attention. They’d always know, of course, because her lips would be stained red, but they never told her off. She later realised that they probably didn’t care because the grapes were a healthy snack and they’d rather she ate those than sugary candy.

Rio caught herself smiling widely at the memories and decided that she’d print out some pictures of her family at some point and put them in the living room to bring a little bit of home to her current accommodation.
Her stomach rudely reminded her that she hadn’t eaten anything yet and she widened her eyes in surprise when the time showed 2pm. Had she really been that long at the garden centre? Actually, she should be more surprised that she wasn’t longer. She could have happily spent hours there. Her stomach rumbled again, protesting its emptiness, so she made some food and settled in front of the TV. She hadn’t found any British shows she enjoyed yet so she watched reruns of Brooklyn 99 while she ate.

Hours went by while she was zoned out watching the show but she told herself that she couldn’t procrastinate any longer and she had to do something with her proposal. She begrudgingly opened her laptop and pulled it up only to be staring at it with no idea what to do. She let out an exasperated groan and shouted into the ether. “What do you want from me?”
Her phone buzzed next to her and a small part of her hoped it would be from Agatha saying that she’d made a mistake and she no longer needed a new proposal, but it was from Alice.

Alice: Our lectures are done for the day. Fancy a drink?

God did she ever !

Rio: Give me half an hour, I’ll meet you guys at the bar.

She got her jacket and shoes on and practically ran out of the door. The air was cooler now, biting slightly at her cheeks as she briskly walked onto campus. She knew she was cutting it fine but honestly, what the fuck what she meant to write? If Agatha was making her overthink this much after only one day what hope did she have for the next three years?

She walked into the bar and immediately spotted Alice and Billy, sliding into the booth next to Alice. “We took the liberty of buying you a pint.” She said, gesturing to the glass in front of Rio and Rio took a healthy first sip. “Not that I don’t enjoy a good pint, but I’m going to have to get you two to expand your palettes at some point.” She smirked at the two of them.
“Oh we’d love to,” Billy began, “but we don’t have the funds to expand our palettes. We’re starving students you know.”
Rio laughed. “Okay, fair point. I’m just saying there’s more to experience than the cheapest lager in the student bar.”
“We get it, the older you get, the more boujee you get. We’re not at your level yet.” Alice said in mock annoyance.
“Hey, I’m only thirty! I can still drink you teenagers under the table!” Rio replied with a confidence she thought she would regret later… and she was right. As soon as the shots came out she knew she was done for. She managed to hold her own against Billy and Alice but she would be lying if she said that they didn’t have her on the ropes.

The bar lights came on at exactly midnight signalling that it was time to go home. Rio insisted on making sure the kids got back to their campus accommodation safely but didn’t spare a thought on how she was going to get home until she was already ten minutes into the half an hour walk. She could stop and order an Uber to take her the rest of the way but that would mean standing in the street and waiting for it. She could walk back to campus and order it from there, but that would be a waste of ten minutes walking, so she just decided to keep going.

She was glad that there was nobody around to see her nearly fall into her flat – she had leaned too heavily on the door as she was unlocking it and it took her with it as it swung inwards. She kicked off her shoes and haphazardly threw her keys onto the kitchen counter before getting herself a glass of water. She leant against the counter to steady herself as she sipped. Maybe she couldn’t keep up with the undergrads any more. But they didn’t need to know that.

Her eyes lazily moved across the living room and focussed on her laptop still sitting on the sofa and she groaned as she turned around, putting her cheek on the cool surface of the kitchen counter. “Some of my best essays during my undergrad were written whilst drunk.” she mumbled against the marble. “How much different could this be?” She allowed herself another few seconds of moping before she forced herself to go to the couch and open her laptop once more.
She decided to stop thinking and just type. Her fingers flew over the keys as she made change after change and some amount of time later it was done. She attached it to an email to Agatha that read:

Dear Professor Harkness,

Please find attached my newly written proposal. I do hope this one is more to your satisfaction.

Sincerely
Rio Vidal

She hit send and relaxed into the sofa cushions. She had been agonising over this for the whole day and now it was finally over. She was annoyed at how easy it had actually been. Why had it been so hard for her to do while sober? Her email notification pinged and she opened one eye to look at it. It was from Agatha.

Dear Miss Vidal,

Thank you for your revised proposal. I would very much like to discuss it tomorrow in my office, 9am.  

Sincerely
Professor Harkness

9am? She could do 9am.

 

__________

 

Rio woke the next morning to the sun burning her eyes. She clearly hadn’t shut her blind before falling into bed last night. She slowly rolled over, very aware of the dull ache in her head. ‘Fucking undergrads.’
She cracked open one eye and grabbed her phone to check the time – thankfully she’d had the brain power to plug it in last night – 8:15am. She groaned and pushed her head further into her pillow for a few seconds before her eyes flew open. 8:15? Her meeting with Agatha was in 45 minutes.
Fuck.
She practically flung herself out of bed, barely able to ignore the pounding in her head, and ran to her en-suite. Had she brushed her teeth last night? The way her mouth felt suggested that she hadn’t. She rushed to get ready and since she didn’t have time for a shower, had to put all of her faith in dry shampoo.

She threw her laptop and keys into her bag and ran out of the door, power walking towards campus. She prayed that she’d make it there in time to grab a coffee.

She did not.

She jogged through the ancient history department, nearly flattening a student as she went, and stopped at Agatha’s office catching her breath. She checked the time, 9:08. FUCK.
She took one last breath before knocking on the door.
“You may enter.”

Rio gingerly opened the door and slowly stepped into the room, nervously anticipating the harsh words that were sure to be fired at her. But instead, Agatha was sitting at her desk just watching her. After a moment she spoke. “Please take a seat, Miss Vidal.” Rio did as instructed and began trying to explain her lateness. “I’m really sorry that I’m late, it’s entirely my fault. I forgo-”
Agatha cut her off by raising her hand and speaking over her. “You don’t need to provide excuses.” There was no harshness in her tone, it was more reassurance than anything. “I would like to start by apologising for my lack of professionalism in our last meeting. I had some personal things that I needed to sort out, but I assure you that nothing will affect my conduct going forward.”
Rio relaxed in her chair and nodded, unsure what to say. Agatha continued. “Speaking of professionalism, let’s discuss your proposal shall we?” Rio nodded again trying to remember what she had written just a few hours ago and realisation dawned on her that she hadn’t actually proof-read it before sending it to Agatha. She hoped that she managed to keep her expression cool enough to hide her panic, though the slight twitch at the corners of Agatha’s lips suggested otherwise.
“I won’t sugar coat it Miss Vidal, this has to be, without a doubt, the best PhD proposal that I have ever read.”
Rio’s eyes widened in surprise. “Really?” She asked incredulously. ’Point Vidal.’ She thought. But her confidence was wiped out when Agatha’s face turned serious.
“No.” She fixed her eyes on Rio, “I don’t think a single word was spelled correctly in the entire document.” Rio shuffled trying to look away but she couldn’t help herself from locking her eyes onto Agatha’s. They were the kind of blue that held you, kept you where she wanted you until she was ready to let you go. Agatha continued her chastisement, bringing Rio back into the room. “I would go as far as to suggest that you were inebriated when you wrote this, Miss Vidal.”

Rio’s head dipped, shame taking over her. She wasn’t a first year undergraduate any more, her headache served as proof of that. She really shouldn’t have written and sent a PhD proposal while she was half-torn. But also, she wasn’t the only one in the wrong. Agatha shouldn’t have asked her to re-send a document that she already had without giving specifics on what she wanted changing, right?

Three times now Rio had had an opportunity to prove to Agatha that she was worthy of having her as her supervisor, and three times now Rio had messed it up. Agatha didn’t seem like the type to give out endless amounts of second chances. She had to find a way to claw this back. “Professor Harkness, I…” She could come up with a myriad of excuses, put the blame anywhere she wanted, but she knew honesty was the best course of action. “Yes, I was drunk when I wrote and sent that to you. I can only apologise and hope that I haven’t painted a picture of myself that is too tarnished to fix.”

Agatha pursed her lips and leant forward, resting her elbows on her desk. “I appreciate your honesty, Miss Vidal.” She seemed to think for a moment before continuing. “How about we wipe the slate clean? Let’s use this moment to start again.” She stood up from her desk to sit in the chair opposite Rio, and handed her her laptop. “Here are my edits on your original proposal.” Rio accepted the laptop and began skimming through the document. “There aren’t many as it is a very strong one. One of the best I’ve seen, actually, but I did take the liberty of changing your title.” That had been the first thing Rio had noticed and she had to admit that it was miles better.
How Modern Media Has Changed The Portrayal Of Greek Mythology To Make It Accessible For A New Generation.

“I guess this is why they pay you the big bucks.” Rio said with a chuckle as she looked back up at Agatha, who gave a satisfied smile in return. Rio gave the laptop back to her and she closed it, setting it on the coffee table in between them. “So tell me, Miss Vidal, what piqued your interest about Greek Mythology in the first place?”
Rio leaned back in her chair. “I read Percy Jackson as a kid, and that was all it took really.”
Agatha matched her posture. “Of course it was.”
“Excuse me?” Was Agatha actually mocking her? Why ask a question if she was just going to ridicule the answer? “Was my answer not up to you-”
“No, no, Miss Vidal, I apologise. I wasn’t meaning to poke fun at you.” Agatha hurried to defend herself. “I just meant that Percy Jackson is a gateway drug for most people.” She smiled softly.
Rio blinked, her mind going blank for a second. “Oh.” ‘Jumped the gun again.’ “Sorry. I guess I’m just used to being the ‘weird kid’ and having to defend myself.” She rubbed the back of her neck sheepishly.
“Oh, you and I both. You don’t need to apologise for that.” Agatha leaned forward, resting her arms in her lap. “Passion like that is a good trait to have. It does dance along the line of hot headedness though… You might want to watch out for that.” She finished with a smirk.
Rio knew that she was right. She usually had a tight grip on her emotions, but this was the second time she’d let that control slip in just a few days. 

Rio found herself looking into Agatha’s eyes, they were shining softly and she swore that she saw two shades of blue in them. She suddenly became hyper aware of the fact that she was staring at Agatha. ‘How long have I been looking at her? How long have we been sitting in silence for? Say something you idiot.’
“Have you ever read them?” She blurted out, inwardly cringing at how loudly she’d said it.
Agatha leaned back again before saying, “I think I was a little too old for them when they came out.” She cleared her throat before speaking again. “What other sources are you planning on using for your thesis? You’ve outlined a few in your proposal, but are you going to expand your research at all?”

They spent the next hour talking about the various books, shows and films that Rio had read and watched as part of her research and Agatha offered up a few new ones that Rio hadn’t considered. The conversation was easy, just two like-minded individuals talking about something they were both passionate about and Rio barely felt the time pass. She was so at ease that she had to keep reminding herself that Agatha was a professor and she was technically her student, although Agatha still hadn’t actually said that she would be her supervisor. She began to wonder why that was. Had she forgotten to say it? She’d mentioned that she’d had some ‘personal things’ on her mind so maybe she’d just been so caught up in whatever that was and it had slipped her mind.  Should she ask her? Or was it redundant now since they were already talking about her research materials and how she was going to structure her thesis?

She was broken from her thoughts by Agatha checking her watch and saying, “I’m afraid we are going to have to call this meeting here, Miss Vidal. I have a lecture to teach in fifteen minutes.” She stood up and started gathering up her laptop and various papers from her desk. “You’re welcome to sit in, you might learn something new.” She had her back to Rio so her expression was hidden but her tone was light.
Rio stood to leave as well but she needed to clarify Agatha’s stance on being her supervisor. “So does this mean that you’re agreeing to be my supervisor, Professor Harkness?” Agatha was on her way to the door, but she stopped and turned. “I thought that was obvious, no? I wouldn’t have changed your title, annotated your proposal and asked about your research methods if I wasn’t planning on taking you on.” She moved to the door and opened it before continuing. “I’d like to set up a weekly meeting at the same time as today to discuss your progress.” Rio’s expression must have been one that conveyed worry because she quickly followed up with, “relax, I don’t need a specific word count. I just like to know that my students are capable of showing that they’re committed.”
Rio agreed and walked past her, leaving the office. “Miss Vidal?” She turned back. “I wouldn’t recommend drinking heavily before our meetings in future. I let it slide this time, but do not expect me to be so gracious should it happen again.”
“Of course, Professor.”

They both went their separate ways and Rio pulled out her phone to message Billy and Alice.

Rio: I’m coming to the lecture today to offer my incredible brain to you two.

Alice: Ha. We’re just grabbing a coffee and we’ll be there

Rio: Can you pick me one up too and I’ll meet you in there?

Billy: Sure, what’s your order?

Rio: Black, like my heart

Billy: Obviously.

Rio shook her head and turned a corner in the corridor, narrowly avoiding walking into someone. “Oh shit, I’m sorry!”
“You’re making a bit of a habit out of this, Miss Vidal.”
She looked up and met Wanda Maximoff’s eyes. “Please, call me Rio, Miss Vidal is so formal. Especially since I’ve nearly killed you twice now.”
Wanda laughed. The sound was bright and Rio couldn’t help but join in.
“I suppose that’s true. Where are you rushing off to?”
“I’m going to sit in on Professor Harkness’ lecture.” At the mention of Agatha’s name, something flashed across Wanda’s face. It was similar to the look that Agatha had had when she mentioned Wanda’s name a few days ago. There was something between them, a history of some kind, but it wasn’t Rio’s place to know – as interested as she was. Whatever the look was, it disappeared quickly as Wanda seemed to steel herself. “Isn’t an undergraduate lecture a bit beneath you?” Her tone was harsh and it took Rio by surprise, but she hid it well keeping her expression neutral. “You’re never too old to learn new things.”
Wanda hummed in thought. “I suppose that’s true. I’ll let you go.” She started to walk away, but turned back to face Rio whilst walking backwards. “I’m sure we’ll see each other again, Rio. Though next time I hope it’s not because I’m about to have a near death experience.” She winked and turned to walk forwards again.

Rio stood there for a second, unsure what to do.
‘Was she just flirting with me?’
‘What was that look she had when I mentioned Agatha?’
‘Was she just flirting with me?’
She felt her phone buzz in her hand.

Alice: Where are you?

Shit.

She checked the time and raced to the lecture hall, sliding into the seat that Alice and Billy had saved for her just in time. “What took you so long?” Alice asked.
“I bumped into Ms. Maximoff and we got talking. I didn’t notice the time.”
