Billy whipped his head to look at her. “You were speaking to Ms. Maximoff?”
But before Rio could respond, the lights dimmed and Agatha began her lecture. She made a mental note to ask Billy why he looked so worried and pulled out her laptop to take notes on the lecture.

Having not immediately embarrassed herself this time, she was able to be fully immersed. Agatha taught with such confidence, knowing exactly where to inject humour and how to bring people back when she could see that she was starting to lose them. She made a few attempts to get the students to speak up and engage but, being scared first years, they didn’t bite. Rio nudged Billy and whispered, “You should join in.” but he just shook his head so she leaned forward slightly to catch Alice’s eye. “Well one of you needs to.”
“No thank you.”
She rolled her eyes. ‘If someone doesn’t start joining in soon, I’m going to have to.’ She thought even though she’d made a promise to herself that she would stay silent. Eventually a quiet voice somewhere near the front piped up, answering Agatha’s question and then there was a trickle of other responses. Rio saw Agatha smile. “Excellent thank you. You see, it’s not so scary to join in.” She cast a glance over the students and Rio was certain that this time, Agatha’s eyes lingered on her.

Chapter End Notes

No I absolutely did not use my own personal experience of getting absolutely wasted and writing essays during my undergad, why would you ask that?

Agatha

6 Years Ago

Agatha stood in front of her wardrobe staring at her clothes as if the perfect outfit would magically appear. Her hair and makeup were done, the final hurdle was just the clothes, and it was causing issues. She wanted to make an impression of course, but didn’t want to go overboard, and towing that line right now was proving difficult.
A banging at her door got her attention, she opened it and was greeted by Jen and Lilia barging into her flat and beelining for her bedroom.
“Don’t panic, we’re here.”
“What are our options?”
Agatha followed them into the room and dramatically threw herself onto the bed with a groan. “I feel like a teenager again. I swear first dates get harder the older you are.”
“Where are you going again?” Jen and Lilia were deep in her wardrobe throwing her clothes into piles of yes, no and maybe.
“She’s taking me to dinner. A classic first date location.” Agatha lifted her head when a jacket flying across the room caught her eye. “Be careful please, some of those are expensive!” She got off of the bed and moved towards the yes pile. “They’re not going to be good choices if they’re wrinkled.” She picked up a pair of plum trousers and scrunched her face up. “These made it to the yes pile?”
“Agatha please, this is a delicate process.” Lilia said, turning to see what she was talking about. “Oh actually, hang on. Jen, pass me that shirt!”
Jen raised an eyebrow in disbelief. “Really?”
“Yes, trust me.” Lilia handed Agatha a white shirt and shooed her into the bathroom to get changed.

She stood in front of the mirror toying with the top button on her shirt. Should she do it all the way up or should she leave a couple of buttons undone? No doubt Jen and Lilia would tell her to  leave them undone. She touched up her makeup and made sure her hair was in place before walking back into the room.
“Oh damn.” Jen said, her eyebrows lifted and her mouth slightly open. “Good job, Lilia.” They high-fived and Lilia gave a satisfied nod, clearly pleased with her work.
“I have to hand it to you, the outfit is good.” Agatha said, doing a twirl.
“Purple is your colour, Harkness. Wear the blue coat with it as well. It’ll pull it all together.”
The three of them went into the living room and Jen started adjusting Agatha’s collar. “Just have it open a little bit mo-”
Agatha swatted her hand away. “Jennifer, get off me.” She checked her watch and started putting her boots on. “She’s picking me up in ten minutes. So thank you for your help but now I need you to leave before you embarrass me. I would like to get further than the first date.” She gave them a smirk before ushering them out of the door.
Lilia stopped at the threshold and said, “Don’t do anything I wouldn’t do.” Punctuating it with a wink.
Agatha rolled her eyes. “Get out!”

She paced around her flat until she heard a knock at her door. She took a deep breath and counted to five before opening it and felt her stomach flip when she saw Wanda standing on the other side. She looked gorgeous. Her red waves framing her face perfectly, making her eyes look like a brighter shade of green. She looked Agatha up and down, a smile spreading across her face. “You look amazing.”
Agatha smiled back, her heartbeat quickening just a fraction as Wanda said, “ready to go?”

Wanda had picked a small, Italian restaurant that was tucked down an alley. “Are you bringing me here on a date, or to kill me?” Agatha asked sarcastically.
Wanda laughed, “now that would be telling.” She winked and Agatha knew that she could no longer deny just how smitten she was.

The date was probably in Agatha’s top three. The conversation flowed easily, a good balance of flirty and serious. Wanda told her that she had a child, a twelve year old boy, and said that she wanted to be upfront about it straight away. “Dating when you have a child can be somewhat of a minefield. It’s best to get the revelation out of the way as early as possible.” She looked nervous and Agatha immediately reassured her that it wasn’t going to scare her off.
“When you’re comfortable with it, I’d be happy to meet him.”
“Agatha, are you implying that this date is going well enough that you’ll reach that point?” Wanda smirked, her tone giving no hint of seriousness.
“I know! How presumptuous of me.” Agatha laughed.

They were there for hours and didn’t notice that they were the only two customers left until a waiter politely told them that they needed to close. Wanda insisted on paying and walked Agatha home. They stood on the front steps of Agatha’s building still talking, not noticing the time passing. Being with Wanda was already so easy and gave Agatha a warm feeling in her chest. The way that Wanda looked at her made her feel like a teenager again. She had butterflies in her stomach and she was filled with giddy excitement.

“Oh wow, I didn’t realise how late it had gotten.” Wanda ran a hand through her hair as she checked her watch. “I don’t think I’ve stayed up this late in, well, twelve years.” She chuckled lightly and Agatha liked the way it made her eyes crinkle slightly.
“I didn’t notice the time passing, honestly.” Agatha said. “It’s been a good night.” She smiled looking into Wanda’s eyes and flinched slightly when she felt Wanda's fingers brushing her cheek. She was pushing a stray strand of hair behind her ear, letting her hand continue around the back of Agatha’s head and loosely holding the brown waves before pulling her forwards into a kiss.

It was gentle and quick, a mere suggestion of what it could be. They pulled back, holding each other's gaze for a second before Agatha grabbed Wanda’s face and brought their lips back together. It was rougher this time, more needy, more passionate. Wanda’s free hand found Agatha’s waist and pulled their bodies closer. Suddenly any space between them felt like the most offensive thing in the world and Agatha knew that this was the start of something good.

Present Day

Agatha had been drifting in and out of sleep for a few hours. Every time she considered giving it up as a bad job, she’d manage to drift back off for a bit, and so the cycle continued – until she heard her phone buzz. ‘Who the fuck is trying to contact me at this hour?’ She thought as she rolled over to grab her phone, the notification showing an email from Rio. This could absolutely wait until morning. This should absolutely wait until morning. So why was she desperate to see what Rio Vidal had to say right at this moment?
Refusing to sit up and risk waking up further, she rolled onto her back and read the email.

Dear Profesor Harlness,

Pleade find attached my newly written propposal. I do hope this on is more to you’re satisfactipn.

Sincerely
Rip Vidal

Was this a joke? What game was Rio playing with this? She was going to save reading the proposal for the morning, but the way this email was written had made her curious as to what she had just been sent.
“Oh. She is definitely drunk right now.” she said aloud, the surprise of the revelation taking over her, but she wasn’t mad about it. Usually receiving an email in the early hours of the morning from a student who is clearly under the influence would have pissed her off. But she had to laugh at the ridiculousness of it. Given how she had behaved in their first meeting, Agatha could hardly be mad at Rio right now. She was many things, but a hypocrite wasn’t one of them. At least she thought it wasn’t, Jen and Lilia might disagree. She replied, setting a meeting for 9am and rolled back over, drifting back to sleep and this time managing to stay asleep.

 

__________

 

She was in her office for 8am sorting her notes for the lectures she was giving that day and adding some revisions to Rio’s original proposal – but the only thing that she really changed was the title. The proposal was good. No, it was amazing actually. Agatha opened her own PhD proposal, from all those years ago, to compare the two and Rio’s won by a mile. She would have absolutely no trouble writing her thesis that was for sure.

9am came and went and Agatha knew that, given the state of her email from the early hours of the morning, there was a high chance that Rio had slept in. But she also knew that someone who had tried as hard as Rio had to impress her on the first day wouldn’t risk missing a meeting. She told herself that she’d give her a ten minute grace period and after that she would embrace the nickname of ‘Professor Hard-arse’ that Lilia had lovingly given her a few years ago.

The minutes ticked by and Rio was so close to sealing her fate, but at 9:08 there was a knock at Agatha’s office door. “You may enter.”
She fixed her eyes on the door and watched Rio carefully step into the room. She was definitely hungover but she’d gotten there just on the right side of the ten minutes so Agatha was going to go easy on her. Well, easy-ish. She watched Rio awkwardly try to avoid her gaze and let her stand for a minute before telling her to sit.
Rio immediately launched into an apology for her lateness but Agatha had already decided to let it go, so she cut her off. “You don’t need to provide excuses. I would like to start by apologising for my lack of professionalism in our last meeting. I had some personal things that I needed to sort out, but I assure you that nothing will affect my conduct going forward.” She kept her tone gentle and her face neutral and saw Rio relax a little bit. Despite her reputation for ‘busting balls’ she didn’t like doing it unless it was warranted. It just so happened that it was warranted more often than not so she didn’t have a choice most of the time. But she knew already that Rio didn’t need her to act like that. She was already a very good academic and just needed a little guidance here and there. That didn’t mean that she wasn’t going to take an opportunity to make her squirm though. Agatha was human, after all.

“Speaking of professionalism, let’s discuss your proposal shall we?” Rio nodded and Agatha could see the panic on her face. It was evident that she hadn’t proof-read the proposal before she had sent it. She had been too drunk to spell, never mind reading it back and making corrections, and Agatha had to fight to control the smile that wanted to be on her lips. She could be kind and tell Rio straight away that this was far from what she expected, rip the band-aid off so to speak. But she wanted to toy with her a tiny bit.

“I won’t sugar coat it Miss Vidal, this has to be, without a doubt, the best PhD proposal that I have ever read.” The look of surprise on Rio’s face was exactly what she wanted. She’d created a false sense of security for Rio to sit in for a moment. “Really?”
When the surprise started to take on an edge of smugness, she took that as her cue to end it. “No.” She fixed Rio with a glare that she knew she wouldn’t be able to look away from. It was a talent she’d picked up many years ago and she’d learned exactly when to use it. “I don’t think a single word was spelled correctly in the entire document. I would go as far as to suggest that you were inebriated when you wrote this, Miss Vidal.” Agatha couldn’t lie, she loved this feeling. The feeling of being in control and having the other person in the palm of her hand. The power she got from walking someone to the edge of what they wanted and pulling them back before they could step over.

The way that Rio hung her head made Agatha falter. Had she taken it too far? She’d only spoken to Rio once previously and didn’t know how far she could push her so it was entirely possible that she had overstepped. Shit. She could already hear the Dean reprimanding her about yet another complaint and so early into the academic year? She was going to feel this one for a while. Rio spoke and it broke her from her thoughts. “Yes, I was drunk when I wrote and sent that to you. I can only apologise and hope that I haven’t painted a picture of myself that is too tarnished to fix.”

Okay, an apology. Maybe Agatha could bring this back. She told Rio that she appreciated her honesty and offered a fresh start for both of them before sitting opposite Rio and showing her the changes that she had made on her original proposal. This seemed to be the right move because Rio relaxed again and Agatha relaxed in turn. ‘Crisis averted. Now behave.’ she told herself.

She realised that she needed to find out more about Rio to avoid this happening in the future. She was also just intrigued by Rio as a person and wanted to know more about her anyway, but the professional context was more important since that was how they were spending their time together. At least, that’s what she told herself. “So tell me, Miss Vidal, what piqued your interest about Greek Mythology in the first place?”
Rio assumed a more relaxed posture, clearly feeling more at ease and possibly a little bit excited to answer the question?
“I read Percy Jackson as a kid, and that was all it took really.”
A classic response. Not a bad one, but maybe an obvious one. Agatha had definitely taught her fair share of Percy Jackson fans and she liked to think that she’d gotten quite good at spotting them. Rio hadn’t given the vibe, but then again they had barely spoken. She really needed to find out more about this woman, for purely professional reasons.

“Of course it was.”
“Excuse me? Was my answer not up to you-”
“No, no, Miss Vidal, I apologise. I wasn’t meaning to poke fun at you.” Agatha hadn’t really thought herself to be a flexible person, but the way that her foot was firmly lodged in her mouth had her reconsidering that. How did she keep managing to do this? She was actively trying to avoid offending Rio but ended up doing it anyway. If she thought about it for too long she might say that Rio made her feel nervous, but she didn’t want to entertain the idea of why that might be. So she wouldn’t. “I just meant that Percy Jackson is a gateway drug for most people.” She smiled as she recalled the memory of giving Billy the books for his thirteenth birthday. The brightness of his smile, the way that he had hugged her and even the way that Wanda had laughed saying that it would keep him occupied for a week.

Rio apologised for her defensiveness and Agatha assured her that it was okay. They shared the experience of being known as the ‘weird kid’ and Agatha was actually happy that she had this kinship with Rio – though she couldn’t resist making a quip about Rio’s passion being mistaken for hot headedness. Was this the pot calling the kettle black? Absolutely. But Rio didn’t need to know that. Agatha had learned to keep a good hold on her emotions. There were, of course, exceptions but Rio wasn’t one of them. Her behaviour a couple of days ago had been a result of seeing Billy again and she had already acknowledged that it had been wholly unprofessional. The incident earlier in this meeting had been a poor judgement on her part and hadn’t been directly to do with Rio, she was like that with all of her students.

Agatha had fully zoned out and was more looking through Rio than looking at her. It wasn’t until Rio spoke that she came back into the room. “Have you ever read them?”
‘Have I been completely ignoring her? How many times has she asked that? How long were we sitting in silence for? Have I ever read what?’ She sat back in her chair, giving herself a second to collect her thoughts. ‘Oh! The Percy Jackson books!’ “I think I was a little too old for them when they came out.” Not a lie, but they’d already traded experiences of being outsiders as children and Agatha didn’t feel comfortable with her students knowing too much information about her.

Agatha had intended for this meeting to last an hour at the most. She did not expect to be sat for as long as they were discussing different books, shows and films that Rio could use for her research. The woman had good taste, Agatha couldn’t deny that, and she was incredibly well read. This shouldn’t have been a shock given her CV and the bibliography she had already listed in her proposal, but Agatha was pleasantly surprised nonetheless.
She enjoyed talking about her interests with someone who understood, it was rare to find someone who shared the same passion that she did and even more rare to find someone who was smart enough to keep up with her. Jen and Lilia weren’t idiots by any stretch of the imagination – and they could definitely hold their own –  but they were experts in other things that she didn’t know much about, and they didn’t really ‘talk shop’ like this. Her past PhD students had been too scared of her to engage in conversation like this and their meetings had often been stale and very much of a muchness. But this, this was something she could get used to.

She started to wonder how long they’d been sitting there, they’d been so engrossed that it didn’t feel like much time had passed. She checked her watch and was shocked to see that an hour had gone by. “I’m afraid we are going to have to call this meeting here, Miss Vidal. I have a lecture to teach in fifteen minutes.”  She picked up her laptop and went to get her lecture notes from her desk. She genuinely didn’t want the conversation to end so she offered for Rio to sit in on the lecture in the hopes that she would chime in again. For purely professional reasons.

“So does this mean that you’re agreeing to be my supervisor, Professor Harkness?”
‘How can someone this smart be this bad at reading the room?’
Agatha turned to face Rio. “I thought that was obvious, no? I wouldn’t have changed your title, annotated your proposal and asked about your research methods if I wasn’t planning on taking you on.”
‘Did she really need this spelling out for her? I know that I haven’t explicitly stated it but we have just spent a literal hour talking about it.’
She went to the door and opened it, telling Rio that she wanted to set up weekly meetings to check her progress. She had to suppress a chuckle when she saw the worried expression on Rio’s face. “Relax, I don’t need a specific word count. I just like to know that my students are capable of showing that they’re committed.”
Rio started to walk away and Agatha couldn’t resist one last quip.  “Miss Vidal? I wouldn’t recommend drinking heavily before our meetings in future. I let it slide this time, but do not expect me to be so gracious should it happen again.” She meant it, it wasn’t something she would usually stand for and she’d given Rio a free pass purely based on her own behaviour.

 

__________

 

She went via the campus café on her way to the lecture hall. The staff knew that when they saw her approaching, her order took precedence and they always had it ready in record time. Her reputation definitely had its perks and she wasn’t in a hurry to deprive herself of them.

She arrived at the lecture hall when students were still filtering into their seats and set up her laptop on the desk. She saw Billy sitting with his friend – who’s name she could not remember to save her life – but there was no sign of Rio. She checked her watch, 10:57. Rio had already been late once today, maybe she should have been more harsh about it earlier.
10:58. She felt a pang of disappointment, but Rio wasn’t required to sit in on lectures, she could come and go from campus as she pleased.
10:59. Rio came rushing through the door and beelined for the seat next to Billy. Had he been saving it for her? Were they friends? Billy, his friend, and Rio exchanged some words but they were hushed and Agatha couldn’t make them out.
11:00. Time to begin. She dimmed the lights and fired up the PowerPoint.

“Today we are going to talk about Hades and Persephone.” She changed the slide to show pictures of statues depicting both of the Gods. “Hades – as I’m sure you all know – is the King of the underworld, God of the dead and riches; and Persephone, his wife, is the Goddess of the dead, grain and spring. Hades was the eldest son of Cronus and Rhea, and the elder brother to Zeus and Poseidon. Persephone was the daughter of Zeus and Demeter, which makes them uncle and niece.” The slides changed to show a very complicated family tree for the Gods. It was so extensive that the text at the bottom was too small to actually read. “Don’t worry, I do not expect you to memorise this whole thing. This is just to illustrate that all of the Greek Gods are related and I promise that it will lose its shock factor.”

She spoke about Hades and Persephone as separate people first, outlining who they were and giving more detail about what they were known for, always enjoying the rapid typing or scribbling of the students taking notes. She noticed that even Rio was writing down the things she was saying. ‘No doubt trying to find things to correct me on.’ She thought, though it wasn’t in distaste.
She moved around to the front of the desk and leaned against it, taking a more relaxed posture. “So now that we’ve covered them as separate entities, does anyone know the story of how they began their relationship?” The students remained silent and she was making a pointed effort to not look at Rio. There was not a single doubt in Agatha’s mind that Rio knew multiple versions of the myth, hell they’d talked about a couple earlier on. But the first years were the ones she was wanting the answers from. “I find it hard to believe that none of you have come across a version of this tale.”
Out of the corner of her eye she saw Rio nudge Billy, trying to get him to join in, but he just shook his head. In truth, Agatha didn’t expect to hear from him much. She was currently just happy to accept that he kept coming to her lectures, it was a start.
She was pulled from her thoughts by a voice in the front row. “Hades saw her in a garden and he fell in love with her.”
She was about to respond when someone else spoke. “He abducted her and Demeter was so distraught that she neglected the earth.”
“Zeus sent Hermes to convince Hades to return Persephone and he agreed to let her leave for six months of the year.”
Agatha smiled, they were starting to gain their confidence. “Excellent thank you. You see, it’s not so scary to join in.” She couldn’t resist stealing a glance at Rio.
For. Purely. Professional. Reasons.

Wanda

Wanda knew that she had royally fucked up when it came to Agatha Harkness. Sure there were times when she hadn't wanted to admit it, times where she had used Agatha's hatred as a reason for her own, but at the end of the day, it had been her actions that had caused Agatha's reactions. At first Wanda had tried to match Agatha's hatred but it had always felt fake and wrong – because it was. The rumour of the reason for their break-up had spread through the faculty like wildfire and Wanda was standing at the spark point holding a match and kindling, nurturing the fire making sure it stayed lit. But then Agatha had allowed the flames to consume her.

She could have fought back, defended herself, told everybody that Wanda was lying, but she didn't. She just let them believe the story they were being told and had to deal with all of the snide remarks, the hushed conversations and blatant bitching that happened in the months following. People had been cruel to Agatha, and Wanda had let them. Her own need for self preservation winning out over her love for Agatha, that had been the problem all along. So many people had gotten hurt because Wanda was scared and the record had never been set straight, Agatha's name had never been cleared. Sure people eventually stopped talking about it and left her alone, but it was still a lie that they believed was the truth. They still took Wanda's side over hers in every little tiff they had at work and Agatha still let them. Wanda still let them. 

After their break-up they had made an agreement to only speak about work – it was a compromise that Wanda had all but begged for – Agatha was more than happy to never speak to her again, but she could hardly be blamed for that. Wanda had tried on a few occasions to have a conversation with Agatha, to explain herself, but she was shot down in a tone of voice that was so venomous she was surprised she didn’t get ill after hearing it. She had been trying when the wound was too fresh and the rumour mill was still churning, so she decided to wait a bit before trying again.

‘A bit’ had turned into a two and a half years and in that two and a half years Agatha showed no signs of opening back up to Wanda. If anything she got more closed off, which didn’t seem possible but she had managed it. At the start Agatha would make snide remarks when passing Wanda in the corridors which dissolved into not even acknowledging her existence and eventually became avoiding her entirely wherever possible. She knew that she deserved every bit of it, but that didn’t stop it from hurting.
Agatha had also changed how she treated other people in that span of time. She was always a no-nonsense kind of person – it’s what had drawn Wanda to her in the first place – but during that time she got more harsh, less forgiving and became downright mean. Wanda noticed that she received a record number of complaints against her from students that had unfortunately become the target of her anger. She was no longer giving it directly to Wanda so it had to go somewhere, and apparently she still had so much of it.

Receiving Rio Vidal's email requesting her as a supervisor had provided a work-related-excuse to talk to Agatha, and resulted in her losing out on an incredible PhD student. Wanda was prepared to stand her ground and fight for Rio as Agatha had been sending her, her rejects for far too long, but Agatha had asked. She had actually, and politely, asked. So Wanda had given in, how could she not? It was the first time in a two and a half years that Agatha had spoken to her in any hint of a nice manner and it had taken her a few minutes to process it, but in the end she couldn't deny her. She had to see this as Agatha giving her the smallest sliver of a chance to start taking a step in the right direction, so she broached the subject of them talking properly. It was completely ignored, but it wasn’t denied and she took that as a small win.

The worst part of their tumultuous past wasn't that she'd hurt Agatha – though that was definitely bad – it wasn't even that she'd hurt herself. It was that her own stupidity had hurt Billy. Her son was her everything and she'd taken Agatha away from him. She'd even made him hate Agatha to make herself feel better, to serve her own self-centred needs above his. That wasn't the trait of a good mother, it wasn't a way of being that she wanted to pass onto him. But she had, and that damage was irreversible. 

Her and Billy's relationship had been strained since she'd told him the truth, but she'd needed to do it. She'd almost lost him and she couldn't let him waste his second chance at life harbouring such intense hatred for a person that he had once loved so deeply. He hadn't looked at her the same since and that killed her, but she'd done the right thing – even if it had taken her far too long to do it. She'd told him to take Agatha's module, she'd not forced him, it was still a decision that he had made on his own, but she had told him that it would be okay. She had assured and reassured him that Agatha wouldn't treat him any differently to any of her other students, that she'd want him there and that she would be happy to see him again. 

There was an undercurrent of selfishness to it though, if Billy was taking Agatha's module then it would give her an excuse to talk to her. With Billy in her class he officially counted as ‘work’. Was it right to use her child in this way? Definitely not. Was she clutching at straws, trying any available option to just be face-to-face with Agatha again? Absolutely.
Agatha had driven her to this, she’d given her no other options. Wanda knew that Agatha would hate her using Billy like this, so she’d crack eventually and Wanda would get what she wanted. She didn’t want to cause any more hurt to Billy though so she hoped that this would also give the two of them a chance to fix their relationship and then everybody was able to win. 

__________


The first day of the new school year was the same as always: introductory lectures for the first years, re-introductions for the second and final years, starting the placement students off on their projects and meetings with the PhD students. Billy, like a typical teenager, had given her a set of rules to follow while they were both on campus. 

“No acting like my mother, no embarrassing me, no trying to spend time with me in public, and under absolutely no circumstances should you tell my friends that we’re related.”
She had laughed but promised to follow them all the same.

She was making her way back to her office to have a quick lunch before having to give more lectures. She liked to have a packed first day because it meant that she could get a head start on the year and hopefully have less work to do down the line. She was musing on how surprised she had been with her first year students. They were surprisingly confident and willing to join in with the lecture, it was a rare occurrence and she had welcomed it with open arms. Her thoughts shifted to Billy and she began to wonder how his day was going, she knew his first lecture had been with Agatha and she had messaged him wishing him a good day but he was yet to reply.

Her wonderings came to an abrupt end when she walked straight into a wall. No, not a wall. A person. The shock made her throw her arms out, forgetting the stack of papers she was holding, and she felt herself start to fall – her thoughts were running a mile a minute.
‘Ow!’
‘What was that?’
‘Oh my god I’m falling!’
‘This is going to hurt.’
She clenched her eyes shut and braced for impact. Another impact. But the feeling of hitting the floor never came, instead she felt a strong grip on her arm and a softer one on her waist steadying her and pulling her into the body of the other person. She instinctively threw her arms around them for support, immediately finding comfort in their grasp, and stayed lost in it for a moment before she felt them pulling away. She came back to herself and unwrapped herself from the poor person that she had just body slammed. They both started apologising, talking over each other.

“Oh my god I am so sorry!”
“No, no it’s fine. It was my fault!”
The other person, who Wanda now noticed was a woman, started picking up the mess of pages that were now scattered around them. “Here let me help you pick these up.” Her long, brown hair was covering her face so Wanda still had no idea who she was, but she didn’t recognise the voice and placed the accent as American. She bent down and started gathering the pages as well, accepting the pile that the mystery woman handed her.

‘Who is she?’
‘Is she an undergrad?’
‘She doesn’t look like a teenager.’
‘Is she a mature student?’
‘Please don’t let her be a teenager.’
Wanda’s thoughts were still racing as they stood back up and she started to process what had just happened. “Thank you for your help and for stopping me from ending up like these papers.” She offered her hand to the other woman, who she could now see was definitely not a teenager – she really didn’t need the scandal of being seen holding a teenager in the middle of a corridor. “I’m Wanda,” she said before correcting herself. “Ms. Maximoff.” The last thirty seconds had left her flustered and she momentarily forgot that she was at work and had just collided with a student. A student who smelled of forest pine and had a gentle smile.
“I’m Rio, Rio Vidal.” She was broken from her reverie by a hand taking hers and shaking it, and a name that she recognised. The PhD student she had lost out on. She had come up with a generic apology should she accidentally bump into her, of course she never thought that it would literally happen. “PhD student right? Sorry for not responding to your email, I’m unfortunately not taking any more students this year.” Wanda became hyper aware of the fact that they were still shaking – no, holding – hands and pulled away feeling awkward, before saying the rest of her prepared lines. “I hope you managed to find someone, I thought your proposal was excellent.” She cringed internally at how robotic she sounded. Rio Vidal’s proposal was one of the best that she had ever read and she had to admit that she was annoyed at how quickly she had folded at Agatha’s request to give her up. But she had to pick her battles with Agatha and if she wanted to have the smallest chance of Agatha letting her in long enough to say her piece, then she knew that she had to make sacrifices.

“Yes I did! Professor Harkness is my supervisor.” At the mention of her name, Wanda shyly looked in the direction of Agatha’s office as if she would appear and demand that Wanda stop talking to her student. But that would mean her actually being in the vicinity of Wanda which only happened if there was no conceivable way that it could be avoided. “Well good luck with that one. You’re gonna need it.” Wanda said before continuing to her office. It wasn’t a lie, Agatha was formidable even without the added anger Wanda had incited and Rio Vidal might seem brilliant on paper, but she had no doubt that she would find ways to pick her apart and break her down.

Wanda walked into her office, dropped her papers on the desk and absentmindedly rubbed her arm where Rio had grabbed her. There had been no intent to hurt her but the force needed to keep her upright had left a dull ache in the area. She picked up her phone, still no reply from Billy. She knew that he had lectures all day and wouldn’t be able to text her, and he probably wouldn’t want to, but she was still his mother and couldn’t help starting to worry.
She was considering messaging Alice as well – she had insisted that Billy give her Alice’s number when they were moving him into his accommodation, just in case – but that was a level of crazy that she didn’t want to be at on the first day.

She had never been an overprotective or overbearing mother, she wanted Billy to experience all the joys of being a child. Running around outside, playing sports, getting muddy when playing in the rain, scraping his knees falling over in the playground. She didn't want a ‘glass child’, it was something her and her ex-husband had agreed on as soon as they found out that she was pregnant. 

She did start to worry about him a little bit when he came out at thirteen. High school was hard enough without the added pressure of being ‘different’, but she was with Agatha then and she'd reminded her that they had both been fine being out in high school, and that he had both of them on his side ready to offer any help and guidance. 

Then they had the accident and she had come so close to losing him. Her whole world was balancing on a knife's edge and she felt like the walls of every room she was in were closing in on her. She had never had a panic attack before that time, but they were frequent until Billy was given the all clear to go home again. After that she was constantly worried about him. She became the overprotective and overbearing mother she'd vowed that she would never be, and their relationship suffered for it on top of the fact that she told him that she'd lied about why she and Agatha broke up. 

“He's fine, he's in lectures.” She said to herself, repeating it a few times until she felt calm again and tried to think about other things. She had about fifteen minutes left to eat her lunch before going back to teaching, throwing herself back into the day was her best option right now. So she did just that. The day didn’t exactly fly by, but it moved at a good pace and when it finally ended, she got a reply from Billy.

Billy: First day went well. Alice says hi.

Hardly the tell-all that she was hoping for, but it was good enough for now. 

__________

The next day she had tried a few more times to get Billy to open up, which was fruitless so she changed her angle and asked about Agatha. But he had just asked her why she cared. A very good question. What did she actually want to come out of talking to Agatha? She definitely wanted Agatha and Billy to fix their relationship, but she knew that would take time and wasn’t something she should meddle in – no matter how much she wanted to.
It was far too late to come clean and attempt to absolve Agatha of the blame that had been placed on her but Wanda at least wanted to apologise, as meek of a gesture as it might be.
It was something she had never actually done. Not with the words “I’m sorry” anyway.

She had told Agatha about the car crash and that Billy was in the hospital, and she had dropped everything and came running. She had even let Wanda hug her in the family waiting room while he was in surgery. That whole time was equal parts a blur and seared into her memory. Some things should recall clear as day and others she wasn’t sure if they had actually happened or if she had made them up. But Agatha being there was a memory she had kept.

She had told Agatha when Billy was awake, when he was home and that she was welcome to go see him, but she never did. Wanda didn’t hold that against her, she knew that when Agatha said she would never step foot into the house again, she meant it. It didn’t stop her from hoping though.

She had even let Agatha know that Billy had passed his A Levels with flying colours and that he had been given an unconditional offer to study at his top three university choices, but Agatha hadn’t replied. The only time she had replied was when Wanda told her that Billy would be taking her module this year and even then it was only, “Thank you for letting me know.”

But none of these situations had contained the words “I’m sorry.”

As time had progressed the words had faded into obscurity. Would they even matter this far down the road? Would Agatha be open to hearing them? Was she ever open to hearing them? They both struggled with expressing their emotions. In the four years that they were together the amount of times they’d said ‘I love you’ could be counted on one hand – and in their final argument, Agatha had wielded that fact like a weapon.

“I should have known that every time you told me you loved me it was a lie. You only ever said it when you needed to tighten the locks on my cage.”

The words echoed in Wanda’s head. They had been there since she’d first heard them, burying themselves into her brain loving to pop up again in moments of vulnerability. She had never quite managed to block them out, but she deserved them being there. She knew that she did, but she didn’t want to admit that they were true. She wasn’t ready to do that yet. She might never be ready.

__________

9am lectures weren’t Wanda’s favourite thing, and she didn’t believe anyone who said they enjoyed them, but she was sufficiently caffeinated and ready to attack the day. She gave her lecture to her final year students who, much like her, didn’t like having to be in morning classes, so she took pity on them and ended the lecture early. The stress of final year was something that she remembered all too well and she liked to do what she could to help alleviate it for her students. She took the opposite approach to most of her colleagues and graded their work on a less harsh curve, the students didn’t know this of course but it made her feel good knowing that her module was one that they didn’t have to worry so much about.

She got herself a fresh coffee and made her way back to her office for a meeting with one of her PhD students. She had decided to take two on this year, usually she had three but the pickings were so slim this year that she had to be more selective and, on top of that, she was working from Agatha’s reject pile as she had been for the last two and a half years.
Agatha was always the top choice for a supervisor, it had been that way since she had decided to become a supervisor. Or more correctly, since Wanda had convinced her to become a supervisor.

She had been toying with the idea for a while and Wanda knew how good she would be at it. She was an excellent teacher and a brilliant mentor.
“Your undergraduate students always achieve a high 2:1 or a 1st, and your masters students very rarely get below a distinction, so why not take that one step further?” Wanda had said and Agatha had finally agreed. It was never a competition between them, Wanda had been doing it for longer but she knew now that the requests would be split between them and she was happy that Agatha was getting the recognition that she deserved.
But since they broke up, it became a competition that Agatha was determined to win, hence her only picking the best and only allowing Wanda to choose from the ones she deemed unworthy of her time.

She was about to turn the corner to her office when she saw someone step around a split second before she did and she side-stepped to avoid colliding with them.
“Oh shit, I’m sorry!”
It was Rio Vidal again. Her eyes were wide and her face was full of concern, probably because she had very nearly knocked her over again. “You’re making a bit of a habit out of this, Miss Vidal.” Their eyes met and Wanda felt her breath catch. She hadn’t really had time to take in Rio’s features the last time they met but now there was no denying that this woman was gorgeous.

Wanda hadn’t dated anyone else since Agatha, she had decided to dedicate more of her time to Billy – even more so after the accident – and the idea of having to start again with someone in her forties was quite a daunting one. But now here she was having to fight to keep her expression neutral as her stomach started to flip while she made eye contact with an attractive woman.

“Please, call me Rio. Miss Vidal is so formal. Especially since I’ve nearly killed you twice now.”
The words Rio said weren’t funny, but Wanda had to laugh at how ridiculous she was being. She was a senior lecturer at Cambridge University getting butterflies over a student. A PhD student, but a student nonetheless. “I suppose that’s true. Where are you rushing off to?”
“I’m going to sit in on Professor Harkness’ lecture.”
There it was, the name that brought Wanda crashing back into reality. Rio wasn’t just any student. She was Agatha’s student and Wanda couldn’t help the animosity that coloured her words. “Isn’t an undergraduate lecture a bit beneath you?” She heard it as soon as she said it, but Rio didn’t react so maybe it hadn’t been as bad as she had thought.
“You’re never too old to learn new things.”
“I suppose that’s true. I’ll let you go.” Wanda started walking away but her thoughts got louder. ‘Why am I letting the mention of Agatha’s name make me scared? Why am I letting her control my life so much? Fuck it.’ She turned on her heel to face Rio again. “I’m sure we’ll see each other again, Rio. Though next time I hope it’s not because I’m about to have a near death experience.” She turned back the other way and continued walking. The wink had been subconscious, but she wasn’t mad about it. A little bit of flirting never hurt anyone. She subtly checked over her shoulder and smiled when she saw that Rio was watching her walk away.


6 Years Ago

Wanda paced around her empty house, Billy was staying with his father for the night – not because she expected to be bringing Agatha home, but because she wanted to be able to process the night without having to worry about him. Also she wasn’t sure how to explain to her twelve-year-old son that she was going on a date. Her relationship with his dad had always been on and off, even during their marriage, so the only person Billy had really known her to be going on dates with was his dad. But this was someone completely new for both of them and she wanted – needed – to wait until she knew it was the right time to tell him.

When she saw Agatha standing in the warm light of her apartment she couldn’t help looking at her – all of her. She looked incredible from her hair to her shoes, she didn’t expect anything less but seeing it with her own eyes was different. She heard the wobble in her voice when she told Agatha that she looked amazing but she didn’t care. The woman standing before her was breath taking and she deserved to know.

Wanda had been worried about bringing up Billy, she had a picture of him on her desk and was not ashamed of being his mother by any means but, she didn’t know if Agatha knew about him and how she would feel about it. The news was incredibly well received and Wanda felt like she was finally able to relax and fully enjoy the date. Talking with Agatha felt effortless, there were no awkward pauses and there was equal attentive listening on both sides. It was mostly flirty small talk but Agatha made her feel like she could say anything and she would be heard.

The time passed around them but it felt like they were in their own special pocket that would last forever. Until a waiter had to ask them to leave. Wanda didn’t want the night to end so she walked Agatha back to her apartment to get every last minute possible from the date. Their conversation didn’t stop when they got to Agatha’s building but there was a point when Wanda knew that they had to say goodnight. Afterall, how could they have a second date if the first never ended?

She’d had the urge to kiss Agatha since she first saw her and when her foot had accidentally grazed Wanda’s leg in the restaurant, the feeling had sent a jolt through her. Now, standing there on the steps of Agatha’s apartment building she couldn’t resist any longer. She needed to feel Agatha’s hair between her fingers, she needed to feel Agatha’s lips on hers and she needed other things that she would definitely have to wait longer for. But she didn’t mind waiting. Not when being with Agatha already felt this right. 

 

Agatha

Chapter Notes

Sorry it's been so long, I had covid and didn't have any energy at all!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The first week of the semester ended quickly and Agatha had found her rhythm – after a bumpy start. She usually found it easy to jump back into the new academic year, but seeing Billy again had knocked her off balance and it had taken her a few days to find her footing again. She didn’t blame him of course, how could she? It was his mother’s fault. It was always her fault.
Well, as of a two and a half years ago anyway. Before that point Agatha found that her mother was to blame for everything, but she had passed the mantle to Wanda as soon as she had given her the opportunity to do so. She couldn’t keep giving her mother the satisfaction of knowing just how badly she had messed up her daughter. The woman had been dead for twenty years for christ sake.

Her phone buzzed on the kitchen counter and it startled her from her thoughts, it was a message from Jen.

Dinner is almost ready, where are you?

She checked her watch and muttered “shit” before grabbing her keys and setting off.
Her, Jen and Lilia had been taking turns to host each other on a Saturday night for years. It had started sporadically, then became a term-time thing, then it became monthly and finally it turned into a weekly affair. Agatha would never admit it out loud but she was glad that she had found a connection with the two of them, having them in her corner during the fallout with Wanda had been a godsend and she genuinely didn’t know how she would have gotten through it if they hadn’t been there.

She pulled up outside of Jen’s house and walked straight through the door. “You know leaving your door unlocked as a single woman isn’t a safe choice, Jennifer.”
“Well it’s a good job you finally turned up, your glare is strong enough to destroy an army.” Jen called back from the kitchen. Agatha snorted, Jen wasn’t wrong. She took off her boots and hung up her coat before making her way to the kitchen to join her friends, taking a deep breath as she went. “Is this an original Kale creation tonight or are we feasting on the stylings of Hello Fresh?” It wasn’t a judgement, she was partial to using Hello Fresh herself.
“It’s a combination.”
“She’s treating us this time.” Lilia said, taking a spoon and helping herself to a taste of whatever Jen was stirring on the hob. “Though she could treat us to a little bit more salt.”
Agatha laughed. “Careful Lilia, you know how precious she is over her seasonings.”

The three of them sat around the table, the wine flowing freely, and enjoying each other’s company. Jen had pointedly, and slightly aggressively, put the salt grinder in front of Lilia and made a quip about women of her age needing to watch their salt intake. Lilia responded by flipping her off and Jen rolled her eyes. “Always the classy lady.”
Lilia waved her fork in Jen’s direction. “Look, it gets to a point where you just have to decide ‘fuck it’”
Agatha raised her glass and said, “I’ll definitely drink to that!” snapping her head to Jen when she heard her snort.
“Oh please, tell me when you’ve ever said ‘fuck it’ to anything.”
Before Agatha could get out a clever retort, Lilia jumped in. “Other than women who aren’t good enough for her, you mean.”
“Oh, I’ll drink to that. ” Jen knocked her glass against Lilia’s and smirked at Agatha.
Agatha put her glass down and threw her hands up in mock exasperation. “Why does my relationship history always get brought up when we’re all together?”

The meal finished and they moved to the living room. The conversation stayed light until Jen took it upon herself to change that. She was sitting opposite Agatha and leant forwards slightly when she asked, “Did you reach a decision on how you were going to talk to Billy?”
Agatha sighed, she truly didn’t have an answer to that question. She had been trying not to think about it, to push it out of her mind and hope that the nagging feeling would disappear. But it hadn’t. If anything, it had gotten more persistent. She knew that she would have to do it at some point, even if it was for selfish reasons. Even if the outcome wasn’t what she hoped it would be.

“Not yet.” She ran a hand through her hair, feeling restless all of a sudden. “It’s… delicate. Also, it’s only been a week. Would it be too soon?”
Lilia turned to face her. “Do you feel like it would be too soon for you, or are you worried it would be too soon for him?”
Agatha looked between her friends quietly hoping that the answer would appear in the air for her and she wouldn’t have to think of it for herself. But no such thing happened. “Yes… Both... Neither… I don’t know.” She leaned back into the sofa. “I know that Wanda told him the same lie that she told everybody else so would he even want to speak to me?”

She shut her eyes trying to quiet her mind. There were only a handful of people that she would allow herself to be emotional in front of, and Jen and Lilia were on that very short list, but she didn’t want to be emotional right now. She wanted to be able to think rationally and attack this head on like she would with any other problem that she faced. But maybe thinking of Billy as a ‘problem’, in itself, was the problem.
He wasn’t something she could solve, he wasn’t something she could fix and he wasn’t something she could just wave away and come back to when she deemed it worth her time. He had been a big part of her life, and she his, and it was killing her that she was so close to him yet so far away at the same time.

“I think the fact that the situation has you reacting like this should tell you that you need to do it.” Lilia said softly. It was a fair assessment. She could put it off as long as she wanted to, but it didn’t change the fact that it needed to happen. She just had to be prepared to accept a negative reaction from Billy and she could do that.

She could do that.  

__________

 

Agatha got home at the end of the day and immediately got in the shower, needing to wash the stress of the day away. She was sure that her final year students were determined to send her to an early grave, how they had managed to make it this far in their education was beyond her comprehension. ‘They’re not going to last the year.’ She thought, rolling her eyes. She was waiting for the inevitable lack of attendance from them, it usually started in the second semester but with the impression the current group had given her, she expected it to start sooner.

Her other students were pretty much what she had expected them to be. The second years had that spark of knowing that this is where everything starts to matter, so they should be vigilant with their attendance and coursework.
The first years were the bright-eyed children that she was used to seeing. Eager to get stuck in and desperate to make a good impression while showing that they had heard the rumours of why you should not, under any circumstances, find your way on to Professor Agatha Harkness’ bad side.
There was one first year student that had taken a place in her mind of course. Billy. She knew that Jen and Lilia were right about talking to him, so she stood under the water deciding how to do it.

When she finally got out of the shower she started checking room availability for the following morning and compared it to Billy’s timetable, to make sure he’d actually have the time. That way, if he said he couldn’t make it, she’d know that he was making excuses and didn’t want to talk to her. But would that be better than not knowing he was avoiding her? She ran a hand through her hair and sighed. As Lilia would say, fuck it . She needed to try anyway.
The next obstacle was choosing between texting him or emailing him. Was emailing him too formal? Was texting him too informal? Does he even still have the same phone number? It had been a two and a half years since they’d last spoken so a text might be too personal. She chose an email.

Dear Mr. Maximoff,

She deleted it. Too formal.

Hello William

Nope absolutely not. She rubbed her temples. ‘Why is this so hard?’ She took a deep breath and tried again.

Billy,

I’m glad that you’re taking my module this semester and I would like it if we could talk.
If you’re open to it, I’ll be in room C24 tomorrow at 9am. Meet me there?

Agatha

She read and reread it until the words no longer made sense, agonising over it until she forced herself to press send. It was done now, she couldn’t take it back. She told herself not to expect a reply. If he turns up then great and if he doesn’t then at least she’ll know that she tried, and that will have to do.

She spent the next few hours zoning out in front of the TV trying to keep her mind as clear as she could.
Her email notification pinged and she opened it. It was from Billy. There was no preamble, just a single word.

Okay

She released a slow, steady breath. “Okay.” A smile started to spread across her face. “Okay.” She repeated, standing up and turning off the TV. “Okay.” She said a final time before taking herself into her room and going to bed.

She woke the next morning to her alarm and laid staring at the ceiling for a few minutes after turning it off. In an hour and a half she would be talking to Billy. She knew that there was no way that they’d clear two and a half years of tension in just one conversation, but it would be a start. A step in the right direction. At least, she hoped it would be. “No. No negative thoughts. This will be good.” She said out loud to motivate herself, and with that she got out of bed and began the day. 

__________

She got to the room fifteen minutes early to prepare. Though what she was actually preparing for, she wasn’t sure. She paced the room, doing lap after lap around the desks in the centre, only stopping when she felt herself become dizzy. She sat on one of the tables whilst waiting for the room to stop spinning, biting her nails out of nervousness. She still had five minutes, she could leave now if she wanted to but the thought of walking out on Billy for a second time made her chest tighten. She couldn’t let him down again.

The door slowly crept open and she stood up, smoothing out her shirt. Billy walked into the room, looking as nervous as she no doubt did. His eyes flicked around the room trying to find anything to look at but her. “Hi.” He said quietly.
“Hi.” She replied, smiling softly at him. He stayed standing by the open door – probably so that he could make a quick exit if he needed to. “It’s nice to see you again, Billy.” He seemed to relax a tiny bit at the softness of her words and took a step closer to her. “It’s nice to see you again too, Professor.”
She chuckled quietly at his choice of words. “You don’t need to be formal, you can say my name.” She wanted to walk to him but decided to give him space, letting him make the choice of lessening both the physical and emotional gap between them. He started playing with the hem of his jumper, looking at the floor. “Why did you ask to see me, Agatha?”
Because I miss you, kid. Because I hate the fact that I let your shit-cunt of a mother ruin our relationship. But she couldn't say that… could she? She couldn't be so open right away and risk scaring him off. 

“Because I wanted to check in, see how you're doing.” He looked back up at her, meeting her eyes for the first time. There was a hint of disbelief on his face. Did he think she was lying? 

“You had a two and a half years to check in . Why wait until now?” 

It was a fair question, but she hadn't gone the whole span of time without checking on him. Not really. They still lived in the same city, just not in the same house any more. She would sometimes park across the street from his school just to catch a glimpse of him leaving, trying to work up the courage to say hi but she tried not to make a habit of it in case she ended up on a register. Jen and Lilia would let her know if they'd seen him out and about and tell her if he seemed happy, had friends and was generally doing okay. 

She was beside herself when she found out that he and Wanda had been in a car accident and he was in the hospital. Thankfully Wanda had seen fit to let her know and keep her updated on his condition. She had gone to see him a couple of times but he had been unconscious and hadn't known she was there. When he had woken up, she rushed over to see him but left again when she saw both of his parents there. She hadn't wanted to add any unnecessary stress for him. 
But now? Now she had an excuse – no, an opportunity – to reconnect with him and she wasn't going to miss it. 

“I know. I could make excuses and blame whomever I wanted, or needed, to blame but I'm not going to do that. I should have done this sooner and I'm sorry.” She couldn't look at him any more. Her guilt was too heavy to keep eye contact and she leant against the table for support. She heard him move, felt him shuffle closer and sit on the table next to her but she still couldn't look at him. Not yet. 

“I'm sorry too. I let my mum get in my head and convince me that you were the bad guy.” She turned her head slightly towards him, still not able to look at his face, but she could see him nervously picking at his fingernails – a habit he got from his mother – as he continued. “I hated you for a long time.” 

Her breath got caught in her throat and her chest tightened. She wasn't naïve, she knew that he would have had negative feelings towards her. But hearing him say it was something else entirely. It made it real, it made the whole situation ten times worse. Suddenly all the hatred she held towards Wanda paled in comparison to the way she felt hearing Billy say those words. 

“I am so sorry that you got caught up in this. You didn't deserve it, you were just a child.” She forced herself to look him in the eye, he deserved her full attention. He deserved so much more than that, but it was all she could offer in that moment. “I can't take back that time and I can't erase the way I made you feel, no matter how much I wish I could.” She took a shaky breath. “But I can promise that I will do anything I can to make it up to you. I really miss you, kid.” 

He smiled, though it didn't quite reach his eyes. “I'm not a kid.”

“Oh sorry. Teen.” She leant into him, nudging him gently with her shoulder and his smile brightened. “I know that we're not going to fix this in one day, but I want you to know that I'm willing to listen to you. You can tell me how you felt and I'll answer any questions you have.”
He dipped his head, thinking for a moment. “Did you ever think about coming to see me?” 

She could feel tears start to well in her eyes, he was still so hurt by her leaving. “Of course I did!” She winced at how harsh her tone was. She didn't mean it to come out like that and consciously softened it when she spoke again. “I spent ages trying to work up the courage to talk to you but I guess I was scared that you wouldn't want to talk to me. I also didn't want you to feel like you had to talk to me if you didn't want to.” 

He looked back up at her, meeting her eyes again, his own eyes starting to shine with tears. “At the start I was angry with you. When I came home from school, and mum told me that you'd gone because you'd found somebody else, I wanted to find you, to scream at you, to ask how you could do that to us.”

Wanda's lie wasn't new to Agatha, the rumour had flown through the faculty at record speed, but it still didn't hurt any less. “Billy you know that isn't true, don't you?” 
He nodded. “I found out about a year later. She told me when we got home from the hospital. I guess that she felt guilty after I nearly died and told me the truth.” He laughed but there was no humour in it. “Every cloud, as they say.” 

She wanted to hug him but didn't want to overstep his boundaries so she opted for a soft and gentle smile instead. “I visited you in the hospital, your mother at least had the decency to let me know that you were hurt. I was there when you woke up as well but I didn't want to add to the stress of the situation and overwhelm you, so I didn't go into your room. I watched you from the window for a few minutes and left.” 
His eyes went wide and his mouth dropped open slightly. “You were there? I thought I was going crazy! I saw you in the window but when it dawned on me that it was you, and I looked again, you were gone.”

Oh that made her heart ache. He'd seen her there but because of her own fear, her own unwillingness to be in the same room as Wanda and Billy’s father, she had denied herself the chance of speaking to him. She had denied him the chance of speaking to her. She couldn't stop the tears that started to fall. “I'm so sorry, Billy. I'm sorry that I didn't go in and see you when you woke up. I'm sorry that I waited this long to talk to you again. I never stopped caring about you.” She gasped when he moved towards her and wrapped his arms around her. It took her a few seconds to process what was happening before she hugged him back. Billy was crying now as well and they both stayed there for a minute holding each other, their combined pain, anger and hurt starting the slow transformation into forgiveness.

“I shouldn’t have listened to my mum.” Billy said into her shoulder. “I knew deep down that the story didn’t add up, that you weren’t the type of person to do that.” He tightened his grip ever so slightly, as if he was trying to scoop up some of the broken pieces of their past.  

When they pulled apart Agatha couldn't resist ruffling his hair. “I like the new look, kid. It suits you.”
He pushed her hand away in feigned annoyance. “I'm not a kid.” 

They sat in comfortable silence for a moment before Billy spoke again. “I think my mum really wants to speak to you. I think she wants to explain herself, you should try to listen to her.” 

Agatha scoffed, it was an involuntary reaction but she meant it all the same. “With respect ki- teen. I won't be doing that.” She stood up and wiped the tears from her cheeks. She didn’t want to think about his mother right now, let alone entertain the idea of speaking to her. “Don't you have a lecture to go to? You shouldn't be late, I hear your professor is a real hard arse.” She said with a wink. 

He laughed. This time it was a real laugh and the smile that went with it reached his eyes. Agatha couldn't help but smile too as he walked to the door. “Agatha?” He said, turning back.

“Yeah?”

“Thank you for this.” 

She gave him a nod and he left the room. Agatha let out a strong exhale and ran a hand through her hair, giving him a few minutes before leaving as well.

She knew that this was the first of many conversations they were going to have, and she was looking forward to their relationship being fully rebuilt. 

__________

1 Year Ago

It was a Thursday afternoon just like any other. Agatha was at work giving lectures like usual and her students were underwhelming, like usual. ‘How hard is it for final years to put some effort in?’ she thought as she scanned the surprisingly small group of students that had actually attended her lecture. She would never have dreamed of missing classes while she was a student, her need for perfection – and her mother – wouldn’t have allowed it. She had always had a perfect attendance from primary school all the way through her masters, and when she became a lecturer that record was maintained with precision. She prided herself on it, even more so now that she had to rebuild her reputation as a person thanks to her wonderful ex’s lies. Which is why there had been so much shock and awe when she had abruptly left midway through the lecture with no attempt to explain herself.

Her phone had been on the table next to her laptop, silent like usual so that it wouldn’t distract her. But as luck would have it she happened to be standing at the laptop flicking to the next slide when she saw the incoming call. Usually she would have ignored it, she was teaching and she hated her flow being interrupted, but the name on her screen gave her pause.

Maximoff

Agatha knew that there was absolutely no way that woman would attempt to call her, especially not in the middle of a teaching day. This was either a mistake or something that needed her immediate attention. She scowled at her phone and rejected the call, she was not in the mood for her right now. She was never in the mood for her. But as soon as she’d pressed the button, Wanda’s name was back on her screen. Not a mistake. She apologised to the few students that had decided her lecture was worth their time, excusing herself from the room before she answered the call.

“Agatha? Agatha, are you there?” Wanda’s voice came through the phone before Agatha had put it to her ear.
“What do you want?” Her tone was biting. This had better be important or so help her god she would make Wanda regret it.
Wanda’s response came in a fast, panicked voice. “I was driving and there must have been a patch of ice. I hit it and I lost control of the car and hit a tree. He was in the back and there was so much blood and he wasn’t breathing.” She was sobbing now, barely able to form the words she was saying and Agatha was struggling to understand her.
“Wanda I cannot understand a wor-”
“Billy!” She choked out. “Billy is dying!”

Agatha felt her blood turn cold and her heart began to pound so hard that she thought it would break her ribs. “Tell me exactly where you are. I’m on my way.” Wanda gave her the address of the hospital and she went back into the lecture hall beelining for the table. She snapped the lid of her laptop closed, disconnected it from the projector and threw her jacket on. “This lecture is over, you are all dismissed.” She didn’t look at her students as she spoke and immediately went to her car, throwing her bag on the passenger seat and sped out of the car park.

She definitely broke numerous traffic laws but she didn’t care, she was getting to that hospital. She sprinted into the A&E building and up to the reception desk. “Tell me where William Maximoff is.” She demanded.
The receptionist was unbothered, probably used to this kind of unruly behaviour. “Ma'am, as you can see there is a queue. If you could joi-”
“I don’t have time for your queue, I need to know where he is now!” She wasn’t one to be rude to customer service workers unprovoked, but these were extenuating circumstances and she didn’t have the mental capacity for niceties right now.
“I appreciate that ma’am, but I can’t do anything for you right now. You’ll have to join the queue.” The receptionist kept their tone calm and their expression neutral, no doubt from years of perfecting it. Agatha wasn’t stupid, she knew that the receptionist wasn’t doing this to personally attack her, they were just doing their job. She huffed and threw her hands up, reluctantly walking to the back of the queue. “Fine!”

She could feel the eyes of everybody in the waiting area on her after her display. She didn’t care, her boy was somewhere in this hospital in god knows what state and she needed to see him.
Her boy.
The thought repeated on her as she stood trying to calm her breathing. He wasn’t her boy anymore, he hadn’t really been her boy at all. Wanda had ruined all chances of that happening.

She could feel a fresh wave of anger building in her chest as the queue slowly went down. She hated that Wanda could still make her feel this way a year after their relationship had ended. She hated that she was standing in a hospital waiting room worrying about Billy but still finding some way to let her past with his mother push its way to the front of her mind. She hated that she hadn’t found a way to move on from it yet.

It was finally her turn at the front of the queue and she approached the desk with a much calmer demeanor. “William Maximoff was brought in here after a car accident. Would you be able to tell me where I can find him please?”
“What is your name please?”
“Agatha Harkness.”
The receptionist typed something on the keyboard before saying, “you can go to Family Room B. It’s just down the corridor to your left and it’ll be the third room on the right.”
“Thank you.”

She wanted to run but she forced herself to walk calmly. She had no idea what was waiting for her on the other side of that door and didn’t want to rush into it. She stood outside the room and took a breath before walking in.
The room was small and square with white walls and a few chairs along each wall. There were a few generic canvases hung up, one was of a beach and another was of a blue sky with a couple of clouds dotted around. They were probably meant to be calming and Agatha would later realise that they didn’t achieve their purpose.

Wanda was pacing in the far corner anxiously biting her nails and it wasn’t until the door clicked shut that she looked up. Her face was red and swollen from all the crying she had been doing and there was a long cut across her right cheek that had been stitched back together.

She ran to Agatha and threw her arms around her pulling her into a tight hug and Agatha instinctively wrapped her arms around her in response.
“You came.” Wanda sobbed into Agatha’s shoulder. Usually Agatha would be shouting at anyone who dared to get close to her cashmere jacket, never mind crying on it. But right here, right now, she couldn’t give a flying fuck. She held Wanda close as the sobs wracked her body absentmindedly rubbing soothing circles on her back. It was like muscle memory, just an instinct that took over.

“Of course I came. It’s Billy.” She could feel her own tears starting to prickle the corners of her eyes but she wasn’t ready for them to fall yet. Wanda needed her to be strong. Billy needed her to be strong. She slowly unwrapped herself and stood back from Wanda’s embrace. “Let’s sit down and you can tell me what happened.”
They walked to the chairs and she noticed that Wanda was walking with a limp. “Is your leg okay?”
Wanda winced as she slowly lowered herself into her seat. “Yeah, just badly bruised. The doctor said I need to rest it for a week and come back if it gets any worse.” She let out a quiet, humourless laugh and Agatha sat in the chair next to her. She looked at the gash on her cheek and could now properly see how deep it was. “Shouldn’t that have an extra covering on it?” Wanda looked at her confused for a moment before realising what she meant. “Oh. They tried but I refused to let them do anything else until I saw Billy. He’s in surgery. They said something about a potential bleed on his brain. I don’t know, it was all so much to take in.” She sighed and closed her eyes, dipping her head slightly.

Agatha looked at her, slowly taking in the understandably disheveled state she was in. She was picking at her cuticles, a nervous habit that Agatha had helped her work on while they were together, but now they were freshly bleeding. Agatha slowly reached over, taking Wanda’s hand and lacing their fingers together. She heard Wanda’s breath catch at the unexpected gesture and they met each other's gaze. “He’s going to be okay.” Agatha said, giving her hand a gentle squeeze.

She didn’t know where any of this was coming from. Ten minutes ago the thought of being this close to Wanda would have repulsed her, but maybe she needed the comfort as much as Wanda did.
“Thank you for being here.” Wanda whispered. “I don’t know what I’ll do if he doesn’t make it.” She started crying again and Agatha pulled her into another hug.
“Don’t think about that. He’s going to be fine.” She was more telling herself than Wanda at this point but it didn’t matter, she needed to be the one who was keeping it together right now so she would say and do whatever she needed to make that happen.
“Is his dad on the way?” It had taken her until now to realise that Wanda had been alone in this room until she had arrived. She hadn’t had any idea what she would be walking into when she came to the hospital but she was now thinking that it was strange that he wasn’t here.

Wanda pulled back and ran her hands through her hair, realisation crossing her face. “Oh god I didn’t even think… You were the first person I called. You were the only person I called.” She stood up and began pacing again. “How could I not think to let him know? I’m a terrible person. His son is dying in hospital and I didn’t let him know.” She kept talking and limping laps around the room. Agatha let her do it for a moment thinking that she would talk out her thoughts and sit back down again, but she kept going, spiraling further and further until Agatha spoke.
“Wanda.” Her tone was clipped now, losing the softness she had entered the room with. Wanda needed someone to ground her, to stop her mind from wandering and Agatha still knew how to tell when to do just that. She’d had four years of learning these things about Wanda but she was surprised by how natural it still felt, how in tune she still was to her.

Wanda stopped mid-step and snapped her head towards Agatha, the sharpness of her tone clearly surprising her. “Call him.” She just nodded and pulled out her phone.
Agatha sat silently, listening to Wanda run through the events again. She was a lot calmer this time around, still pacing but no tears and Agatha sat patiently, waiting for the phone call to finish.

Wanda sighed. “He’s on his way.”
“Good. Now sit back down, you need to rest your leg.”
Wanda did as she was told and they sat in silence for a few minutes. Given the circumstances the silence couldn’t be described as comfortable but there wasn’t any awkwardness in it. Agatha thought back to the hug and how she had welcomed it without question, how the hatred she had towards Wanda had faded away as soon as she’d seen how broken she looked. She thought about the gentleness in how she’d held Wanda’s hand, the fact that she had been Wanda’s first port of call and what it all meant.
‘No, I’m here for Billy and nothing else. He is my only concern.’

It would be easy to read into all, to try and decipher all the hidden meanings, but it wouldn't do any good. It wouldn’t fix anything between them. There was still a deep lack of trust that Wanda had planted and its roots had grown too thick to be pulled out by this one thing.
There was also the fear that if – no, when – Billy woke up, he wouldn’t want to see her. But she couldn’t let herself get hung up on that. She just needed to be there in the moment.

Wanda cleared her throat, breaking the silence. “Will you stay?”
Agatha looked at her, raising an eyebrow in confusion. “What do you mean?”
“When Vis gets here, will you stay?”
Absolutely fucking not. I would rather die than be in a room with the both of you. Why would I want to put myself through that?
These were all the things she wanted to say, they were the words that immediately came to her mind in response. But she didn’t say any of them, she just nodded. She didn’t trust herself to speak in case she verbalised her thoughts. At the end of the day, she was there for Billy and that was it.

She stayed at the hospital until Billy was out of surgery and played nice with his dad, though it did take some effort to keep her snide remarks to herself. When she said that she was leaving, Wanda gave her a hug goodbye and thanked her again for being there. The hug lingered until Agatha saw Billy’s father watching them and she pulled away. She smoothed out her shirt and cleared her throat. “I’ll come back in a couple of days. Let me know if anything happens.”
Wanda nodded. “I will.”

Agatha managed to hold herself together as she drove home, but as soon as she stepped over the threshold of her house she broke. She couldn’t stop the tears that fell or the way that her knees buckled and she immediately sank to the floor. She sat there leaning against her front door for hours, letting out every single bit of emotion that she had kept locked away all day.
It had been decades since she’d cried herself to sleep, but that night, the counter reset. 

Chapter End Notes
