Agatha

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Having had a talk with Billy, Agatha felt more at ease. She felt like she was no longer struggling to keep her balance while navigating being his lecturer. It wasn’t easy to knock her confidence, not outwardly anyway, she always had a response or an answer for everything. It kept her two steps ahead, just where she wanted to be. Where she belonged. But she couldn’t deny that the uncertainty that surrounded seeing him again had worried her to the point that other faculty members had noticed that she was slightly off her game. A couple of them had even dared to approach her after a staff meeting and ask if she was okay. That had been the kick in the arse she had needed to talk to him – Lilia and Jen had also had a hand in it but if she had to be fueled by an emotion, she would rather it be spite than anything else.
She couldn’t have the people who had once shunned her for her supposed affair think that it was suddenly okay to check up on her.
No, that simply would not do. So she had spoken to him and felt infinitely better for it.

__________


She was sitting in her office waiting for her weekly meeting with Rio to begin, feeling positive that she would be able to devote her full attention to it now that the distraction of Billy was in the process of being righted.
There was a knock at her door at 9am exactly. “You may enter.”
Rio walked into the room with a polite smile. “Good morning, Professor Harkness.”
“Good morning, Miss Vidal.” Agatha returned the smile. “Please, take a seat.” She waited for Rio to sit down and take her laptop out of her bag before continuing. “Why don’t you tell me where your research has taken you this week.”
“Well, after your lecture, I went down a bit of a Hades and Persephone rabbit hole.” She opened something on her laptop. “I’ve always been intrigued by their story and the different ways in which it has been told over time. You know like how some people view it as a great love story and others view it as an abusive relationship et cetera.”

She handed her laptop to Agatha and she lifted her eyebrows in surprise. It was a powerpoint presentation. Rio had actually taken the time to make a slideshow to give to her. She had expected “I read this book…” or “I watched this movie…” but this was above her expectations. It was twenty slides on the variations of the myths surrounding the Gods, compiled from a myriad of sources. She flicked through it, skimming the information Rio had written down. It was almost as good as her own. Almost.

“Miss Vidal, this is–”
“I know, it’s a lot. And I know a powerpoint is strange but it helps me arrange my thoughts better.” Her tone was sheepish and she gave a nervous chuckle after.
“I have to say tha–”
“Oh, I know the writing leaves some things to be desired but this is just notes and nothing is set in stone yet.”
Agatha lifted a hand to silence her. It was a gesture that she had perfected and it always worked. The joy she felt being able to control someone with a simple motion never failed to give her a rush.

“Miss Vidal, are you going to let me speak?” She kept her voice carefully neutral, but there was a commanding undertone that suggested she chose to phrase it as a question in a gesture of being nice. She saw the surprise flash across Rio’s face and noticed her throat bob as she swallowed. She felt a satisfied smile tug at the corners of her mouth and let the silence hang for a second. “Thank you.” She waited a beat, before continuing. “This is good work. I can tell that you’ve put effort into this and that you haven’t haphazardly thrown it together.”
She was impressed but she wasn’t going to tell Rio that. “Your list of sources is good and the information is laid out nicely.”

There was a moment of silence before Agatha realised why Rio wasn’t responding. She was waiting to be told that she could. Interesting. Agatha sat back in her chair. “You may speak.”
Rio’s shoulders dropped slightly like she had just released a breath. “Thank you, Professor.” She shifted her position in her chair slightly, and Agatha couldn’t tell if it was because she was uncomfortable or if it was something else.
Rio cleared her throat. “I also started doing some research on Orpheus and Eurydice on the back of this because of the musical Hadestown, and how it links them in with Hades and Persephone. I don’t know if you’ve heard of it, but it's really good.”
Agatha gave a small smile. “I’m familiar with it.” In truth, she loved it. She had seen it three times and – she would never tell another living soul this – she had cried every time.

She handed Rio her laptop and had to fight to ignore the feeling in her chest when their fingers brushed, she also had to fight to not linger. “Do you think you could do it?”
“Do what?”
She moved from her desk to sit in the chair opposite Rio, feeling her eyes on her tracking her movements. “Do you think you could lead Eurydice back to the surface and not turn around?” She crossed her legs. “Or Orpheus, I don’t know your preferences.” She tacked on, nonchalantly. Not that she wanted to know Rio’s preferences, she just wasn’t one to assume.

Rio chuckled before saying, “I would be leading Eurydice.” Agatha felt her stomach flip but she wasn’t about to get bogged down by thinking of why that was. “But I honestly don’t know if I would be able to do it. I think I would be too in my head, like Orpheus was.” Their eyes met and Agatha noticed the way Rio’s shined as she thought about the question, and she began to wonder who Rio was picturing as her Eurydice. Probably a young blonde with bright blue eyes, they were everyone’s type these days.
“What about you?” Rio’s voice brought her back into the room.
She hummed, mulling it over. “I’ve never really thought about it.” Would she ever love someone enough to try? Would this hypothetical person do it for her? Now she was putting too much thought into it. “I suppose if I loved someone the way that Orpheus loved Eurydice I would definitely give it a go.”
“So you would be leading Eurydice too?” Rio asked while raising an eyebrow, a smirk beginning to spread across her face.
“That is an extremely personal question, Miss Vidal. One that has no place in our meetings.” Her tone was back to the cold, no-nonsense one she usually carried. She never shared personal information with anyone, let alone a student.

Rio’s smirk dropped and the teasing sparkle in her eyes faded into something different. She didn’t strike Agatha as someone who liked to be put in her place but she also wasn’t making any moves to defend herself either. Agatha felt a surge of satisfaction rise in her chest at the fact that she had managed to regain her control over their meetings. After the unfortunate way the first couple had gone, it was about time she got her grip again.

Rio now looked incredibly uncomfortable, which Agatha liked. She was used to students doing everything they could to avoid her gaze, it was familiar territory. It reminded her that she was very much in charge and that was where she belonged. “I beg your pardon.”
“You asked me what my preferences were. How come personal questions are only off the table when they’re about you?” She lazily leaned back in her chair.

She felt the flush rising onto her neck and clenched her jaw, keeping her gaze locked on Rio. “I’m not sure that I know what you’re implying, Miss Vidal.” She was getting irritated now. She still had the upper hand but she could feel her grip loosening. If Rio kept pushing, she would snap. She was not ashamed of who she was, far from it. Her mother had tried her hardest to make her feel like she was born wrong and she would damn well not stand for it again from anyone. But Rio was her student and she did not discuss her personal life with her students. She might have had her share of complaints against her for how she spoke to her students, but her professionalism was never called into question and that was how it would stay.

“I’m not implying anything. I am simply offering information up freely.” Rio stated and crossed her arms. Agatha took a deep breath trying to ignore the way that her pulse had quickened. None of this has anything to do with Greek Mythology, and since that’s why we’re here, I think it would be appropriate for us to continue in that direction. Don’t you agree?” Her tone was clipped and she knew that her eyes conveyed her annoyance because the cocky smile on Rio’s face faltered slightly.

Rio uncrossed her arms and sat straight in her chair again. “Of course, you’re right. My apologies Professor.” The words were sincere but there was an undertone in Rio’s voice that Agatha couldn’t quite work out. Either way she would not rise to whatever this was, whatever game Rio was trying to play with her. She would not lose control of the meeting. “Do you have a structure for your research, or is it just whatever takes your fancy in the moment?” She leaned back casually in an attempt to appear unbothered by the conversation that had just transpired. She didn’t know if it worked because Rio gave nothing away. She just kept her eyes trained on her, watching her every move.

“I don’t have a structure as such, but I’m working on it.” She leaned forwards. “That’s the thing I tend to have trouble with actually.”
Agatha uncrossed her legs and recrossed them the opposite way, watching Rio’s eyes follow the movement before lazily making their way back to her face. It gave her a feeling in her stomach that she didn’t want to acknowledge. “Well that’s why you have a supervisor, is it not? It is quite literally my job to help with things like that.”
Rio laughed “I can send you the chaos that is my notes and you can see if you can save them. But I will warn you, it’s not for the faint of heart.” She punctuated it with a lopsided smile.
“I’m sure my heart can handle the disorganisation of a PhD student, Miss Vidal.” She had to work to keep her voice flat because it was verging on being playful and that was not the tone she wanted to set for her interactions with Rio. She didn’t ‘play’ with her students. She was their superior, that’s the way it had always been and that is how it would remain.

“What exactly is it about structuring your thesis that you’re struggling with?”
Rio crossed her legs and folded her hands in her lap. “I’ve never really been good at getting the flow right. That was always the feedback I got on every essay that I turned in.” There was a vulnerability in the way that she spoke and Agatha wondered if it was because she was embarrassed about it. Her CV showed that she was very academically inclined so the fact that she struggled to structure her work might cause some self-consciousness.
Agatha nodded. “When you say flow, do you mean getting all of the information to link together?”
“Yeah, that’s exactly it. The information is correct, it’s just a bit disjointed.”
Agatha hummed. “Okay well, that is definitely something that I can help with. Keep making your notes as you usually would and in our next meeting we will work on organising them.”

“Just try to keep it as concise as you can for the time being, you have plenty of time to flesh it out and add more to it. There’s no sense in burning yourself out before you’ve even started.”
Rio nodded and hummed her agreement.

Agatha checked her watch, there was still some time until she had to give her lecture. The meeting didn’t need to last the entire part of her schedule that she had allotted for it, but it would be silly to not use it. “We still have some time left. Is there anything else you want to discuss?” She put the decision of using the remaining time in Rio’s hands. These meetings were for her benefit after all. 

Rio fidgeted with her hands for a moment before responding. “What piqued your interest in Greek Mythology.”
Agatha sighed. “I meant about your thesis, Miss Vidal.” ‘When will she get the hint that I don’t discuss myself with students?’ She thought.
“This is for my thesis.” There was an insistent tone to her voice and Agatha couldn’t deny that she was interested in how Rio could spin this to be relevant.
“Please, enlighten me.”
Rio leaned forwards again. “You haven’t read Percy Jackson which is, to use your own words,  a gateway drug. So what piece of media opened your mind to it?”

Agatha thought before answering. She could be honest and risk inviting further probing questions or she could lie and pick something generic like Clash Of The Titans and be done with it.
“My mother read The Odyssey to me when I was a child.” Not a complete lie, but not the complete truth either. It was safely in the middle.
“Oh wow, one of the OGs.” Rio’s eyebrows were raised in surprise. “How old were you?”
“This is getting personal again, Miss Vidal.” She shifted in her seat, straightening her back and taking on a more authoritative posture.
Rio dipped her head and exhaled in a way that could be interpreted as annoyance. But she wouldn’t dare express that in such an obvious way, would she? If that was the case then Agatha simply would not stand for it. “I am not in the business of discussing myself or my life with my students, Miss Vidal. I am your supervisor and our meetings are in place to work on your thesis and, when it comes to it, your viva.”

Rio raised her head to look at her again and straightened her posture. “I’m not trying to pry into your personal life, Professor. Surely you can see why inquiring as to how you found your interest in Greek Mythology to the point where you wanted to teach other people about it, is relevant to my thesis.” There was no mistaking it this time, there was definite annoyance in the way she spoke. “You don’t have to tell me your life story but a discussion requires both parties to be able to share information that relates to the topic at hand.”

Agatha tensed her jaw and narrowed her eyes, her voice dropping low. “I do not take kindly to being told off by a subordinate, Miss Vidal.” She spoke slowly, enunciating each word precisely. Never before had a student spoken to her in this manner but she would be damned if she let it throw her off.
“And I don’t take kindly to being spoken down to by someone who thinks their title gives them the right to.” There was a fire in Rio’s eyes that Agatha noticed immediately. She recognised it as the same fire that she had herself. This woman was infuriatingly similar to her and it was beginning to cause issues.

“If you cannot respect me as your superior, Miss Vidal, then I suggest that you find a new supervisor.” She could hear the volume of her voice rising. She usually favoured the quiet anger, the kind that strikes fear into people, but Rio Vidal was pissing her off and she could feel the heat burning in her chest.
Rio scoffed. “When you give me a reason to respect you, Professor Harkness , you shall have it.” The callback to their first conversation wasn’t lost on Agatha – and neither was the way that Rio spat her name – she was very aware that she was using her own words against her. Rio stood up and threw her laptop back into her bag.
“Miss Vidal, sit back down.”
“No!” Rio’s voice was raised now as well. “Other people might allow you to speak to them in this way, but I won’t. Your reputation at this university might be good, but it does not give you the right to talk to people like they are beneath you. Like I said before, you aren't the only lecturer that I wanted to be my supervisor so I will gladly go and find her.” She started towards the door.

Absolutely. Fucking. Not. Rio was once again wielding the threat of Wanda Maximoff and Agatha would not, under any circumstances, allow that woman to win anything. Even if that thing was an obscenely, irritatingly, impressive PhD student who had managed to rile her up to this extent.

“Wait.” She said, standing up too. Rio’s hand was on the door handle but by the grace of god, she stopped.
“What?” She bit out, not turning around.
It was a good question. What was Agatha going to say? What excuse was she going to come up with to rationalise the way she had just behaved?
“Don’t go” was pathetic.
“Please come back” was even worse.
“Don’t go running to my ex because I can’t seem to keep a grip on myself around you” was absolutely fucking absurd.

The silence stretched as Agatha battled her own thoughts and Rio just stood there, still holding the door handle, but doing as Agatha had asked. She was waiting.
“I’m sorry.” Agatha hated how weak her voice sounded, how weak her choice of words was.
Rio laughed, it was dark and colored with disbelief. “Are you being fucking serious?” She dropped her hand and finally turned around. “You accuse me of prying into your personal life, talk down to me, call me a fucking subordinate and the best you can come up with is ‘I’m sorry’?” She shook her head, still laughing.
Agatha was definitely blushing now. She wasn't used to students, or anyone for that matter, fighting back. People usually cowered under her gaze and flinched at her words – they certainly did not hurl profanities at her. But Rio wasn't like everyone else, she stood her ground. She wasn't afraid to speak to Agatha in the way that she spoke to her and she clearly wasn't going to give her the satisfaction of sticking around while Agatha used her as a verbal punching bag. No, this woman was different and Agatha found her intriguing. 

“Well what do you want me to say?” She threw her arms out in exasperation. “Do you want me to beg for your forgiveness? Because I can assure you, Miss Vidal, that will not be happening.” God this was all so juvenile. Why was she arguing with a student over something as mundane as this? Maybe she should just let Rio go to Wanda because this was clearly not going to work.
Rio took a step towards her, slow and deliberate. “Answer my question.”
“Which one?” Agatha did her best to come across as nonchalantly as possible but she heard the quiver in her voice. Her cage had been rattled and now she was frantically flapping around trying to find her perch again while a flurry of feathers cascaded around her.

“How old were you when you read The Odyssey?”
Was she being fucking serious? Why was she so stuck on this?
Agatha quirked an eyebrow, “Seriously?” The word was dripping with incredulity. What was Rio hoping to achieve with this? What was her goal?
She was just standing there waiting for Agatha to answer her.
Agatha sighed and rolled her eyes. “Ten.” She said, louder than she intended. “I was ten years old. Are you happy now?” She crossed her arms, feeling like a petulant child who had just been forced to admit to breaking a glass ornament.

How had the roles been reversed so easily? How had she let them be reversed so easily? She wouldn’t usually stand for this, she wouldn’t usually allow anyone to come close to this. She always had the upper hand, she was always at the helm of every conversation she was a part of, so how had this managed to spin so spectacularly out of control? How had Rio gotten so under her skin and why did she care so much?

The way that Rio was looking at her made her stomach clench. There was something in her eyes. Did she look pleased? Or did she look excited? No, that couldn't be it. She looked smug, and Agatha didn’t like that one bit. She had allowed herself to be backed into a corner by a student and it would absolutely never happen again. “I’m not sure what you hoped to achieve with this, Miss Vidal, but I assure you that this is the first and last time anything like this will happen. I do not share personal information with students and I am the one who gets to determine what classes as personal information.” Her arms were still crossed, but her fists were now clenched on the sleeves of her shirt. “Now stop acting like a child.”

Rio’s eyebrows went skyward. “I’m acting like a child? You’re the one that threw a tantrum when I asked you a basic question about yourself.” She took another step towards her. “I get that you want to keep your work and private lives separate, and I am aware that I overstepped when I asked if you would be leading Eurydice so I apologise for that. But, like I said, if we are to be having discussions then some generic information will have to be given on both sides.” There was still a harshness in her voice but it was quieter now and the sharp look in her eyes had softened.

Agatha slowly unclenched her jaw, feeling the dull ache of the muscles complaining about the strain she had put them under. She had been staring intensely at Rio for so long now that she could probably sculpt her face out of marble – not that she would ever want to. 

She began to question why it was that she was so unwilling to give even the smallest piece of herself to another person. Her mother was the obvious answer. Being raised by an emotionally stunted woman had done wonders to influence her self-esteem. There was so little that Evanora Harkness approved of that she learned to hide parts of herself until the parts that were left on show were just a tiny sliver of who she actually was. 

And of course there was Wanda. She'd had relationships before Wanda, but none of them had been that intense, none of them had lasted that long and she wasn't sure she had actually been in love before Wanda. She had opened up to her, told her about her mother, her childhood and she had started to feel like she wasn't broken anymore.

But when they broke up, she packaged all of that back up and buried it deep inside herself somewhere that it could never be found and opened again. She panicked when she thought that the smallest fraction of herself would be on display because that meant there was a chance that someone could use it to hurt her. Take her vulnerability, turn it into a weapon and cut her down. 

It had taken years to let Lilia and Jen in and even now she didn't show herself to the full extent. She had never let them see her cry, she had never let them see her so angry that she wished she could go wild and destroy things, even the way that she had been after Wanda had broken her heart had been watered down in front of them. Those were emotions that were just for her, the ugliest parts of herself that no other living being would see.

So something as simple as being asked how she gained her love for Greek Mythology was a threat to her carefully constructed walls that kept her safe and hidden. Rio was a stranger and she wasn't someone that Agatha was prepared to give any ammo to. 
But she already had some, she had worked out that Wanda was a button that she could push to get Agatha to act how she wanted and Agatha hated that. God help her if Rio and Wanda ever had a conversation, she would be well and truly fucked. 

She let her head dip and looked at the floor. The worn grey carpet offering a small escape from the way that Rio was looking at her. “You're right.” Her voice cracked which made her cringe. She cleared her throat and looked back up at Rio. “You're right.” Rio's features softened. “I flew off the handle and conducted myself in an extremely unprofessional manner, for which I apologise.” She searched Rio's face for a reaction, any reaction, but she was just looking at her so she continued. “I'm not used to being challenged and it's rare that people have a spine when conversing with me. But it seems that you don't have that problem.” 

Rio laughed, but this time it was light. “My parents raised me to speak my mind and stand up for myself.” She ran a hand through her hair. “I guess they never thought about how it would translate into speaking with authority figures.” She smiled softly and Agatha's heartbeat picked up again, though not because of irritation but she wasn't going to acknowledge the reason. 

Her phone pinged with a reminder that she had fifteen minutes until her lecture was due to start. She smoothed out her shirt and gathered her things from her desk to compose herself. “Well I have some first years to scare so we're going to have to end this here. Once again, you are welcome to attend. I think your presence gives them confidence since you were the first one to speak out.” She allowed herself to give Rio a small smile and went to open the door. “There's no pressure though.” 
“I'll think about it.” Rio said jokingly as she headed out the door. 
“Don't think about it too hard. Remember what I said about burning yourself out.” 
Rio spun on her heel to face Agatha again. “Ha! Fair point, well made.” She turned back and walked away and Agatha absolutely did not catch herself watching her go.

Would they ever have a normal interaction? Was that even in the realm of possibility? And more importantly, did she want them to have a normal interaction?

__________


It was Agatha’s turn to cook Saturday night dinner which meant that her kitchen became a bombsite. Even the simplest of dishes turned into chaos. She was a good cook but her process had a certain drunk-toddler quality to it and, for some unknown reason, she had decided to bake dessert.

She opened the door to Lilia and Jen who immediately burst out laughing.
“Wow, Harkness. I always think that there’s no way you can be worse than last time and yet you still manage to top it.” Lilia beamed as she walked past her.
“Don’t panic, we’re here.” Jen said, walking straight into the kitchen. “Just tell me what needs doing and go shower.”
Agatha told them when to stir the pot that was in the oven and what time to take the cake out and went to her bathroom. She had thought that Jen was overreacting when she had told her to shower but she laughed when she saw the flour on her face and cake batter in her hair.

When she returned downstairs, the kitchen had been cleaned up, the pots had been washed and the table had been set. “You know the whole point of us taking turns is that we each get time off from having to do this stuff, don’t you?” Jen asked.
“Leave her alone Jennifer. We all have our flaws.”
“Thank you Lilia, glad to know one of you has my back.” She sent a pointed look in Jen’s direction in mock annoyance.

Agatha plated up the food and they all sat around the table talking, or more accurately complaining, about various work related things.
“And he just stood there watching it boil over! It fucked up the bunsen burner, it fucked up the table and, more importantly, it fucked up my dress!” Jen very animatedly finished telling them a story from the other day.
“That’s what you get for teaching the kids how to make potions.” Lilia shrugged.
“Medicinal Chemistry.” Jen corrected.
“Same thing.”
Jen rolled her eyes. “I’m not going to dignify that with a response.”
Lilia smiled, clearly satisfied in thinking she had won.

“Anyway,” Jen started, facing Agatha, “you’ve been quiet tonight. You’re usually the first to complain about your students. How is it going with that PhD girl? What’s her name again?”
Agatha took a sip of her wine. “Rio.” She had actively been trying to avoid thinking about Rio Vidal, but she seemed to make her way into her mind at least once a day in one way or another. “It’s going well. She’s … intriguing.”
Lilia leaned forward, resting her elbows on the table. “And that’s a bad thing?”
Agatha sighed. Was it a bad thing? She was just a student. An irritating student, but a student nonetheless. “Not necessarily.” She eventually replied. “She’s very sure of herself and seems to enjoy talking back to me.” ‘But I don’t hate it,’ her thoughts finished for her.

Jen raised her eyebrows in surprise. “Has the great Agatha Harkness finally met someone who won’t let her talk to them like a piece of shit?”
“I do not talk to people like they’re pieces of shit.” Agatha shot back. “I am simply preparing them for life in a world that won’t cater to their every need.” She took another sip of her drink. “And if they feel like a piece of shit afterwards then maybe they are one and I have helped them realise it before it’s too late.”
Lilia raised her glass. “Here, here!” They all laughed and cheersed their glasses.

They ate in silence for another few minutes before Agatha spoke again.
“I spoke to Billy the other day.”
Both Jen and Lilia stopped mid chew, their eyes going wide and said their responses in unison.
“You did?”
“What happened?”
Agatha held up her hands. “Calm down! It went well.”
Lilia pointed her finger at Agatha, “details Harkness. Now.” 
Agatha rolled her eyes and pointed at her mouth to indicate that she would talk once she had swallowed her food and Lilia tapped her foot impatiently.
“We spoke about why I’d left it so long to reach out to him and how I had thought about trying to talk to him quite a few times over the last two and a half years.” She paused to give the other two a chance to chime in but they were both uncharacteristically silent. “We touched on the lie his mother told about why we broke up, but I didn’t go into detail. Apparently she told him that it was a lie when he got home from the hospital.”

“Good!” Jen said, probably a bit too loudly. “I’m still mad about that. I mean why the fuck did she say that?”
“And why did you just let it go?” Lilia added.
“Why am I now under fire?” Agatha asked, surprised. “You know why I didn’t fight it, it was more effort than it was worth. People had already accepted it as truth and I’m above playing ‘he said, she said.’” She waved her hand dismissively and brought the conversation back to Billy. “ Anyway , I told him that I had visited him while he was in the hospital and he said that he’d seen me through the window but had convinced himself that he was seeing things. And that’s about it really.”

Lilia reached across the table and grabbed Agatha’s hand, squeezing it gently. “For what it’s worth, I’m proud of you. I know that that was hard for you to do.”
Jen took Agatha’s other hand and added, “I’m glad it went well. How are you feeling about it now?”
Agatha smiled at them both and felt a lump start to form in her throat so she pulled her hands free. “Please, we look like we’re about to have a séance.” She ate another forkful of food. “I’m feeling good about it. It feels like a weight has been lifted.” She smiled again, allowing herself to feel the full extent of her happiness before remembering a final detail. “Oh he said that his mother wanted to talk to me, but I shut that down immediately.”

Jen scoffed. “The nerve that woman has to get her son to ask you to talk to her. You’re not going to do it, I hope?”
“Obviously not, Jennifer!” But if Billy asked her again then she might consider it. If he wanted her to do it, could she say no to him? Would she be able to do anything that felt the slightest bit like letting him down again?
She really hoped that he wouldn’t ask her.

__________

Agatha was sitting in her office, at her desk when there was a knock at her door.
“You may enter.”
In walked Rio Vidal.
‘Of course. It’s Wednesday.’ She thought. Her days had gotten away from her this week.
Something about Rio was different today though. Her hair was up in a messy bun instead of down, framing her face like it usually was but that wasn’t it. Her clothes were the same: a jacket, a t-shirt and tight jeans – not that Agatha had paid particular attention to the tightness of her jeans in the past.

No. None of this was out of the ordinary. It was the confidence with which she entered the room that was different. Rio usually carried herself well but today was strange. She had captured Agatha’s eyes with her own the second that she had crossed the threshold and, even from a distance, Agatha could see that there was something in them, they were darker, and the smile that matched them was teasing her almost.

Rio walked to her usual seat and dropped her bag on the floor, but she didn’t sit down. She carried on towards Agatha. “You’ve been thinking about me, haven’t you?” She all but purred and Agatha’s breath caught. “Are you going to let me sit down?” Rio motioned to Agatha’s lap but Agatha just stayed where she was, thoroughly confused.

Rio laughed lightly and spun her chair so that her legs were no longer under her desk. She slowly put one of her legs on either side of Agatha’s and gently lowered herself so that she was sitting on her. “That’s better.” She said and smiled when Agatha instinctively put her hands on her hips. “You’re catching up.” She put a hand in Agatha’s hair, running her fingers through the waves before pulling gently at the roots. Agatha closed her eyes almost involuntarily. She felt Rio shift, leaning down close to her ear. Her breath was warm against her skin as she whispered. “Open your eyes.”

Her eyes flew open and she found herself staring at her bedroom ceiling, breathing heavily. She pulled her hands down her face and groaned.

Fuck.

There's gonna be a few Agatha chapters in a row because I want to cover all of this stuff in one go from each of their perspectives rather than jumping between the two!

Agatha

Chapter Notes

This chapter is disjointed af and I'm not super happy with it, but it's the best I could get it with the stuff that I wanted to cover, sorry in advance.

It was just a dream, everybody dreams. Dreams don’t mean anything unless you want them to, and she didn’t want it to, so therefore it meant nothing.
Absolutely nothing.
She dreamt about work related things all the time, that’s all this was. Just another dream about work and nothing else.
Absolutely nothing.

__________

Agatha noticed that Billy looked a lot more at ease in her lectures, he stopped tucking himself into a corner and started to sit in the centre more, even answering a couple of questions here and there. This in turn made her feel better, he was warming back up to her and she couldn’t help reminiscing on how close they had been once upon a time.

She remembered his thirteenth birthday. It was during the height of the pandemic, the country was in lockdown and almost everything had ground to a halt. He was upset that he wouldn’t be able to spend the day with his friends so Agatha had organised a zoom call with them all as a surprise. She had gone to all of their houses and picked up the presents they had gotten for him and arranged them all in the living room so that they could still see him open them. She had spent probably more money than she should have getting pizzas for each of them so that they could pretend they were all eating party food together, but the look on Billy’s face had been more than worth it.

The way that he had hugged her so tightly and told her that he loved her would stay with her forever.
“You’re his favourite person, you know?” Wanda had said to her as they watched him from the kitchen and Agatha had laughed. “I’m just doing what anyone else would have.” 

__________

Rio had taken to attending more of her lectures, branching out from the first years and joining the second and final years as well. She would usually sit in the back corner, if she wasn’t sitting with Billy, which meant that it was all too obvious when Agatha looked at her. She tried to not make a habit of looking in Rio’s direction but it was becoming increasingly more difficult, especially when the events of her dream replayed in her mind every time she caught her gaze. Luckily it had been the only one of her dreams to star Rio Vidal, and for that she was grateful.

Their next meeting was spent structuring Rio’s notes, or trying to anyway. Rio, while being the one that required the help, had a hard time accepting it. They were working from a shared google doc and the idea had been that Agatha would tackle the first half, Rio would tackle the last half and then they would fine tune it. They had managed a good fifteen minutes before Rio had decided to take a look at the edits Agatha had made.

“Miss Vidal I am trying to help you, why must you challenge every damn thing I say?” She had been trying very hard to not let her frustration take over like she had in their previous meeting, but Rio had an incredible talent for fraying the edges of her composure.
Rio casually leaned back in her chair, a sly smile plastered on her face. “When your suggestions make sense, Professor, then maybe I’ll accept them.”

Agatha closed her eyes and took a breath, counting to five. She would not let Rio Vidal get under her skin.
She would not let Rio Vidal get under her skin.
“Look,” she opened her eyes again and fixed her gaze onto Rio. “I know that you are very precious about your work, I am not saying that you shouldn’t be because it is good work.” She leaned forward resting her elbows on her desk. “However for this to work,” she gestured between herself and Rio, “you are going to have to accept at some point that I know more than you.”
She wasn’t sure that she could actually carry on like this, because Rio was going to give her an aneurysm. Why was talking to her so fucking difficult?

Rio tensed her jaw, clearly wanting to voice the retort that she was holding in her mind but thought better of it. “Fine.” She eventually said. “You’re right, I’m sorry.”
Agatha straightened her posture again, satisfied that she had come out on top. “Now go back to your section so that we can finish this.”

Her eyes wandered absentmindedly in Rio’s direction as they worked. She didn’t linger because lingering would imply something and there were no implications in how she felt about this woman. Rio was a student and she didn’t look at students like that. Then again, she also shouldn’t dream about students the way she had dreamt about Rio, but it was just a dream. A dream in which the woman sitting to her right had straddled her and played with her hair. But it was just a dream.

“What?” Rio asked, her brow furrowed in confusion.
“Excuse me?” She blinked, just as confused as Rio looked.
“You were staring at me.”
“No I-” Fuck. “I was looking through you Miss Vidal.” She cleared her throat to stall for a second. “I was thinking of the best way to save this travesty in front of me.”
Rio smiled and licked her lips. “Okay then.” She said before returning her attention to her laptop.
Agatha knew that Rio didn’t believe her, but was thankful that she didn’t press further.
God, she really needed to get a grip. 

__________

Agatha hated it every time Wanda’s name flashed up on her phone, it always brought her mood down. She would be happy if she never had to hear from her again, but unfortunately they worked at the same university, in the same damn department and she could never fully escape her.

Maximoff: Billy told me that the two of you talked the other day. How did it go?

Of course Billy had told his mother that they’d talked, and she couldn’t be mad at him for it because she had expected it. But she hadn’t expected Wanda to ask her about it.

Agatha: I’m sure he told you everything you need to know.

She wasn’t about to engage in this conversation, it was another pitiful attempt from Wanda to get the attention she so clearly still craved from her.

Maximoff: He told me how he felt about it. How do you feel about it?

Agatha rolled her eyes. Why could Wanda not take the hint? Surely this was getting embarrassing for her by now. Agatha shot her down every single time she tried to talk to her about anything that wasn’t work related.
She could just not reply, it would be easy to do, but she couldn’t resist a chance to be petty.

Agatha: Why do you care?

Was it childish? Yes. Was it satisfying? Also yes. She would be lying if she said that she wasn’t a little bit interested about how Wanda would reply. What lies would she tell? What excuses would she come up with?
A few minutes went by without a reply and Agatha smiled, Wanda usually ran from questions like that. Probably because she could never form an answer that was believable.
But then her phone pinged again.

Maximoff: Because I’ve always cared, Agatha.

Oh, she just had to laugh at that. Wanda was really bringing out the big guns today wasn’t she? Agatha might go as far as to suggest that Wanda was drunk, because there was no other plausible explanation for this level of misplaced bravery.
She shouldn’t reply, she shouldn’t give Wanda the satisfaction. But there were a lot of things that she shouldn’t do.

Agatha: Whatever you are trying to do, it will not work.

Maximoff: I’m not trying anything. I’m being honest, Agatha.

Agatha: Well I’m glad that you have finally learned this basic human trait, but I’m not interested.

Agatha stared at her phone, waiting to see the three dots appear again but they didn’t. Five minutes went by and there was no reply from Wanda, she had finally left her alone for the night.

She tried to sleep but her mind wouldn’t let her. Why was Wanda trying to talk to her so much lately? What did she want? Agatha had made it clear ten times over that she wanted nothing to do with her and yet she was still trying. Maybe she should give her a chance.
“Absolutely not. Get a fucking hold of yourself Agatha.” She chastised herself because why was she considering it? She had gone two and a half years without talking to that woman and she was not going to start now just because Wanda was putting a bit of effort in. She didn’t deserve Agatha’s time or attention so she wouldn’t be getting it.
Except she was getting it. She was getting it right now because Agatha couldn’t get her out of her mind.

Has this been her plan all along? To slowly break Agatha down until she had no other choice but to talk to her, if only to get her out of her head? If it was then Agatha would not give her the satisfaction. She was stubborn and it was going to take a hell of a lot more than this to get her to break.

She closed her eyes and forced her mind to switch gears and think of something, anything, else. She couldn’t – wouldn’t – allow Wanda to bury herself into her brain. Of course her mind was cruel to her, so the next thing it chose to latch onto was equally bad.

She was back in the hospital, stood outside of Billy’s room watching Wanda and Vis standing on either side of his bed. Both desperate to hold him, but not wanting to hurt him, as he woke up from the accident. Her hand was on the door handle, ready to go in but she held herself back. She had managed being with both of his parents when he had first been brought in to the hospital, but the idea of doing it again, even to see him awake and okay, was too much for her.

She rolled over and pushed her face into her pillow with a groan. She had no idea why her brain was deciding to punish her right now. It wasn’t the first time she had thought about Billy’s accident in the last year, it had played on her mind multiple times. The fear, the anger, the pain, the heartache, she was familiar with all of it. But why now?
She knew that there wasn’t really an answer, she wasn’t any more in control of her mind than anyone else was, but she was usually better at blocking things out than most people. It was something she had learned as a child – and it had been a huge help in adulthood – so she put up her mental walls and caged those thoughts in where they wouldn’t bother her for a while so that she could finally get some sleep.

__________

It had definitely been a surprise when Billy had asked her if they could have lunch together one day, but a pleasant one. There was a café just off campus that she asked him to meet her at to avoid being seen by other students and staff as much as possible. She wasn’t ashamed of having lunch with him but she knew how fast the rumour mill churned in those halls, having been on the receiving end of it herself, and didn’t want anything to be misconstrued. She also didn’t want it getting back to Wanda before Billy was ready to tell her. She expected him to tell Wanda at some point and for her to then, once again, use it as a way to try to get Agatha to talk to her; but that was his choice and she would accept it if he did it.

“How are you finding your first year? Are you settling in okay?” Agatha asked when they’d ordered their food.
“I’m enjoying it! The lectures are interesting, I’m living in a house with Alice and the student bar prices are nice and low.” He said the last part with a cheeky grin which made Agatha laugh.
“Ahh yes, the main focus of every first year student. The bar.”
“Well first year doesn’t count towards your final grade, so it’s the perfect time to sample all of the cheap beer.”
She shook her head, but was still smiling. “As your lecturer, I have to tell you that I disapprove of this mindset. But as your…” She faltered. What was she to him? How did he see her? She knew how he used to see her but that had long since changed and they were now in a strange limbo of picking up where they left off and getting to know each other all over again. “Friend?” She said the word carefully, reading his reaction. He smiled softly and gave a little nod which made her chest warm. “As your friend, I couldn't agree more. I definitely did the same in my undergrad.”

She laughed when she saw his eyes widen in surprise. “Don’t be so shocked, kid. All students are the same.”
He stuttered for a second, trying to find the right words. “Yes but I mean, you’re my… you.” While it was somewhat comforting to know that he also didn’t know how to define their current relationship, it also saddened her because she could tell what he was going to say before he changed it. What he should call her had never been something that she and Wanda had discussed, they had left it up to Billy to choose as and when he was ready. He had always called her by her name, but for purposes such as parents evenings she was his stepmum – even though her and Wanda weren’t married – and she felt the absence of it in the sentence as he spoke.

She smiled, though it didn’t reach her eyes, and quickly changed the subject. This wasn’t the time or place to start spiralling. “Are you finding it easy to talk to people and make new friends? I know you have Alice, but it’s nice to have a group.” She said, keeping her tone light.
He seemed glad that she had taken the conversation in a new direction and some of the tension left his shoulders. “I don’t have a group yet, that takes time, but me and Alice met someone on the first day of freshers week actually.” He took a bite of his wrap. “Oh I think you know her actually. She’s doing her PhD and she said that you were her supervisor.”
“Rio Vidal.” Saying her name was a subconscious action and as she said it, it dawned on her that this was the first time she had ever said Rio’s full name out loud. It had plagued her thoughts but she had never said it, and now she wanted to say it again.

Luckily, Billy spoke before she could. “Yeah that’s her!” He was oblivious to whatever place she had gone to inside her head.
“Well she’s very smart. She could be a big help for you and Alice.” She took a sip of her drink, feeling her throat going dry at the thought of Rio and Billy spending time together. It wasn’t that she didn’t want them to be friends, she meant what she said about Rio being able to help him with his work, but she had a hard time keeping a professional head around Rio as it was and she didn’t need that to be made harder by Billy telling her things that she would rather Rio didn’t know.

He laughed, still blissfully unaware of the effect of just saying Rio’s name had had on her. “I already asked her if she would write my essays for me and she said no, so I don’t think she’ll be that much help.” He had a cheeky smile plastered on his face and Agatha couldn’t help but laugh, he really hadn’t changed much at all. He was still the same kid that she knew and loved and it made her feel nostalgic for when she and Wanda were together. Not for the relationship necessarily, but for the family dynamic that the three of them had. Eating dinner together every night, going to the cinema, lazy Sunday afternoons, helping Billy with his homework. She missed all of those things and it made her chest tighten to know that she would never have them back. But she now had the opportunity to create a new dynamic with Billy, and the memories that came along with it, and that was something to look forward to.

“I didn’t mean for her to do your coursework for you, I meant she could read it before you submit it. I would know if she had written it for you.” She gave him a stern look but still had a smile in the corners of her mouth.
“Yeah, yeah I know. She said the same thing actually.” He took another bite of his food and his shoulders tensed again. Agatha ate her own food, giving him space to say what he wanted to say.
“So I told my mum about the other day.” He stared down at his plate. “She was happy that we talked.” Agatha stilled, predicting where this was going. “She wants to talk to you too, Agatha.”
Agatha put her fork down and sighed. “Billy, I don’t know what she told you exactly bu-”
“Please Agatha. Talk to her for me.”
There it was, the thing she had been hoping that he wouldn’t do. She couldn’t say no now, no matter how much she wanted to. He was specifically asking her to talk to Wanda and the pleading look in his eyes nearly broke her. How could she turn him down again? It was simple, she couldn’t. She was going to have to talk to his mother.
“Okay.”

__________

 

5 Years Ago

Agatha woke up alone in her bed in her flat and the excitement immediately flooded her, this was the last time that she would be doing that because she was officially moving in with Wanda and Billy today. Her flat was bare because all of her things were already in the new house, her new house. It felt like the first day of the rest of her life and she couldn’t wait for it to start.

She quickly got ready and did one last walk through of all the rooms for nostalgia sake. She stood in the kitchen and remembered the first time that she had cooked dinner for Wanda. It had been a mess, obviously, because she couldn’t cook anything without spilling something or using every utensil available for some reason, but Wanda had laughed and said that her chaos was cute before pulling her in for a kiss.

She went into the spare room that she had turned into her office and remembered the nights that Wanda had spent helping her apply for her professorship at the university. She had been nervous about it and the imposter syndrome had got her in a vice grip, but Wanda had assured her over and over that she deserved it. She had taken Agatha’s hands in hers and said, “darling, you are more than worthy of this. You’re a brilliant lecturer and your results speak for themselves. Believe in yourself as I believe in you.”

She went to the living area where she and Wanda had spent many nights curled up on the sofa in front of the TV, on some occasions Billy had been there too watching a movie with them. She smiled as she thought about the time that Billy had fallen asleep whilst being leant against her. Wanda hadn’t planned on staying over that night since she had Billy with her, but neither of them wanted to wake him so they gently got up, laid him down with a blanket over him and went to bed themselves.

She walked out onto the balcony, the place that she had stormed to after she and Wanda had had an argument. She couldn’t remember what it was about, something small and insignificant now, but she remembered Wanda following her out after giving her a few minutes to calm down. She remembered the gentle way that Wanda touched her arm to get her attention, she remembered the way that Wanda had put her hand on her cheek to make her look at her. She remembered the way that Wanda had kissed her, the unspoken apology evident in the way that she held her, so close and so steadily that her knees felt weak. But more than all of that, she remembered that moment as the moment that Wanda had first told her that she loved her.

It had taken her by surprise, as a confession like that always does, and all she could do was stare at Wanda, her mind blank. Wanda had laughed awkwardly and said, “one typically expects a response to something like this.” worry beginning to work its way into her demeanour.
Agatha had stuttered, not sure what to say. “I… Uhh, I wasn- I didn’t expect you to say that.”
“If it helps, I didn’t expect to say it either.” Wanda had taken her hand and looked at their fingers, weaving them together. “You don’t have to say it back if you’re not ready. I don’t want you to feel forced.”
“No I.. I want to. I just- fuck.” Agatha had looked at the floor and taken a breath. “Let me try again.” She looked back up, locking eyes with Wanda's, the bright green grounding her. “I love you too.”
It was her favourite memory that she had in her apartment and she was looking forward to making new ones in her new home with Wanda and Billy. 

She got to the front door and had a rush of happiness pass through her when she put her key in the lock. She'd had a key to the house for months now, but this was the first time that she was doing it as someone who was a permanent resident of the house. She pushed the door open and walked in to be instantly greeted by Wanda and Billy both hugging her. Wanda kissed her and said, “welcome home, darling.”
Agatha smiled. “It’s good to be home.” 

Billy

Attending the university that both his mum and his ex-almost-stepmum taught at was definitely a choice, but it also happened to be the third best university in the world for Ancient History courses; so it was a choice well-made. He just had to figure out how he was going to handle seeing said ex-almost-stepmum again after a year and a half of hating her followed by a year of wishing that he hadn’t hated her. He had braced for an argument when he told his mum that he wanted to be enrolled on Agatha’s module over hers for his first year, but no argument came. His mum almost seemed happy about it actually.

Moving into the campus housing was easy since he didn’t actually live that far away from the university in the first place, but both he and his mum had agreed that part of the quintessential student experience is living away from home.
“I really enjoyed my time living away.” She said with a nostalgic smile. “It was nice to get some freedom, and I met your father in my first year halls.”
“So you’re saying I could meet my future ex-husband this year?” Billy laughed.
“Well I’m hoping he won’t turn into an ex but essentially, yes.” She ruffled his hair and he swatted her hand away.

He was happy that he was sharing accommodation with Alice, they had been best friends since primary school and he didn’t know what he would have done without having her there through everything. When his mum and dad had been fighting he had basically moved into Alice’s house, and when they eventually told him that they were getting a divorce, he spent every weekend there. He had expected his parents to try to stop him, but they just let him do it, giving him the space he needed to come to terms with it on his own. He had been grateful for that.

When his mum had started dating Agatha, he immediately told Alice and they talked it out over and over. It wasn’t that his mother was dating a woman, he hadn’t been raised to see that as a problem, it was that his mother was dating someone who wasn’t his dad. They had been on-again-off-again his whole life so he was just used to them being together, but now there was a completely new person in his mum’s life and subsequently, his. He didn’t know how to feel about it and he had given Alice his every thought as and when they came to him. But when he met Agatha for the first time he could see how happy his mum was – how happy they both were – and he quickly grew to like Agatha and knew that she was the right person to join their mother-son duo.

Then when he came home from school to find Agatha screaming at his mother saying that she would never set foot in the house again, he was confused because this had been the first time they had ever fought. They’d had arguments sure, he wasn’t naïve enough to think that no couple had the odd tiff, but this was very different. Agatha was crying and throwing her clothes into a suitcase telling his mum to stop talking to her because everything that came out of her mouth was a lie, and he was just standing in the doorway without a clue as to what was happening.

Agatha had finally seen him standing there and hugged him saying, “oh kid, I love you so much.” She had pressed a wrapped box into his hands before she left and said, “happy birthday, Billy. We’ll talk soon, I promise.” and walked out of the house with her suitcase in tow.
His mum had tried to explain what had happened and had stopped him from chasing after Agatha, so he went to Alice instead. She had listened to him talking about it until the early hours of the morning when they eventually went to sleep, and had gone back home with him to talk to his mother. Wanda had said that she wasn’t going to talk about it with Alice there but he had said “either Alice stays, or I go.” So she had conceded and told them both her story.
That had ruined his sixteenth birthday.

And then there was the day that he came home from the hospital and his mother had sat him down and told him the true story about what had happened. How she had lied, how she was the reason that Agatha had left and how she wished she could take it all back and fix it. His instinct had been – once again – to go to Alice, but his mum had insisted that he stay home since he had only just been discharged and she wanted to keep an eye on him. So Alice had stayed over at his house that night and he had refused to leave his room because the thought of seeing his mother made him feel sick.

It had taken months for him to be able to look her in the eye again and even then she wasn’t the person that he had once known.

__________

After making his mum promise that she wouldn’t embarrass him in any way he and Alice set out to enjoy freshers week together.
“Are you hoping things will get better between the two of you now that you’re sharing a campus?” Alice asked.
He thought for a moment. “I guess if I can talk to Agatha and get her version of events, and if they match what my mum said, then maybe. I’m still not sure how much I believe her.”
“So you want to talk to Agatha then?”
He sighed. “I don’t know honestly. She promised me when she left that we’d talk, but we never did so I’m not sure if she wants to talk to me.”
Alice linked her arm through his as they walked. “There’s only one way to find out.”
“I know.”

They walked to the ancient history department to attend the welcome event, the room was filled with fellow first years and some second and final years who would be leading them through the department, and answering any questions that they had. They stood on the outskirts of the group, seemingly the only two who hadn’t already made a few friends, and scanned the room.
He hadn’t been shy in high school, he’d found it easy to talk to people and make friends but something about being at uni felt more intimidating. His grades had always been fine and he had passed all of his exams but he suddenly felt out of his depth among all of these people.

His eyes landed on a girl who looked as out of place as he felt and his ability to talk to people returned. He muttered “wait here,” to Alice and walked towards the girl, offering her his hand.
“Hi I’m Billy, are you studying ancient history too?”
The girl shook his hand with a smile and said, “nice to meet you, I’m Rio, and I’m here to get my PhD but I figured it couldn’t hurt to check out the department and meet some people.”
He smiled back and gestured to where he had left Alice standing by herself. “My friend Alice is over there, we’re kind of on our own at the moment, but if you’re wanting to expand your social circle you’re more than welcome to spend the day with us.”
Rio went with him back to Alice and introduced herself.
“Nice to meet you, Rio. Are you another nervous first year like us?”
Rio laughed. “Actually I’m a PhD student. I’ve already done the nervous first year schtick, now I’m just a jaded post-grad.”

The three of them spent the day together touring the department and Billy tried to look as normal as possible as they passed his mothers office, and again when they passed Agatha’s office. He silently prayed that neither of them would choose that moment to appear and decided that god did in fact exist when his prayer was answered. The person guiding them made a joke about not getting on Professor Harkness’ bad side and he exchanged a look with Alice. It seemed that Agatha still didn’t tolerate fools and it sent a pang of nervousness to his stomach. What would her reaction be to seeing him again? His mum had told him that she would be happy that he was taking her module, but his mum had told him a lot of things that weren’t true lately and he found it hard to trust her.

Over the course of the week, he, Alice and Rio went for drinks a few times and got to know each other a bit better before the first day of the semester came around.
He grabbed Alice’s hand as they got near the lecture hall, feeling uneasy about the fact that their first lecture was with Agatha.
“You’ll be fine.” She assured him, giving his hand a gentle squeeze. “Even if she was going to act like a dick, I doubt she would do it in a room full of people.”
His throat was dry so he just nodded and they walked into the room together finding Rio in the back corner and sitting next to her.
“I didn’t think PhD students needed to attend lectures.” He asked, furrowing his brow in confusion.
“Oh we don’t, but I have a meeting with Agatha today about her being my supervisor so I thought I’d sit in.”
Billy looked at Alice and could see her eyes widening, he gave her a stern look begging her not to say anything stupid.
“Agatha Harkness is your supervisor? You’re a brave woman.”
He swallowed hard and was grateful when Rio didn’t get a chance to say anything else, but that gratefulness was instantly replaced by dread when he saw Agatha walk into the room.

The room fell silent and he couldn’t tell if that was because Agatha had entered or because his brain had started to shut down. He barely heard the words that she said over the sound of his heart beating in his ears and when she looked directly at him, he couldn’t help flinching. Alice noticed and mouthed “you okay?” to him. He just nodded and looked straight ahead, disassociating until the lights dimmed, the darkness offering him some comfort.

He found it easier to listen to Agatha teach in the dim light, though his pulse was still racing. She was a good lecturer and he knew that he would enjoy learning from her if he could get over the discomfort that being in the same room as her again provided. His palms started to become less clammy as the lecture went on until Agatha looked in his direction again and he stilled. No, she wasn’t looking at him, she was looking at Rio who had just muttered something under her breath. Had she really just done that? He couldn't help but look at her in surprise, nor could anyone else in the room.

He watched the interaction between Rio and Agatha play out, instantly forgetting his nervousness and replacing it with admiration for Rio. Maybe he could get her to lend him some of her courage.
The lecture ended and Rio bolted out of the room, he couldn’t blame her as he did the same, unable to stop himself from looking at Agatha as he left and caught up with Rio and Alice outside of the lecture hall.
“Well you’re brave, I’ll give you that.” He said to Rio.
Rio snorted, “stupid is what I am. I never could keep my mouth shut. Come on, I need a coffee.”

They found a table in one of the campus cafés and exchanged small talk until Alice had to say something he didn’t want her to. “You’re gonna have fun with Agatha as your supervisor after that stellar first impression.” She laughed. “Although Billy is grateful that you took some of the heat off of him.” She nudged him with her shoulder. He knew that she was trying to joke with him, but he didn’t want her to do it in front of Rio she he shot her a look which promptly made her stop talking. Thankfully Rio didn’t push for more and left.

He punched Alice on the arm.
“Ow what the fuck?”
“Why did you say that shit in front of Rio?”
Alice rubbed her arm in an exaggerated way. “Well was I wrong?”
“No, but you didn’t need to say it.” She was still rubbing her arm. “Oh grow up, I didn’t hit you that hard.”
She dropped her hand and looked at him softly. “How are you feeling after the lecture?”
He shrugged. How was he feeling? It had only been one lecture and it wasn’t like he and Agatha had actually interacted. “Weird.”
“Oh careful Shakespeare, Billy Maximoff is coming for your job.” Alice grinned at him.
“Shut up, dick.” He said, though there wasn’t any anger in the words. He was glad that Alice was joking like she always did, it helped him feel normal about everything, and he knew that when he needed her to be serious she would be. They knew each other incredibly well and could be what the other needed at the drop of a hat. He was really glad that he had her on his side.

__________

Billy knew that his mum cared about him, she had never given him a reason to think otherwise, but he couldn’t help but be annoyed every time she messaged him to ask how his day was going. He had asked her to give him space once the semester started and she seemed to be having a hard time doing it.

Mum: How have your lectures been?

Billy: They’ve been good

Mum: Are you enjoying them?

Billy: Yeah

Mum: Is Alice enjoying them too?

Billy: Yeah

Mum: Was Agatha okay?

That question took him by surprise, he hadn’t been expecting her to ask about Agatha. She had barely mentioned her outside of telling him the truth about their break up and telling him that it was okay to take her class, so why was she asking now?

Billy: Why do you care?

She didn’t respond, it was probably for the best. He didn’t really want to hear her answer, he wouldn’t be able to trust what she said. 

__________

The first week passed and Billy felt more settled. He was still nervous when in Agatha’s lectures but she didn’t single him out or do anything in particular to make him feel uncomfortable, he was just a victim of his own thoughts. Rio tried to get him to join in and answer questions but the idea of it made his heart pound, though he wasn’t sure if that was because it was Agatha or if it was the act of speaking in a lecture in general. Either way, he wasn’t going to do it.

He was in the bar with Alice when his phone buzzed with an email notification and she noticed when his eyes widened as he read it.
“What is it?”
He didn’t speak, instead he just handed her his phone and let her read it for herself.

Billy,

I’m glad that you’re taking my module this semester and I would like it if we could talk.
If you’re open to it, I’ll be in room C24 tomorrow at 9am. Meet me there?

Agatha

She handed his phone back and said, “what are you going to do?”
He sighed and sipped his drink. “I have no clue. I want to but also…” He trailed off, not having an ending to that thought. He wanted to speak to her, he really did, but something was holding him back. Previously it had been wondering if she wanted to speak to him and now that she had shown that she does, he couldn’t help thinking of his mum. What would she say about it? Was Agatha asking him to meet her because his mum had asked her to? Had the two of them started talking again? What would Agatha want to say to him?

All of the questions were swirling around his head and it wasn’t until Alice touched his arm that he realised he’d zoned out. “You don’t have to reply now, we can talk it out for a bit first.”
He nodded. “Yes please.”
Alice leaned back in the chair. “What are all of your thoughts? Hit me.”
He rattled off all of the questions he’d had moments ago and a few more that he had thought of as he was saying them.

Alice listened to him and only spoke when he was done. “I mean, the fact that she’s the one to reach out to you can only be a positive thing right?”
“I guess, but what if she wants to tell me that she hates me?”
Alice scoffed. “And why the fuck would she do that?”
Billy looked down and started picking at his fingernails. “I don’t know. I’m just trying to prepare for the negatives.”
“No, you’re looking for negatives.” Alice said sternly and he looked back up, meeting her eyes. “Sure she hates your mum, but she doesn’t hate you. I refuse to believe that.”
“How do you-”

He sighed. “Okay, yes, I’ll do it.” He gulped down the rest of his pint. “Should I tell my mum?”
Alice followed suit before answering. “I’d wait until after, no use in opening that can of worms before you’ve got the information to follow it with.”

“I always am.”

Billy made his way to the room that Agatha had asked him to meet her at. He was nervous, which was a given, but he was also a little bit excited. This would be the first time since she left that they were going to properly see each other, and he missed her. He wished that this had happened sooner, but he was glad that it was happening now and was trying to only think positively about it.

He got to the room and waited outside. Should he knock? Should he just walk in? Would Agatha already be there, or was he the first to arrive? He gingerly pushed the door open and walked into the room, Agatha was already there and any excitement that was working to tame his nerves vanished.

“Hi.” He practically whispered. He tried to walk further into the room, but he felt rooted to the spot where he was standing until he knew the direction that the conversation would take.
“It’s nice to see you again, Billy.” Agatha’s voice was soft and quiet, more like the voice he was used to, not the voice of the professional lecturer he had experienced over the last week. Hearing it took the edge off of his apprehension a little and he was able to take another step into the room. “It’s nice to see you again too, Professor.” He had no idea how to address her now. They weren’t family anymore and this was now unchartered territory for both of them.

Agatha didn’t reply straight away and the silence was starting to feel heavy around him.

This made him look at her and he couldn’t hide the questioning look on his face as he remembered the last words she had spoken to him. “We’ll talk soon, I promise.” He did not count a two and a half years as ‘soon’. There’s not a lot that two and half years could be counted as ‘soon’ for.

I hated you for a long time.” He didn’t like telling her that, but the only way that anything good was going to come out of this was through honesty. He was still hurt by her walking out – even when the reason he was told had turned out to be a lie – and the fact that she hadn’t tried to talk to him until now made him feel slightly resentful towards her.

You didn't deserve it, you were just a child.” Agatha started, looking back up at him. “I can't take back that time and I can't erase the way I made you feel, no matter how much I wish I could. But I can promise that I will do anything I can to make it up to you. I really miss you, kid.”

His mother had tried to call him ‘kid’ after Agatha had left but it felt like a twisted version of it, of the relationship that he and Agatha had once had and it had only made him cry.

I also didn't want you to feel like you had to talk to me if you didn't want to.”

There were so many unspoken feelings between them and he just wanted to skip to the part where they had fixed everything and could go back to the way that they were, but that wasn’t possible and they had to go through the pain and the hurt if they were going to come out at the other end together.

“I found out about a year later. She told me when we got home from the hospital.” He recalled how it had felt to hear and how his heart had broken for Agatha. “I guess that she felt guilty after I nearly died and told me the truth. Every cloud, as they say.”
He wanted to hug her, wanted her to hug him, but he didn’t know if it was appropriate because they were on campus and she was his Professor. Agatha smiled at him. “I visited you in the hospital, your mother at least had the decency to let me know that you were hurt. I was there when you woke up as well but I didn't want to add to the stress of the situation and overwhelm you, so I didn't go into your room. I watched you from the window for a few minutes and left.”
This took him by surprise because he had sworn that he had seen her there, he was going to ask his mum about it but had forgotten with everything else that was happening around him.  “You were there? I thought I was going crazy! I saw you in the window but when it dawned on me that it was you, and I looked again, you were gone.”

As soon as he finished speaking Agatha started crying, and he didn’t know what to do. The last – and only – time that he had seen her cry was when she left. She started speaking, her voice thick from the tears. “I'm so sorry, Billy. I'm sorry that I didn't go in and see you when you woke up. I'm sorry that I waited this long to talk to you again. I never stopped caring about you.” He couldn’t hold himself back, his own tears started to fall and he had to hug her.

“I shouldn’t have listened to my mum. I knew deep down that the story didn’t add up and that you weren’t the type of person to do that.” He wrapped his arms around her tighter and they stayed there for a bit. It was a nice feeling to be able to hug her again after all the time of uncertainty surrounding how he felt about her. It was nice to know that she didn’t hate him and that she was sorry for not seeing him sooner. It felt good to begin the process of healing and being back in each other's lives.

After they pulled apart, they sat in silence for a moment. It felt comfortable, they were just enjoying each other’s company like they used to but he had a nagging feeling, something that he had to mention. “I think my mum really wants to speak to you.
