He knew that it probably wouldn’t get a positive response and Agatha’s unamused scoff confirmed his suspicions. He couldn’t blame her. He was pissed off at his mum so he couldn’t imagine how Agatha felt.
“With respect ki- teen. I won't be doing that.” She stood up and swiftly changed the subject. “Don't you have a lecture to go to? You shouldn't be late, I hear your professor is a real hard arse.” She said with a wink.
He laughed and started towards the door but before he left, he turned back. “Agatha?”
“Yeah?”

“Thank you for this.”

He meant it, he truly was grateful that she had asked to see him and he was glad that he had agreed. He felt lighter, happier and he was looking forward to talking to her again.
After the lecture, he went for coffee with Alice and told her about it and he was smiling the whole time.

__________

Billy knew that he should tell his mum that he had spoken to Agatha, he just didn’t know how to bring it up or how much he should tell her. She would have questions but he wasn’t sure what they would be or if he would want to answer them. He considered asking Alice to be there while he told her but he knew that it wasn’t fair to always rely on Alice to be around every time he needed to have a difficult conversation with his mother. She hadn’t been there while he talked with Agatha and he had survived, so he could survive talking to his mum about Agatha.

He picked up his phone and started drafting out a message to his mum asking if she would want to hear about it but he stopped because it didn’t feel right. He knew that his mum would definitely want to know about it but did he want her to know about it? Could this not just be a thing for him and Agatha to have to themselves? Did she need to know?

He threw his phone on his bed and put his head in his hands. He didn’t anticipate this being the thing that stressed him out in his first semester. He thought that the workload would take the gold on that one, but this had crept up in the inside lane and overtaken it just before the finish line. He wished that he could go back in time to before everything was so fucked and find a way to stop it from happening.

He was still caught in the middle of whatever was going on between Agatha and his mother and he wanted to scream because how were they being so childish? Agatha had every right to be angry at the start but it had been two and a half years and she hadn't found a way to be civil with his mum while they were at work. It could be the most fake performance of her life, but it would at least be something.
But on the other hand, his mum didn’t seem to understand that Agatha was under no obligation to talk to her and hear what she had to say. She was trying to push Agatha into doing something that she clearly didn’t want to do, and that had never worked while they were together so why would she think that it would work now?

If he was going to tell his mother then it would be on his terms and in a way that he wanted to do it. He picked his phone back up and texted his mum.

Billy: Can I come home for dinner at the weekend? Pot noodles aren’t as sustaining as I originally thought

Mum: Yes of course you can! Are you wanting anything in particular?

Billy: Can you do the chicken thing that you used to do?

Mum: Sounds perfect! Is Alice coming as well?

He thought about it for a moment and wondered if Alice would be mad that she wasn’t invited. ‘No, she’ll understand.’ He thought.

Billy: No it’ll just be me

Mum: Okay, I’m looking forward to it

__________

The weekend came and Billy confidently walked into his home – he had told Alice about it and she had reminded him that she was only a phone call away if he needed her. He could smell the spicy Cajun chicken that he had asked his mum to cook and he could hear the soft music coming from the kitchen. He took off his boots and left his bag by the door before finding his mother at the cooker stirring a pan.

He cleared his throat before saying, “it smells good.”
His mum jumped, startled by his voice, and turned around. “Oh I didn’t hear you come in!” She set down the spoon she was using and walked over to him, pulling him into a hug. “Hi, sweetheart, it’s nice to see you.”
“You too.” He said, returning the hug.
She pulled back and looked at him for a second before ruffling his hair. “Your roots need re-doing before your friends start to suspect that we might be related.” She said with a smile.
He laughed. “Yeah I know. Alice is going to do it for me tomorrow.”
She ruffled his hair again before turning back to her pan. “Can you get the plates out please? The rice is nearly ready.”

He took a bite of his food and had to stop himself from violently swearing in front of his mother. “This is so good! Why did you ever stop making it?”
She laughed. “I’m not sure actually, I learned a couple of new recipes and forgot about this one I guess.”
“Well make sure you don’t forget it again.” He said, eating more.

As they ate, they exchanged small talk. His mum asked questions about his courses and his housemates and he asked questions about her students and lectures. It felt comfortable but he was thinking about how to broach the topic of Agatha. It wasn’t an easy one to work into conversation and would feel out of left field no matter how he chose to do it, so he decided for the head on approach.

He looked his mother in the eye as he spoke, not wanting to seem embarrassed or sheepish about it, because he wasn’t. “I spoke to Agatha the other day and we talked some stuff out.”
He had expected it to take her by surprise but he hadn’t expected her to actually choke on her food. He rushed to the sink to get her a glass of water and she gulped it down.

“Sorry, I didn’t expect you to say that.” She said once she’d gotten her breath back.
“I know but I didn’t think you’d react that dramatically.” He tried to joke but his tone was wrong.
“Billy-”
“I’m sorry, that came out wrong. Are you okay?”
She smiled softly at him. “I’m fine, sweetheart.” She ate some more of her food. “What did you talk about?”
‘Head on approach, Billy.’ He reminded himself.
“We didn’t cover much, it was mostly just apologising to each other actually.” He paused, giving his mum a chance to react, but she stayed quiet. “I told her how I felt when she left, how I was angry for a while before I fou-” He faltered slightly, choosing his words. “Before you told me the truth.”

His mum dropped her gaze, avoiding his eyes. He almost felt guilty but he was right, he hadn’t accidentally found out what had happened, she had chosen to tell him.
She cleared her throat, still not looking back up. “What did she say to that?”
He ate another spoonful, making her wait for his answer. “She said that she was sorry that I ended up in the middle of it and she told me that she came to visit me in the hospital.”
“That’s true!” She cut in, almost too eagerly. “She was the first person I called.”
His brows knit together in confusion. “Why?”
“Because she… I…” She sighed and Billy could tell that she was struggling with figuring out which version she should tell him. “Because I knew how much you meant to her, and her to you, and I needed her there.”

He scanned her face looking for any hint that she wasn’t being truthful, but he couldn’t find one. He wasn’t sure how to respond so he just nodded.
“I’m not lying, William.”
He flinched at her tone and, tripled with the intensity in her eyes and the use of his full name, shrunk into himself. “I know, but you can’t blame me for thinking that you might be.” He spoke quietly but he knew that she heard him clearly.
He expected her to be angry at him for speaking to her that way, he expected her to shout at him for being insolent. But instead she looked regretful and her gaze softened. “Yes, you’re right. I’m sorry.” Her tone was still clipped but her words were genuine.

They finished their food and the tension slowly dissipated as he helped her clean up.
“Could you do me a favour?” She asked as she handed him a pan to put in the dishwasher.
“Sure.”
“Can you ask Agatha if she would talk to me?”
He closed his eyes and clenched his jaw, thankful that he had his back to her so that she couldn’t see his expression. He opened his eyes again and turned to face her. “I don’t want to play messenger boy in whatever you’re planning. I’ve only just started repairing my relationship with Agatha and I don’t want you to ruin that.” Again. It was unspoken but both of them knew that it was heavily implied.
She gave a defeated sigh. “Please Billy. I wouldn’t ask you if I had any other option. I don’t want to use you like this anymore than you want to be used.”
He turned his back to her again, needing a second to take a steadying breath and think about his response.
“I will ask her once.” He said, still not facing her and adding stress to the final word. “Whatever her answer is, I want you to leave me out of anything that comes next.” He turned to face her again. “Thank you for dinner.”

He left the house and stepped out into the pouring rain, letting it soak him through. He hadn’t worn a coat which was a massive oversight for someone used to the British weather, but he didn’t care because the feeling of it was grounding. He couldn’t believe that his own mother was shamelessly using him to get her ex to talk to her. This was the kind of shit that happened in high school, not between grown adults with incomes and mortgages.

He put his headphones on and stuffed his hands into the pockets of his hoodie, balling them into fists. He was so angry that he almost turned around and stormed back into the house telling his mother to go fuck herself, but that would be immature and he knew that it wouldn’t achieve anything.

When he got back to his room he discarded his wet clothes and got in the shower, warming himself back up after his cold walk. He got out of the shower and saw his notification light blinking on his phone, he checked it and saw a message from his mum.

 Mum: I love you

He scowled and swiped it off his screen.

__________

Billy was a lot more comfortable in Agatha’s lectures after they had broken the ice with each other, he and Alice slowly started to sit in a more central spot with Rio joining them when she decided to go to the lectures. His mother hadn’t texted him since he hadn’t replied to her last message, which he was happy about. He was still mad at her and needed to allow himself time to stew before he talked to her again.

He started to get to know his housemates better and they all started to spend more time together, he wouldn’t say they were friends yet per se but they were getting there. He felt like he was really finding his feet and was happy with the rhythm that he had settled into.

Feeling confident after a lecture, he approached Agatha after everyone had left the room and asked if she wanted to have lunch with him at some point. She had happily agreed and he let her pick the day and place.
They met at an off campus café and, other than a few awkward moments where neither of them was sure how to refer to their relationship, it was a good time. They chatted easily, comfortable in each other’s company and it felt natural. He wished that he didn’t have to ruin it by handing Agatha his mothers request, but he needed to do it so that he could remove himself as much as possible from the situation that the two of them caused for him.

She didn’t agree straight away, he knew that she wouldn’t, but thankfully he didn’t have to push too hard. In fact he barely had to push at all, and they were able to finish their lunch with no more awkwardness or tension.
When they went their separate ways he texted his mother. They still hadn’t spoken since the weekend, but he unfortunately had to be the one to break the silence.

Billy: She said yes.

Mum: Thank you Billy! I love you

He didn’t reply.

Agatha

Chapter Notes

Happy Valentines Day, love is a lie I guess!

4 Years Ago

Nervous did not even begin to describe how Agatha was feeling, but she couldn’t find the right words, if they even existed, so nervous would have to do. She had enlisted the help of Jen, Lilia and Billy to make tonight the most special night of her life to date.
It was hers and Wanda’s two year anniversary and she had booked them a table at the Italian restaurant that Wanda had taken her to on their first date. While they were out, it was down to The Three Musketeers – the name Billy had insisted on giving them for the night – to decorate the living room and their bedroom ready for when they got home later. Billy would be spending the night with his dad and promised that the house would be empty by the time she and Wanda got home.
Agatha wasn’t usually one for clichés, but this felt right.

When she went to the bathroom between courses, Agatha thought back to the conversation she’d had with Billy three months prior.
She had sat with him in the living room while Wanda was out with some of her school friends and asked how he would feel about her asking Wanda to marry her. His eyes had immediately lit up and a comically wide smile had appeared on his face. “Are you kidding? I would love that!” He had hugged her with such force that it knocked the air out of her lungs for a second. “I can’t wait for you to be my new dad.” He had said with a cheeky grin and Agatha had responded by pushing him off of her with a hand planted firmly on his forehead. “Cheeky bugger.” She had said affectionately, ruffling his hair for good measure.

“Do you have a ring?”
“Not yet. I was wondering if you’d want to come with me to pick one.”
He stood up excitedly. “Um obviously! The only thing better than one gay picking out a ring is two gays picking out a ring!”
Agatha chuckled, she found his antics thoroughly endearing. “Calm down kid, we need to do this with cool heads so that we get it right.”
He flopped back down onto the sofa. “You’re right.” He said, putting on a calm exterior which lasted about two seconds before he was stood up again. “I’m sorry, I’m just so excited and happy.”
Agatha smiled widely. “Me too, Billy. Me too.”
God she loved this kid.

She took the ring with her to the restaurant to make sure she knew where it was at all times and wouldn’t be frantically looking for it when the time came, and she couldn’t resist taking out to look at it one last time before it was on Wanda’s finger where it belonged. The band was fairly simple, gold to accentuate the colour of the stone with three diamonds increasing in size embedded either side of the centre stone. The stone itself was red agate, polished to perfection and cut into a square with rounded corners. She had chosen agate because of what it represented: inner peace, emotional healing, and courage. All of the things she felt when she was with Wanda and the things that she hoped Wanda felt when she was with her.

She put the ring back in its box, and the box back in her clutch and went back to their table to finish the meal. She kissed Wanda’s cheek before sitting back in her chair, just in time for dessert to be brought out. They shared the huge slab of chocolate cake and finished their wine – Agatha had ordered the most expensive bottle – before Agatha paid and they went outside to wait for their Uber. Agatha sent a quick text to Billy letting him know that they were on their way home and that he had better be out of the house. He responded by sending a picture of him and his dad playing Mario Kart in his dad’s living room and she smiled. It was nearly time.

Knowing that they were going back to an empty house had made them both feel like randy teenagers and they had to fight to not start a steamy make-out session in the back of the Uber. Instead they resorted to playing with each other’s hands and occasionally putting a hand suggestively on the other’s thigh and whispering in each other’s ears.

When they got out of the car they couldn’t resist anymore, Wanda had Agatha pinned against the front door leaving hot kisses on her neck and nipping at her collar bone. “Wanda,” Agatha said breathlessly. “Wanda, we’re still on the outside.”
Wanda groaned but stopped, looking her in the eyes. “Then get your arse through that door.”
Agatha nodded and fumbled with her keys, nearly forgetting the entire purpose of the night. She turned the key but didn’t go in. “After you.”
Wanda planted one last kiss on her lips before opening the door and walking into the house.

She stopped after a few steps and turned back around to face Agatha, her mouth open in awe. “Did you do this?”
Agatha looked past her at the trail of rose petals on the floor, and candles on the end table that they had in the hall to the right of the archway that led into the living room. The only instructions that she had given her helpers were to make the living room the main event and to keep the bedroom classy, other than that they’d had free reign.
“Happy anniversary, baby.” She said, kissing Wanda. “Want to follow those petals?”
“Oh absolutely, but I need to get out of these shoes first.” Wanda said, already bending down to unbuckle them. Agatha laughed, doing the same and she let Wanda go ahead so that she could take the ring box out of her bag and put it into her trouser pocket.
“Oh my god!” She heard Wanda shout from the living room and she quickly followed, eager to see what Jen, Lilia and Billy had done.

The trail of petals turned into a huge heart in the centre of the floor. They had rearranged the furniture to make space, put real candles on the coffee table that was now to the right, and fake tea lights along the bookshelves. They had also draped fairy lights over the bookshelves which bathed the room in a soft, white light. ‘Nice Job, Musketeers.’ She thought.
Wanda pulled her into a tight hug. “Agatha, this is amazing.”
Agatha could hear the waver in her voice, indicating that she was close to crying. She pulled them apart and said, “there’s one more thing.” She spun Wanda around so that her back was to her and pointed to the bookcase in front of her. “Look on there.”

As Wanda walked forward, Agatha bent down onto one knee as quietly as she could.
“There’s nothing there.” Wanda said, confused.
“Oh, my bad. It’s the one on the opposite side.”
She watched Wanda turn around and take a second to find her, but when she looked down and saw Agatha on one knee holding the open ring box, she gasped and covered her mouth with both hands. Her eyes were shiny and reflected the fairy lights. Agatha was close to crying herself, but she had to hold it together for just a moment longer.

“Wanda Maximoff, you have brightened up my life in ways that words cannot describe. You and your son are my whole world and I don’t ever want to be without you both. I love you so deeply and nobody has ever made me feel the way that you do. Will you marry me?”
Wanda sank to her knees in front of her, tears now streaming down her cheeks. “Yes! Of course I will, yes!”
She took Wanda’s left hand and slid the ring onto her finger, it was a perfect fit. As soon as the ring was where it belonged, Agatha’s own tears spilled over.

Wanda spent a minute admiring the ring before looking back up at Agatha and saying through her tears, “I love you so fucking much Agatha Harkness.” She pulled her into a kiss, wet from both of their tears but full of passion nonetheless. When they broke apart Wanda breathlessly said, “Now take me to that bedroom.”
Agatha led her by the hand up the stairs, which were lined with more of the fake tea lights, and into their room.
There were more petals on the floor and on the bed and another string of fairy lights wrapped around the curtain rail. She was definitely going to have to take her Musketeers out for dinner to thank them for this.

Present Day

When Rio had first brought a coffee to their meetings and handed it to Agatha, it had confused her. No other student had done that, probably because they were scared that she would string them up if they got her order wrong… and they were correct. The drink that Rio confidently placed on her desk was, quite frankly, an abomination. It was a joke that besmirched the good name of coffee.
“What in god’s name is this?” Agatha asked, making no attempt to hide her disdain. Whipped cream had absolutely no place in coffee and neither did ice.
Rio shrugged, a smirk beginning to form on her lips. “Well I didn’t know your order, so I had to guess.”
“And you thought that this,” Agatha gestured unamusedly to the cup, “would be my drink of choice?”
The smirk was now full and there was a playful glint in Rio’s eyes to accompany it. “What do you mean? This is a perfectly good coffee.”
Agatha gave a long-suffering sigh, it was far too early in the morning for whatever the fuck Rio was doing.

Seemingly happy with the reaction that she had gotten, Rio dropped the smirk and swapped the cups. “Okay, you got me. This one is actually yours.” She put a handful of sugar packets on the desk next to it and sat down in her usual seat. “You don’t know what you’re missing though. This is really good.” She swiped her finger through the cream gathering it up before putting her finger in her mouth and sucking the cream off. She gave a satisfied hum as she took her finger out of her mouth. “Delicious.” She flashed Agatha a proud smile.

Agatha on the other hand was having a perfectly normal reaction to watching Rio eat cream off of her finger. It definitely wasn’t like a scene in a cheesy rom-com where the conventionally attractive female lead did something mundane that could be twisted into being sexual, and the editors decided to make that moment slow motion. Agatha absolutely experienced it in real-moving time.
She did not feel her pulse quicken or feel the heat starting to creep its way up her neck – and as for crossing her legs, well that was just something she did. There was nothing to read into where that was concerned. Most importantly, she definitely, with one hundred percent certainty, was not staring.

“You’re not subtle.” Rio’s voice snapped her out of the trance that she had slipped into.
“Excuse me?” She asked once she had come back to herself.
“I can tell that you’re jealous.” The smirk was back and Agatha was really starting to hate it.
She took the lid off of her cup needing to do something with her hands. “Of your coffee, if it can even be called that?” She took a sip. “If I drank that, I’m pretty sure the amount of sugar in it would kill me off.” She was well aware of the irony of her adding two sugars to her own coffee.

Rio snorted as she unwrapped her straw but was silent for a moment as she took a sip. The silence lasted all of about three glorious seconds. “I have a question for you.”
Agatha closed her eyes and took a breath. When she opened them again they were met with Rio’s and she swore she could see the sarcasm  that she was about to be met with in them.
“I am sure that I will regret this immediately, but go on.”
Rio smiled and Agatha was correct, she regretted it. “If you were a child of the gods, who would your parent be?”
Agatha just blinked at her. Where did that question come from? Usually there was something to prompt Rio’s ridiculous need to probe information out of her, but this was an odd one. Where was she going with this?

Agatha thought about it, mentally flicking through the rolodex of all the Greek gods she had in her head. There was Oizys the goddess of loneliness and misery but she felt a bit too on the nose.
Nyx the goddess of night who was said by Homer to be feared even by Zeus, Agatha enjoyed the sound of that a lot.
Artemis who was mostly known as the goddess of the hunt, nature and healing but was also known for her stubbornness which Agatha related to. However, Artemis didn’t have any children so technically it wouldn’t be possible.
An obvious one would be Athena, goddess of wisdom, warfare and handicraft, known for her smarts and tactical brilliance.

When she had first read The Odyssey, Agatha had been drawn to the idea of Athena. Having someone watching over her, protecting her and guiding her as she found her way through many dangers was very appealing to her. It might be an obvious answer, but it was the one that she kept coming back to.

The look on Rio’s face suggested that she was expecting some push back to the question, expecting Agatha to shoot her down like she usually did. But Agatha took this rare opportunity to catch Rio off guard.
“Athena. She was my favourite when I was a child.”
Rio’s brows lifted in surprise – she definitely hadn’t been expecting an answer, especially an answer with a shred of personal detail added to it. Agatha pursed her lips to hide the smile that was in danger of showing at her satisfaction.

The feeling didn’t last long because smugness started to settle back over Rio’s features. “Really?” She asked, all too snarky.
Agatha rolled her eyes at Rio’s impertinence. This woman was becoming way too comfortable in the way that she spoke to her and Agatha needed to shut it down before it became a problem. More of a problem.
“Miss Vidal, your tone is bordering on disrespectful. You asked me a question which I answered and I shan’t entertain this any further.” Her tone was clipped, asserting her dominance over the conversation but Rio’s face remained unchanged.

She heard Rio mutter something but couldn’t make it out. “Excuse me?”
Rio cleared her throat. “I said that I’d lean more towards Dionysus.”
Agatha crossed her arms and scoffed. “And why would that be?”
‘So much for not entertaining it.’ She chastised herself. But she couldn’t help it, she couldn’t resist biting.
“Because of your penchant for being dramatic.” Rio leaned back casually, her smile now showing her teeth as she moved her tongue on the inside of her cheek.

Agatha clenched her teeth and exhaled strongly through her nose fixing Rio with a glare, she needed to stop letting this woman, this student, get under her skin. Where did she get her audacity from?
“Let me ask you a question, Miss Vidal.”
Rio spread her arms. “Fire away.”
Agatha uncrossed her arms and adjusted her posture so that she was sitting straighter. “Did you adopt this casual manner when speaking with your previous teachers, lecturers and professors?”
Rio laughed and it ignited a fire in Agatha’s chest and she had to focus on not marching over to Rio, picking up that atrocious drink and throwing it over her.
“I did actually, yes.”
“And they just let you do it?”
“Well they didn’t complain so I’m inclined to say yes.” She crossed her legs and let her hands fall into her lap. “They were a lot more… laid back.”
“Laid back doesn’t achieve my results.” Agatha shot back, probably too quickly.

Rio hummed and gave a small smile. “That wasn’t a personal attack on you, professor. It was just an observation. Their results didn’t suffer for it though, I still got a first.”
Agatha took another sip of her coffee. She had left the lid off and her office wasn’t the warmest so it had quickly cooled down, and she had to hide her grimace as she swallowed the tepid liquid. “Well I am incredibly happy for them, but I think I shall stick to my own methods.”
Rio licked her lips slowly as if considering how she should respond, she nodded and said “fair enough,” taking her laptop out of her bag and turning her focus to that instead.

A couple of minutes passed with them both working and neither of them talking until Rio asked, “how’s the coffee?”
Agatha didn’t look at her as she replied. “It’s gone cold.” She saw Rio pick her own coffee up out of the corner of her eye and take a gratuitous sip.
“See, I don’t have that problem.” Agatha didn’t need to be looking at her to know that that fucking infuriating smirk was plastered on her face.
“Shut up.” Agatha said without thinking. Her eyes immediately went wide and darted to Rio who was stifling a laugh but remained looking at her laptop screen and, by the grace of god, she didn’t offer a retort.

If she had said that to any other student then she would be expecting to be summoned to the Dean’s office for yet another scolding, but since Rio hadn’t put in a complaint about her thus far, she felt that she didn’t need to worry. 

__________


The meetings with Rio started to follow a pattern: Rio would bring Agatha a coffee with her two sugars already stirred in, they would have a senseless discussion which would leave Agatha questioning if jail time was a valid option, and Rio would present her with work and research that had no right being as good as it was.

Rio continued her attempts to make Agatha “loosen up” – a direct quote that had made Agatha seethe when she had heard it – and Agatha continued to do nothing of the sort. She had no reason to ‘loosen up’, her way of teaching had worked for her entire career and there was no need to change. If it isn’t broken, why fix it?
She knew that Rio was speaking and acting in that way to get a rise out of her and she became better at not giving in since her usual biting remarks did nothing to dissuade Rio, in fact they only made it worse. If she wanted the upper hand then she was going to have to change her approach.

She had not reacted when Rio had called her “Prof” instead of the full word and delighted in the disappointment she saw in Rio’s eyes. She was becoming more attuned to Rio’s cockiness and was able to plot a path through the field of landmines that was laid at her feet whenever Rio walked into her office.

Not allowing herself to snap at Rio did mean that she had to let that annoyance out in other ways, and on other people. She had made the barista that failed to prepare her midday coffee in time cry when she had said: “as if working in a coffee shop on the campus of a university that you were not smart enough to actually attend wasn’t disappointing enough for your parents, you also cannot do the incredibly simple task of preparing said coffee.”

She earned herself a few more tips to the Dean’s office as the complaints trickled in, which she didn’t mind because she knew how to handle him. It was his secretary that she hated seeing, her shrill voice set Agatha’s teeth on edge every time that she spoke.
“Back again dear?” She basically screeched. “We might have to get you a desk next to mine at this rate so you don’t have as far to walk.”
It was an attempt at a joke that Agatha ignored, barely grunting a response in her direction.

During her Saturday nights with Lilia and Jen, they brought up the increasing amount of time that she spent being reprimanded by the Dean.
“What’s been going on with you lately?” Jen asked.
Agatha shrugged. “What do you mean?”
“I mean that you seem more…” She didn’t finish her sentence, probably unsure on how to phrase it.
“Wound up?” Lilia offered and Jen hummed her agreement.
Agatha took a drink of her wine. “I’m the same as always. People are just getting more sensitive.”
Jen and Lilia exchanged a look and Agatha couldn’t read what it meant which annoyed her. If they had something to say to her, then they should grow up and say it. “What?” She bit out. “Speak your minds.”

They looked at each other again and Lilia shook her head. “Fine I’ll say it then, coward.” Jen said to Lilia through gritted teeth. She turned to face Agatha and tried her best to keep her face neutral but Agatha could see the nervousness in the way her eye twitched.
“Is something going on with you and Wanda?”
Agatha’s eyebrows went skyward. She hadn’t expected that, she would never have expected that. “What on earth makes you ask that?”
Jen shuffled in her chair, looking to Lilia for some help and she finally piped up.
“We’ve just noticed that you’re behaving in a similar way to how you did when you broke up with her and, well, we’re worried about you.” She spoke quickly and Agatha looked at them both, taking in the concern on their faces.

Has she really been that bad? No, surely not. Yes, she had made that one person cry. Sure, she had told her final years that they were a waste of perfectly good oxygen. And yes, she may have walked directly into a student who was in her way as she was walking to her office. But that was normal behaviour for her, she had always been that way.
In the back of her mind, she knew that Rio was the reason that she was acting like this – however that was not a conversation that she wanted to have with them, she didn’t even want to have it with herself – but she was going to have to tell them something to get their minds away from Wanda because she couldn’t have them thinking that any longer.

She angled herself so that she could look at both of them as she spoke. “No, nothing is happening with Wanda. Nothing will happen with Wanda again, I want to make that perfectly clear.” She noticed them both relax a fraction. “I understand that you’re concerned, and maybe I can admit that I have been a little more… harsh of late. But I assure you that I am fine.” Her tone was direct but she kept her voice soft, checking their faces for a reaction.

They both smiled but it was Lilia who spoke first. “Okay so it’s not Wanda, that’s good. I was panicking for a second, I won’t lie.“ She chuckled. “Is it Billy?”
Agatha sighed and dipped her head slightly, she knew that they wouldn’t push if she told them not to. She could stop the questions right now, but she also knew that they were her friends and they were only asking because they cared. “No it’s not Billy. Things with Billy are going well actually.” She smiled at the thought of him. 
“But there is something?” Jen asked.

Agatha ran a hand through her hair, trying to think of a way to phrase her next sentence so that it wouldn’t make her sound like a lunatic. “It’s not any one thing. I guess I’ve just had a lot of pent-up… feelings.” It wasn’t incorrect, having to stifle her temper around Rio meant that she had to express it in other ways. She watched them as her words landed and she saw Lilia’s eyes widen comically. “Oh, I understand now!” She exclaimed, pointing at Agatha, and both Agatha and Jen looked at her expectantly, waiting for her to voice her thoughts. “She needs to get laid!”

Agatha groaned at the same time that Jen started cackling.
“Nope, no way. Shut that down right now.” Agatha said, giving them both pointed looks.
“No wait, I think she has a point.” Jen gasped out, recovering from the laughter that took over her. “It makes so much sense actually!”
Lilia reached out and grabbed Agatha’s hand. “Think of it as a research project. ‘Do orgasms help to make me less angry?’”
Agatha ripped her hand away and stood up. “I am done with both of you, I’m going home.”
Jen stood up as well and blocked her path out of the living room. “Hang on.” She said, putting both hands up to stop her and Agatha responded by crossing her arms and exhaling through her nose. Jen continued, “can we at least know who the lucky lady is that’s got you acting this way?”
Agatha rolled her eyes. “Goodbye, Jennifer.” She pushed her way past Jen and headed for the door. As she walked out she heard Lilia shout after her. “If you won’t tell us, we have our ways of finding out.”
She looked over her shoulder, firing back “fuck you both,” before shutting the door and getting into her car.

Agatha chuntered to herself the entire drive home and while she got ready for bed. They were both being absolutely ridiculous. She didn’t need to ‘get laid’, she needed Rio to stop pissing her off, she needed people to stop being incompetent, and she needed Rio to stop pissing her off.
Rio was the real problem here, not anything else. She needed to find a solution quickly before Lilia and Jen became unbearable.

She decided that in her next meeting with Rio, she would change the narrative. She was done with letting Rio run things. Her office was her turf and it was high time that she reclaimed it. 

__________


Agatha started the week strong, she didn’t make anybody cry, she didn’t reprimand her students – not unnecessarily anyway – and most importantly, she didn’t have to hear the vocal equivalent of nails scraping down a chalkboard coming from the Dean’s secretary. She didn’t verbalise her impatience when she had to wait yet again for her midday coffee – she did cross her arms and tap her foot in annoyance, but she wasn’t perfect.

She had decided that the best way to beat Rio was to join her, subscribing to the popular adage. Instead of pretending that Rio’s behaviour didn’t get to her, she simply just wouldn’t let it. If Rio was sarcastic and cocky, then Agatha would be sarcastic and cocky. If Rio acted brazenly, then Agatha would act brazenly. It would be easy.

Agatha sat in her office, but not at her desk like usual. She was sitting in the chair opposite the one that Rio favoured at the coffee table, with her laptop perched in her lap. As soon as the clock showed 9am she heard Rio’s knock at the door.
“You may enter.”
Rio entered the room holding two coffees like usual and held one out to Agatha. Usually Agatha would greet her with a polite “good morning” but Rio’s choice of clothes caught her eye. She was wearing a dark green jacket and black skinny jeans which was normal, but the white button-up was new.

Agatha’s eyes passed over the shirt as she took the coffee from Rio. “Did you put your best shirt on just to see me?”
Rio’s expression hardened. “I’m going to a funeral after this actually.”
Agatha gulped, she hadn't anticipated that. Everything had gone catastrophically wrong in an instant, this is why she wasn’t casual with her students!
The speed of her breathing was starting to increase until she saw the smile spreading across Rio’s face. “Just kidding. I need to do laundry, this was all I had left.” She sat down looking very pleased with herself.
Agatha made her expression neutral despite still feeling the shock. “Hilarious.” she deadpanned. “When tickets go on sale for your stand up comedy show, make sure you reserve a front row seat for me.”
Rio raised her eyebrows. “You’d want to be in the front row?”
“Of course!” Agatha said in mock seriousness. “I’d want to have the best view of you crashing and burning on stage.” She cocked her head slightly and tried her best to recreate the smirk that she’d seen Rio wear so many times.

Rio pushed her tongue against her cheek. “Touché, Professor. Touché.”
Agatha felt pride swell in her chest at the fact that she had managed to match Rio, maybe this would have its benefits after all. She shut her laptop and put it down on the coffee table. “Fortunately for you, comedy isn’t what we’re here to do. Where has your research taken you this week?” 

Rio reached into her bag and pulled out her laptop. “I think you’ll like this one. You inspired it, actually.”
Agatha held out her hand to take the laptop. “Oh, you flatter me, Miss Vidal.” She set the laptop on her knee and began scanning the work in front of her. It was all about Athena and the various ways that she has been portrayed.

She lifted her eyes to look at Rio again, who was sitting there with an expectant smile, but she didn’t say anything and carried on reading. The list of references was strong but there was one that she didn’t recognise. “What is this ‘Epic The Musical’ that you mention?”
Rio’s eyes lit up and Agatha felt something in her chest that she didn’t want to acknowledge. “You’ve never heard of Epic?” She asked, her eyes widening in disbelief.
Agatha chuckled. “I know that I have a wealth of knowledge that could rival an encyclopaedia, but there are some things that have not yet reached me.” She gave Rio her laptop back and relaxed in her chair. “Why don’t you educate me?”

Rio immediately launched into an explanation of Epic. She told Agatha about the concept of it and how the composer assigned specific instruments and motifs to each character and situation to represent them in the score. She spoke about how Athena was used in the narrative as well as the other gods, and Agatha couldn’t help but listen to her. The way she talked so excitedly about it was endearing and Agatha made a mental note to listen to it when she got home.

When Rio came to the end of her explanation, she sat back in her chair and gave Agatha a thoughtful look.
Agatha quirked an eyebrow. “Yes?”
Rio opened her mouth and closed it again before finally saying, “I think that was the longest you’ve ever let me speak without cutting me off. I’m not used to this feeling.”
Agatha scoffed. “You exaggerate, Miss Vidal. Maybe it’s you who is the child of Dionysus.”
“Nah, he’s too obvious. “ She said with a smile.
Agatha hummed her agreement and checked her watch. “There’s still some time left, do you have anything else to show me?”
Rio reached down into her bag. “Actually, I thought I could do more research while I’m here.” She pulled out a book. “If that’s okay with you?”
“I don’t see why not.” Agatha picked her own laptop back up and opened the word file that she was using before Rio got there.

Rio adjusted her position in her seat, getting comfy, and started reading her book. Agatha immediately zeroed in on the title. “Are you reading The Odyssey?”
Rio flipped the book round to look at the cover as if she’d forgotten what she was reading. “Yeah. I figured it was about time.”
Agatha couldn’t stop her mouth from dropping open slightly in surprise. “You’ve not read it before?” Rio shook her head. “You’ve just explained an entire musical to me that is based on The Odyssey but you’ve never read it?”
Rio shrugged. “I’ve never been to Pandora but I’ve seen Avatar.” Her lips quirked into a lazy, half smile as she turned the book back so that she could read it again, but Agatha couldn’t let it go. “The two are entirely different. The Odyssey is one of the oldest works of literature to still be read by a modern audience.” She had to consciously keep her voice at a respectable volume because she had strong feelings about this topic.
Rio sighed and rolled her eyes. “Oh my god will you relax, I’m reading it now aren't I?” She fixed Agatha with a pointed look. “Or at least I’m trying to.” Agatha saw the teasing grin and rolled her own eyes, she put her glasses on and brought her attention back to her laptop.

The time passed with them both sitting in comfortable silence. The only sounds were Agatha typing and Rio turning the pages, making the odd noise at what she was reading. Agatha desperately wanted to know which part of the story she was at and what her thoughts were so far, but she told herself to not distract her. They could discuss it later.
When she was about a quarter of the way through the book, Rio looked up at Agatha, Agatha didn’t see it happen but she could feel Rio’s eyes on her. She could feel the way that they were searching her, taking in all of the detail as they passed over her.

Knowing that Rio was looking at her intently made a warmth start to build in her stomach but she didn’t react to it, she didn’t want to think about it. Instead she said, “can I help you, Miss Vidal?” without looking up from her laptop.
Rio didn’t reply straight away, she shifted in the chair and Agatha now looked at her over the frame of her glasses. Was Rio uncomfortable about the fact that she had caught her looking at her?

“I was just wondering what you were doing.” Rio eventually said. Agatha lifted a brow – it wasn’t believable but she wasn’t going to press further.
“I’m writing the essay questions for the first year students.” She looked up at Rio properly.
Rio smiled. “So what I’m hearing right now is, I can find out what the questions are and tell the kids so that they can get a head start.” She wiggled her eyebrows.
Agatha laughed. “Surely you’re not suggesting that I let you help them cheat, Miss Vidal. As a PhD student there’s no way that would be the case, right?”
Rio leaned forwards, adopting a more serious look. “Oh no, of course not. I wouldn’t suggest anything of the sort, Professor.“ She said, feigning innocence. “But if I found out what the questions were and accidentally told them, I surely wouldn't be at fault for that.”
Agatha hummed in thought, tapping her finger against her lips for extra effect. “No. I’m pretty sure that would still be cheating.”
“And here I was, thinking that you were slowly starting to take a more laid-back approach to teaching.” Rio leaned back and smiled wide, proud of herself for referencing one of their past meetings.

Agatha chuckled. “‘Laid-back’ doesn’t equate to allowing cheating, Miss Vidal. Surely you’re smart enough to understand that?” As she spoke, she realised something. She was enjoying herself. Talking to Rio like this felt… fun? It was refreshing to not feel like she had to push back all the time and it definitely made conversing a whole lot easier. Maybe Rio had a point about being more relaxed, not that she would ever tell Rio that. Her ego didn’t need to be any bigger than it already was.

“Well, how about this?” Rio started, crossing her legs. “What if I wrote all of the essays first so that you had something to compare them to?”
“Oh, that’s not a bad idea actually.” Agatha saw Rio’s cocky, self-assured grin start to creep in before she continued. “Set the bar low so that there’s no way I can be disappointed further.” The way that the smile instantly dropped from Rio’s face gave Agatha a rush. She hadn’t really engaged in banter before, but she could get used to this.

Rio put a hand on her chest and feigned hurt. “Ouch. That’s no way to talk to a student, Professor. What would the Dean say?”
Agatha gave a curt laugh. “I can handle him.”
“I sense that there’s a story there.” Rio said curiously, but it wasn’t intended to goad her. For once it was simply just a statement that wasn’t requiring a follow up.
“Oh, there’s many stories. But we don’t have time for them right now.” She chuckled lightly.

Rio hummed and raised her arms above her head to stretch. As she did, the shirt she was wearing lifted up and revealed a small part of her stomach. If Agatha was staring she would have noticed that the tiny part that she could see was toned, a hint at what Rio’s abs would look like if she could see them fully. If she had been paying attention then the moan that left Rio’s mouth as the stretch set in would have made her stomach flutter and caused her to subconsciously cross her legs. But she wasn’t doing any of that so there was no reason to panic. No reason at all.

She managed to regain her composure as Rio settled again. “Comfortable?” She asked, having to force the nonchalance into her voice.
“Very.” Rio said, beginning to read again and Agatha went back to her laptop. “Let me know when we need to leave please, so that I can stop reading this horrible book.” She dead-panned, a hint of a smirk tugging at the corner of her lips.
“I’m glad that you find yourself funny, Rio.” It took Agatha a second to realise that she hadn’t said Miss Vidal and had, in fact, called her by her first name. When it hit her, her head shot up to look at Rio who was looking at her equally surprised. Agatha cleared her throat and corrected herself. “Miss Vidal.”
Rio gave a small nod in acknowledgement and went back to her book, and Agatha tried her best to sneakily check her watch. There was still fifteen minutes left, she could handle fifteen minutes.

Each minute felt like an hour as she waited for the reminder on her phone to ping, she had typed out the same question five times just to make it look like she was doing something while she was very obviously distracted. When the reminder finally went off, she was so far in her own thoughts that it made her jump.
She heard Rio snort. ‘Of course she saw that.’ She thought.
“I take it that’s our cue to leave?” Rio asked, a hint of laughter in her tone as she turned the corner of her page and closed the book.

Agatha removed her glasses and stared at Rio in disbelief. “I’m sorry, did you just dog ear the page?”
Rio rolled her eyes. “Oh please don’t say that you’re one of those people.”
“By ‘those people’ I’m assuming you mean people who look after their books?” Agatha crossed her arms, getting defensive.
Rio mimicked her pose which made her clench her jaw. “Are you that desperate for an argument right now?”
“Watch your tone.”
Rio scoffed, hurriedly put the book and her laptop back into her bag and stood up, slinging the bag over her shoulder. “I don’t understand you. One minute you’re fine and the nex-”
“Miss Vidal.” Agatha cut her off, her voice low but authoritative, and stood up as well. “I implore you to think carefully about the next words you say.”

Rio shifted her weight between her feet. Was she actually considering what to say next? “How am I supposed to have a conversation with you if you change the rules on a whim?”
Agatha narrowed her eyes. “Let me make one thing perfectly clear, Miss Vidal. We are not, and never will be, friends. I am your professor, you are my student and our relationship will remain as such. I am well within my right to put a stop to any conversation if I feel it is inappropriate and I have already let you get away with a damn sight more than I would have any other student.” She saw something settle over Rio’s features but couldn’t place what it was. “Now, are you going to keep questioning me and make me late for my lecture, or are you going to concede so that we both may leave?”

Rio sighed and ran a hand through her hair. The act made her shirt ride up again and Agatha had to force herself to remain looking at her face. “You’re right, I apologise.” She made her way to the door. “I wouldn’t want to make the great Professor Harkness late for a lecture.”
Agatha rolled her eyes as Rio walked out and then pressed her palms to her eyes. This woman would be the death of her.

___________


Agatha wasn’t well, she couldn’t be. She hadn’t been sleeping properly, she was nauseous and her head was pounding. She got herself an emergency appointment with her GP only for him to tell her that there was nothing wrong with her except maybe lack of sleep. He had asked if there had been a new instance of stress introduced into her life recently and she had scoffed and said, “Rio Vidal.” Then he’d had the nerve to ask if Rio was a new ‘romantic partner’ at which she had laughed and said “absolutely not.” What an absurd question to ask.

Anything she had felt when she watched Rio eat the cream or when her shirt had ridden up were perfectly normal things to feel. They were abstractly attractive things and had nothing to do with the person that was doing them, and as for that godforsaken dream? Well it didn’t mean a thing. Her subconscious had picked a random face out of the thousands that she had seen and it could just have easily been any one of them, reading into it was pointless. She was human and these were just things that humans did.

His incredible stupidity aside, her doctor had helped her to identify Rio as her problem and she decided that the best thing to do would be to put a stop to their meetings. They were clearly causing her more stress than she could handle and who was she to ignore the things that her body was telling her? When she got home she sent Rio an email.

Dear Miss Vidal,

Upon much consideration I have decided that you no longer require weekly meetings, so I am terminating them.
Please feel free to send anything you wish for me to look over and I shall make my best efforts to get back to you in a timely fashion.

Sincerely
Professor Harkness

She felt a sense of relief as the whoosh sound of the email sending played through her laptop speakers – now there was one less thing occupying her mind.
Agatha ran herself a bath, feeling the tension she usually carried in her shoulders ease slightly as she slipped into the warm water, and brought her wine glass to her lips. She allowed herself to close her eyes and have a few moments where her mind was clear and she felt relaxed, the only sounds being the bubbles softly popping and the crackle of the WoodWick candle she had lit on the windowsill.
She hadn’t had a bath in a while and had forgotten how necessary they were to maintain her composed nature. This is what she needed, less Rio and more baths.

She must have dozed off because when she opened her eyes again, the bubbles were gone and the water had gone cold. Now shivering, and her neck feeling sore, she drained the bath and went into her bedroom to dry herself off and wrap herself in her fluffy dressing gown. She looked at her phone to check the time but instead saw a message notification, the name ridding her of her previously relaxed state.

Maximoff: Billy told me that you wanted to talk.

She scowled. She knew that this was going to happen at some point, but she refused to be the one to initiate it. She was surprised that it had taken Wanda this long. Billy better not have phrased it that way though, or she would be having words with him the following day.

Agatha: He asked me if I would talk to you and I said that I would.

She needed to clear that up right away, she needed Wanda to know that this was not her decision, nor was it really her choice. She would be doing this for Billy and that was the only reason.

Maximoff: When and where?

Agatha hadn’t expected Wanda to let her have this much control so she took her time to ponder the question. ‘When’ was simple, getting it over and done with was preferable so tomorrow it was. As for ‘where’, she had no idea.
Definitely not somewhere public, she wouldn’t allow Wanda the comfort of having a crowd there to tame her bite. They could use an empty room like she had with Billy, but that opened up the risk of someone walking in, or walking past and hearing them – and Agatha wasn’t going to let those people that had poked their noses where they didn’t belong, have access to any more gossip concerning her.
They could use her office, but that denied Agatha the chance to make a quick, or dramatic, exit should she need to.
Wanda’s office wasn’t a bad location. It was tucked out of the way down one of the less frequented corridors which meant it was less likely that their conversation would be caught by the wrong ears. Agatha just had to get over the fact that the idea of being in Wanda’s office made her feel sick, and she would be fine.

Agatha: Tomorrow 9:30, your office.

Maximoff: Okay.

__________


 Agatha woke the next morning with a sense of determination. She had told Billy that she would talk to his mother, she never said anything about how she would talk to her, nor did she make any promises that it would go well.
She put care into her outfit choice for the day, picking out a top that she knew Wanda liked and paired it with trousers that clung to her hips just right. She sprayed herself with perfume that Wanda had once loved and she was happy in the knowledge that she was going to make Wanda suffer.

She strode onto campus and into her office with a smile that showed no sign of wavering. She was going to tackle this head on and finally put to bed any further attempts that Wanda might make to get her attention. This would be a good thing for her and no matter how the conversation went, she would come out as the winner.

She made her way to Wanda’s office, walking the corridors that she had avoided for two and a half years, walking past offices and rooms that she hadn’t given thought to in such a long time. She turned a corner and was face-to-face with the door of Wanda’s office. Now she was faced with a dilemma: should she knock, or should she just walk in?
Wanda knew that she would be there, obviously, so was a knock necessary? If she was to be the victor of whatever was about to happen then she would have to maintain the air of decorum whilst slapping Wanda down with her underhand.
She knocked.

A few seconds passed before Wanda’s annoyingly bright voice was heard through the door. “Come in.”
Agatha took a deep breath and pushed the door open, her smile overly friendly and her voice way too saccharine. “Well, what a pleasure it is to see you Ms. Maximoff.”
Wanda was sitting at her desk, eyes fixed on the door as Agatha walked through it. Her smile was tight before she spoke. “Feel free to have a seat if you would like.”
Agatha looked at the chairs, but remained standing. “I’m fine for now, thank you.” She put her hands in her trouser pockets to hide the fact that she was having to fight against balling them into fists to keep her grounded. “What would you like to talk about?”
She saw Wanda’s eyes follow the movement of her hands and realised that she knew what she was doing. Wanda was still annoyingly in tune with her and Agatha hated that.

Wanda took a shaky breath, clearly making a lot less effort than Agatha was to hide her nervousness. “Given the fact that my son is now one of your students, I thought it would be best if we could try and reach a level of civility to make it as easy for him as possible during his time at this university.”
Agatha could tell that was a front, hiding what Wanda really wanted to say, but she would play this game. “Of course. I would hate for Billy to feel like he’s caught in the middle of our past, Ms Maximoff.” She kept her voice sweet, knowing full well that both her tone and her choice of words would come across as fake. She did mean it though, she didn’t want Billy to be bearing the weight of her and Wanda’s past.

Wanda smiled, it was polite but it wasn’t a real smile. “You can drop the niceties, Agatha. I think we both know that you don’t mean them.” She leant forward and steepled her hands on her desk. “What do you need from me in order to make this work?”
Agatha took a slow step forwards, bringing her a few inches closer to Wanda. “What are you willing to offer?”
“No.” It was only one word, but it was weighted. Wanda was putting her foot down.
Agatha lifted an eyebrow. “No?”
“No.” Wanda repeated. “I’m not playing games, Agatha, not where my son is concerned.”
Agatha had to laugh, she couldn’t help it. Wanda really couldn’t stop herself from telling lie after lie. “The same son that you begged to ask me to speak to you?” Agatha didn’t know if that was the truth, she had guessed that Billy might have had a push from his mother, but Wanda didn’t need to know that. “You don’t seem so bothered about games when you’re the one orchestrating them, Wanda.” She added an extra bite to the way that she said Wanda’s name. She wanted to say more but this was a dance that she was choreographing on the spot, so it had to be done carefully.

A hint of hurt made its way onto Wanda’s face letting Agatha know that her words had landed right where she had wanted them to. “What do you need, Agatha?” She repeated her question, her voice level but betrayed by a slight waver as she said Agatha’s name.
Whoever had done the surgery to reinforce Wanda’s spine hadn’t done a very good job, she was cracking already, and Agatha could feel a smile tugging at the corners of her mouth. “Why don’t you start by telling me why you wanted to speak to me?”
Wanda sighed. “I’ve already told you, Billy is-”
Agatha held up a hand, cutting her off. “Yes I heard that, but come on Wanda, we both know that isn’t the truth, don’t we?” She held Wanda’s gaze in her own, daring her to look away.

Wanda tensed her jaw and took a long breath, in and out through her nose. But to her credit, she didn’t look away from Agatha’s eyes. “Okay. Fine.” She spoke each word with precision, clearly unhappy about the fact that her lie had been caught out so quickly. “In order to fix my relationship with my son, I have to at least try to fix my relationship with you.” She sat up straight. “Does that suffice?”
Agatha took another step closer. She was barely having to try and Wanda was coming apart at the seams, this would be easier than she thought. Wanda had left a thread dangling in front of her, she had to see what would happen if she gave it a gentle tug. “Oh so it’s not about Billy at all then, not really.”
“Excuse me?”

She took one of her hands out of her pocket and pointed at Wanda pulling on the thread again. “This is all about making yourself feel better. You want to fix your relationship with Billy for you, not for him.” She tucked her hand back into her pocket.
Wanda stuttered, probably trying to form her next lie. “No that- I’m not- it isn’t-” She clamped her mouth shut and Agatha took another step forward.
“No, no, go on. Talk your way out of it.”
Wanda narrowed her eyes and Agatha felt the satisfaction settling into her, she was getting to her. “I am not going to sit here and let you verbally assault me, Agatha.”
Without missing a beat Agatha said, “stand up then,” and she finally let the smile that she had earlier stifled come to life. It was steeped in smugness that she was making no effort to hide, Wanda was right where she wanted her.

Wanda threw her hands up, exasperated. “What do you want from me? Do you want an apology, do you want me to say that I know that I fucked up and that I wish I could take it all back? Because I do!” Her voice had gotten louder as she was speaking which made Agatha do the opposite. She kept her voice low and controlled, channelling all of her anger into her hands as she balled them tightly in her pockets and took another step.

She spoke slowly, making sure every word was delivered perfectly. “Let me see if I’ve got this right. Not only do you use your son to emotionally manipulate me into speaking to you, you cheat on me, not once, not twice, but three times. You lie to everybody including your son, telling them that the reason we broke up was because of my infidelity. You get to play the part of the woman grieving a relationship and get everybody’s love and support, whilst I am cast into the shadows and made into a social pariah. And you think an apology is going to cut it?” She shook her head and gave a humourless laugh.

Wanda’s face dropped, her mouth hanging open slightly as the shock of Agatha’s words set in. “H- How did you…?” She trailed off, clearly unable to find her words.
Agatha raised her brows. “How did I what, Wanda?” She took a final step forward, now at the edge of Wanda’s desk. “How did I know about the other two times that you slept with someone else while we were in a relationship?” She removed her hands from her pockets and put them on Wanda’s desk, supporting herself as she leaned forward and looked Wanda directly in her eyes. “Well you can thank your darling ex-husband for that. I suppose the guilt weighed heavier on him than it did you.” She gave the surface a tap. “Oh the things this poor desk has endured.”

That was the final tug, the thread had been pulled free and all of Wanda’s lies had been unveiled. Agatha had been holding on to that knowledge for nearly two years and it felt so good to finally get to use it, to finally lay it out in front of Wanda and use it to break her down. “I am curious about one more thing, though.” She said, standing back upright. Wanda didn’t respond, she just gulped so Agatha continued. “You say that you’re desperate to fix your relationship with Billy, but did you tell him the whole story about why I came home that day?” Wanda opened her mouth to respond but Agatha held up her hand, silencing her. “Don’t bother. I already know the truth, and quite frankly I do not trust you to tell it. But maybe I’ll tell him. He has a right to know.”

Wanda shot out of her chair, looking frantic. “Agatha don’t.”
Agatha quirked her eyebrow, a smirk forming. “Are you going to tell him?” Wanda dropped her head, looking at the floor and Agatha shot another barb at her. “Of course not. You’re pathetic.”
“If I have any hope of repairing my relationship with him, he can’t know. It’ll only make it worse.” Wanda’s voice was meek and when she raised her head again her eyes were shiny. “Please Agatha. Don’t do that to him.”

Agatha scoffed and it turned into a dark laugh. “You’re still using him to get what you want.” She jabbed a finger at Wanda. “Can you really not see how monumentally fucked up that is Wanda?”
Agatha rolled her eyes when she saw Wanda’s tears starting to fall. “Don’t start with that bullshit, we both know it’s not real.” She crossed her arms. “I won’t tell him but I want it to be perfectly clear that I am doing it for him and not for you. Do you understand?” Wanda nodded. “Good. You can tell him that we are now on civil terms, or whatever the fuck you need to tell him to get yourself back into his good books, but if you fuck up where he is concerned again then he will find out. Am I clear?”
“Yes.”
“Well done. Now you can reflect on why you needed to be blackmailed into being a good mother. Have a nice day, Wanda.”
With that, Agatha turned and walked out of the room. She would be riding this high for the rest of the week.
