Rio

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio was cooking dinner for herself, alone, on a Saturday night. She really missed the big family meals that would happen almost every weekend at home. She missed hearing her abuela telling her cousins that they weren’t allowed in her kitchen because they couldn’t be trusted to boil water, never mind cook a full meal. She missed hearing the Spanglish bullshit echoing around whoever’s house they were in. She even missed it when her uncle would say something slightly homophobic and then ask her if it was still okay to say. He meant well, and he did try – most of the time – but he was also someone who believed everything he read on Facebook, so he had to be taken with a pinch of salt.
Every family has one.

She had facetimed with her friends and her parents a few times and that had helped to fill the void a little bit, but it didn’t get rid of it. She knew that moving to England was a big step and that being so far away from home – from everything and everyone that she knew – would be hard, but she hadn’t expected to miss it this much or this quickly. She had hoped that she would have been too busy to really think about it, but her PhD was starting slowly and wasn’t occupying her mind nearly enough.

There was Alice and Billy who she was really starting to get along with and they were the only people that she had really talked to, but at the end of the day they were teenagers and she was thirty. She'd need to find some friends her own age at some point, ones that wouldn't be able to out drink her and put her to shame. 

During her masters she had become friends with her lecturers more than her fellow students, she would find herself at a bar with them most nights – and woken up next to one of them the following morning – but she couldn't see that happening with any of the staff this time. Not right now at least. 
Well, maybe Wanda. Wanda had definitely been flirting with her, right? She hadn't made that up. 

She was still early in her efforts to get to know Agatha so she couldn't say for certain how that would go. Agatha struck her as the type of person one has to work at. Steadily chip away at the hard exterior to reveal the truth underneath, but would Agatha be willing to let that happen? Only time would tell. Rio was determined to get into her good books either way, it was vital to her survival as one of Agatha's students. 
When she had finished eating, she opened her laptop and started doing the research to bring to her next meeting with Agatha. Hades and Persephone had been on her mind since Agatha’s lecture about them so she decided to start there, and it didn’t take long for her to be engrossed in it. She worked until the early hours of the morning and only stopped because her eyes were starting to hurt and none of the words were making sense anymore. 

__________

There was a monotony to the following few days and Rio couldn't help feeling bored. She had taken some more trips to the garden centre and her flat was slowly filling up with the various plants that she had bought to fill the space, adding colour to the otherwise quite bare living quarters that she was spending her time in. During her last call to her parents they had said that they'd send some more of her books and other creature comforts over to help the apartment feel more lived-in, and she hoped that having more pieces of home around her would help to break her out of the slump that she was currently stuck in. 

She woke up on Wednesday morning ready to have her first official meeting with Agatha. She had arranged her notes on Hades and Persephone into a powerpoint presentation, a study technique that she had adopted during her undergrad. The idea was given to her by her girlfriend at the time and had been the only positive thing that she had taken away from that relationship.

She gave Agatha her laptop so that she could look over her notes and watched her eyes widen as she took it in. Rio hoped that the surprise on Agatha’s face was the good kind and not her realising that she had made a mistake in taking Rio on.
“Miss Vidal, this is–”
Rio spoke over her, feeling the need to defend herself before she even had a reason to. “I know, it’s a lot. And I know a powerpoint is strange but it helps me arrange my thoughts better.”
“I have to say tha–” Agatha tried to continue but again, Rio jumped in.
“Oh, I know the writing leaves some things to be desired but this is just notes and nothing is set in stone yet.”
She stopped speaking when Agatha held up her hand, the universally recognised sign for ‘shut the fuck up.’

When Agatha spoke, her voice was commanding and Rio knew that she was keeping her tone neutral on purpose. “Miss Vidal, are you going to let me speak?”
Rio didn’t respond, she wasn’t sure her voice would work if she tried because her mouth had suddenly gone very dry.
“Thank you. This is good work. I can tell that you’ve put effort into this and that you haven’t haphazardly thrown it together. Your list of sources is good and the information is laid out nicely.”
She took Agatha’s praise but remained silent, part of her was waiting for Agatha’s permission to speak, the other part of her was trying to not think about the fact that she was waiting for Agatha to give her that permission.

Agatha was an attractive woman, any creature with eyes could corroborate that fact, but Rio wasn’t usually the type to be made speechless by an attractive woman. If anything she preferred to talk to them, to find out what made them tick and which buttons she could press to elicit the reactions that she wanted – even if they weren’t actually her type and her goal wasn't to sleep with them. Flirting as a general act was fun to take part in. Sure there were things that women could say or do that would cause her brain to buffer, but she wasn’t often left without a clever retort or flirty answer on the tip of her tongue. Had it really been long enough that she had lost her game?

Rio watched Agatha lean back in her chair before saying, “you may speak,” and she dropped some of the tension sitting in her shoulders. “Thank you, Professor.” She forced out and adjusted herself in her seat as a feeling sank low in her stomach. She cleared her throat to try and get her voice to sound normal again. “I also started doing some research on Orpheus and Eurydice on the back of this because of the musical Hadestown, and how it links them in with Hades and Persephone. I don’t know if you’ve heard of it, but it's really good.” She had no idea if Agatha was a musical theater kind of person so this could fall flat, but she felt more at ease when Agatha said that she was familiar with it.

Agatha gave Rio her laptop back. “Do you think you could do it?” She asked.
Rio’s brow creased in confusion. “Do what?”
She watched Agatha stand up from her desk and make her way to sit in the chair opposite the one she was currently in.
“Do you think you could lead Eurydice back to the surface and not turn around? Or Orpheus, I don’t know your preferences.”
The last part sounded like an afterthought and Rio couldn’t help but wonder if Agatha was not-so-subtly trying to figure out her sexuality.

It wasn’t something that she hid, she’d never had a reason to. She knew that she was incredibly lucky to have parents who had accepted her without question when she came out, and her abuela had said “as long as you let me meet your girlfriends so that I can make sure they’re right for my granddaughter, I don’t have any problems.” Rio had made good on that promise and let her abuela interrogate every one of her girlfriends. Upon reflection, that was probably the reason that many of her relationships hadn’t lasted much longer past that point – but if they couldn’t handle her abuela then the relationship wasn’t going to work anyway.
She chuckled at Agatha’s thinly veiled attempt at nonchalance. “I would be leading Eurydice.

But I honestly don’t know if I would be able to do it. I think I would be too in my head, like Orpheus was.” Her eyes met Agatha’s and she took in the vivid blue for a second before asking, “what about you?”
Agatha gave the question some thought and Rio patiently waited for her answer. She enjoyed these kinds of conversations, they were a good way to get to know someone, how they think, how they view certain things. Much better than generic small talk.
“I’ve never really thought about it. I suppose if I loved someone the way that Orpheus loved Eurydice I would definitely give it a go.”
The way that Agatha worded her answer caught Rio’s attention. “The way that Orpheus loved Eurydice.” Was Agatha saying that she would be Orpheus in that situation? Rio had been forthcoming with her answer so maybe Agatha was returning that.
“So you would be leading Eurydice too?”
“That is an extremely personal question, Miss Vidal. One that has no place in our meetings.”

Rio’s smirk faded as quickly as it had appeared at the tone of Agatha’s voice. It was the kind of tone that you didn’t argue with, the kind of tone that let you know that she was the one in charge, the kind of tone that Rio couldn’t tell if she wanted to comply with or act against.
One of her exes had called her a brat because of her need to challenge everything, and her ability to always have answers ready – that had led to a wonderfully long night.
But she still had no idea where she stood with Agatha, she was hard to figure out which made Rio want to try harder. She was avoiding her eyes as she could feel them on her, likely trying to read her reaction. 

When Agatha spoke, some of the chill had been removed from her voice but it was still hard. “I like to keep my personal and professional lives separate. I apologise for snapping.”
It was a fair statement, one that most professionals followed, however Rio found it slightly odd. Earlier Agatha had basically asked her if she was into men or women, but when she was faced with the same question her reaction had been defensive. Rio wasn’t one to let the ‘one rule for you, one rule for myself’ attitude slide, she never had been, so she had to push back a little.
“You didn’t seem too concerned with the separation of personal from professional when you asked me.” The corners of her mouth lifted slightly knowing that Agatha wouldn’t be expecting this response.
“I beg your pardon.”
“You asked me what my preferences were. How come personal questions are only off the table when they’re about you?” She lazily leaned back in her chair.

Agatha’s attempt to not rise to Rio’s challenge gave Rio a feeling of satisfaction that sat in her chest and warmed her skin, she was starting to enjoy this.
“You offered that information up freely, Miss Vidal. It isn’t my fault that you didn’t keep it to yourself.”
Rio recognised this defensiveness, she had seen it in many people throughout her life; she had seen it in herself. The need to hide, the fear of being known and Agatha wore her defensiveness like armour. But all armour has a weak spot and Rio was willing to work at finding Agatha’s, so she took a wild shot.
“I didn’t feel the need to keep it to myself. I’m not ashamed of it.”
“I’m not sure that I know what you’re implying, Miss Vidal.” Agatha’s jaw was clenched and Rio could see the redness slowly making its way up her neck. The shot had landed, now she just needed to make sure that it stuck. She crossed her arms as she said, “I’m not implying anything. I am simply offering information up freely.”

Agatha took a deep breath and caught Rio’s eyes with her own, her displeasure at the conversation evident in the way that they narrowed. “We have wondered spectacularly off topic. None of this has anything to do with Greek Mythology, and since that’s why we’re here, I think it would be appropriate for us to continue in that direction. Don’t you agree?”
Rio let her smile drop and adjusted her position in her seat to be sitting up straight before replying. “Of course, you’re right. My apologies Professor.” She knew that if she pushed too far straight away, it would end up having the opposite effect to the one that she wanted. This was a delicate game that she had played many times with her professors in the past, though none of them had been this difficult but she liked a challenge.

Agatha leaned back, adopting a more casual posture. “Do you have a structure for your research, or is it just whatever takes your fancy in the moment?”
“I don’t have a structure as such, but I’m working on it.” Rio leaned forwards, resting her elbows on her thighs. “That’s the thing I tend to have trouble with actually.” Her eyes were drawn to the movement of Agatha uncrossing and recrossing her legs. She saw a hint of something black and light blue on her ankle, peeking out over the top of her heeled shoe. A tattoo. Rio filed the information away to ask about at a later date and brought her eyes back up to look at Agatha’s face again.

They spent some time discussing the structure of her thesis and the areas that she struggled with. It was a slight source of embarrassment for Rio, the thing that she always lost marks on. Not enough to make her worry about not getting a high grade, but enough that the perfect mark she strived to achieve was always just out of reach. She had always rejected the help offered to her because she felt that she should be able to do something this basic by herself, if she couldn’t then she didn’t deserve the marks that she got. But Agatha offering to help felt different, it didn’t feel like she was speaking down to her or viewing her as less than because she struggled with this basic concept of writing. It was purely because she wanted to help and wanted Rio to achieve her full potential.

After asking Rio to bring all of the notes that she had made thus far to their next meeting, Agatha checked her watch and asked if there was anything else she wanted to discuss with the remainder of their time.
Rio thought for a minute, she had already stepped too close to the line so she needed to take a few paces back. “What piqued your interest in Greek Mythology?”
The question was innocent enough and could be linked back to her thesis so Rio thought that it was a happy medium. The way that Agatha sighed, however, alerted her to the fact that she was wrong.
“I meant about your thesis, Miss Vidal.”
“This is for my thesis.” Rio insisted.
Agatha spread her arms out. “Please, enlighten me.”
“You haven’t read Percy Jackson which is, to use your own words, a gateway drug. So what piece of media opened your mind to it?”

There was a beat of silence as Agatha thought about the question. Rio wished that she could hear her thoughts, wished that she could know what was going on in Agatha’s head as she formed her response. Would she answer truthfully, or would she just say something to get Rio off of her back and shut the question down?
“My mother read The Odyssey to me when I was a child.” Agatha said in a matter-of-fact tone like she was trying to keep any emotional link out of the sentence.
Rio couldn’t hide her surprise, her eyebrows shooting up involuntarily. “Oh wow, one of the OGs.

How old were you?”
She watched Agatha adjust herself, any semblance of a casual nature removed as she straightened her back and hardened her features. “This is getting personal again, Miss Vidal.”

Rio huffed and dropped her head, shaking it. She didn’t care to hide how the way Agatha had spoken had annoyed her – it was no wonder that she had so many complaints against her. At first Rio had thought that it was just people being overly sensitive and not being able to take criticism, or expecting to be mollycoddled through their degrees and being unable to face the harsh reality, but if this was how Agatha spoke to all of her students then she could understand it a bit more. She wouldn’t complain though, clearly the previous complaints had not had the effect that was hoped of them. She wouldn’t be surprised if they’d managed to make it worse, if they’d only made Agatha double down on it and really earn them.

When Agatha spoke again, there was an edge to her voice, a coldness seeping into the words. “I am not in the business of discussing myself or my life with my students, Miss Vidal. I am your supervisor and our meetings are in place to work on your thesis and, when it comes to it, your viva.”
Rio looked at her again and mimicked her straight-backed posture. “I’m not trying to pry into your personal life, Professor. Surely you can see why inquiring as to how you found your interest in Greek Mythology to the point where you wanted to teach other people about it, is relevant to my thesis. You don’t have to tell me your life story but a discussion requires both parties to be able to share information that relates to the topic at hand.” She tried to keep her voice steady and her tone flat but she couldn’t stop the bite that curled around the edges of her words, nor did she want to. She would match the way that Agatha had spoken to her, something she was sure was a rare occurrence for Agatha.

Agatha tensed her jaw and narrowed her eyes, her voice dropping low. “I do not take kindly to being told off by a subordinate, Miss Vidal.”
“And I don’t take kindly to being spoken down to by someone who thinks their title gives them the right to.” Rio didn’t miss a beat in her response, making sure every word landed where she wanted it to.
“If you cannot respect me as your superior, Miss Vidal, then I suggest that you find a new supervisor.” Agatha’s voice was slowly starting to increase in volume and her eyes were starting to burn with intensity.

Rio scoffed but kept her voice level when she spoke. “When you give me a reason to respect you, Professor Harkness , you shall have it.” She knew that Agatha would recognise the reference to their first meeting and hoped that the way she spat her name would carry the weight that she intended. She didn’t mind Agatha calling her Miss Vidal, she knew that it was a polite yet professional way to address her, but the way that Agatha used it when she was trying to assert her authority over her made her skin prickle.

Rio was officially done entertaining this conversation – no, this chastisement – so she stood up and threw her laptop into her bag.
“Miss Vidal, sit back down.”
Agatha’s command caused something in Rio to snap. She could no longer keep her voice down, she didn’t want to keep her voice down. “No! Other people might allow you to speak to them in this way, but I won’t. Your reputation at this university might be good, but it does not give you the right to talk to people like they are beneath you. Like I said before, you aren't the only lecturer that I wanted to be my supervisor so I will gladly go and find her.” She was once again holding the empty threat of Wanda Maximoff over Agatha’s head, and she hoped to god that Agatha never called her bluff because then she would be truly fucked. She had no idea what the shelf life of this threat was and she knew that she probably wouldn’t be able to use it again any time soon, but it was the only thing she had at the moment that could give Agatha pause. She was also desperate to know what exactly it was about Wanda Maximoff that made Agatha panic this much, but that would have to wait.

Rio started towards the door, her hand firmly on the handle already trying to prepare her words to beg Wanda to take her on when she heard Agatha call after her.
“Wait.”
She stopped, but didn’t turn around. “What?”
The seconds ticked by as silence stretched between them. Rio refused to turn around until Agatha gave her a reason to, she was ready to just walk out if Agatha didn’t speak soon.
Right as Rio had reached the end of her tether, Agatha spoke, her voice quiet, merely a ghost of the way she had spoken only moments ago.
“I’m sorry.”
Rio’s immediate response was laughter, it was the only way that she could express her disbelief at Agatha’s pathetic choice of words. “Are you being fucking serious?” She dropped her hand and finally turned around. “You accuse me of prying into your personal life, talk down to me, call me a fucking subordinate and the best you can come up with is ‘I’m sorry’?” She shook her head, still laughing.

Agatha was grasping at straws, she had to be. There’s no other way that she would be resorting to a simple ‘I’m sorry,’ if she had anything else to try, any other words to throw out. She made this evident with her next question. “Well what do you want me to say?” It wasn’t a question that was open to a reply so she continued. “Do you want me to beg for your forgiveness? Because I can assure you, Miss Vidal, that will not be happening.”
Rio didn’t want her to beg for her forgiveness, that wasn’t her goal. She just wanted to have a conversation with Agatha, to talk like normal people and get to know each other a little bit – just basic things that humans did when they interacted, especially if she was to spend at least three years at this university, at least three years with Agatha as her supervisor.

Rio slowly stepped towards Agatha. “Answer my question.”
“Which one?”
“How old were you when you read The Odyssey?”
Rio heard the way that Agatha asked if she was serious. She heard the questioning tone, she saw the way Agatha’s eyebrow raised in disbelief but she just waited. If Agatha didn’t answer her then she would leave, and this would be the end of the odd meetings, the strange conversations and the annoying interactions; and Rio would be left without a supervisor, but that was better than whatever the fuck this was.

After some time of the only sound being the faint hum of people talking as they walked past Agatha’s office, and the steady click of the clock on the wall, she eventually answered. “Ten. I was ten years old. Are you happy now?”
Rio felt a wave of satisfaction wash over her and felt the corners of her mouth lift slightly. She had to admit that she did get a certain amount of joy from pushing people and she suspected that Agatha felt the same, which is why she was so unwilling to let it happen to her. Agatha was used to being the one who was in charge, the one who got her way, the one who always came out on top and that ignited something within Rio. Maybe she wouldn’t be beating the ‘bratty’ allegations any time soon.

Agatha clenched her jaw and tightened the cross of her arms. “I’m not sure what you hoped to achieve with this, Miss Vidal, but I assure you that this is the first and last time anything like this will happen. I do not share personal information with students and I am the one who gets to determine what classes as personal information. Now stop acting like a child.”
Rio’s eyes widened in surprise. “I’m acting like a child? You’re the one that threw a tantrum when I asked you a basic question about yourself.” She inched herself closer to Agatha. “I get that you want to keep your work and private lives separate, and I am aware that I overstepped when I asked if you would be leading Eurydice so I apologise for that. But, like I said, if we are to be having discussions then some generic information will have to be given on both sides.” She couldn’t believe that she was having to gentle parent a college professor and teach them the basics of having a conversation.

She didn’t know why Agatha was so against sharing anything about herself, it was a defence mechanism sure but there was something else, something that made Agatha seem almost scared. There was a story to it that intrigued Rio and she was searching Agatha for any hint of what that story was, any crack in the walls that Agatha hid behind but she couldn’t find anything. Even after pushing the way that she had Agatha was still blocked in.

Agatha looked at the floor and spoke in a quiet voice. “You’re right.” She cleared her throat and looked back up at Rio, repeating herself. “You’re right. I flew off the handle and conducted myself in an extremely unprofessional manner, for which I apologise.” She paused waiting for Rio to interject, but Rio just waited patiently for her to finish. “I'm not used to being challenged and it's rare that people have a spine when conversing with me. But it seems that you don't have that problem.”
Rio gave a soft chuckle. “My parents raised me to speak my mind and stand up for myself. I guess they never thought about how it would translate into speaking with authority figures.”

There was a soft ping from Agatha’s phone and it seemed to snap Agatha back into Professor mode. She turned to her desk and picked up her laptop and various papers. “Well I have some first years to scare so we're going to have to end this here. Once again, you are welcome to attend. I think your presence gives them confidence since you were the first one to speak out.” She gave Rio a small smile and went to open the door. “There's no pressure though.”
“I'll think about it.” Rio said jokingly as she headed out the door.

Another confusing meeting with Agatha had been acquired, maybe she should start writing them down and compare them all at the end of the year to see which one was the winner for ‘most absurd interaction with university staff.’ The fact that sleeping with her lecturer during her masters wasn’t even on the list at the minute made her laugh. 

__________

Rio did go to the lecture, Agatha was back in teaching mode effortlessly commanding the attention of a hundred students as she spoke about Heracles’ twelve labours.
“Depending on the version of the myth that you come across, the circumstances surrounding his twelve labours differ. In one version, it is a fit of madness, induced by Hera, that causes Heracles to kill his children and wife, Megara. This in turn directs him to serve King Eurystheus for ten years and perform any task Eurystheus required of him – the twelve labours.” She paused to allow time for people to take notes.

Rio glanced to her left to look at Billy’s laptop and whispered. “You’ve spelled Eurystheus’ name wrong, it's a ‘Y’ not an ‘I’.”
Billy made a dramatic show of turning his laptop so that the screen was angled away from her and whispered back in mock seriousness. “I know that you’re not very smart, but can you not copy my notes please?”
Rio snorted. “It’s cute that you think your notes are anything of interest to me.”
He moved his laptop back and amended the spelling. “Happy now, you fucking nerd?” 
She nodded, “very.”

Agatha continued. “In some traditions, there was only a divine reason for Heracles's twelve labours. Zeus, in his desire not to leave Heracles the victim of Hera's jealousy, made her promise that, if Heracles executed twelve great works in the service of Eurystheus, he should become immortal. In the play Herakles by Euripides, Heracles is driven to madness by Hera and kills his children after his twelve labours.” She paused again as she changed the slides on her presentation. “Can anyone tell me one of the twelve labours in question?”
Rio watched with amusement as seemingly every student in the room forgot every single one of Heracles' labours. She chuckled and smiled when Alice leaned back to look at her past Billy and mouthed, “help.”

She glanced at Agatha who was standing patiently, waiting for an answer before looking back at Alice and whispering – probably too loudly, “hydra.”
Alice’s eyes widened comically as the realisation that she’d forgotten the most obvious one hit her. She cleared her throat and said, “he had to kill the Hydra.”
Agatha was already looking in their direction, Rio had definitely whispered too loudly, but she smiled and nodded all the same. “Yes, correct.” She typed ‘Slay the nine-headed Lernaean Hydra’ onto the blank slide. “Anyone else?”
Rio covered her mouth with her hand to try and hide the fact that she was whispering to Billy, “Capture and return Cerberus.” But he didn’t hear her properly and drew Agatha’s attention again by leaning towards Rio and asking, “what?”

Agatha cleared her throat and set her gaze squarely on Rio. “Miss Vidal, I take it that all this whispering means that you know the answers.” It wasn’t a question, it was an observation. Agatha was definitely aware of the fact that Rio knew all twelve of them; she would have been insulted if Agatha had implied that the opposite was true. “Would you care to do us the honour of listing them all?”

Rio huffed out a breath. “Gladly, Professor.” But are you sure that you can type quickly enough to keep up with me? The question sat on the tip of her tongue begging to be asked, needing to be turned from thoughts to words, but Rio knew that this wasn’t the time or place for it so she swallowed it and replaced it with the remaining eleven labours. “Slay the Nemean Lion, capture the Golden Hind of Artemis, capture the Erymanthian Boar, clean the Augean stables in a single day, slay the Stymphalian Birds, capture the Cretan Bull, steal the Mares of Diomedes, obtain the belt of Hippolyta, Queen of the Amazons, obtain the cattle of the monster Geryon, steal the golden apples of the Hesperides, capture and return Cerberus.” She paused in between each one, giving Agatha a chance to type them out before saying the next.

When Rio had finished the list, a girl a few rows in front scoffed and rolled her eyes at her and turned to her friend to whisper something, but Rio couldn’t make out what it was. It gave Rio a sense of pride, a feeling of smugness, but she also felt the tendrils of anxiety creeping their way in. It wasn’t her fault that she’d memorised all of this years ago and no one else in the room – except maybe Agatha – had bothered to do so too. She knew that she was in a lecture for first years but this was basic knowledge that everyone should know, right? There was no way that she was still the ‘weird kid’ in a room where time was literally dedicated to speaking about one of her interests.

At the age of thirty she should not be made to feel this insecure by a fucking teenager all because she was smarter than them. At the age of thirty she shouldn't be overthinking it as much as she was.

When the lecture ended she was heading for the door with Alice and Billy when Agatha stopped her. “Miss Vidal, stay behind please.”
Billy and Alice exchanged a look before Alice said, “We’ll wait for you outside,” and they both left the room.
Agatha waited until the last person had left and the door was closed before speaking. “Miss Vidal, I know that these lectures may seem rather pedestrian to someone of your academic expertise, and while I appreciate that you are trying to help your friends, I would also appreciate it if you let me do my job and teach them.”
Maybe she was reading too much into it, but Rio couldn’t shake the feeling that this was Agatha trying to regain some of the control that she had lost earlier, trying to reassert her authority and let Rio know that she was in charge.
The urge to fight back was strong but Rio fought through it and said, “I understand, Professor. My apologies.”
Agatha nodded once and said, “you may go,” then she turned her attention to her laptop as if Rio had stopped existing.

Rio opened her mouth to respond but didn’t actually know what to say so she just turned and walked out of the room. Billy and Alice were waiting in the corridor and both turned to look at her when they saw her walk out of the door. “Well you’re not crying so it can’t have been that bad.” Alice said, feigning concern.
“She told me off for telling you two idiots the answers.” Rio laughed. “So really, this is your fault for not being as smart as me.”
Billy scoffed. “Oh so because we’re not massive fucking nerds, we’re the problem?”
“Exactly.” Rio said, matter-of-factly.

The three of them went to get lunch and then Rio went with them to the rest of their lectures for the day. Being able to do her own research on her own time and on her own terms was the good thing about doing a PhD, but she had to admit that she missed going to lectures and not having to think for herself so much. The first years were basically spoon-fed all of the information they needed and could put in zero effort and still pass.

She remembered her first year well, which was surprising given how much alcohol she drank during it. As a child she had always been fascinated by pretty or cool looking rocks that she had found on the beach, and the time that she found an ammonite fossil had sparked a new interest in her, so studying archaeology had been a no-brainer. The thought of being able to discover history and pull parts of it out of the ground with her bare hands had been extremely exciting to her.

She had met some of her closest friends during her first year, they had lived together throughout all three years at college and had gone on all of their summer placements together, and they all still met up every couple of months – they were all going to Virginia at Christmas to see her when she flew back home for the holidays.

She had also met, who she thought was at the time, the love of her life. Cassidy had been in her final year and they met by chance one night in the campus bar, Rio took Cassidy back to her flat and she never left. Her friends joked about how ‘lady killer Vidal’ had finally been tamed and had gone soft, but they were also very vocal about how much they liked Cassidy and how they were so well suited together. Cassidy had survived the grilling that Rio’s abuela had given her and she was all Rio saw when she thought about the future. Unfortunately, Cassidy had not felt the same way. A week before their two year anniversary, Cassidy messaged Rio to say that she wasn’t “feeling it anymore” and that they should break up.

Rio had tried to fight for them, to fix whatever had been broken, but her efforts were thrown back in her face when Cassidy’s new girlfriend showed up at her student flat and threatened to call the police if she didn’t stop harassing her.
“Cassidy doesn’t need some doe-eyed undergrad following her around and holding her back. Get a fucking grip and grow up.”
Rio had been so depressed that she stopped attending her lectures and put little-to-no effort into her coursework which resulted in her nearly failing her final year and, in turn, failing her degree. Her friends had helped her pull herself together in time to save her grade, absolutely knocking her dissertation out of the park and getting herself the first that she knew was easily within her grasp. She did need to beg for an extension on her dissertation deadline, but thankfully that didn’t reflect badly on her.

__________

As the trio were leaving the final lecture of the day, Rio turned to them and asked, “fancy a pint?” 
“Can't right now, we have band practise.” Alice said. 
Rio raised an eyebrow. “You're in a band?” 
Billy nodded. “Yeah! I mean it's just other students and it's nothing proper at the minute, but we're trying to put a set together to play at the end of year ball that the department has.”
“What's your band name?” Rio asked. 
“We don't have one yet.” Billy and Alice replied in unison. 
Rio widened her eyes in mock surprise. “What? Everyone knows that a band is only as good as their name. Mine was called Big Gulp.” She laughed as she recalled the memories. “As you can tell from the name, we weren't very good.” 

Alice put her arm out to stop them all from walking. “Why have you kept this potentially embarrassing information from us? Please tell me there’s videos!” 
Rio stepped around her arm. “Yes there are, but you two will never see them.”
“Oh come on,” Alice begged. “At least tell us what instrument you play.”
Rio laughed and shook her head, but told them anyway. “I was the drummer.”

She walked away before Alice and Billy could hit her with their barrage of questions, and went to cut across the car park that she had recently found took ten minutes off of her walk home. Towards the back of the car park she could see someone standing at their car with the hood open, as she got closer she recognised the person. It was Wanda and she was staring at her car looking thoroughly confused.
“So you’re either a powerful witch who is fixing her car with mind magic, or you have no idea what you’re looking at right now.” Rio said jokingly as she got close enough for Wanda to hear her.

Wanda jumped slightly having not heard Rio approaching. “Jesus Rio! I didn’t see you.” She chuckled softly. “It’s most definitely the latter. This has never made sense to me.”
“You want me to take a look?” Rio asked as she moved around Wanda to get a closer look at the car.
“If you know what you’re doing, by all means! It wouldn't start when I tried it just now.”
Rio hummed. “Did any warning lights come up or could it not get to that point?”
Wanda shook her head. “It didn’t get to that point.”
“Do you mind if I try it, just to see what I’m working with?” Wanda offered her keys to Rio and Rio slid into the drivers side and put the keys in the ignition. “Tell me if anything happens when I try to start it.”
‘The English might drive on the other side of the car, but everything else should be the same… I hope.’ She thought as she turned the key.

The engine tried to start and the dashboard flashed for a second but that was the only sign of life that the car gave her so she took the keys out and stepped out of the car again. “Did anything happen with the engine?”
Wanda shrugged. “I’m going to be honest, Rio, I wouldn’t have been able to tell you if it did.”
Rio laughed. “Fair enough. I can have a look under the hood for you, but I can’t make any promises. Do you have any tools on you?”
Wanda walked to the boot and pulled something out of it. It was a small red toolbox that looked like it had never been opened. “My ex husband got me this years ago when he tried to teach me how to fix it myself, but I’ve never used it. I wouldn’t know where to start!”
She gave the toolbox to Rio who put it on the ground and started shrugging her jacket off. “Would you mind holding this for me? I don’t want it to get dirty.”
Wanda took the jacket off of her and her eyes went wide when she touched it. “Is this real leather?”
Rio smiled. “Yeah it is, it’s custom made.” She saw Wanda’s mouth drop open when she looked at the tag.
“This is a custom Ralph Lauren?”
Rio chuckled as she rested the toolbox on the edge of the car and leant over to get a better look inside the hood. “Yes it is. Now you see why I didn’t want it getting dirty.”
Wanda hummed her agreement and watched Rio as she checked a couple of things with the engine; she pulled a rag out of the toolbox and wiped the battery terminals.

She straightened up, wiping her hands on the rag. “Try it again now.”
Wanda gently put the jacket on the passenger seat before getting in the driver's side, and Rio smiled at how careful she was being with her jacket.
The engine roared to life and Wanda got back out of the car. “I don’t know what you did, but thank you!” She pulled Rio into a hug and Rio awkwardly tried not to touch her with her dirty hands.
Rio put on a fake southern drawl. “All in a day's work, ma’am.”
Wanda put her hand on her hip and mimicked the accent. “Well how will I ever repay you for your kindness?”
“No need Darlin’, a true gentleman don’t need nothin’ in return.”
Wanda laughed and dropped the accent. “Seriously though, I want to thank you. At least let me give you a lift home.”
Rio smiled and also returned to her normal accent. “Okay yeah, I’ll take that.”

They both got in the car and Wanda insisted on putting Rio’s jacket in the back to make sure that the remaining grease on her hands didn’t get on it. The drive to Rio’s flat was only five minutes so it didn’t leave any time for conversation but before Rio got out of the car, Wanda smirked and said, “Look at us being able to have an interaction without you trying to kill me.”
Rio pretended to be serious when she replied. “Don’t speak too soon, your car could still blow up.”
“Well actually, you make a good point.”
Rio laughed as she got out of the car. “Thanks for the ride.”
Wanda smiled and said, “Thank you for fixing said ride.”

Rio watched Wanda drive away before letting herself into her flat. She set her bag down and took off her shoes before flopping onto her sofa and turning on her TV for background noise as she picked up a book that she had started reading, and settled in for the evening.

Chapter End Notes

I know absolutely nothing about cars so don't @ me please

Rio

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

As she was getting ready to leave her flat, Rio realised that Wanda had driven off with her jacket still on the back seat. Had Wanda done it on purpose so that they’d have an excuse to see each other again? No, surely not. Rio was reading too much into it.
She would just swing by Wanda’s office on her way to the library and ask her to bring it in tomorrow. Or was that too informal? Should she email her instead? She didn’t know what terms they were on. “Fuck it, I’ll go to her office.” She said to herself as she pulled a burgundy hoodie from her wardrobe.

She got onto campus around ten o’clock and veered towards the building that had the ancient history department in it – it was at the opposite end to the library so it wasn’t really ‘swinging by’ but it was her favourite jacket. She took the lift up to the third floor and, when she stepped off, she realised that she didn’t actually know where Wanda’s office was. All she had to go off was the place that they had bumped into each other twice previously, so she started there and followed the corridor round until she saw the plaque that had Ms. Maximoff engraved into it.

She knocked four times on the wooden door and waited. Five seconds, ten seconds, thirty seconds, a minute, but no-one answered – she was probably teaching. On her way back to the lift, Rio pulled out her phone and started looking up Wanda’s schedule. She was in back-to-back lectures until one o’clock so Rio decided to try her office again around that time.

She got herself settled in a corner of the library, put her headphones on, and soon enough she had built a protective shield out of all of the books that she had pulled from the shelves. She didn’t have a ‘happy place’ per se but this felt pretty close. Surrounded by books, finding meaning in their subtext, shutting out the world and being in her own little space for a while. It wasn’t quite perfect, it was missing something, but she was yet to figure out what that was. For now though, this would do.

She was so engrossed in her research that feeling her phone buzz on the table made her jump. It was a message from Alice.

Alice: We’re going to the pub after lectures today if you want to join?

Rio: Sounds good. I’m having a library day so let me know when you’re there.

Alice: Will do, nerd

Rio rolled her eyes affectionately, Alice and Billy would both quickly learn not to underestimate the importance of a good library day.
The hours seemed to fly by and when Rio checked the time it was 1:15. She had barely made a dent in the pile of books that she had acquired, so she made notes of all of their titles to make sure that she could find them again easily after she had spoken to Wanda, and returned them all to their respective shelves.

She made her way back to Wanda’s office and knocked on her door.
“Come in.”
The cheery way that Wanda invited her in was a stark contrast to the way that Agatha did it. Wanda’s was happier, more welcoming, whereas Agatha’s felt more like she was only allowing you access to her space provided that you knew it was on her terms, and she was in charge of how long you would be staying.
Rio walked into the room and immediately noticed that it looked a lot more ‘lived in’ than Agatha’s office. There were significantly less books, but every wall was covered in pictures and motivational posters. The chairs and table that were in the centre matched Agatha’s and Rio guessed that they were the same in all of the offices in the building, if not the whole university.

Wanda was sitting behind her desk and greeted her with a smile. “Hi Rio, what can I do for you?”
Rio stepped further into the room. “I’m just here to ask you a few questions about a kidnapping that happened last night.”
“A kidnapping? I’m not sure I follow.” Wanda’s brow furrowed in confusion.
Rio moved closer to Wanda adding a teasing lilt to her voice. “Oh you know. A jacket, dark green, very expensive. Last seen on the back seat of your car.”
Wanda’s eyes went wide as she breathed out a sigh of relief. “You actually had me worried there for a second!”

Rio laughed and stopped walking in front of Wanda’s desk. It was kept very tidy with the papers organised into different baskets and there was a small picture frame, but Rio couldn’t see the picture that it contained because it was facing away from her. “So are you going to return the poor victim, or do I have to fight you for it?”
“As much as I’d love to fight you, I’ll save you the embarrassment of losing and graciously return your jacket to you. I can drop it off tonight if you want?”
Rio smirked. “It’s cute that you think you’d win but I’m out tonight so can you bring it in tomorrow and I’ll grab it then?”
Wanda offered her hand. “Deal.”
Rio took her hand and shook it. “Pleasure doing business with you, Ms. Maximoff.”
“Likewise, and please, call me Wanda.”
They pulled their hands apart and Rio gave a small nod. “See you tomorrow, Wanda.”
She left the office and made her way back to the library.

__________

Rio worked until Alice and Billy told her that they were in the pub. She had managed to add a fair few pages to her notes and since Agatha was going to help her organise them, she didn't focus on anything in particular. She just let the inspiration take her wherever it wanted and, if it didn't cause her more work further along the line, she would absolutely do it more often. There was a freedom to working this way, not being tied down by a particular subject, topic or theme but being able to jump between them as and when she wanted. 

She had always preferred that way of being in all aspects of her life, it's why she had so many hobbies – she had managed to make herself somewhat of a jack of all trades through doing this. It wasn't that she got bored per se, but when she started to lose interest in something it was really hard for her to get it back. So instead of having a few fully developed skills, she had a myriad of skills that were underdeveloped but looked good to a layperson.
It had also caused contention with a couple of her exes, her inability to fully commit to anything had been the reason for the breakdown of most of her relationships. The catalyst for this behaviour in her relationships however, had definitely been the almost-two-years that she was with Cassidy. When Cassidy broke her heart she became more guarded and stopped letting people get so close to her, keeping them at arm's length and pushing them away before they could inevitably do it to her – it was safer that way. She would manage a few months but would then start to distance herself which would lead to an argument which would then turn into a breakup. She had gotten used to the cycle and had a pseudo script that she would follow when the situation arose.

The only things she had managed to stick at were her academic endeavours, having to constantly split her attention between learning all of the various subjects at school had given her the environment that she needed to thrive. Where other students got burnt out with having to study so many different things, Rio was like a duck to water – easily able to jump between all of the different modules and topics throughout her academic career.
It did provide a hindrance though. It was the reason that she struggled to structure her work because finding a way to link everything together was hard, but now she had Agatha to help with that and she trusted her – and maybe Wanda would be willing to read her work and offer some advice as well.

When she got a text from Billy letting her know that he and Alice were waiting for her, she packed up her things and headed over to the pub. Before she could sit down, Alice let her know that it was her turn to get a round in. She rolled her eyes but asked what they wanted and went to the bar to get the drinks. When she got back to the table she caught the end of their conversation.
“I don’t think she’ll want to.”
“It won’t hurt to ask.”
She set the drinks down and asked, “Do I want to know what you two are talking about?”
Billy looked at her. “Probably not, but we’re involving you anyway.”
“Oh god.” She said, feeling slightly worried. “Go on, tell me.”
Alice slid her pint over to herself and drew a pattern in the condensation on the glass. “So we kind of need a drummer.”
Rio laughed and shook her head. “I knew I’d regret telling you that. I haven’t played properly since high school. I know that for you guys that wasn’t that long ago, but for me it was…” she made a show of counting the years on her fingers, “twelve long years ago.”

Billy gave Alice a look that could only be read as “I told you so” and Alice put her finger up to tell him to wait. “Please just think about it. We’re having another practise on Sunday around twelve, you don’t have to commit to anything yet but just try it.”
Rio rolled her eyes and sighed. “If I come to this one practise, will you shut up about it?”
Their replies came in unison.
“Yep.”
“Promise.”
Rio shook her head again and said, “You two are the worst.” She was met with wide grins from the both of them.

The three of them stayed at the pub for a couple more drinks before going their separate ways. Rio zipped her hoodie up and stuffed her hands in the pockets, this really wasn’t an acceptable replacement for her leather jacket. As soon as she got back into the warmth of her flat, she checked Wanda’s schedule for the following day to figure out the earliest time that she could get her most prized possession back. Wanda had office hours between nine and eleven every Friday morning which meant that Rio didn’t need to be up too early. She set her alarm for nine-thirty and got in the shower, starting her process of winding down for the night. 

__________ 

Rio woke up to her alarm and spent the first fifteen minutes of her morning scrolling aimlessly through TikTok, she had refused to download it until the pandemic hit and she was forced to spend more time alone, and now she found herself ‘doom-scrolling’ more and more often. She dragged herself out of bed and got ready for the day, hesitating about whether to wear a hoodie again or to brave it in just a t-shirt until she got her jacket back from Wanda. She checked the weather for the day and saw that it was supposed to be sunny for most of it – she still hadn’t quite mastered how to predict the British weather, but she was pretty sure that even people that had lived there for their whole lives hadn’t mastered it either – so she chose to stick to just the t-shirt and started her walk to the campus.

She got to Wanda’s office just after ten-thirty and knocked on the door.
“Come in.”
 The greeting still caught her off guard a little, but she walked in.
“Ah Rio, I was wondering when you’d be here.” Wanda said, smiling. “As you can see, the victim has been returned safe and sound without a scratch on her.” She gestured to the wall where the jacket was on a coat hanger that was hanging on a nail. Rio walked over to it, took off her bag, then removed the jacket from the hanger and slipped her arms into it before putting her bag back over her shoulder. “Thank you so much, the past twenty four hours have truly been the hardest of my life. There were times where I didn’t think that I would make it through.” She forced a crack into her voice to fake being close to tears.

Wanda chucked and stood up from her desk, picking up a canvas that had been leaning against it. “I’m glad that the two of you have finally been reunited and I am truly sorry for the part I played in your anguish.” She walked over to the wall and took the coat hanger down, putting the canvas back up in its place. “I have to say though, I’ll miss it.”
Rio tilted her head slightly. “Oh?”
Wanda continued. “It was a great conversation piece with the students that have come in to make use of my office hours this morning. It was truly heart-breaking to have to tell them that it wasn’t mine.” She turned and leaned with her back against the wall next to the canvas.

Rio laughed. “You can always buy one, then you don’t have to suffer such terrible heartbreak again.”
“You’d be okay with us wearing matching jackets?” Wanda said, raising her eyebrow.
Rio smirked. “They wouldn’t be matching though, this is a custom, remember?”
Wanda laughed lightly. “Yes of course. How could I forget that you’re a student who can afford to buy a custom, real-leather jacket? How silly of me.”
Rio looked at her for a moment, taking in her soft features, the way the corners of her mouth wrinkled slightly when she smiled, the way that the red of her hair made her eyes seem like the most vivid shade of green. “Be honest with me for a second?” She asked.
Wanda’s brow dipped slightly, taken off guard by the question. “Of course.”
“Did you try it on?” She gestured to the jacket.

Wanda sighed and visibly relaxed, her shoulders dropping. “You need to stop worrying me like that! No I didn’t try it on, I will admit that I was tempted though, but I didn’t want anything to accidentally happen to it.”
Rio smiled. “It’s not as breakable as you seem to think it is, with the amount I paid for it I’d be mad if it was.”
“Well, I’ll be less careful in future then.” Wanda replied with a smirk.

Rio was about to respond but she was interrupted by a knock at the door. Wanda pushed away from the wall and walked to the centre of the room, clearing her throat before she spoke. “Come in.”
A boy walked into the room and seemed surprised to see Rio standing there. “Oh, I’m sorry Ms. Maximoff, I didn’t realise you were with another student.”
“No, no, it’s okay Eddie.” She gestured for him to sit in one of the chairs. “Rio and I were done. “ She turned to Rio. “I’ll see you soon.”
Rio nodded and left the office.

As she walked towards the library, ready to spend another day hiding behind a fortress of books, Rio's mind was doing a deep dive into the last thing Wanda said to her. 
 “I'll see you soon.”  
 What did she mean by it? Was it just the polite, passing statement with the same meaning that it always had? Or was she implying that she wanted to see her soon? 
 It wasn't like Rio to overthink this kind of interaction, usually she would just lean into the flirting and see where it took her – but then again they were interrupted so the flow was stopped. She and Wanda hadn't had the chance for an actual conversation yet so there was no real way of telling if this was just a bit of harmless flirting or if it could lead in a more interesting direction. 

__________

It was yet another Saturday that Rio was spending in her apartment, alone. Cooking dinner, alone. Watching TV, alone. The past few days when she’d had her meeting with Agatha, gone to the bar with Alice and Billy and the three times she had seen Wanda had been the most consecutive time that she had spent with other people since moving, and now that she had gone a whole day without seeing anyone, she was finding herself wishing she was around other people.

After she had finished her food and washed her pots, she decided that she was done moping. She wasn't going to sit in her flat feeling sorry for herself any more, so she got in the shower and got ready to go out. She wasn't really one for ‘dolling’ herself up but she could dress well, choosing a pair of black, leather-look trousers and pairing them with a navy blue blouse – she spent some time deciding on how many buttons to leave undone and ultimately making the choice to leave three, just enough to make people look but not enough that anything was on show. She pulled out a black, fitted jacket that fastened with a single button and stopped just below her hips, in case she needed an extra layer in the cool air of the night. The final piece was a pair of black, pleather boots with enough of a heel to give her an extra couple of inches to her height.
When she was happy with her outfit she grabbed her keys and headed out.

She put her hands in her pockets to keep them from meeting the same fate and being coloured with the same red that she was sure had already made its home on her face, and walked until she found the least offensive looking bar. Rio found that she was starting to enjoy her meetings with Agatha, she was determined to peel back the layers and find what made her tick. She didn’t like her authority being challenged, that much was obvious, and Rio loved to prod her. She was getting to know which buttons to press to get a reaction and Agatha seemed incapable of not providing said reaction.

Agatha liked control, she liked knowing that she was in charge and that everything that happened to or around her was all her doing. They were her strings to pull, her orchestra to conduct, her script to write and direct, and Rio simply could not resist threatening to crumble Agatha’s carefully constructed walls.
She respected Agatha, that was never in question. She knew that ultimately Agatha was the one with the power in their dynamic, which was exactly why it was so fun to play with that power. She liked catching Agatha off guard and watching her scramble to quickly put herself back together.

She noticed that Agatha wasn’t used to people pushing back, she wasn’t used to people not letting her walk all over them, and Rio was pretty sure that Agatha would implode if she thought for one second that Rio didn’t find her ‘scary’ like everyone else did. She was used to being feared and using that to get the respect of her students and colleagues.
Rio respected Agatha as her superior but that didn’t mean that she wouldn’t try to have some fun with her from time to time.

She had caught Agatha staring at her a few times now and each time had sent a tingle down her spine. There was a difference between simply looking at someone, and regarding someone with such intensity that you get lost in the curve of their nose, the way their hair falls or the shine in their eyes. Of course she couldn't speak for Agatha, nor could she assign a fully accurate meaning or reason to her actions, but she was well versed in the sapphic urge to stare longingly at any attractive woman that wandered into your field of vision. It didn’t necessarily mean that you wanted to sleep with them – one could look at the menu and not order – it just meant that you noticed and appreciated their attractiveness on a base level.

She didn’t fully know if Agatha was into women or not, Agatha hadn’t exactly been forthcoming with that information, but the way that she had reacted when Rio had asked had, in itself, been an answer. If she wanted to know for sure she could ask Wanda – there had definitely been something between them at some point, she’d worked that out – but she was now trying to keep Wanda at a distance to avoid giving her the wrong impression.

They had done an exchange of clothes and since then Rio had deflected any attempts that Wanda made for the two of them to spend time together. A one night stand was fine, perfectly normal behaviour, but twice would lead to a third and a third would lead to feelings that Rio would inevitably have to hurt, and it was just easier to cut all of that out. Her memory of that night was almost fully returned, there was just the odd bit that the alcohol had held back but she couldn’t deny that the bits she had regained were good – great, even. Wanda had fucked her in a way that made her legs feel weak just thinking about it, even when she was sitting down, but she knew that she couldn’t let it go further for both of their sakes.

Rio had gone to the campus café to find out what Agatha’s usual order was – a latte with two sugars – and had purposefully ordered something that she knew Agatha would hate, just so she could mess with her a little bit. It had worked beautifully and when she made a show of licking the cream off of her finger Agatha’s reaction had been exactly what Rio had wanted. The way her eyes had followed Rio’s finger as she swiped it through the cream and put it in her mouth, the way that her throat bobbed as she swallowed when Rio gave a low hum of satisfaction. She was about as subtle as a brick to the face.

Rio wasn’t immune to the sapphic urge to stare any more than Agatha was, but she was less shameful about it. The black framed glasses that Agatha wore were a personal favourite of Rio’s and when Agatha looked at her over the top of them she was very aware of the way that her stomach reacted.
She kept catching a glimpse of the tattoo that Agatha had on her ankle and wondered if she had any more, if so what were they and where were they? It was still a question that she wanted to ask but she was waiting for the right way to slip it into conversation.

She enjoyed working in Agatha’s office, it was comfortable enough that she didn’t get distracted but not so comfortable that it had the opposite effect and she’d rather relax than work. She got a surprising amount of work done sitting in that armchair with Agatha either sitting opposite her or at her desk, and she liked that she was able to get Agatha’s input instantly as opposed to having to wait for her to return an email. But her brain did have a limit on the length of time that she could concentrate for – and when that limit had been reached, she usually became curious about what Agatha was doing.

She looked up from her laptop and saw that Agatha’s brow was knitted together in confusion as she was reading something on her own laptop. “Did you accidentally lock yourself out of your emails?”
Agatha looked up at her, the confusion still on her face but now aimed at Rio. “What do you mean?”
Rio nodded towards Agatha's laptop. “You were looking very puzzled for a moment there.”
“Oh.” Agatha's expression changed to understanding. “No believe it or not, I can operate my emails just fine.”
“So what, you changed the language to Mandarin or something and you can't change it back?”
Agatha sighed and took off her glasses. “Miss Vidal I am perfectly capable of using my laptop correctly and, last time I checked, your thesis wasn't on my technological skills.” She put her glasses back on and fixed Rio with a look that said what her words didn't. Stop bothering me with useless questions and go back to your work.

Rio did just that and started mentally counting backwards from ten, knowing that Agatha eventually wouldn’t be able to resist telling her what she was doing. Rio had figured out that Agatha secretly liked it when Rio showed an interest in what she was doing. It was subtle and often hidden behind something else but there was a change in Agatha’s demeanour whenever Rio made her inquiries. There was often some surprise at the fact that she had cared enough to ask – Rio guessed that, due to the persona Agatha put out into the world, she didn’t get very many people asking about her – and then a very quick flash of something akin to joy before it was all replaced by the neutral expression she always worked hard to maintain.

Rio made it down to four before she heard Agatha sigh and say, “I’m looking over some dissertation outlines from the students I’m supervising.”
Rio took a dramatic gasp of air and said with mock hurt, “I thought I was the only student you were supervising! Are you cheating on me, Professor?”
Agatha rolled her eyes and breathed out in exasperation, taking off her glasses and pinching the bridge of her nose for good measure. Rio smiled to herself. Eliciting these reactions from Agatha was all too easy, it didn’t take any of the fun out of it though. “I’m kidding, obviously, you can supervise as many students as you like, it’s kinda part of your job description.” Agatha looked back up at her and she caught her eyes, enjoying the annoyance that was evident in them. “As long as you admit that I’m your favourite, that is.”

The expression on Agatha’s face hardened and Rio knew that she was dancing on the line between what Agatha would allow and what would make her flip the switch and put Rio in her place. If she was being honest with herself, sometimes she stepped over the line on purpose. There was a certain part of her that liked it when Agatha put her foot down and told her off, but she kept that part of her buried because letting it out wouldn’t serve her well.

When Agatha spoke there was an air of amusement in her voice that didn’t match the stony look on her face. “Miss Vidal I do not play favourites. But if I did, you could be safe in the knowledge that you would be nowhere near the top of that list.”
“The lady doth protest too much.” Rio quickly responded and began working her tongue against the inside of her cheek. Agatha rolled her eyes again and turned her attention back to her laptop.

Rio started to split more of her time between Agatha’s office, lectures, the library and the music room, happy that she had more things now to occupy her ever wandering mind.
She was really enjoying being part of a band again, the camaraderie between musicians is something that is hard to match. Being able to have a connection with people where you don’t need to use words to communicate, Eddie could just nod at her and she’d understand that he meant ‘half-time’. Or Ash could walk towards her and she knew that they wanted her to make the kick match their rhythm.

It became a little tradition for the five of them to go to the pub after practise and have a few drinks to wind down – and Rio ended up paying the majority of the time. She didn't mind since she had more money than the average student, and they all drank the cheapest lager so it wasn't the end of the world. There was only so much cheap lager she could stomach though, so she treated herself to a glass of wine on occasion. Usually no one commented but this once, Billy decided to pipe up.
“Are you too good for pints now?” He asked with a cheeky smile on his face.
“Oh I'd happily drink this by the pint if they served it.” Rio shot back.
Billy's eyes lit up. “So what I'm hearing is, Rio is a secret hardcore drinker and we should all go round to hers one night.”
Rio immediately shook her head. “Absolutely fucking not. I am not letting you four loose in my apartment.”
Billy was about to say something else when Eddie cut in. “That's probably a wise choice since this one,” he gestured to Billy, “can't hold his drink like he thinks he can.”

Billy tried to defend himself but was cut off by Alice, Eddie and Ash all jumping in with various examples that proved him wrong, and he eventually stopped and started pouting instead. “You’re all just jealous that I can spend less money on a night out than the rest of you.”
Rio laughed and shook her head, being able to relive her undergrad through her four friends was a nice feeling.

The conversation shifted towards work with Alice asking Eddie if he could give any insight on what she and Billy could expect in their second year.
“Don’t expect to get away with the stuff you do now, they really crack down from second year onwards. You already know what to expect from Professor Harkness, she doesn’t really change much.” He took a sip from his drink. “That’s a good thing though because you’re prepared from the off with her. Professor Maguire is okay, he’s just a bit boring to be honest. Ms. Maximoff is a lot nicer and way more lenient, she’s my favourite lecturer by far.”

Alice shrugged. “I don’t know, I’ve not noticed.” She quickly changed the subject by asking Ash what it was like on their course, so Rio dropped the conversation. There was definitely something going on but she wasn’t going to find out that night.

Rio began to wonder how many times Wanda had thought about it. Had she thought about it the same amount that Rio had? More? Less? Was this the first time that her mind had gone back to it? Surely not.

In the same department that she taught in.

So it’s just safer to stop it before it can get to that point.”

But while we’re on the subject of my ex-husband, our relationship was always more of a casual thing which is why we mutually decided that the best thing to do was to get divorced. We can co-parent perfectly fine, but as a couple? We were never meant to work.”
Rio was now very curious about Wanda’s relationship history – she hadn’t expected it to be this intriguing. Wanda didn’t seem like the type to have a scandalous dating life, but then again Rio hadn’t expected her to have a son either so maybe she couldn’t read her as well as she thought.

I did something that I’m not proud of, they found out and rightfully broke up with me. Rumours flew through the department and now they avoid me at all costs.”
Rio pressed her lips together, unsure of what to say. This is not the direction she had thought that this conversation would go. The best she could manage was a quiet, “yikes.”
Wanda nodded slowly. “Yeah. So relationships really aren’t high on my list of things that I’m desperate for right now.”
Rio nodded too and an awkward silence settled in the room, and she couldn’t find anything to say to attempt to shift it.

She couldn’t help trying to figure out who Wanda’s ex was. She hadn’t met a lot of the lecturers at the university, in fact the only two she had spent any time with were Wanda and Agatha. Her brain was trying to form a connection, she was close to something. Wanda’s ex works in the department, it’s probably how they met, the breakup was messy and now they hate her and avoid her.

Oh.

Oh.

The look that Agatha had gotten on her face the two times that Rio had mentioned Wanda came careening into her mind. The fact that after their meetings, Rio would take the short way to the lecture hall past Wanda’s office and Agatha would go the opposite direction taking the long way.
It was so obvious but she wasn’t going to mention it, it wasn’t her place to bring it up.

They sat silently for an excruciatingly long time before the door buzzer made them both jump. “Food’s here.” Rio said, hating the way her voice cracked, and jumped up all too quickly, basically sprinting to the door. She collected the bags from the delivery driver and took them into the kitchen, getting plates and cutlery out of the cupboards and drawers. “I had to guess at what to order for you, I hope you like Chinese food.”
Wanda joined her, pulling the cartons out of the bags and looking at what they were. “I love Chinese food. All of these are solid choices, well done.”

“Oh but that’s the beauty of ordering a Chinese, you can feed yourself for at least three days if you know what you’re doing.”
They plated up their food and went back to the sofa, sitting closer than they were when they first sat down, the awkward tension starting to dissipate.

Wanda raised her eyebrow as she took the remote. “That’s an incredible amount of trust to place in me.”
“Oh I’m aware, don’t worry.” Rio smirked.
Wanda navigated the menu and clicked on Disney Plus. When she saw the show that was at the top of Rio’s continue watching section she snorted. “Of course the most recent thing you watched was Percy Jackson.”
Rio quickly chewed her food so that she could respond. “It’s for research I’ll have you know.”
Wanda hummed and said, “sure.” Dragging the word out for extra emphasis.

Rio reached in Wanda’s direction, making a grab for the remote. “Okay, you’ve lost your privileges. Give it back.”
Wanda held it out to the side, keeping it out of Rio’s reach. “I’m not judging you! My son loves those books, he got them for his thirteenth birthday and spent every waking minute reading them.” Rio made another attempt to get the remote, knocking into Wanda. “Hey watch it, you’re gonna knock my plate over!”
Rio pulled back and they were both laughing. Any residual awkwardness from their earlier conversation had gone and they had fallen into a comfortable rhythm. “How old is your son?” 

Wanda smiled fondly. “He’s eighteen. He’s studying at the university actually, but I can’t tell you any more because he made me promise not to tell anyone that we’re related.” She laughed.
Rio quirked an eyebrow having found a challenge in the subtext of Wanda’s words. “I’ll just keep my eye out for the most vividly ginger boy then.”
“You do that. Please let me know if you spot him.”

Wanda switched from Disney to Netflix asking if Rio had ever seen Derry Girls.
“Nope.”
Wanda pressed play on the first episode. “I think you’ll like it, it’s your kind of humour.”
“We’ll see.” She said with a wink. Wanda rolled her eyes and started eating her food.

They had made it through three episodes before finishing their platefuls and were now sitting with their shoulders touching, which Rio was all too aware of. She was able to keep quiet about it until Wanda absentmindedly put her hand on her thigh. She shifted causing Wanda’s hand to slide off of her leg and onto the couch cushion and turned so that she was facing her. “Okay, if we’re going to do this then there need to be rules.”
Wanda angled herself so that she was also facing Rio. “I’m listening.”
Rio held up her hand and started counting. “Number one: no sleepovers.”
Wanda snorted. “Fine by me, you snore very loudly.”
“I do not. Also that’s irrelevant. Number two: this is just sex and nothing more. We don’t need to spend time together outside of it.”
“So what we’re doing right now is-”
Rio cut her off. “This doesn’t count, this was pre-rules.”
Wanda nodded. “Aye aye, captain.”
“And finally, the most important one. Number three: do not, under any circumstances, fall in love with me.”
That one made Wanda laugh. “We’re not in any danger of that happening, do not worry.” She gave Rio a pointed look. “You, on the other hand, need to not fall in love with me .”
“I think I can handle that.” Rio smirked.

Wanda then did one of the most quintessentially British things that Rio had ever seen. She slapped her thighs and said, “right,” before standing up and making her way to the door. She put her shoes on before nonchalantly saying, “thank you for dinner but some of us have work in the morning.” She opened the door and stepped out, throwing, “I’ll let you know if I require your services.” over her shoulder before shutting the door.

Rio sighed. She knew that there was only one way that this could end, the same way they all ended, but maybe Wanda would surprise her. She put the plates and cutlery in the dishwasher, pressing the quick wash cycle and put the leftovers in the fridge before stripping off and getting in the shower, ready to settle in for the night.

Her next meeting with Agatha followed the same pattern as the rest of them. Rio would give Agatha her coffee, Agatha would make a decent effort at engaging with Rio’s banter – a more recent development but Rio took it as a win since it opened up the possibility of Agatha loosening up a bit – and then Rio would blow her mind with her work. The last part was a given, obviously, and Rio was often tempted to hand Agatha the version that was written half in Spanish just to mess with her a bit, but ultimately decided against it.

Her friends used to hate borrowing her notes in their undergrad because they could only understand about forty percent of it. They’d jokingly complain saying that it was discrimination and Rio would tell them that it wasn’t her fault they only spoke one language and she would remind them that Duolingo was free.

Rio often chose her research topics based on what she knew Agatha liked, that’s why she had previously asked what Agatha’s gateway into Greek mythology was and who her godly parent would be. It helped her narrow down what to work on next and aided her in her attempts to get onto Agatha’s good side. She could tell that it made Agatha happy when she told her that she had been the reason for her most recent deep dive; she could see the pride in her eyes and body language. For a teacher she imagined that one of the best things you could experience is witnessing your love and knowledge of a subject inspiring someone to do their own work on said subject, and knowing that she was providing that for Agatha did give her her own selfish point of pride.

Reading The Odyssey, a book that Agatha had previously named as the reason she took an interest in Greek mythology, for the first time in front of her had been a plan that Rio had had since their argument about it all those weeks ago. She’d been waiting for the right time to do it, waiting for Agatha to curb the defensiveness that she dressed up as professionalism just enough for her to be tempted to have a casual conversation about it. Rio purposefully kept a blasé attitude about reading the book because she knew that Agatha wouldn’t be able to resist showing a little bit of personal interest since the story obviously meant a lot to her – and she was right.

Every time she made a noise of approval or gave a quiet chuckle at something she had just read she could feel Agatha’s gaze snap to her, reading her reactions and trying to decipher her thoughts. She smiled to herself because Agatha was fighting so hard to try and seem as uninterested as she could, but betrayed herself every time. Rio was so close to getting her to open up, she could feel it – Agatha accidentally saying her name instead of calling her Miss Vidal only worked to cement that fact. But just as Rio thought they were finally getting somewhere, Agatha turned everything on its head by starting a fight. Over dog-earing the page of all things.

Rio could barely believe that it was happening. Had Agatha all of a sudden realised that they’d managed to go the past few meetings without having an argument and now she was desperate to reset the counter? She had the infuriating skill of being able to twist the situation to make it Rio’s fault, like she had been the one to start it. It was childish and thoroughly annoying.

Rio still went to the lecture, mostly out of spite because she would not let Agatha have any reason to think that she had ‘won’ whatever that was. She was five minutes late in an act of pettiness which prompted Agatha to say, “nice of you to join us, Miss Vidal.” as she ascended the stairs in the seating bank and shuffled into the middle to take her seat next to Alice. She smiled sweetly and added a sugary tonality to her voice. “My sincerest apologies Professor, please continue.”
Agatha tensed her jaw and went back to teaching about Daedalus’ Labyrinth.

Alice leaned towards her, the seat creaking from the movement. “I wish I had your bravery. How has she let you live for this long?” She whispered.
“You just need to know how to handle her.” Rio whispered back.
With her back to the seats, using a laser pointer to indicate something on the big screen, Agatha said, “I hope that the whispering coming from the middle is about the Labyrinth and nothing else.”
Rio rolled her eyes and sat back in her seat, pulling her laptop out to start taking notes – though they ended up being severely lacking due to her annoyance at Agatha still being strong.

She used the band practise that evening to get out the anger that was still there, hitting the snare and crash with more force than was necessary but damn did it feel good.
