Rio really couldn’t figure Agatha out. Every time she thought she was making progress, Agatha would drag them back about ten paces and Rio wasn’t sure how much more she could handle. It wasn’t fair for Agatha to be doing this to her, to change what was acceptable in the middle of an ongoing conversation and to get mad when Rio didn’t immediately follow the new set of rules that were laid before her. How could she possibly keep up when Agatha’s attitude changed with the direction of the wind?

Was it all some kind of fucked up test? Was Agatha seeing how far she could push her before she broke? If that was the case then Rio wouldn’t allow it to happen, she didn’t care how much it would make Agatha fly off the handle, the next time it happened she would stand her ground and challenge it.

The chance to do that never came, however, because on Thursday night Rio received an email from Agatha telling her that their weekly meetings would be coming to an end. It caught her completely off guard. Granted Agatha was hard to read, but this hadn’t been something that Rio had expected. She knew that the meetings would stop eventually because Agatha had said at the start that they would only continue while she deemed them necessary, but Rio had imagined that this information would have been delivered face to face. She could only read this as an overreaction to the previous day. Childish.

She wasn’t going to let Agatha do this without an explanation, this was entirely unfair and was nothing close to the professionalism that Agatha was so desperate to cling on to.
Rio decided that she was going to catch Agatha after her morning lecture and demand to know what was going on, it was the least that she deserved. Almost every interaction with Agatha had left Rio feeling either irritated or confused and she was done with it. She was finally going to get Agatha to talk to her normally and communicate with her.

Her plan was to get onto campus early and give herself time to properly think about what she wanted to say. She didn’t want to go in half-cocked, speaking erratically. Rio took her time, savouring the look on Wanda’s face as she slowly sucked on her fingers. The redness that was around her eyes had moved into her cheeks, giving them a deep glow and there was a hint of smug satisfaction in her smile.

Wanda took her hand out of Rio’s mouth and led her towards the desk. “I’m not done with you yet. Take your jeans off and sit here.” She tapped the desk like Rio needed clarification.
Rio looked between the desk and Wanda sceptically and Wanda seemed to read her thoughts. “It’s sturdy, trust me.”
That only gave Rio more questions. How often has Wanda had sex in her office? Who has Wanda had sex in her office with? Was it Agatha? Or was it her ex-husband? How much action has this desk seen?
She opened her mouth, ready to voice one of them, but Wanda put a finger to her lips, stopping her. “I didn’t tell you to speak, I told you to sit.”
Rio smirked around her finger and started to slide her jeans down, making sure to maintain eye contact the whole time, and then perched herself at the edge of the desk. She watched Wanda slowly sink to her knees and let her head fall back when Wanda put her face between her thighs. 

__________

Rio had lost track of time, and for a damn good reason. Her legs were shaky, making it difficult to walk, but she still walked with purpose. She still had a mission today and she was going to complete it. She checked Agatha’s schedule and saw that her lecture finished at noon so she made her way to the lecture hall and waited outside until the doors opened and the students came pouring out. She slipped into the room and waited for the last person to leave, and the door to close behind them before speaking – Agatha was busy with her laptop so she didn’t notice Rio standing there.

“Professor Harkness.”
Agatha didn’t look up. “You know when my office hours are, please use them.”
Rio scoffed and crossed her arms. “I’ve spent enough time in your office.”
That made Agatha look up, and when she saw that it was Rio who was speaking her expression hardened. “What do you want, Miss Vidal?”
Rio’s eyebrows shot up. “I want you to speak to me like your equal for a start.”
“In the unlikely event that you become my equal, I shall do as such. But since that is yet to happen I am disinclined to acquiesce to your request.”

Rio tensed her jaw as she felt her pulse quicken in anger. It was a miracle that she had put up with Agatha for so long, but she wasn’t going to continue allowing her to speak to her like shit. “Does putting other people down make you feel better?”
The look in Agatha’s eyes sharpened. “Excuse me?”
Rio stood her ground. “You heard me. Answer the question.”
Agatha casually returned her attention to her laptop and calmly said, “I’m not taking part in whatever ridiculous game you’re trying to play Miss Vidal. I have another lecture to give in half an hour and I need to prepare.”
Rio wasn’t sure what possessed her to do the thing she did next, but by the time she had done it, it was too late. She walked over to the table that Agatha was standing behind, reached out and shut the lid of her laptop, the room was so quiet that the soft click seemed to echo in the space.

Agatha’s head snapped up, her jaw clenched and her eyes wild. “What on earth do you think you are doing?”
Rio turned and walked to the seating bank, settling into the middle seat of the first row. “You’ve got half an hour, so we’re going to have a conversation.” She crossed her legs and let her hands rest on the desk that was attached to the chair. “You can start by answering my question.”
Rio wasn’t lacking when it came to confidence, far from it. She knew who she was and what she stood for, and she wasn’t about to leave without getting what she came for.

Agatha remained silent, just glaring at her with her arms crossed looking wholly unamused by the situation.
“You don’t want to talk now? That’s fine. I can wait until after your next lecture. I’ll just stay right here.” Rio leaned back in the chair and kept her eyes locked on Agatha's.
“What is this really about, Miss Vidal?”
“Your blatant inability to regard anybody with respect.” Rio said without missing a beat.
Agatha exhaled strongly through her nose. “I offer respect to those who deserve it, and right now Miss Vidal, you do not qualify.” She lifted the lid of her laptop again.

Rio hummed as she thought. “Okay, let’s talk about that then. Why do you not deem me worthy of your respect? And you can’t say it’s because I’m a subordinate, you’ve already used that one.”
Agatha rolled her eyes. “I don’t need to explain myself to you, Miss Vidal. But I do need you to leave.” She was forcing her voice to stay level and calm. There was a lot more chance of someone walking past and hearing them in this room than there was in Agatha’s office and Rio used that to her advantage.
“Why are you avoiding my questions? What’s that really about?”
“It’s about you trying to antagonise me and get a reaction, though for what reason I have no idea.” Agatha switched up her tone to a very patronising one. “Are you bored? Lonely? Or are you just a spoiled brat who’s used to getting her own way all the time?”
That made Rio seethe. She leant forwards, feeling the heat starting to rise in her chest. “For a woman in her forties, your immaturity is quite astounding.” She said, her jaw tight and her voice low.

She saw Agatha gasp at her words. It was small, barely audible, but she noticed it. The small rise in Agatha’s chest as she took the breath, the tension that shot into her shoulders, the look of utter disbelief that settled on her face and the way that her neck started to develop a red hue. It was the perfect fuel for the fire that was starting to build within Rio. She wasn't going to storm out this time, she wasn't going to use Wanda as a threat – despite how tempting the new information she had was – and she wasn't going to back down.

She held Agatha's gaze tightly in her own, daring her to respond, to get angry. Agatha continued to scowl at her, her breathing getting heavier as the frustration took hold of her. “You need to leave.” Agatha eventually said, speaking slowly making sure to enunciate every word and crossing her arms tightly.
“I'll leave when you treat me like a person and not just some inconvenience dumped into your life with the sole purpose of making your existence difficult. You chose to be my supervisor, remember?”
“I do remember, and you have made every effort to make me regret that decision ever since.”

Rio scoffed and crossed her arms. “So that's why you stopped the meetings out of the blue? Because after six weeks you finally came to the conclusion that you regret your decision?” 

Agatha's eyes widened and she threw her arms out, laughing humourlessly. “So that's what this is about? You're throwing a tantrum because I decided that you're okay on your own for a bit?” She shook her head in disbelief. “Your codependency issues are not my problem.”
Rio had picked up on the fact that when Agatha feels threatened, she goes on the attack. Firing at her personality, trying to dissect her actions and boil them down to their simplest form in order to invalidate them. “I’m not throwing a tantrum, I’m asking for an explanation. We had a disagreement, which is far from out of the ordinary for us, and then you ‘terminate’ the meetings without telling me why. Forgive me for wanting to know the reason.” Rio kept her voice steady and calm, she wasn’t going to stoop in an attempt to match Agatha.

Agatha sighed and pinched the bridge of her nose. “If I give you a reason, will you leave?”
Rio spread her arms. “That's literally why I’m here.”
Agatha walked round to the front of the table and leaned back against it, letting her hands rest on the edge. “The reason is that you don’t need weekly meetings, you never really did.”
“Then why-”
“Do you want an explanation or not?”
Rio held her hands up and pressed her lips together and Agatha continued.
“I wanted to see if you could keep up with the demand of constantly finding something to research and always be thinking ahead to the next topic whilst still being able to link them together. A PhD is a lot of work and you proved that you were capable of doing that.” She paused but Rio didn’t interrupt her. “However, I did notice a pattern of you showing work about topics that I had given lectures on – or things that you had asked me about like Athena and The Odyssey – and while that is okay, the inspiration on what to research was still coming from me and you can’t rely on me to tell you where you should look next. It is important that you can do independent work and think for yourself.”

Rio didn’t speak for a moment, she just took the time to process and understand what Agatha had said. It all made sense, but there was something that was still bugging her. “So if that’s the truth, then why couldn’t you have just told me that?”
Agatha rolled her eyes. “It is the truth and I don’t have to explain every thought I have to you.”
Rio slowly stood up and stepped off of the seating bank. “Which brings us back to you not seeing me as someone who ranks high enough for a basic level of decency and respect.”
“Miss Vidal, I-”
“Say my name.”
“Excuse me?”
Rio stepped towards Agatha. “Say my first name. You did it once and didn’t burst into flames, so you can do it again.”
Agatha crossed her arms and sighed. “I address you by your surname for the same reason that you address me by mine.”
Rio continued to slowly walk towards Agatha. “That’s not true though, is it? I address you as Professor Harkness as a gesture of politeness and recognition of your title. You say my surname in an effort to do the opposite. To make me less of a person almost. To show that I’m beneath you. We are not the same.” She stopped about two feet from where Agatha was still leaning against the table. She glanced down to Agatha’s hands and saw that her fingers were twitching, restless.

Rio was about to speak again when she heard a voice from outside the room, slightly muffled behind the closed door. “The doors are closed, does that mean that we can’t go in yet?”
The voice was enough to startle both of them and Agatha quickly pushed off of the table and walked back around it to her laptop, firing up the projector and loading up her PowerPoint.
“Well this has certainly been fun, Miss Vidal, but I really do need you to leave now.”
Rio gave a low chuckle. “Okay Agatha.” She stayed long enough to see Agatha’s head snap up and then turned and walked out of the room.

Chapter Notes

Sorry it's been so long since the last update, hopefully the length of this chapter makes up for it a little bit!

Agatha was standing in Lilia’s kitchen leaning against the counter with a glass of red wine in her hand, listening to her friend sing to herself as she finished plating up their dinner.
“Grab a plate and sit down ladies.” Lilia instructed and Agatha and Jen complied, taking their plates and glasses to the table.
When they were all sitting, Lilia raised her glass and said, “a toast to us surviving the first half of the semester.” The three of them knocked their glasses together and took a sip before Lilia continued. “And another toast to Agatha only being in the Dean’s office five times, I’m proud of you.” She winked at Agatha and Agatha rolled her eyes in response but raised her glass anyway.
“I hate you.”
“I know.”

Lilia and Jen were trading stories about students that had impressed them in both positive and negative ways – the negatives were winning this time around – but Agatha wasn’t paying attention. Her mind had drifted to thirty hours earlier, to Rio standing arms length away from her demanding that Agatha call her by her first name. She had been replaying the whole interaction on a loop since Rio had walked out of the lecture hall, muscle memory guiding her through her lectures for the rest of the day since her brain was occupied by a five-foot-something with a sarcastic attitude and an answer for everything.

When she was younger Rio would have been exactly her type. The way that she carried herself, the effortless way that she existed, that smirk. It would have all made her melt. It would have made her want to follow Rio around, it would have made her want to have any excuse to just be near her, in her space, have any shred of Rio’s attention focussed on her. She would have done anything to be on Rio’s radar.
But that was then, and now she was older, she was more mature, and her tastes had changed with her. She had realised that the reason she liked women like that was because they were exactly the type of women that her mother would hate. Her mother hated the fact that she liked women full stop, but a woman like that – like Rio – would make her mothers head explode, and that made them all the more appealing.

She had spent so long moulding herself into something that would piss her mother off that, when her mother died, she didn’t know who she was anymore. Her entire motivation for being the person that she was had vanished and she was left navigating the world without a map, wandering aimlessly searching for something to latch onto, something to give her purpose again.
Her step-father had been just as bad as her mother. At her mother’s funeral he had pulled her aside and told her that she was a disgrace and that she was dishonouring her mother because she had worn a suit instead of a dress – the fact that it was late November had clearly been lost on him and if it had been a summer funeral then she would have absolutely worn a dress.
Her half-sister – who was ten years her junior – had been standing nearby, watching the interaction and making a show of twirling around in the black dress she was dutifully wearing.

But since she no longer lived at home and she wasn’t actually his child, that was the last time he spoke to her. Twenty two years had gone by where Agatha had grown as a person. Twenty two years where she no longer had to hide parts of herself and she could live her life exactly as she wanted and yet she still struggled to do it.
Her mother’s voice was still in the back of her mind judging her for every little thing that she did. The damage that woman had done had burrowed deep within Agatha and its roots had grown too strong and too thick to just be torn out. It had to be carefully dug out. It had to be gently chipped away at and removed with care to make sure that it wouldn’t cause more damage on the way out or just grow back.

Doing so was a long, arduous process and the idea of it scared Agatha. The idea that someone might see those ugly parts of her, the damaged-beyond-repair pieces that she clung onto like a lifeline. Before her mother had died she proudly stood in front of her trauma, letting it push her into certain decisions, letting it be her motivation and her guide, her reason for being. But after her mother died she hid behind it, let it cover her, protect her. It reminded her why it was there, manipulated her into thinking that she needed it, and relied on it to survive. It was there to make sure she didn’t let those things happen to her again. It wouldn’t let her open herself up to more pain. It was the reason that she hadn’t kept any of the friendships that she had at university or had any form of relationship since her mother passed.

She had fought with it when she and Wanda had begun their relationship and it had been an ongoing battle for the first two years. She had managed to quiet it, to push it down when Wanda had shown no signs of leaving. When she had opened up slightly about her past and it hadn’t scared Wanda off. Or when an argument had triggered her fight or flight and Wanda just let her have some time to cool off and figure herself out before finding her so that they could talk it out and make it better. Wanda had understood that she couldn’t help it and that had made it easier to handle.

But then, of course, Agatha had found out that Wanda had cheated on her. She had come home early to surprise both her and Billy and had found Wanda in their bed with her ex-husband, the engagement ring that Agatha had given her two years prior still sitting on her finger.

The door that she had used to seal off all of the negative thoughts and feelings that her mother had supplied her with was blasted off of its hinges and everything came barrelling forwards, racing towards the surface and devouring her, shrouding her in a thick cloud of smoke that blocked out all the light Wanda had previously been the symbol of. It caged her in and broke her down. 
It sat on her shoulder, whispering in her ear, telling her that this was what she deserved, that this was the life she chose and a sinner could never be happy. 

Agatha still couldn’t figure out if Wanda keeping the ring on was better or worse than if she’d have taken it off.

Then a few months later, Vision had the bright idea to go to her and tell her that the time she caught them wasn’t the first and that it had also happened two times before. She had been living at Jen’s house at the time, a pit stop until she found herself a new house, so the fact that he knew where she was meant that Wanda had to have told him and that made her skin crawl. Knowing that Wanda knew where she was living, knowing that she had been keeping tabs on her made her feel dirty, too exposed, unsafe.
The new information also added fuel to the ever-burning fire that her mother had left behind. She could have gone her whole life not knowing that it hadn’t only been a one time thing, a ‘small lapse of judgement’ as Wanda had called it.
He told her that Wanda didn’t know that he was telling her and that he was doing it of his own volition. He didn’t need to mention that it was to alleviate his own guilt, that much was obvious. The subtext was so bold that it might as well have just been text.

It still didn’t make any of it better, it did nothing to loosen the grip that her trauma had on her, it made it tighter. It made her pull back more and shrink further into herself, her self worth ebbing away with every passing second. 

It took Agatha nearly a full year to get back to herself, to put the blame fully on Wanda where it belonged. To build up her walls, carefully laying each brick and reinforcing them so that they wouldn’t come down again. It was protection, self preservation, a means of survival. A way to ensure that no one would come close to tearing her apart the way that Wanda had, that there was no chance that she would be offered the hope of love and a family to have it ripped away from her and shredded to pieces in front of her.
She resigned herself to the fact that, if she hadn’t managed to find a relationship, a level of love that she deserved by the time she turned forty, then it was never going to happen for her. It just wasn’t in the cards.

The way that Rio was so unapologetically herself, not afraid to voice her thoughts, undeterred by people – by Agatha – trying to put her down and make her fit into a box that wasn’t the right shape or size for her. Rio wore her heart on her sleeve and she didn’t care who saw it.

Rio didn’t have anything holding her back. She was incredibly smart and so self-aware that it almost intimidated Agatha.
The way that Rio asked Agatha questions about herself so casually like giving the answers wouldn’t cause something to break within her, and the way that she was always so relaxed until she’d had enough of Agatha’s bullshit was terrifying.
Agatha was used to being able to intimidate people into silence, she was used to being able to control a conversation and guide it in the direction that she deemed the safest, but Rio didn’t let her. She resisted and didn’t back down.

When Rio confronted her the previous day and sat so casually like she owned the room, demanding that Agatha talk to her like they were on the same level, it made Agatha’s chest tighten with a feeling that she didn’t want to name.
Agatha never had to explain herself to anyone other than the Dean, and even then it was only the most simple of explanations, enough to get him off her back until the next time he summoned her. But Rio had sat herself down and made it clear that she wasn’t leaving until she got what she wanted, she had all the time in the world to stare Agatha down and wait patiently for her to finally fold. To finally show her a part of herself that was real instead of the fake, pre-constructed jargon she usually threw out.

She couldn’t keep letting Rio push her boundaries, she couldn’t keep letting Rio burrow her way under her skin and remind her of the confidence and couldn’t-care-less attitude that she had lost when her mother had died. She needed to care, she needed to be cautious, she needed to be sure that she was safe and Rio was a threat to that.

Her hands were twitching, her fingers restless with a nervous energy that she didn’t understand or know how to sate. She had no idea what would have happened had they not been interrupted by the students turning up to attend her lecture.

Agatha looked up, forcing herself to look into Jen’s eyes. They were gentle, shining with worry. “I’m fine.” Agatha said, all too quickly. An answer to a question she didn’t even know if she’d been asked.
Jen smiled, softly, cautiously. She definitely hadn’t asked anything that required the answer that Agatha had hurriedly given.
Jen slowly took her hand away from Agatha’s arm and nodded her head towards her plate. “You’ve barely eaten anything. Where did you go?”

“Do you want me to put it in the microwave for you, warm it up again?” Lilia asked. Agatha said that it was okay but Lilia was already taking the plate from her and taking it back into the kitchen.

Agatha took another bite, the warmth of it now making her realise just how hungry she actually was.
“You’ve already answered, but it was before I actually asked.” Jen started. “Are you okay?”
Agatha nodded, pushing the food to the side of her mouth so that she could speak. “Yeah I’m fine.” She could hardly tell them that she had been thinking about Rio which had caused a spiral that led back to her mother. They would think she was insane.

She watched Jen and Lilia exchange a look before they both returned their eyes to her. She put her fork down and said, “Okay, you two looking at me like I’m a stray puppy you’ve found on the side of the road is really putting me off my food.”
They exchanged another look which made Agatha roll her eyes. “Come on, out with it.”
Lilia spoke first. “It’s just that we were trying to get your attention for a solid five minutes, but you were really out of it. We were starting to worry.”
Agatha ate some more before replying. “You don’t need to worry, I’m perfectly fine. And I’m sure five minutes is an exaggeration.” She knew that it probably wasn’t given the temperature her food had been when she had tried to eat it.
“Right,” Jen began, speaking slowly, choosing how to navigate the sentence, “but you never usually disappear like that. You don’t have to tell us anything, but we can tell when something is wrong.”

Agatha knew that they were coming from a place of concern as her friends, but she couldn’t tell them what she was thinking about. She didn’t know how to describe it to herself, never mind them, but she needed to think of something before they inevitably started guessing. They always said that she didn’t need to tell them anything, but they could never resist.
“It was just your run-of-the-mill disassociation, nothing to write home about.” That clearly wasn’t enough because they started guessing anyway.

“Is it Billy?”
Agatha sighed. “No.”
“Wanda?”
“No.” That one was sharper, quicker. More out of annoyance at them constantly thinking that she was at the centre of Agatha’s thoughts.
“Another student then? Your final years?”
“Nope.”
“Rio?”
The name made her shoulders tense, just for a split second. Unnoticeable if you didn’t know to look for it, if you weren’t trained in spotting such things. Unfortunately for Agatha, Lilia was a professor of psychology, she had multiple degrees in reading people and spotting behaviour patterns. It had been her job for decades before she decided to take a step back and switch to teaching instead of retiring completely.
Her voice remained level, controlled, but Agatha’s eyes subconsciously flicked to Lilia when she answered. “No.”
Huge mistake.

Lilia made a pointed effort to not psychoanalyse them, she had always said that she didn’t want them to feel on edge around her, that they couldn’t be themselves out of fear that she would read into every little thing they said or did – and the vast majority of the time she stuck to it. But sometimes, when she deemed it necessary, she gave into it.

Jen hadn’t noticed anything, so she continued. “Is it the Dean? No, the Dean’s secretary! I know how much you hate her and honestly I can’t blame you.”
Agatha was actively trying to avoid Lilia’s gaze but the woman’s eyes hadn’t left her face, giving Agatha the chance to say it herself but she knew Agatha was too stubborn to do it.
“You can stop guessing Jennifer. She’s already told us.” Her voice was gentle and warm.
Jen stopped mid-sentence, confusion making her wrinkle her brow. “... Huh?”
Lila turned her head in Jen’s direction, her eyes briefly leaving Agatha allowing her to relax slightly in their absence. “It’s Rio.” She turned her head back to Agatha, the weight of her knowing gaze settling back over her making her feel cornered. “Isn’t it?”

Agatha sighed, closing her eyes and dipping her head in defeat. She couldn’t run from it any more, not now that Lilia was aware of it and had made Jen aware of it in turn. She had no choice but to face it head on in the knowledge that anything she couldn’t voice, anything that she didn’t fully understand, Lilia would be able to figure out and help her figure it out as well. There was no turning back now.

Agatha opened her eyes and lifted her head. Jen was still looking thoroughly confused but Lilia looked calm, her face was perfectly neutral giving nothing away. She was good at this.
Agatha took a deep breath to steady herself before she spoke. “I don’t fully understand it, any of it. It’s all a confusing jumble.”
Lilia smiled gently, her eyes crinkling softly at the corners. “That’s okay. It’s my job to understand it, you just need to talk.” Agatha nodded, picking her fork back up and stabbing it into her food trying to think of a way to start. Lilia now fully in ‘work mode’ picked up on this. “Why don’t you start with what happened earlier? Tell me what your thoughts were.”
Agatha half expected her to produce a notepad and start writing down everything she said, but she knew Lilia didn’t need one. The woman had a memory like a steel trap.

Agatha bought herself a few seconds by taking another bite of her food. “Okay so, I’ve been having meetings with Rio since the first Wednesday of the semester and this Thursday I made the decision to stop them. I sent her an email to let her know and that was that.” She paused, looking at Lilia but she only gave a small nod, encouraging her to keep going. “But yesterday she cornered me after a lecture and demanded that I tell her why.”
Lilia spoke up at that. “When you say that she cornered you, what do you mean?”
“I don’t mean that she physically backed me into a corner and intimidated me. I mean that she waited until the lecture was over and came into the lecture hall. She sat herself down and asked for an explanation. Well, she asked for other things before that, but that was the main point of her coming to see me.”

Lilia waited for her to eat another forkful before asking her next question. “What other things did she ask you?”
Agatha thought back to the conversation, the timeline of it had become jumbled in her memory and she wasn’t sure about the order of the things that Rio had said. “I can’t remember it chronologically but there was something about wanting to know why I was avoiding her questions and why I didn’t see her as an equal who was worthy of being respected.” She scoffed lightly, remembering the smug look on Rio’s face as she spoke.
“Okay, and why don’t you see her as someone worthy of your respect?”
Agatha had been playing with her food again whilst speaking but that made her head snap up. She narrowed her eyes. “Who said that I don’t?” Lilia was meant to be on her side, but she had immediately jumped to Rio's defence.

Lilia’s expression didn’t change, neither did the calm neutrality of her voice. “Rio did. She wouldn’t have asked it if there wasn’t some truth in it. Also your immediate defensiveness as you recalled the memory and then again when I asked you why you don’t respect her.”
Agatha rolled her eyes, which was a reaction she was very aware that Lilia would have added to the list of defensive behaviours she had exhibited in the last sixty seconds.

She forcefully assembled the last of her food on her fork and shoved it into her mouth, chewing aggressively. “I do respect her, she just…” She trailed off, not sure how to articulate her thoughts. “She’s annoying. She likes to antagonise me. Forgive me if that pisses me off and lowers my valuation of her.” Agatha knocked back the last of her wine and put the glass back down with a bit more force than was necessary which of course Lilia clocked, but she didn’t mention it thank god. Instead she just asked, “She likes to antagonise you, or you let her antagonise you?”
“I do not let her, she just does it. It’s like her default setting or something. She’s cocky and overconfident.”
“Does she respect you?”
Agatha breathed out a short, humourless laugh. She could provide at least a hundred pages of evidence that would show that Rio definitely did not hold any respect for her. “She claims to but she obviously doesn’t with the way that she tries to push me all the time.”
“Why does that mean that she doesn’t respect you?”

Agatha suddenly became aware of the fact that Jen was still sitting there, watching this evaluation as if she were an audience member watching a film in the cinema. She whipped her head towards Jen. “Are you going to contribute or are you just going to continue sitting there catching flies?” She spat out.
Jen’s eyes went wide but Lilia didn’t give her a chance to respond. “Agatha. Don’t try to deflect your feelings onto Jen, we are both your friends and we’re trying to help you.” Her voice was no longer annoyingly calm, it was a sharp, no-nonsense tone. Agatha had never heard Lilia speak that way and it jolted her. The shock ran through her body and made her brain reset. She turned back to face Jen, slower and calmer this time, her voice softer. “I’m sorry Jen, you didn’t do anything to deserve that.”
Jen smiled, the way it reached her eyes showed that it was genuine. “It’s okay, this is difficult. I won’t take it to heart, don’t worry.”
Agatha returned the smile and gave a gentle nod, a silent ‘thank you.’

Lilia brought Agatha’s focus back to her. “Now, stop avoiding my question. Why does Rio pushing you mean that she doesn’t respect you?” Her voice had slipped back into the neutral tone again.
Rio accusing her of avoiding questions was one thing, but coming from Lilia? It gave her pause. It made her consider that it might actually be something that she did, that there was some truth in Rio’s accusations, and if there was truth in that then what else has Rio been right about? She wasn't ready for that deep dive. She wasn't ready to admit to anything that would favour Rio.

Agatha puffed her cheeks, blowing out a steady breath while she considered how to answer. “Because, if she did respect me, then she wouldn’t be trying to push my boundaries all the time. She would accept it when I say that I don’t discuss my personal life with my students and she wouldn’t ask so many probing questions.”
“What kind of probing questions?”
Agatha thought for a moment, casting her mind back to remember them. “She asked me how I first found my interest in Greek Mythology, what age I was when I first read The Odyssey, who my godly parent would be if I had one,” Agatha paused, considering if she should say the last one or not. Fuck it . “And she asked me about my sexuality.”
Lilia raised a brow. “She asked you what your sexuality is?”
“Not in those words, but essentially yes.”
“How did she phrase it?”
Agatha ran her hand through her hair, trying to remember the exact context of the conversation. “We were talking about Orpheus and Eurydice and I asked her if she thought she would be able to lead Eurydice through the Underworld and pass the test, unlike Orpheus. But I made it clear that I was not asking about her preferences, just about the nature of the test. She said that she didn’t know and offered up the context of her leading Eurydice of her own volition, completely devoid of any prompting from myself. She then asked me the same question and I said something along the lines of if I was in love the way that Orpheus was I could try it and she took that as an opening to ask if I would also be leading Eurydice, which I immediately shut down.”

For the first time since they had started this ridiculous exercise, Lilia’s expression changed. She sighed in exasperation and rolled her eyes, a wholly unprofessional reaction. “Agatha,” She started, her disbelief evident in just the one word. “Rio isn’t asking probing questions. She isn’t even overstepping boundaries. She’s just trying to find something in common with you, something you both share so that she can relate to you a bit. She isn’t challenging you, or questioning your authority, she’s doing a very normal thing called trying to have a conversation. She wasn’t trying to drag some deeply personal information out of you when she asked if you would be leading Eurydice, she was using the context clues from how you phrased your answer to try and find something that you both have an understanding of, something you can both identify with. It’s part of being human.”

Agatha knew that Lilia was very good at her job and that her knowledge of psychology went deeper than anyone could fathom, but it couldn’t be that simple. Rio was sarcastic, she was smug. She saw Agatha as a game to be played and was making damn sure that she would be the winner. “Okay fine, but you haven’t seen her attitude or heard the tone of her voice when she was asking those things. You can't possibly draw that conclusion purely based on the things I've told you.”
Lilia threw her hands up. “Have you considered that it isn’t a personal attack on you? That maybe, that’s just how she is? She can respect you and your authority as her supervisor and also want to get to know you a little bit. The two aren’t mutually exclusive!”
Agatha tried to refute it, she racked her brain for something to say but she couldn’t find anything. The memory of Rio telling her that she spoke to all of her previous lecturers and professors in the same way that she spoke to her flickered through her mind and she hated that it was further proof that Lilia was right.

Lilia, knowing that Agatha had no way of proving her wrong, continued her questioning. “How does she address you?”
Agatha didn’t want to answer, she knew that Lilia was just using anything that she could to drive her point home. “She addresses me as Professor Harkness, the same as everyone else. The way that she should.” She reluctantly said.
“Exactly. She respects your title and I can’t see that stopping unless you give her a reason to, which it sounds like you have been doing. But also, would it be the end of the world if she felt comfortable enough around you to use your name if you gave her permission to? Would it erase any of that respect or control you’re so desperate for?” She gestured between the three of them. “We don’t use each other's titles and yet we all still respect each other.”
“Barely.” It was Jen’s first contribution but it was perfectly timed and Agatha couldn’t help giving into the laughter that Lilia started.

The tension that she had been carrying throughout the whole meal started to fade as she gave into the humour of Jen’s comment. “Well thank you very much for helping me Lilia, you have actually opened my mind a little bit.”
“Oh no, we’re not done.” Lilia said, still laughing.
Agatha rolled her eyes. “You can’t be serious?”
“We’ve barely started, there’s still more that I want to unpack and I’m on a roll.” She shifted uncomfortably in her chair. “We are going to have to move this to the living room though, this chair is starting to fuck with my back.” She stood awkwardly and started limping towards an armchair. “Jen be a dear and fetch the glasses and a fresh bottle would you?”
“You’ve got two hands.” Jen said in disbelief.
Lilia put on a show of holding her back and turning her limp into a shuffle. “Yes but I’m an old woman.”
Jen pointed in Agatha’s direction. “What about Agatha? She’s not carrying anything!”
Agatha shrugged and started making her way to the sofa. “I’m the patient, I can’t be expected to do it.”
Jen threw her hands up. “Ridiculous!” But she got a fresh bottle of wine and gathered up the glasses, bringing them into the living room despite her protests.

Lilia settled into her arm chair and Agatha sat on the sofa opposite her. She felt more at ease about the whole thing now but she was a bit apprehensive about what else Lilia could be interested in.
Lilia had never outright asked any questions about Agatha’s childhood – or, more specifically, her mother – she hadn’t even tried to find out everything about Wanda, she just let Agatha tell her the details as and when she wanted, but Agatha knew that she was interested. It was in her nature to be interested in people's baggage and Agatha had at least four tightly packed suitcases worth, if not more.

Agatha was aware of the fact that Lilia was under no impression that her mind wandering earlier was solely about Rio, she had just been the catalyst for the twisting path that her brain had decided to take her down and Agatha was wary of the things that she might have to confront now that Lilia’s interest was piqued.
She was notoriously a closed book, someone who kept everything locked away, safe from evil hands that might twist it and corrupt it and use it against her. Allowing someone access to that, letting them see it for all it was, letting them reach in and hold it was terrifying.
She knew that she could trust Lilia but it didn’t make bringing her walls down any easier. They were there for a reason, they had a purpose and Lilia was wanting her to bring them down and grant her entry like it was the most simple thing in the world.

Agatha was still processing the revelation that Rio hadn’t actually been doing anything wrong and that she had been overreacting the whole time, she wasn’t sure that she was ready for round two just yet. Especially when she didn’t know what round two entailed.
Jen filled all of their glasses back up and took a seat on the sofa next to Agatha. The three of them took a quiet sip of their wine and Agatha was trying very hard to not show that she was anxiously waiting for Lilia to pick up where they left off. 

“I don’t think I’ve ever seen you this nervous before, Agatha.” Lilia finally said.
Agatha took another drink, trying to appear nonchalant. “I’m not nervous, I’m just waiting for you to start again.” She heard Jen hum her disagreement next to her but kept her attention on Lilia. “Is this the part where you tell me to lie down and close my eyes so we can take a mind walk through my tumultuous childhood and unearth some deep repressed memories?”
Lilia lifted one shoulder noncommittally. “We can do that if you want, though it was never my method of choice.”
“Hmm, pass.”

Lilia set her glass down lightly on the end table to her right and Agatha did the same, making sure to get the round base of the glass perfectly central on the square coaster. In that moment she truly understood what Lilia had meant when she said that she didn’t want Agatha and Jen to be on edge and worried that their every move would be scrutinised, because that was exactly how she felt right now. She was second guessing everything she did and wondering if it was a sign of something that Lilia was tucking away to bring up later on.

Lilia crossed her legs and settled back into the chair. “We’ve spent some time on Rio so I want to move on from her for a bit.” Agatha felt a small amount of relief at that. “Let’s talk about your visits to the Dean a few weeks ago, walk me through that.”
The relief instantly vanished.
“We already talked about that and you reduced it down to me, what were your exact words?” Agatha made a show of pretending to think. “Oh yes, ‘needing to get laid.’” She curled her fingers in air-quotes.

Jen snorted quietly next to her which earned her an eye roll from Agatha and Lilia nodded. “I stand by it and I can tell that it hasn’t happened yet.”
Agatha let an annoyed breath loose from her nose. “Well of course it hasn’t happened. You two are unfortunately the only people that I spend a significant amount of time with.” She gestured between Jen and Lilia. “So unless either of you wants to volunteer, then it doesn’t look likely.”
Lilia laughed. “Thanks but you’re not my type. Jen might be down though.”
“No thanks, I don’t shit where I eat.” Jen said whilst shaking her head.

Agatha sighed and pinched the bridge of her nose. “I thought we were talking about the Dean.”
Lilia spread her arms and shrugged. “I tried but you deflected.”
“Well I’m un-deflecting, let’s get back to him.”
Lilia laced her fingers together and rested her hands in her lap, her face neutral once again. “Okay, so what was happening to cause you to act in a way that got you pulled into his office so frequently?”
Agatha adjusted herself on the settee, shuffling more into the corner, seeking comfort in the cushion that she pulled into her lap. “I don’t know. I guess I just had some repressed feelings to get out.” As she was speaking she stopped looking at Lilia and instead focussed on a stray piece of thread that was sticking out of the corner of the cushion.

Lilia didn’t do anything to try and shift Agatha’s focus, she just asked, “What kind of repressed feelings?”
Agatha started twisting the thread between her thumb and index finger, watching it spin. “Just feelings, I don’t know.”
“Right but feelings come from somewhere, they’re rooted in something. So what feelings were they?”
Agatha sighed. “I don’t fucking know, Lilia. Frustration? Anger?” She started to pull at the loose thread. “Having to hold myself back.”
She still wasn’t looking up but she heard Lilia shift in her chair, the fabric groaning softly against the wooden frame.
“Why were you holding yourself back?”
Agatha tugged at the thread again and it started to unravel from the seam. Shit. She looked up at Lilia again and saw that she had uncrossed her legs and was leaning forwards, resting her forearms on her legs with her hands still clasped. She looked to her left at Jen who was just slowly sipping her wine, listening intently.

Agatha dipped her head for a second but forced herself to look back at Lilia. “Because I… because…” She trailed off not being able to find her words and even if she could find them, she wouldn’t know how to phrase them.
Lilia’s voice and face remained neutral and calm and Agatha had to admit that it was helping her feel safe. “Because of what?”
She could lie, it would be so easy. She could blame her mother, it wasn’t like she was here to defend herself. Hell she could even say that it was because Billy had asked her to speak to Wanda again. It would fool Jen but Lilia would know, and with Lilia actively looking out for tells, it would only drag the whole thing out and make it worse.
“Because of Rio.” Agatha eventually said.

Lilia raised her eyebrows slightly and leaned back again. “Why Rio?”
Agatha returned her attention to the cushion and its slowly unravelling seam. “I thought you said we weren’t talking about her.”
“We weren’t, but you brought her up again.”
For fuck sake.
Agatha picked at the seam some more, pulling more of the thread away from the cushion. “Okay fine, whatever. I was stopping myself from snapping at her and from rising to her attempts at pushing my buttons, so that annoyance had to go somewhere.” She lifted her gaze once more to give both Jen and Lilia a pointed look. “But none of what I said or did was invalid. Everyone deserved it.”
Lilia smiled. “Oh, I’m sure.”
“Yes I’m sure that poor barista deserved to be told that they were a disappointment to their parents.” Jen added.
Agatha chuckled to herself. “Okay, maybe that one was worded a tad too harshly, but you didn’t see how slowly they were moving, and I was going to be late.”
Jen sighed and shook her head.

Lilia reached for her glass and took a few sips, allowing the levity to sit for a moment before bringing Agatha back. “So the common theme that I’m seeing so far is your feelings towards Rio.”
Agatha picked up her own glass and sipped it before responding. “I don’t have any feelings towards Rio, and she’s only the common theme because those are the things that you’re asking me about.” 
“I’m asking about those things because those are the ones that are relevant right now.” Lilia said, a little too curtly for Agatha’s liking.
Agatha scoffed and quirked an eyebrow. “You’re the one that started this whole thing, Lilia. Don’t get snippy with me.”
“I’m not getting snippy, you’re getting defensive.” The calmness that Agatha found comforting five minutes ago was now starting to get on her nerves.
Agatha huffed and crossed her arms. “I’m not getting defensive.” She snapped.

Lilia didn’t speak, she simply moved her eyes down and nodded her head to where Agatha had tightly crossed her arms and then moved them over to Jen and raised her eyebrows. A silent question which Jen answered with a half smile and a nod.
The inaudible exchange annoyed Agatha. They did this too often and it pissed her off. “Okay fuck you both and your ability to read each other’s minds. Just speak out loud like normal people.”
Lilia took a deep breath and steadily exhaled it. “Why are you guarded right now? Which part of you are you protecting?”
“I’m protecting whichever part of me you’re picking at right now.” Agatha said with a sneer.
“I’m not picking at you, you’ve got your back up about something and I’m trying to help you figure out what that is.” Lilia smiled sweetly which only made Agatha prickle more.
“I’ve got my back up because you’re trying to find connections where there aren’t any. But if you’re so wise and all-knowing, why don’t you just tell me what it is?”
“Because it’s important that you work it out for yourself.”

Having not been able to get a rise from Lilia, Agatha turned on Jen again. “I assume that look was her asking you if you’ve figured it out?” Jen looked at Lilia. “What do you need her fucking permission to speak now or something? Did she cast a spell on you to make you silent?”
“Agatha Harkness!”
Lilia’s raised voice and clipped tone instantly got her attention and she could feel the burning sensation start to rise in her cheeks. “I will not tolerate you attacking Jen. This isn’t about us, this is about you not being able to confront your own feelings and using that as a reason to lash out at the nearest person.”
Agatha was startled by the way that Lilia was speaking to her. She had never seen this side of Lilia before and she definitely didn’t like it. She could feel the redness blooming on her face and making its way into her ears but she couldn’t speak due to her shock. All she could do was sit there with her mouth hanging open looking at Lilia and feeling like a little kid enduring one of her mothers many tirades.

Lilia’s eyes were sharp and held Agatha’s in a vice grip. “Rio is the common denominator in your behaviour of late because you like her.” All sense of calm had now left Lilia’s demeanour and frustration had taken over in its wake. She was no longer gently guiding Agatha through this and instead, was shoving her head first into a confrontation with herself that was long overdue.
But Agatha, true to form, dug her heels in. “I do not like Rio. How old are we, twelve?”
The accusation was completely without merit. A suggestion that should never have been given life. Sure Rio would have been her type twenty five years ago, but that was twenty five years ago. She wasn’t the same person she was when she was in her teens – something Jen and Lilia should be very grateful for.

Jen threw her hands up, breaking Agatha out of the hold of Lilia’s gaze. “You like her, you’re attracted to her, you have a crush on her. It doesn’t matter how you phrase it, the meaning remains the same.” She turned to face Agatha fully. “You’re just too afraid of getting hurt to see what’s right in front of you. Rio gets under your skin the way that she does because you like her, and that’s okay.”
Agatha drained the rest of her glass and placed it back on the coaster, once again making sure it was perfectly centred. She could feel Lilia’s eyes on her, watching her adjust the glass until she was happy with the alignment. “I suppose you’re going to say that me doing this is a sign of sexual frustration or whatever Freudian bullshit is your go to.”
“Actually,” Lilia began, the edge to her voice dulling, “I was going to say that you don’t have to feel out of control right now. Lining up the glass like that speaks more to your need to have a tight grip on your surroundings when you don’t feel like you’re in charge of your emotions. You’ve been denying this for so long and trying to push it down that it’s been manifesting in different ways.” She leaned back in the arm chair, adopting a more relaxed posture after sitting in the tension that had just taken over the room. “I do agree that you’re sexually frustrated though, you should really do something about that.” She smirked.

Agatha rolled her eyes and began absentmindedly messing with the seam on the cushion again. They were both being ridiculous and were way off base. Rio was no longer the type of woman that she was attracted to, she liked more mature women – not necessarily older women, but women who conducted themselves in a more grown-up way. Rio didn’t take things seriously enough, everything was either a joke or some sort of game to her and that was something that Agatha did not enjoy in the slightest.
If she was forced to, at gunpoint, then she could maybe admit that Rio was attractive. Only in the conventional sense, it didn’t mean that Agatha found her attractive. They were two very different things. She wasn’t in denial about anything, they were just simply wrong.

The seam on the cushion had fully come undone now and she was gently rolling some of the stuffing into a ball in her palm. The texture of it was somehow soft and wiry at the same time, the kind of fibres that felt like they should make a creaking sound when rubbed together, but she couldn’t hear anything.

Agatha sighed. “I’m not denying anything, you’re just incorrect.” She didn’t look up, but she heard Jen’s gasp and could feel Lilia’s eyes going wide as she took in the words.
“The fact that you couldn’t look at me while you said that implies that you know how wrong that statement is.” Lilia said. “But it’s clear that we’re not gonna get any further tonight so I shan’t rise to it.”
Agatha finally looked up and regarded Lilia with a cautious look. “Great, so does that mean that this topic is dropped and we never have to speak of it again?”
Lilia pursed her lips as she considered the question. “Sure. For now. But you’re going to have to confront this at some point, Agatha. It isn’t healthy to continue on like this.” She raised an eyebrow and pointed at the cushion that Agatha had basically destroyed. “I want that mending as well.”
Agatha rolled her eyes and put the cushion back in its spot on the settee. “I’ll buy you a new one.”
“I don’t want a new one. I want you to fix that one.”
Agatha made a noise of malcontent and said, “fine,” through gritted teeth.

She sat up properly and turned to Jen, giving her an apologetic look. “I’m sorry for what I said and how I said it earlier.”
Jen smiled. “You don’t need to apologise. I’m not saying that I like being your target, but it’s better that it’s me rather than some poor, unsuspecting shop worker or student.”
Agatha dipped her head slightly in embarrassment before coming back up to meet Jen’s eyes. “I appreciate that, but I’m doing it anyway.”
“I accept.”

When Agatha got home around an hour later, her mind was swimming. Of course that could partially be due to the wine – she really should stop driving to these Saturday night get-togethers. She was rooting through her drawers for a t-shirt to sleep in and was stopped in her tracks. Buried right at the bottom of a pile, pushed so far into the back corner was an old, crumpled, white shirt. The design was so faded that it was barely visible but she recognised it instantly. She pulled it out and laid it on her bed, staring at it.

It was an Oasis shirt from a decades old tour, insignificant in the fact that it was one of many old pieces of band merch that she had collected over the years, wholly significant in the fact that it wasn’t hers. She had never been a fan of Oasis, if one of their songs came on while she just had a playlist going in the background as she was doing something then she wouldn’t turn it off, but she didn’t actively seek them out. Wanda, however, was a very big fan of their music. The shirt was hers. A relic both in age and meaning.

The first time that she had slept at Wanda’s house she had spilled something on the shirt that she had brought to sleep in and Wanda had given her the Oasis one as a replacement. She had taken it home with her after that weekend and kept it the whole time they were together. Wanda often teased her about wanting it back because she wanted to sell it, but she never made any attempt to actually get it back, letting Agatha continue to use the shirt as a pyjama top.

Agatha sat on the edge of her bed next to the shirt. Looking at it now nearly two years after their break -up, she didn’t know how to feel. There was nostalgia attached to it, memories of a better time when she was happy. Memories of living with Wanda and Billy and being the family unit that she never got to experience growing up. Memories of when Wanda made her feel like the most special person in the world. But those memories were tinged with sadness and anger and hatred.
They were blurred by the image of Agatha walking into the bedroom, her bedroom, to see Wanda and Vision tangled in the sheets. The edges of the polaroids that she had turned those memories into were charred from when she had tried to erase them, tried to forget about those four years and put them behind her.

When she had hurriedly packed her suitcase that one afternoon she must have accidentally grabbed the shirt along with her other clothes. It was entirely possible that, since she’d had it for so long and worn it so often, she had forgotten that it wasn’t actually hers and had picked it up out of habit. Either way it had been a mistake and the shirt had ended up being accidentally shoved into the back of her drawer and hidden away.
Until now when the universe decided that it wanted to fuck with her.

She ran her fingers over the fabric and gently traced the faded logo that was printed on it.
“Why now?” She asked to her empty bedroom. There was no answer of course, she would have questioned her sanity if she had heard one. Still, that didn’t stop her from wanting one, needing one.
Every part of Wanda had been erased from her life, save for the ones that she couldn’t actually shift like their jobs and Billy. Now this.
She should throw it away, burn it, just get fucking rid of it. But she stayed sitting next to it just staring at it, completely at a loss for what to do. She could give it to Billy, he had a collection of ‘vintage’ band shirts, or at least he used to – the fact that Oasis were nowhere near old enough to be considered vintage aside – it could be a two-birds-one-stone situation. She’d be able to get rid of the shirt and when Wanda saw him with it, it would fuck with her.

Agatha let herself indulge in the moment of schadenfreude that the thought provided. Knowing that Wanda would recognise the shirt instantly and would also have to hear Billy tell her that he got it from Agatha made her smile darkly.
But she couldn't do it. She couldn't use Billy like that, that was something Wanda would do and she would not, under any circumstances, act the way that Wanda acted. Even if giving Billy the shirt was purely because she knew that he would like it, there would still be some part of it that was about getting to Wanda. She wasn't going to do that to him.

She folded the shirt up and put it on top of her dresser to decide what to do with it at a later date, and pulled a different shirt from her drawer to sleep in. She crawled into bed and pulled her quilt up so that it rested under her chin and let out a long, heavy sigh. Agatha wasn’t a spiritual person, she didn’t believe in fate or destiny but she couldn’t help feeling like finding that shirt now carried some meaning. Finding something that belonged to her ex-fiancée the same night that her friends had unceremoniously shoved her into the realisation that she might like someone else couldn’t just be a coincidence could it?

As she laid there with her eyes open, knowing that sleep wasn’t going to come any time soon, she couldn’t stop her thoughts from wandering through the twisted path that was Rio Vidal.
She couldn’t recall all of their interactions in perfect order but there were ones that stood out more than others.

There was their first official meeting, the one that Rio had shown up to ten minutes late sporting an obvious hangover. Agatha had admired Rio’s confidence in still coming in to face her, despite the potential embarrassment and possible chastisement, but of course Agatha had let her off with a warning. A courtesy rarely awarded to anyone, but that was only because of the way that she had acted previously, it wouldn't have been fair to reprimand Rio. Then again, she never usually cared about what was ‘fair’. If a student acted out of line, they acted out of line and were treated accordingly.
But she was allowed to offer politeness to people when she thought they needed it. Rio was deeply apologetic and clearly embarrassed by the situation so reprimanding her wouldn’t have served any purpose.

There was the day that Rio had decided to start bringing Agatha a coffee for their meetings. No other student had done this, it was probable that no other student had had the confidence to do this, but Rio had. Rio had taken the time to actually find out what her order was and bring it to her. Of course she’d had to play a joke first by offering her that horrid iced coffee before swapping the cups and looking entirely too happy with the reaction that Agatha had given her, but she had still gone out of her way to find out what Agatha ordered and made it part of her routine going forwards.

The time that they’d had an argument about Agatha not wanting to tell Rio the age she was when she first read The Odyssey flashed through Agatha’s brain. Rio had so casually thrown Wanda out as a threat as if she had known that it would make Agatha back down, and it had.
Lilia had helped her realise that she had overreacted and she had to admit that she regretted it. She shouldn’t have flown off the handle the way that she did, it didn’t achieve anything, it only made Rio double down and made the whole situation worse than it needed to be.

But none of this equated to liking her. Using the word like in that context made Agatha’s skin itch. It was immature, juvenile. She was forty two for christ sake, she didn’t like people, it was a very high school way of phrasing things. Even when she was in high school she hadn’t used that phrase, she hadn’t cared enough about the girls that she slept with to get to a point of liking them. She only needed them to be around long enough to piss off her mother and step father.
An argument could be made in favour of her liking Wanda, but Agatha preferred saying things like, ‘I find her attractive’, or, ‘I’m drawn to her personality’. It was more mature and more articulate. It was just better.

The memory of her dream about Rio came careening into her skull and it made her cringe. She thanked every deity imaginable that she hadn’t brought it up earlier that evening, Lilia would never have let her hear the end of it.
She maintained that it didn’t mean anything, that dreams weren’t a representation of your wants or desires. It could have been anybody in that dream, the fact that it was Rio was completely irrelevant; she just happened to be the face that Agatha’s subconscious had randomly picked.

Agatha was officially done with this spiral that she had sent herself on, so she rolled onto her side and tried to go to sleep. She shut her eyes and focussed only on the dark expanse that the back of her eyelids created. She tried to quiet her brain by using an old technique of reciting the phonetic alphabet in time with her breathing, but by the time she had gone through it for the third time, she decided to give it up as a bad job. Her mind wasn’t going to let her sleep.
Why did Lilia have to choose now to remind her how good she was at her job?

Agatha woke up the following morning very aware of the fact that she hadn't had enough sleep at all. She wanted so badly to go back to sleep and get the rest that she needed. It was a Sunday after all and she had nothing to do, but she forced herself to keep her eyes open and roll out of bed. She drowsily brushed her teeth, noticing the dark circles under her eyes straight away, and did her morning skincare routine. She wasn’t convinced that it even did anything but it was more out of habit than actually expecting results at this point.

She changed into her usual Sunday attire – her old Yale hoodie and a pair of navy sweatpants – and padded downstairs to get some breakfast. Treating herself to a truly lazy Sunday she opted for just a bowl of cereal and glass of orange juice, too tired to even bother making a cup of coffee, and curled up on the sofa. She was part way through a Gossip Girl rewatch, a guilty pleasure that she actually felt no guilt towards in the slightest, so she picked up where she left off as she munched on her cereal.

When she had finished her bowl she retrieved her sewing kit from the spare room and picked up Lilia’s cushion that she had all but destroyed the previous night. She considered taking the easy option and just doing a running stitch along the seam, but it wouldn't match the other seams and she could already feel Lilia’s disappointment at her even thinking about phoning it in. She would have to suck it up and do a ladder stitch. It wasn’t that she couldn’t do a ladder stitch, it was that they were annoying and she often had to restart them at least three times to get it right.

She finished the seam and admired her work. There were no loose pieces of thread hanging out, which had been the reason the cushion had come undone in the first place. If that hadn’t been there, then she wouldn’t have been messing with it and she wouldn’t have had to fix the shoddy sewing work. Technically speaking, the cushion coming undone hadn’t fully been her fault and she would only accept partial blame for it.

She attempted to zone out and only have her attention on the TV, following Chuck and Blair’s numerous antics and trying not to see Joe Goldberg instead of Dan Humphrey every time Penn Badgley was on screen. But her mind couldn’t stay still. It kept wandering off in different directions that ultimately led to the same destination. She was beginning to wonder if she’d ever be able to stop thinking about Rio.
Maybe Lilia and Jen were right…

Agatha had caught herself staring at Rio more times than she wanted to think about. She never intended on doing it, it just sort of happened. Her eyes would subconsciously drift in whichever direction Rio was from her and then they would stay there until Rio caught her, or she caught herself, and she’d have to make up some thinly veiled excuse for why her attention had been focussed on her for so long.

Using ‘I find her intriguing’ as a way to explain it away to herself could only work for so long before she had to admit what was really going on. Despite her detestation of the word, she had to use it. She liked Rio.
She’d liked Rio since she’d first seen her in the crowd of first year students that had attended her first lecture of the year, since she’d called her out on being wrong about the origin of Heracles’ name.

“Which part of you are you protecting?”
Lilia’s question repeated in her head. Which part of herself was she protecting? Her heart was the obvious answer but it was more than that. There was some part of her that was holding back, it had stopped her from realising that she had feelings for Wanda for nearly a year before Jen and Lilia had basically held an intervention for her to make her see it… She was beginning to sense a pattern.
But that apprehension had turned out to be correct. Wanda had cheated on her two times, she had said yes to marrying her, worn the ring that Agatha had bought and still slept with someone else for a third time. Who was to say that this time would be any different? 

__________

Agatha was finishing up her Monday morning lecture and Rio hadn’t attended. After their last conversation Agatha hadn’t expected her to, but part of her had stupidly still hoped that she would have.
Billy gave her a smile as he walked past her towards the door and she asked him to wait behind. When everyone had left she said, “I was wondering if you’d like to come round for dinner at some point this week.”
“Yeah, for sure. What day did you have in mind?” He replied, an excited smile making his eyes shine.
“Whichever day works for you. You can bring Alice as well if you want.”
“Oh, amazing.” He looked towards the door where she assumed Alice would be waiting on the other side. “I’ll ask her and text you later?”
Agatha ruffled his hair. “Sounds good kid.”

She waited for Billy to leave, giving herself five minutes before following him out, nipping back to her office to pick up the cushion, and walking across campus to Lilia’s office. She knocked on the door and walked in upon Lilia’s approval, holding the cushion up and waving it a little before putting it on one of the chairs.
Lilia smiled and stood up from her desk, making her way over to Agatha and picking up the cushion to inspect it. “This is a lot neater than I was expecting, Harkness. I’m impressed.”
Agatha scoffed. “I am offended that you thought my sewing skills would be anything less than excellent.”
Lilia chuckled. “Well I know your kind are known for their nimble fingers, but this is precision work. Some people just don’t have the talent.”
Agatha rolled her eyes but didn't deign to respond to her friend's silly comment.

She stayed standing in Lilia’s office, wanting to say something else but struggling to find the words. Thankfully Lilia picked up on her awkward demeanour. “Was there something else you came to me for, Agatha?”
Agatha swapped her weight from one foot to the other before steeling herself and forcing the words to come out of her mouth. “Yes actually.” She paused to clear her throat. “I realised yesterday that you might have a point… about Rio.”
Lilia laughed and sat in the chair. “Obviously.” She gestured to the chair opposite her. “Sit. I have half an hour.”
Agatha gave the chair an apprehensive look. “Thanks, but I don’t need another session. I’m not in denial anymore.”
“This isn’t a session, it’s two friends having a chat.”
Agatha rolled her eyes but sat down anyway. “Nothing is gonna come of it, so I don’t know why you’re so invested.”
Lilia lifted an eyebrow. “Why do you think nothing is going to come of it?”

Agatha thought about it for a moment. Were there any actual reasons that she could give, or was this just self sabotage?
The age gap was a glaringly obvious one. There were twelve years between them and thinking about it like that made her feel uneasy.
“Because she’s a student. She’s my student. Also, she might not be single.”
Lilia nodded her head in understanding. “Fair points, but you don’t know that she isn’t single.”
Agatha made a sound of dismissal. “Please, a woman like Rio? I would put money on the fact that all the twenty-something-year-old queer girls on this campus are falling over themselves to chase after her.”
“Careful Harkness. You’re sounding a little jealous.” Lilia said with a smirk.
Agatha rolled her eyes. “Piss off. Even if she is single, she’s still a student so I would never pursue anything with her anyway.”
“A PhD student.” Lilia corrected. “She’s not a teenager. And it’s not illegal, just…” She waved her hand through the air while she was trying to find the right phrasing. “Morally grey.”

Agatha shook her head. Morally grey was one way to put it for sure. “It’s also fucking embarrassing.” She ran her hand through her hair. “I’m forty two years old with a… crush ,” she made a face like the word left a bad taste in her mouth, “on a thirty year old who also just happens to be one of my students.” 
Lilia leaned forwards, resting her elbows on her legs and sitting her chin on her clasped hands. “It’s okay to embarrass yourself a little in the pursuit of human connection.”
She said it like it was the easiest thing in the world, like it wouldn’t get Agatha fired if Rio reported her for unwanted advances or sexual harassment.
Then again Rio hadn’t reported her for anything thus far so maybe she wouldn’t. Maybe she liked Agatha as well, maybe it wouldn’t be such a bad idea to at least try. But of course Agatha had already fucked up any chance of it happening by acting like a prize idiot in treating Rio like shit and cutting off their meetings. Even if she wanted to, she had no way of progressing with this now. She had ruined it like usual.

Agatha sighed. “That may be so, but I’m pretty sure I’ve made her hate me by now.”
Lilia gave a kind smile. “You never know unless you try.”
If only it were that easy. “And how do I do that?”
“You’ve got to figure that one out for yourself, I can’t do everything for you.”
Agatha hated it when Lilia was right, but she couldn’t fight her, she knew that she had to do this by herself.

This slow burning fire is finally getting stoked tee hee

Wanda

Chapter Notes

It's the return of everyone's favourite ginger!

See the end of the chapter for more notes

If someone had told Wanda that at forty-two she would be a divorced mother to an eighteen-year-old, who spent most of her time sleeping with someone who was twelve years younger than she was, she would have laughed in their face and told them that they needed to seek help. Wanda breathed out as much of a laugh as she could manage before saying, “well I’m glad it didn’t, that was some of your best work.”
Rio laughed softly and finished getting dressed, making her way out of Wanda’s bedroom.
Wanda propped herself up on her elbows and shouted after her. “What, no goodbye kiss?”
She didn’t need to see Rio to know that she was laughing and shaking her head.
She listened for the soft click of her front door opening and closing, letting her know that Rio had left.

She leaned back again, this time shifting herself so that she was leaning against the headboard. She found herself craving a cigarette, there really wasn’t anything that matched the feeling of a cigarette after sex, but she hadn’t smoked in years and there were none in her house. She would definitely have to remember to buy a packet for next time.
She sighed at the lack of nicotine and picked up her phone, there were six messages. Five from her ex-husband and one from Billy.

The message was followed by three gifs all portraying various different ways to say happy birthday. One was a cake with a sparkler candle, the second one was a tortoise in a party hat and the final one was a cartoon of a pea that had a smiling face and sticks for arms and legs that said “Hap-PEA Birthday!”

Vision: I didn’t get chance to post your card so I’ll swing by your office in the afternoon to give it to you

She tapped out a quick reply.

Wanda: Thank you! I’m free between two and three

Vision: Roger that! 🫡

She smiled and opened Billy’s message.

Billy: Happy birthday!

Wanda: Thank you darling 😊

Billy didn’t reply further so she took that as her cue to get ready for bed.
