Her Monday morning lecture wasn’t until ten so she would usually get to campus around nine, but given that it was her birthday she knew that the Head of Department would put on a pseudo party in the staff room under the guise of an emergency meeting.
Sure enough when she woke up and checked her phone there was a message on Teams.

Dottie Jones: Meeting in the staff room at 8am sharp. Everyone must attend.

Wanda smiled, everyone knew that she did this for people’s birthdays but she clearly enjoyed it so no-one said anything against it. It was also just a kind gesture since she bought some decorations, a cake, candles and a few snacks out of her own pocket for every staff member in the Ancient History department who had a birthday during term time.

Wanda showered, got ready for the day and set off to the campus, making sure to swing by the petrol station first to pick up a packet of Benson and Hedges to enjoy post coitus – and at fifteen Great British Pounds per pack, she would make fucking sure that she enjoyed them.
When she had quit smoking nearly a decade ago it had mainly been because the prices had risen too much and she couldn’t justify paying that much every time she bought a new packet. Oh how she wished for those prices again. Fifteen pounds was an absolute joke.

She put the cigarettes in her bag and walked into the Ancient History building, heading straight for the staff room. She opened the door and was greeted with a cheer of “happy birthday!” and a few party poppers going off, covering her in streams of brightly coloured tissue paper. Though she knew it was happening, the smile that she wore was genuine as she looked around the room and saw the happy birthday banner on the wall with a foil balloon held down by a weight floating next to it. On one of the tables in the centre of the room there was a cake with a pile of cards in envelopes and a few gift bags sitting next to it.

Every lecturer in the department was there, except for Agatha but that was a given, and they all gathered around her as she was ushered towards the cake for the candles to be lit and Happy Birthday to be sung. They all clapped when she blew out the candles and she started opening the cards. A few of them had some money in them and there was one that had an obnoxiously large badge that was pink, sparkly and read ‘birthday girl’ in all caps that she was instructed to wear for the entire day. She tried to put up some resistance but folded pretty quickly and pinned it to her cardigan.

The cake was cut and split between everyone and people started to slowly filter out to go teach their lectures and do whatever work they needed to do, leaving Wanda, Dottie and a couple of stragglers who were making the most of the free snacks.
Dottie turned to Wanda. “I’m sorry it wasn’t much, but I hope you liked it.”
Wanda smiled. “Dottie, it’s lovely that you even thought about it. We all appreciate that you do this for us.”
Dottie returned her smile. “It’s just a shame that not everyone joins in.”
Wanda knew who she was talking about, she was referencing Agatha’s lack of attendance.

Agatha hadn’t gone to a single one of the birthday gatherings since they had broken up and Wanda didn’t blame her. The staff had treated Agatha pretty harshly when Wanda had told them the lie that Agatha had cheated on her, a lot of them judged her from afar and conveyed their dislike of her through their facial expressions and body language, but a few of them had had the courage to actually talk to her about it. They had  asked questions, asked how and why she could have possibly done that to Wanda and told her that she was a terrible person for hurting Wanda like that. Agatha had ignored them and done nothing to defend herself or try and set the story straight. She had just let them believe the lies that Wanda had told them and it had confused Wanda but she was also grateful that Agatha hadn’t pushed back because she didn’t know how she would have handled it.

Wanda had gotten everyone on her side so easily, and at first she liked it. People were being extra nice to her, checking on her and making sure that she was never alone with Agatha. They were offering to take a couple of her lectures if she needed some time to herself and offering to have her and Billy round for dinner so that they weren’t alone in the house too much.
She took on the gestures and accepted them all because, while the story they all knew wasn’t true, she was still hurting. She was still going through a break-up and was trying to soothe Billy through it as well.

Billy had been the reason why she had lied. Wanda had loved Agatha, she really had, but it went beyond that for Billy. She realised not long after she had first introduced them that Billy had formed an attachment to Agatha, a bond that connected them more than he was connected to her, his mother, and she had been jealous. Billy went to Agatha with everything, she was his best friend, his favourite person on the planet, his support system.
After he had come out to the two of them Agatha had later told her that he had actually come out to her first and that she had convinced him to come out to them together so that Wanda’s feelings weren't hurt.

She had seen the break-up as a chance to claim back some of the love that he had supplied Agatha with in the four years that they had been together, a chance to show him that she could be everything he saw Agatha as and more. So when she had lied to him, she’d had to lie to everyone else as well. She had to keep the ruse up so that she could keep Billy.
Wanda had been scared that if he had known the truth straight away he would have followed Agatha out of the door and never gone back. He would have chosen Agatha over her and the thought of it tore her heart in two.

Two and a half years on though, she regretted it. Agatha was always able to take hits and let them roll off her like they were nothing, but after being with her for four years Wanda was able to tell when the jabs had hit their mark. The subtle twitch in her eye, the small beat as she composed herself before responding, the slight downturn in the corners of her mouth. Wanda had seen all of these in every interaction Agatha had had with their colleagues following the split. Wanda was safely cocooned in the web that she had spun and she had left Agatha to fend for herself against the elements.

The fallout had died down and people had moved on from making their remarks but the damage had been done, and any relationships that Agatha had with the other staff members in their department had been destroyed. The window where Wanda could have made things right had long since closed, and she was left looking through it, watching Agatha exist on the outside, forever tarred with the brush that Wanda had painted her with. And now that Billy actually knew the truth, knew that it had been Wanda that had cheated on Agatha and she had manipulated everyone including him, their relationship had been strained. She hadn’t told him why she had lied, but just knowing that she had was enough to make him distance himself and she knew that there was no way that she could fix it.

Wanda moved her gaze away from Dottie's eyes when she replied. “You can’t really blame her though. She never fully recovered from the way that she was treated.”
“Yeah, I suppose.” Dottie put a reassuring hand on Wanda’s shoulder. “Well anyway, happy birthday. I have to actually go do some work now so I’ll see you later!” Dottie gave her shoulder a squeeze before leaving.

She wasn’t sure what kind of game Agatha was trying to play, but she was going to put a stop to it.
She picked up her phone and sent Agatha a message.

Wanda: We need to talk

She didn’t need to wait long for the reply.

Agatha: I doubt that

Wanda: Let me rephrase. We will be talking on Monday.

Agatha: Let me know how that goes for you

Wanda clenched her jaw and exhaled through her nose. She was going to put this out of her mind until Monday, Agatha wasn’t going to ruin her night with Vision and Billy.

Wanda knew when Agatha’s downtime was on a Monday, she knew when her downtime was every day. Agatha hadn’t changed her schedule since before she got her professorship and Wanda was choosing that Monday as the day that she would make her regret it.

Wanda waited outside Agatha’s office for a few seconds to check if she could hear anyone in there with her, but it was silent so she walked straight in.
“It is basic manners to knock upon a door and wait for permission before entering.” Agatha said, not looking up from her laptop.
Wanda smiled and forced sweetness into her voice. “Oh, I think we’re past basic manners at this point. Don’t you, Agatha?”
Agatha’s head snapped up at the recognition of Wanda’s voice. She tensed her jaw and slowly removed her glasses, setting them on the keyboard of her laptop before placing her elbows on her desk and resting her chin on her clasped hands. “Well this ought to be good.”

Wanda stormed forwards, stopping at the edge of Agatha’s desk. “That’s all you have to say to me?”
Agatha leaned back in her chair, a ghost of a smile on her lips. “Oh no, I have plenty to say to you, Wanda. But we are at work so there is an element of decorum that must be upheld.” She ran her eyes up and down Wanda’s form. “Which I see you are doing so beautifully well.” Her voice was low and controlled like she knew that she was in command, and this made Wanda’s blood boil.

She leant forwards and put her hands on the desk to support her, trying to mimic the way that Agatha had done it just over a week ago. “And where does hypocrisy fit into your decorum?” She asked, keeping her voice level.
Agatha looked wholly uninterested in Wanda’s accusation, rolling her eyes. “Wanda, if you have something to ask me please get to it instead of dancing around it. Unlike you, I actually have some work to do.” She sat upright in her chair again and slipped her glasses back onto her face, returning her attention to her laptop.
Wanda reached forwards and shut the lid of the laptop. Agatha threw her hands up and mumbled, “is this becoming a trend?”

Wanda had no idea what she meant so she continued on the track she had started on. “You accuse me of using my son to play games with you and then he comes home and just happens to be wearing that shirt? Your sanctimonious display got me for a second, I won’t lie. But now I know that you’re no better than how you see me. Maybe you were just projecting.” Wanda straightened again and crossed her arms over her chest, a satisfied smile spreading across her face.

She watched Agatha’s face, looking for anything that might hint at a crack but she was holding strong. “I assure you Wanda, I have no idea what you are talking about.”
“Cut the bullshit Agatha. Billy told me that you had him over for dinner and gave him the Oasis shirt. My Oasis shirt. The Oasis shirt that you took with you when you stormed out of the house two and a half years ago.” Wanda knew that Agatha was just trying to toy with her but she was tired of it. Agatha had attacked her in her own office and Wanda had just let it happen, but she was standing her ground today like she should have then.
Agatha rolled her eyes again. “That’s what this is about? It was in a pile of clothes that I was going to give to charity and the kid saw it and wouldn’t take no for an answer. It’s just a shirt Wanda, it doesn’t mean anything.” A look of knowing flashed across Agatha’s face.

Agatha was lying, there was no question. Wanda had zero doubt in her mind that Agatha had found that shirt and come up with this plan to fuck with her. Agatha knew the significance that shirt held to Wanda. It was more than just a simple item of clothing, it was from the concert that Vision took her to on their first date. It was a symbol of her family, of how that date led her into falling in love and having her son, the most important person in her life. It was a symbol of accepting Agatha into said family and having her be present in Billy’s life in a parental role alongside herself and Vision. It was a damn sight more than just a shirt and Agatha knew that.

Wanda kept her arms crossed, balling her hands into fists but Agatha continued before she could speak. “I’ve never had an interest in Oasis. If you hadn’t spent so much time with your legs wrapped around your ex-husband, you might have known that.”
There it was. Wanda had wondered how long it would take Agatha to go there, it always ended up there.
“This isn’t about that.” Wanda bit out. “This is about you using an innocent teenager, a teenager whose world used to revolve around you, as a way to get back at your ex-fiancée.”
Agatha laughed darkly, like she couldn’t believe what Wanda had said. “And now you’re weaponising my past relationship with Billy to try and make me feel guilty for doing something that made him happy. I was giving the shirt to charity in an attempt to avoid,” she gestured at Wanda, “whatever the fuck this is.” She leaned back in her chair again. “Did this make you feel better? Did you get the result that you wanted? Or are you going to admit that any way you happen to be feeling about seeing that old shirt again is a direct result of your own actions?”

Wanda could feel her pulse hammering. She had gone into this thinking that she would be able to catch Agatha off guard, to gain the upper hand. But Agatha had managed to stay one step ahead like she always did, Wanda would never be able to match her no matter how hard she tried. She had lost once again and was going to be leaving Agatha’s office feeling defeated. Since they broke up, arguing with Agatha had always been a losing battle, there was very little that Wanda could do now to come out on top and that fact made it very hard to keep a level head.

The heat in Wanda’s chest started to creep into her face, a stark contrast to Agatha’s calm and collected demeanour. If she clenched her fists any tighter, her whole upper body was going to start shaking so she jabbed a finger in Agatha’s direction and snarled, “stop manipulating my son.” before turning and storming out of the office.
“Always a pleasure chatting with you, Wanda.” She heard Agatha call after her but she couldn’t respond. She slammed the door and practically ran back to her own office because she didn’t want anyone to see her until she’d had a chance to calm down.

She shut her door and immediately collapsed against it, sliding to the floor and pulling her knees up to her chest. As long as it was hers to wield, Agatha would use Wanda’s mistake as a weapon, and it would work every time. Wanda was powerless against it and that was entirely her own fault.

Had that actually just happened? Had she actually just spoken to Agatha Harkness like that and lived to tell the tale? How many people could say that? Rio was probably the only one, she had to be. Why had Agatha let her get away with it, and what was that look on her face? 
Anger? No, she'd seen Agatha angry and that wasn't it.
Fear? Also no. Agatha wasn't scared of her. The thought was laughable. 
So what was it? Arousal? 
Okay, maybe Rio's head was still a bit scrambled from being in Wanda's office earlier but could you really blame her? 

She made her way to the library because she'd walked all the way to campus so she might as well make it worth her while and get some work done. Her favourite corner was free so she set up camp and started perusing the shelves, pulling out five or six random books to start with.
‘It is important that you can do independent work and think for yourself.’ Agatha’s words replayed in her head as she realised that the sections of the books she was focussing on were all about the Labyrinth or the Minotaur, the things that Agatha had been teaching about on Wednesday.
Maybe she had a point, but Rio was too petty to admit that right now so instead she told herself that it was because Theseus’ story interested her and she hadn’t covered it in her research yet.

She managed a few good hours of working before her brain was begging for a distraction, just half an hour of solace before returning to the grind. She opened a new tab on her laptop and went to YouTube to watch some drum covers of the songs the band had narrowed the setlist down to. She had managed to get away with learning the intro and making up the rest thus far, but she knew that she really should try and learn them properly before they had to perform.

She was halfway through a cover of Call Me by Blondie, trying to quietly tap along with it so as not to disturb the other people using the library, when her phone lit up showing a new message in her group chat with Billy and Alice.

Billy: Yo Lars are you around?

Rio scoffed. You mess up the groove one time and you’re nicknamed after the drummer from Metallica.

Rio: I’m in the library

Billy: Should’ve known tbh that’s on me

She rolled her eyes and went back to YouTube – her research for the day was definitely over because this was far more interesting right now. By the time the song finished she could see two people approaching her in her periphery. She hoped that they weren’t going to try to share her table but she only turned her attention to them once they were standing on either side of her. It was Alice and Billy.

She took out her earphones and looked at each of them. “Can I help you?”
Billy pulled out the seat next to her and sat down. “You’re coming to the Halloween thing tonight, right?”
Rio hadn’t even noticed what date it was. Usually on Halloween she would be getting dressed up and going out with her friends to the gay bars, drinking god knows what and then waking up god knows where, next to god knows who. But the day had completely slipped her mind this year, and she suddenly felt FOMO about the fact that she wouldn’t be causing chaos with her friends. She hadn’t even factored Halloween into her packing to come to England.

Rio shook her head. “I have nothing to wear so I’m gonna have to pass.”
Alice sat on the table instead of the free chair and started swinging her legs. “We can find you something between us.”
Billy snapped his fingers as a thought came to him. “You could be Reggie from Julie and The Phantoms!"
Rio looked at him confused. “Who?”
“No, fuck that.” Alice cut in. “Danny from Grease!”
That wasn’t a bad idea actually, but she still wasn’t feeling it. “I think I’m gonna sit this one ou-”
Billy and Alice continued talking over her.

“My mum and dad were Danny and Sandy when I was like six and I had to stay at my uncle’s house that night.” Billy shuddered slightly as he recalled the memory.
“But your dad’s blonde?” Alice started. “And your mum’s… not blonde.”
Billy shrugged. “He used a temporary dye and she wore a wig. It’s not rocket science.”
Rio put her hands up and said, “okay,” definitely too loudly considering the fact that they were still in the library. The two of them stopped talking and looked at her and she lowered her voice again. “First of all, the two people you suggested for me are guys and I’m not sure if I should be offended or not. Second, my hair is too long to be Danny and I’m guessing it would be for that other one you said as well.”
Alice waved her hand, dismissing Rio’s comments. “You could tie your hair up and quiff it at the front, it would achieve the same effect. I’m assuming you have a white t-shirt and you already have the leather jacket and skinny jeans.” She spread her arms like it was an obvious answer. “Seems like Danny is a done deal to me.”

Rio sighed and looked at Billy who was just staring at her with a goofy grin while nodding his head. She closed her eyes and tipped her head back, sliding forwards in her chair until her head touched the back of it. She took a deep breath and breathed out, “fine,” which prompted a whoop from Billy and earned them all an annoyed shush from the people around them.
Billy and Alice stood to leave. “We’re doing pre-drinks at ours so get there around seven.”
Rio widened her eyes. “Seven? What time does this thing start?”
“Nine.”
Nine? Nine? Either she was getting old or the start times for these events were getting unreasonably late.
The shock must have been evident on her face because Alice patted her on the shoulder and said, “You can’t back out now, see you later.” And with that, they both left, leaving Rio to question her decisions.

Rio was giving herself one last look over in the mirror and she hated that Alice had been right about her hair. It was simple but it really did make her look like a female Danny Zuko minus the curl, and she looked damn good. She twisted to the side to get a view of her butt in the mirror and nodded approvingly. She had found her tightest pair of jeans, these ones were a size too small so they weren’t comfortable to sit in but she’d survive knowing that she looked this good. The people in the room all turned to her in unison. She recognised Billy, Alice, Eddie and Ash but she had no idea who the other three people were – Billy and Alice’s housemates, she assumed.

Eddie gave a low whistle followed by, “damn Rio.”
Ash nodded. “I second that.” They walked over to Rio and handed her a bottle of beer. “Billy has something for you.”
“For fuck sake, what now?” Rio took a drink of her beer and looked over at Billy who had the same goofy smile as he did earlier in the library.
He proudly held up a large square of black paper that had the T-Birds logo drawn on it in white pen. “Gotta make sure people know who you are.”
Rio rolled her eyes. “You are not putting that on my back.”
Alice held up a box of safety pins and shook it back and forth, making them rattle. “Oh yes we are.” She matched Billy’s smile. “Turn around please.”
Rio was really glad that she hadn’t worn her expensive jacket.

When they had finished pinning the logo to her jacket Billy introduced her to everyone – she almost immediately forgot their names and instead referred to them by the names of the things they were dressed as, but no-one complained.
The pre-drinks were kicked off in style with a game of Ring Of Fire and her bandmates weren’t kidding when they said that Billy couldn’t hold his alcohol. The more drunk he got, the more he kept messing up the rules and having to drink more. Two and half rounds in, Eddie swapped his drink for water. It was unclear if he noticed or not but he kept drinking it regardless.

It had been nearly a decade since Rio had played this game but the muscle memory kicked in pretty quickly. She made sure not to answer anything that was posed as a question, nor did she ever have her drink less than a thumbs length from the edge of the table. Who knew that drinking game rules she learned in her teens would be useful in her thirties?

By the end of the fifth round everyone was pretty nicely buzzed and the two decks of cards that had been spread around the kings cup – which was a fucking stein of all things – were getting thin. Four out the the eight kings had been pulled and the liquid inside the cup was looking horrid. Whoever the poor soul was that had to drink that was, they were in for a nasty time. Rio pulled a seven from the pile and subtly pointed her left index finger upwards, keeping an eye on everyone around the table to catch the person who was last to follow suit.
“Ah bad luck Beetlejuice,” She said, pointing at him, “Time to drink.”

Another couple of rounds later there was only one king left in play, and the likelihood of breaking the circle was just as big as picking up the final king. There were three people before Rio. Alice picked up a five, but the circle remained intact. Lara Croft picked up the final queen, but no broken circle. Ash picked up a four, which meant all the girls had to drink, but somehow the circle was still going strong. Rio’s turn came and she took her time picking her card, standing up to get a better look.

“Don’t rush me, this is delicate work.” She said, not taking her eyes off the cards as if the right one was going to make itself known to her. About ten seconds later, she made her choice and picked up a card.

Time seemed to slow down as she lifted the card from the table – though that could have been an effect of the alcohol – and gasps echoed around the table as the realisation set in that the card she had picked had broken the circle. She groaned and flipped the card anyway to see what it was. It was the final king, a double whammy.
“Oh fuck me.” She said as she sat back down.
The guy who was wearing a lion onesie looked at her with his eyes full of sympathy. “Yikes bro, that’s a bad do.”
Rio gave herself a final moment to prepare before she picked up the cup. The liquid was a disgusting shade of brown and the smell could not be described in any of the known languages on planet earth.

The seven other people began chanting “We like to drink with Rio, ‘cause Rio is our mate. And when we drink with Rio, she sees it off in eight…”
As soon as the countdown started she put the stein to her lips, immediately screwing her face up at the taste. It was the most vile thing she had ever had in her mouth, but she wasn’t going to pussy out in front of a group of undergrads so she kept going until the cup was drained.
“Joder, quiero morirme.” She muttered before leaning forward and resting her forehead on the table in front of her

Billy, now sobered up thanks to the water, asked, “What did that taste like?”
She lifted her head just enough to look at him and managed to say. “Your mom.”
“You’re not her type.” He replied with a cheeky smile and she put her head back down on the table.
“Soy demasiado vieja para esta mierda.” She said to herself when she felt a hand patting her back reassuringly.
“You took that like a champ, dude.” Eddie said before clapping his hands and continuing. “Okay, fifteen minutes to piss, finish your drinks, have a tactical chunder if you’re Rio, or whatever else you want to do before we head to the bar.”

Rio slowly sat back up. She’d only been slightly tipsy due to her incredible retention of the rules, but that cocktail of death had gone straight to her head and the room was starting to spin. She made sure to have some water before they left, though it didn’t do anything to help. It just sat on top of all the other liquid that was moving around her stomach. She knew pre-gaming would be a bad idea.

They set off to the bar and could hear the music coming from it before the building even came into view, the Halloween party in full swing. Beetlejuice offered to buy Rio a drink for enduring the kings cup but she insisted that she just wanted water. The short walk and the fresh air had helped slightly, but she’d done this enough times to know her limits and she’d need at least an hour before she could even think about alcohol again. 

After some time her head and stomach started to settle so she had a few more drinks and danced with Billy, Alice, Ash and Eddie. 
Around midnight she decided that it was time for her to call it a night – much to her friends’ disappointment. They made some attempts to get her to stay a bit longer since the bar was staying open until four, but she stayed strong and said her goodbyes before making her way home. 
When she got in she went straight to bed, looking forward to a lazy weekend.

Sunday afternoon band practise was a good one. They drilled the songs over and over trying to make sure they had them as tight as they could be.
“I'm still not sure about Seven Nation Army.” Ash said. “Are You Gonna Be My Girl is a better fit for us I think.”
“That’s just because Seven Nation Army isn't actually played on bass, isn't it?” Rio asked with a smirk.
Ash turned to face her. “It's not just that… but yes that is the main reason.” They said with a light laugh. “I'm also thinking of you, because the drums for Seven Nation Army are boring as fuck.”
“The whole song is boring as fuck.” Alice chimed in and Billy agreed.
Eddie put his hands up. “Okay. Seven Nation Army is out and Are You Gonna Be My Girl is in. Let's run it.”

They finished their practice and went to the bar for a couple of drinks before parting ways.
Rio made herself some food and settled in front of the TV. About an hour later she got a text from Wanda asking, or more accurately, telling, her to go over – which she happily did.

She was happy with her arrangement with Wanda and she tended to let Wanda take the lead on when and where they would be meeting. It was usually in the evening at Wanda’s house, which worked better for Rio because it meant that she could leave and didn’t have to deal with the awkwardness of asking Wanda to leave her apartment after they were done, and Rio was pretty sure she could find her way to Wanda’s with a blindfold on at this point. But there was something about it that she couldn’t quite identify. It felt like there was something missing, though she didn’t know what that thing was. The sex was good, great even. Wanda understood the assignment and was happy with Rio leaving afterwards. She made the odd joke about Rio staying for dinner or giving her a goodbye kiss but they were just jokes.

Wanda was another notch in her bedpost that gave good head, so why was there something that didn’t feel quite right? She had been casually sleeping with women for the better part of a decade and she had never had this feeling before so why was it happening now?

It wasn’t the fact that Wanda had a son, Rio really couldn’t care less about that. It wasn’t the fact that Wanda was older than her, she liked older women. So what the fuck was wrong with this situation?
There shouldn’t be anything wrong.

Wednesday morning came around and since she didn’t have to be in Agatha’s office for nine o’clock, Rio didn’t bother setting any alarms. But it appeared that her body clock hadn’t received the memo and she woke up at eight on the dot. She groaned and rolled over trying to go back to sleep but it was futile since her brain was wide awake and ready to start the day. She begrudgingly sat up, her mind might be under the illusion that she had things to do this morning but she sure as hell wasn’t going to do anything. She had her Wednesday mornings back and she was going to enjoy it.

She spent the day becoming one with her couch and playing her Switch. Technically playing Hades for ten hours counted as research since it was mythology based, so she was still doing work, she just wasn’t frying her brain by reading massive walls of text over and over again.
She was, however, embarrassingly bad at the game. She could make it to Asphodel pretty easily if she got the right boones, but anything after that and she died instantly. She could almost understand why men threw controllers and broke TVs over losing a game.
Almost.

They played through the song again, adding more distortion to the guitars and Eddie sang with a rougher tone to his voice. Pop punk was a genre where Rio felt comfortable, it was the type of music that her old band played, so she sent it. Who needs a double pedal when you can do heel-toe?

Maybe she had dumbed down her drumming ability a little bit when she had first joined them. It was safer than going into it being cocky and not being as good as she thought she was years ago. She had also lied a little bit when she told them that she hadn’t played properly since high school. She had continued her lessons through college and she had an electric kit at home that she played just to make sure that she didn’t lose the skill, she just hadn’t been in another band. Playing an instrument by yourself in your own house was different than playing with other musicians.
Rio shrugged. “Maybe you just underestimated me.”

They played through the setlist from start to finish at Taylor’s request so that she could come up with the perfect name for them. The set was quite a mish-mash of different genres, a combination of songs that they all liked and songs that they knew would be crowd pleasers.
Taylor told them all to give her a minute to think and Rio started a drumroll, hitting the crash when Taylor said, “Okay, I’ve got it! How do you feel about Twisted Symphony?”
They looked between themselves for a moment, nodding.
“Wait, why twisted?” Ash asked.
“Well, I’d say Straight Symphony but…” Taylor smirked.
“Yeah, not in this band.” Alice deadpanned and they all laughed.

The next couple of days passed without much happening.
On Monday afternoon Rio read over one of Eddie's essays and sat in the library with him to help him refine it since the deadline was that night.
In the evening she was at Wanda’s for a few hours and accepted a cigarette from her for the walk home. She breathed the smoke into her lungs, savouring the slight burn in the back of her throat. She much preferred a joint after sex, but since weed wasn’t legal here, she would take what she could get.

She spent Tuesday morning in her flat reading and enjoying some time to herself and in the afternoon she had a group call with her friends to catch up and get updated on the home gossip.
“You remember Natasha from homeroom, the one that bullied you for being gay?” Maddy, her high school best friend asked, and Rio rolled her eyes.
“Of course I remember her, she made my life hell.”
“Yeah well, she got married last week. To a fucking woman.”
Rio sat up from where she was laid on the sofa. “I fucking knew it! I said that she bullied me because she wanted me and you laughed at me. I was fucking right!”
“Yeah I know, your gaydar has always been impeccable. That one's on me.” Maddy said.
“Damn right, I knew you were bi before you did.” Rio grinned.

Chloe, a friend she had made in her final year of her undergrad piped up. “Speaking of being gay, have you found your hot, British, future wife yet?”
“C’mon Chloe, you know me, I don’t want to be tied down. Unless they’re into that.” Rio wagged her eyebrows and her friends made various noises of disapproval.
“Boooo!”
“You always have to bring the tone down.”
“That was such a cheap joke!”
Rio just laughed, fuelled by their criticism.

In the evening she was playing Assassin's Creed when her phone pinged with an email notification. She finished the fight she was in before pausing the game and checking her phone, and lifted her eyebrows in surprise at what she read.

Rio,

Given the nature of our last conversation I understand that this might not be something that you would want to do, but would you be able to come to my office at 9am tomorrow morning (Weds 12th)?

Apologies for the short notice.

Agatha

What the actual fuck? Agatha had made it very clear the last time they spoke that she didn’t want to see Rio again, so what was this about?
This was the first time that Agatha had purposefully used Rio’s name and referred to herself as Agatha.
Rio had no idea what Agatha could possibly be wanting, but she wasn’t going to entertain it.

Dear Professor Harkness,

Since you have already acknowledged that you are aware of my possible unwillingness to agree to this meeting, it should come as no surprise to you that I am disinclined to acquiesce to your request.

Sincerely,
Rio Vidal

P.S. The short notice is not the issue.

She debated whether she should keep the last sentence or not. She had already been petty enough by not using Agatha’s name and by using Agatha’s own words from their last conversation, leaving that on the end might cause more issues than it was worth. She loosed a frustrated sigh and deleted it before hitting send and throwing her phone on the coffee table in front of her and unpausing her game.

Rio began working her frustration out on some unsuspecting villagers, racking up a bounty that put her on the radar of some high level bounty hunters. About ten minutes, and a pile of dead villagers later, her phone pinged again. She rolled her eyes and paused the game once again.

Rio,

Understood.

I would like to have an actual conversation with you regarding the way things were left, so I will be in my office from 9-11am as usual should you change your mind.

Agatha

Rio just stared at the email, completely devoid of a response. Why was Agatha choosing now to treat her like a person? Was she only doing it because Rio had forced her to come to terms with the fact that she had previously spoken to her like shit, or was this a genuine attempt at an apology?
Rio couldn’t deny that her interest was piqued. Not at what Agatha could possibly have to say, but why she wanted to say it.
She thought for a couple of minutes about how to reply and ended up sending only one word.

Fine.

She laid in bed, staring at the ceiling, scrolling on her phone, anything to make herself even the slightest bit late. She stayed there for about twenty minutes before she huffed out a groan, dramatically threw her quilt off of her body and swung her legs out of bed. She slowly got herself ready and unhurriedly began her walk to campus, choosing to take the long way to the building where the ancient history department was instead of cutting across the car park like she normally would.

She considered pressing every button between the ground floor and the floor she needed in the lift just to make it take longer, but two other people got in just as the doors were closing so she didn’t want to inconvenience them with her own need to be as petty as possible – though the temptation was definitely still there.

“You may enter.”

It was childish but Rio allowed herself a moment of satisfaction at the knowledge that Agatha was having to get her own coffee again on a Wednesday morning again.

It was weird that Agatha had suddenly decided that not calling her Professor wasn’t a huge breach of the rules that she herself had been so adamant to set and maintain. And I can admit that I didn’t know how to handle that since it very rarely happens.”

No, there had to be more. Agatha wasn’t giving her the full story, she was talking around it. She was purposefully omitting bits and pieces, and for what? To save face? To save herself from the embarrassment of admitting the full truth? Why had Agatha needed to talk about Rio to her friends? How much of her brain did Rio take up and why?
There were so many questions, so many things that Rio needed clarification on but she couldn’t ask them all yet. She would have to bide her time and get her answers slowly because she predicted that the answers wouldn’t be straight forward. This was Agatha after all.

Rio shifted in her chair, sitting further back so that she could rest her back without slouching, and crossed her legs. “Well I’ve got plans to start a movement, give the student body more backbone. So you might have to get used to it.” She gave a half smile and Agatha laughed.
“I’ll keep that in mind.” The silence settled again, neither of them in a comfortable enough place to stop it just yet, until Agatha said, “Do you have anything else you want to ask me?”
‘So many fucking things!’ Rio thought but didn’t voice, instead she said, “I don’t know. Why don’t you tell me some things about you? You know a lot about me and if we’re to build a rapport, it should be equal on both sides.” This was the safest way Rio could think of to try and get information out of Agatha. She didn’t want Agatha to feel like she was being backed into a corner and forced to give explanations to all of the thoughts that were currently swimming around Rio’s head.

Agatha smiled and leaned back, crossing her legs. “Well, my name is Agatha, I’m forty two, I’m a professor at Cambridge Univ-”
“I obviously didn’t mean that.” Rio cut her off with a smile. “I mean like what was it about The Odyssey that made little Agatha want to explore Greek Mythology as a career? Why did you get so bent out of shape when I dog-eared the page instead of using a bookmark? You know, real things.”
“Okay first of all, there is no reason to turn the corner of a page when literally anything can be used as a bookmark. An old receipt, and out of date credit card, a blade of grass if you’re so inclined. If pages and spines get bent through general wear and tear then that’s fine, but to purposefully do it is psychopath behaviour.”
Rio couldn’t help but laugh at how easily Agatha got annoyed at such an insignificant thing. “I’ve been called a psychopath before, but that is by far the stupidest reason I’ve ever been given.”
“As for The Odyssey,” Agatha continued, ignoring Rio’s comment. “All you gave me when I asked you the same question was ‘I read Percy Jackson.’ So if you want tit-for-tat, you’re gonna have to elaborate as well.” A smug smile spread across her lips.

Rio pulled her bottom lip between her teeth and shook her head. Agatha had her with that one. “Touché. My parents got me The Lightning Thief as a late birthday present, because it was released after my birthday, and I became obsessed with the gods. I started researching them on my own time, checking out book after book from the library and when we started learning about it at school I was in my element. I scored top marks on all the tests about it, obviously.”
“Oh, obviously.” Agatha repeated in sarcastic seriousness.
Rio continued. “I’ve lost count of how many times I’ve read the books, but each time a new one was released, I’d get it and re-read them from the start before reading the new one. I did the same with Heroes of Olympus too. And from there it just spiraled really.”

Agatha was still looking directly into Rio’s eyes, smiling softly as she listened. Rio prompted her to tell her side by saying. “Your turn.”
Agatha adjusted the position of the watch on her wrist, breaking eye contact for the first time since it had been established. Her body language made Rio think that she might turn this one down, but she didn’t.
Agatha settled her hands in her lap. “I wasn’t entirely truthful before. My mother didn’t read The Odyssey to me. It was still my introduction to Greek mythology and I was ten when I read it, but I read it of my own accord. I snuck it from the bookshelf in her home office and read it under my covers at night when I was meant to be asleep.” She paused waiting for Rio to interject, but Rio just wanted to let her continue. “I liked the escape that world offered, so I kept hold of it.” She smiled, but it wasn’t full. It looked like it was tinged by the memories that clung to that part of her life.

Rio hadn’t expected that at all. She had figured that Agatha’s story would be similar to hers, and in some ways it was. But Rio’s was a happy one and Agatha’s didn’t seem to hold the same level of childhood joy. She was curious to know more, but now definitely wasn’t the time to ask. Despite what Agatha might have previously assumed, she did know when a question went beyond a simple want to know something and became an unwanted attempt to peek into someone's private life.

Instead of asking anything she just smirked and said, “So we’re both just massive nerds then? Good to know.”
“Oh come on Rio.” Agatha returned the smirk. “We already knew that.” She adjusted herself in the chair for a second and drained her coffee. “What’s next? Hit me.”
Rio thought for a moment, she wanted to keep the conversation light to avoid the risk of it turning sour like so many of their conversations had done in the past. She also wanted to know what the outcome of this meeting would be since it was out of the blue and she still wasn’t a hundred percent on board with Agatha’s reasoning for calling it. “Does asking me to come here today mean that the meetings are back on, or is this a one off?”
Agatha took a breath and ran her hand through her hair. The way that it caught the light coming in through the window made it look almost golden and Rio was nearly mesmerised by it. If Agatha hadn’t spoken, Rio could have happily kept staring at her hair. “We can go back to having regular meetings if you would like, though I wasn’t being dishonest when I said that you didn’t need them anymore. I do have something for us to do today if you’ve got the time. I know that you said you had plans, so it’s up to you.”
Rio had forgotten about the fake plans she had used as her get out of jail free card and made a show of checking her phone. “I hadn’t fully committed to them, so it’s cool.”
Agatha smiled. “Excellent.” She stood up and walked to her desk.

She returned with her laptop and the stack of papers that Rio had noticed when she walked in, and put them in the centre of the coffee table between them. “I thought you could help me mark some essays.”
Rio raised an eyebrow. “You want me to do your work for you?”
Agatha stuttered. “I- Uh- I can see how it would come across that way, but that wasn’t my intention. I thought you might want to try it since we both know that you can do your own work to a high standard, marking someone else's might be fun for- well, maybe not fun. It might be interesting for you. You don’t have to though if you don’t want to, I’m not going to force you.”
Rio tried to suppress the smile that was forming at watching Agatha flounder, but she couldn’t. God damnit, Agatha’s attempt at atoning for her past actions was unintentionally endearing.

Rio leaned forwards to get a closer look at the essay on the top of the pile. “You can stop panicking, I’m in.” She looked back up at Agatha. “Seems like it would be fun. Or would it be interesting?” She smiled and moved her tongue against her cheek.
Agatha rolled her eyes. “Just grab a chunk of them. The marking sheet is on my laptop so you can have that in front of you as you go. Do you want to do the first couple together so you can get a feel for it?”

Neither of them mentioned it, nor did they move their chairs or shuffle themselves away from each other.

They both reached for the top paper at the same time, Rio getting there a fraction of a second before Agatha, which meant that Agatha accidentally grabbed Rio’s hand. They lingered for one second, two seconds, before Agatha quickly pulled her hand away.
“I know I’ve never done this before, Agatha. But I don’t need you to literally hold my hand.” Rio said jokingly as she picked the paper up, testing her use of Agatha’s name rather than her title.
Agatha swallowed, looking slightly uncomfortable. “We’ll see how you feel after you’ve marked this first one.”

Agatha took time to explain the marking sheet to Rio, most of it was pretty self explanatory but she was still grateful that Agatha was covering it in detail. It was better to know exactly how to mark the work to the university’s standard than to wing it and hope that it was okay.
Agatha then went through the first paper with her, pointing everything out and indicating the corresponding guideline on the marking sheet. Of course there were things that they disagreed on, it wouldn’t be an interaction with Agatha if there wasn’t a debate of some sort.

Rio pointed to the marking sheet. “How are you saying that the use of sources is a three? It’s clearly a five!”
“Rio, you can’t be serious. They’ve only got six books and two journals in their bibliography.”
“Okay first of all, they’re in their first year so cut them some slack. Second, they’ve also got four websites which they’ve cross-referenced with the books. And they’ve done it really well.”
If this was how harsh Agatha was when marking the work of her first year students, Rio was having reservations about Agatha reading her full thesis. If she ever got the thing written.

Agatha sighed. “As a source, websites don’t hold the same weight as books. The English Heritage website had the wrong plans for Stonehenge out there for public consumption for so long.”
“It’s the twenty-first century, Agatha. People are going to be using websites now. Just because you had to chisel your college work into a stone tablet, doesn’t mean it’s the right way for everyone to do it.”
Agatha’s eyes went wide and her mouth hung slightly open. Fuck. Rio had spoken without thinking. She definitely, without a shadow of a doubt, should not have said that.
Agatha stared at her for a moment, the surprise at what Rio had said all over her face. Rio’s heart began to pound. Why did she say that? What had possessed her?

Agatha closed her mouth and pursed her lips. “I’ll have you know that I did not ‘chisel my essays into a stone tablet.’” She curled her fingers in air quotes as she repeated Rio’s words back to her. “We had progressed to reed pens and papyrus by then.” She held her stern look for a second longer before a grin started to spread across her face. 

Rio released the breath that she had been holding and turned it into a relieved, breathy laugh. “You’re right, my bad.”
“Shall we split the difference and mark it as a four?”
“I can agree with that.”
Agatha wrote it down on the paper. “If you keep going like this, I’m gonna lose my reputation as a harsh marker.”
“All I’m hearing is that your grade average will go up, which can only reflect well on you. No need to thank me.” Rio smirked.

Agatha calculated the overall percentage score for that essay. “Looks like this one gets fifty seven percent so it’s a 2:2. Do you agree with this, or would you like to dispute it?”
Rio made a show of scrutinising the score, checking the marking sheet a couple times for extra effect. “Nope, looks good to me.”

“I reckon I could give it a go.”
Agatha handed her the next essay and turned the laptop so that it was facing her, expressing that she had done this enough times by now to not need the marking sheet anymore.

They made their way through a fair few of the papers, significantly lessening the pile that was in front of them. They got into a rhythm with it, occasionally leaning over to check how the other was scoring certain things. Neither of them noticed the time passing, too involved in what they were doing. Their knees touched a few more times as one of them was leaning to get a new essay, or one of them shifted slightly to get more comfortable. It became more frequent, not enough that it was obviously a conscious thing but enough that Rio wondered if there was some part of Agatha that was doing it as a subconscious thing. By the time Agatha’s alarm went off, making them both jump, they had stopped bumping their knees and were just resting them against each other.

Agatha pulled out her phone and silenced the alarm. “We’re gonna have to wrap this up and go to the lecture.” She stood up, grabbing her laptop and her bag. “Are you coming?”
Rio nodded and followed Agatha out of her office.

Instead of turning left like she usually would, she turned right with Agatha.
Agatha gave her a confused look. “You don’t have to chaperone me, I know these halls like the back of my hand.”
Rio shrugged. “I noticed that you always walk this way instead of the short way. I wanted to see what was so great about it.”
“The café is what’s so great about it. I can’t teach without caffeine.”
“A perfectly valid reason.”

They walked together to the café, chatting a little bit but not about anything with substance. It was mostly Rio trying to convince Agatha to expand her horizons and order something other than a white coffee.
“What if I buy it for you, then you technically haven’t lost anything?” Rio tried.
“Nope. I’ll still have lost the caffeine hit that I desperately need.”
“Not if you stop being weird and just drink it.”
Agatha rolled her eyes as they approached the café. “If it’ll shut you up, fine.”
Rio moved to join the queue but Agatha stopped her. “We’ll be late if you wait for this.” She gestured to the queue that was only four people long, including Rio. “Just go straight to the front and say it’s for me. They’ll make it quicker.”
Rio’s brows shot up. “You’ve scared them into prioritising your order, haven’t you?”
Agatha lifted her shoulders in a shrug. “I like the efficiency.”

Rio snorted in incredulity but made her way to the collection counter all the same. She gave the barista the order and they looked scared. “Prof- Professor Harkness wants an iced caramel latte?” They stammered out.
Rio nodded. “Yep. With cream on top.”
The barista shuffled awkwardly. “She definitely doesn’t want her white coffee? It’s already done.”
“She’ll take both, but we’re kinda in a rush. Lectures to teach and all.”
The barista nodded and got to work, causing the other people in the queue to roll their eyes. One person mumbled, “We all have places to be, why is she so special?”
Rio would never abuse this kind of power, but she had to admit that it felt good.

Rio paid and the coffees were ready and placed into a cup holder in no time at all. She took them back over to Agatha and pointed to the white coffee. “This was already made and I think that barista would have cried if I told them that you didn’t want it, so you can have it in case your tastebuds are too delicate for a fun drink.” She smiled smugly and they set off to the lecture hall.

They split the coffees up and walked into the room, Agatha going left towards the desk to set up her laptop, and Rio turning right and climbing the seating bank to the spot Billy had saved for her. When she sat down he turned to her and whispered, “That’s not the kind of coffee I expected Agatha to drink.”
She looked towards Agatha who was unwrapping her straw and sliding it into the cup. “Turns out it is when she’s not the one paying.”
Agatha looked at Rio as she took her first sip and Rio had to stifle her laugh when she saw the surprise on Agatha’s face. She liked the drink. She actually liked the fucking drink. She was trying her best to hide it, but the speed that she went in for the second sip gave it all away.
Rio gave a cocky smile and tilted her head in a silent ‘told you so’ which made Agatha roll her eyes and set the coffee down on the desk.

Rio faintly heard Billy speak next to her, but she was too caught up in her silent exchange with Agatha to hear him. “Huh?” She asked.
“I said, why did you buy her a coffee? Are you moving on from second years to the staff now?”
She dipped her brows in confusion. “What are on about?”
He gave her a look that said, ‘you know exactly what I mean’ but continued out loud anyway. “Oh come on, don’t act coy. Me and Eddie heard you and Taylor after the bonfire. Sounded like she really enjoyed herself.”
“All women enjoy themselves with me Billy. It’s just a fact. Ask your mother.” She wiggled her eyebrows at him and he rolled his eyes.
Alice joined in. “You slept with Taylor? Nice.” She held up her hand for a hi-five, which Rio returned, reaching across Billy.
He moved both of their arms down as Agatha started clearing her throat to get the class's attention.

When everyone’s attention was on Agatha, she started talking. “I’m sure you’ll all be pleased to know that I have started marking your essays and you should get the results by the end of the month, so keep an eye on your emails. I know some of you might not be happy with the marking,” She passed her gaze over Rio, a smile tugging at the corner of her mouth. “So please utilise my office hours if you wish to discuss it at all.”
With that out of the way, she started the lecture.

After the lecture Rio messaged Wanda.

Rio: Are you free tonight?

It might only be coffee and pastries but it’s still something. These small acts will add up, you just need to be consistent.”

It wasn’t something that she flaunted, the money had come from her mother so she never really saw it as something that she had. It was just a product of her mother dying, and some expensive lawyers to make sure that her mother didn’t screw her over in her will. Her half-sister had gotten a small portion of it but Agatha got the bulk.
As soon as she’d received the money she had put it straight into a savings account, vowing to only use it on things that would make her mother spin in her grave – like gifts for her long-term girlfriend, an engagement ring for the woman she was planning to marry, or donating to LGBTQ+ charities.
She didn’t like to use it on things like cars or houses because it felt like her mother was the one buying those things for her and, even though the woman had been dead for twenty two years, she never wanted to feel like she was indebted to her mother. She could wait a lifetime for people to come to her and apologise for the way that they treated her. “Okay.” Agatha repeated. “I’ll think of a way to give Rio my number, and I’ll ask her to go to the end of year thing with me. I’m not sure how though. I don’t think ‘sorry I was weird, I wanted you’ would be the best course of action.” She gave a light chuckle.

Billy, Alice and Rio were all sitting together in the centre, the anomaly of Thursday morning seeming to be sorted. She gave her lecture on the weapons of Greek Mythology and had to stifle a smile when she saw both Billy and Rio’s reaction to the inclusion of Percy Jackson’s sword ‘Riptide’ in one of the slides. She wasn’t originally going to put it in, but she knew that it would make them both happy so she amended the slide on Sunday night.

“You know that you’re a PhD student right?” Agatha asked, walking round her desk to lean against it. “You don’t need to beg for extra credit.” She crossed her arms and smiled.

She had no idea where the wink came from, but she wasn’t going to dwell on it. 

Rio fell into step beside her. “Do you want me to grab us some snacks again?” She asked as the café came into view. “Or would that kickstart the horrific rumours that you don’t hate all of your students?” She smirked.
Agatha pretended to think for a moment. “Hmm. I’m sure that my reputation could survive . Also, I’m not gonna turn down free snacks.”
Rio bought them another selection of pastries, and a coffee each, and they carried on to Agatha’s office. Agatha took them via the lift instead of the stairs, not because she was in a great rush, but because Jen and Lilia were right. She needed to reclaim things, and one of those things was the short way to her office. However she told Rio it was because she didn’t trust her to carry the coffees up the stairs and not drop them.

When they stepped out of the lift, Agatha didn’t hesitate when it came to passing Wanda’s office.
“You can’t take steps forward if you’re always looking behind you, Agatha.”
“You can’t have a future if you’re stuck living in the past.”
She recalled Jen and Lilia’s words as she walked, keeping her head held high until they arrived at her own office. She unlocked the door and let them both in, holding the door open for Rio to walk through, and they got to work on the essays. Between them they’d managed to get through all of the first year essays – Rio had marked both Billy and Alice's work and Agatha had double checked them to make sure Rio hadn’t padded their marks out because they were her friends, but she had marked them fairly – and were now on to the second and final years.
Rio was still a little more forgiving in her marking than Agatha would have liked, but it wasn’t going to do any damage so she let her keep doing it. There was no use starting an argument.

Tuesday was the day that Agatha held her office hours. A few of her better final years had taken the time to bring the research designs for their dissertations for her to look over before they submitted them. She had high hopes for these students, they actually put the work in and didn’t leave everything until the night before the deadline. Which was more than could be said for the rest of them.
She had sat through so many presentations on the tomb of Tutankhamun and how the ancient Romans did wonders for modern plumbing in the last couple of weeks that she was starting to regret specialising in ancient Egypt and ancient Rome as well as ancient Greece.
It was refreshing when she was given a proposal by one student on how Hippocrates had greatly influenced modern medicine, and she was genuinely excited to read the full dissertation when it was written.

She had just finished giving advice to a student who could not have cared any less when her laptop let her know that she had a new email. She dismissed the student and opened it.

I know you have office hours today, so I won’t take time away from your other students. Gotta make sure those rumours don’t fly!

Oh how she wished she was marking essays with Rio instead of dealing with the riff raff that kept trailing its way in and out of her office. Maybe she could rope Rio into helping with this too.
No, she couldn’t subject her to this, that would be cruel. Also Rio wasn’t her teaching assistant, so there would be no need for her to do it.

Rio,

Oh please come save me from this hell. I swear there’s barely a brain cell between my final years.

She paused in writing her response. Would now be a good time to suggest that they move from emailing to texting? The worst that could happen is that Rio rejects the idea, right? There’s no need to overthink this.
She continued typing.

Also we don’t have to keep using the formality of emails if you don’t want to. 

My number is: 07879871102
There’s no pressure though, it’s completely up to you.

Agatha

She pressed send, the whoosh noise letting her know that she couldn't take it back now. A minute passed, then another, then another. No response from Rio. Maybe it had been too forward. Maybe she felt awkward and didn’t know how to respond saying that she didn’t want to move on from emailing. Maybe she was emailing the Dean and letting him know that Professor Harkness had tried to give her her number. If that was the case then she was screwed. She could say goodbye to her career.

Her phone buzzed on her desk next to her, freeing her from her thoughts. It was two messages from an unknown number.

Unknown: I’ve never been given a number via email before.
Is this how you had to date back in your day?

Unknown: This is Rio btw not some rando who intercepted your email

Agatha breathed out a laugh, she could imagine Rio laughing to herself, thinking that she’s hilarious.
She saved the number and replied.

Rio: Hey don’t rag on pigeons, they’re hella smart
During both world wars pigeons were used to carry messages that helped save lives and win battles. They were even given medals for it

Agatha couldn’t help but smile at her phone as she read the message. Of course Rio would know random facts about pigeons. Why would Agatha have thought anything to the contrary?
They texted a few more times before Agatha had to go give a lecture and her good mood couldn’t even be brought down by the lacklustre attitudes of her final year students.

Agatha was sitting in her office opposite Rio. They were both marking their own pile of essays in comfortable silence, pastries on the table between them, and an iced coffee for each of them. It felt nice. It felt normal.
She saw Rio shift in front of her and stand up, but Agatha didn’t look up at her, she remained reading the essay she was reading – though she had been staring at these papers for so long that the words were no longer making sense.
Rio walked around the table to where Agatha was sitting and crouched down next to her.
Still not removing her eyes from the paper, she asked “Can I help you, Rio?”
“You were just concentrating so hard, I had to come and see it for myself.” Rio gently put her hand over the one Agatha was using to hold the essay and tilted it so that she could get a better view of the paper.
The contact finally made Agatha look at Rio. But Rio wasn’t looking at the essay, she was looking directly at Agatha. Their eyes locked and Agatha felt her breathing start to quicken and how close they were.

Rio smiled softly. “Your eyes are so blue. I could look at them forever.” She reached up with her other hand and gently brushed a few strands of hair from Agatha’s cheek, letting her hand rest on Agatha’s face. She leaned in by an inch, ever so slightly closing the already small gap between them. “I don’t want to mark these essays any more.”
Rio was now close enough that Agatha could smell the coffee on her breath, but she didn’t mind. It brought her a strange sense of comfort.
She swallowed, trying to calm the feeling in her chest. “What do you suggest we do instead?” She heard the waiver in her voice, felt the weakness in her knees even though she was sitting down.

Rio’s eyes flickered down to her lips and she slowly leaned in again, but stopped just millimetres away from making contact. “I’ll only kiss you if you want me to.” Rio’s voice was barely above a whisper but Agatha felt it vibrate through her entire body.
Her own voice was quiet when she spoke. “I do.”
Rio moved her gaze back up to Agatha’s eyes and smiled. She stayed like that for a few seconds before finally leaning in the rest of the way and filling the space between them.

Their lips had barely touched before Agatha’s eyes flew open and she found herself staring into the darkness of her bedroom. The crushing weight of realisation that it had been a dream sat on top of her, pinning her to the mattress.
She brought her hands up to her face and rubbed circles around her eyes, trying to wipe the dream from her memory. But every second of it stayed printed on the backs of her eyelids.

She was fucked.

Rio stood in the shower trying to process the new information that she had found out wholly against her will.
She was fucking her friends mom. 

It definitely wasn’t the first time that she had fucked someone's mom, but it was one hundred percent the first time that she had known about it.
How the fuck was she supposed to deal with this?

The skin on her hands was starting to prune with how long she had been standing under the water, so she turned the shower off, wrapped herself in her towel and sat on her bed.
She was going to have to talk to both Wanda and Billy about this but she had no idea how to navigate that conversation. There wasn’t a rule book for something like this, even though there really should be.
Maybe she could write one if she managed to make it out of this situation alive.

Wanda didn’t text her to let her know that Billy had left. She probably realised that Rio would need time to work through this revelation and left her alone for the night, which Rio was grateful for. She had no idea what she would even say right now. What could she say right now?
It would be easy for her to go on the attack and blame Wanda for keeping this secret but Wanda hadn’t actually done anything wrong.
She had mentioned before that Billy had asked her not to let anyone know that she was his mother, all she had done was comply with his wishes. Rio couldn’t hold that against her, it wouldn’t be fair, but she would be lying if she didn’t say that she was a little put out by it.

She forced herself to stand up and dry herself off, getting into her pyjamas and crawling into bed. It wasn’t even ten o’clock but she was so mentally exhausted that she just wanted to get comfy and close her eyes.

When she woke the next morning she felt a little bit better. There was still a pit in her stomach but it wasn’t as bad as it had been yesterday evening. She checked the time and saw that she had about forty minutes until Agatha’s lecture. She hadn’t decided if she was going to go. Would it be too awkward with Billy?
She had only just started to accept Agatha’s apology so would it be too soon?
She rolled out of bed and started to get ready. She didn’t actually need to be there so if she wanted to leave then she could just leave without an excuse.

She was surprised when Agatha called her over and said that she’d bought her a coffee. Rio had actually forgotten about buying her one the day before, the fact that Agatha would want to return the favour had never crossed her mind. She was grateful that she had though because she hadn’t had enough time to buy one before the lecture.
When she was looking for a seat neither Billy nor Alice looked at her.
That was fine. She should have known that Billy would tell Alice that he’d seen Rio at his moms house with her shirt on fucking backwards, making lame excuses as to why she was there.
It probably would have been better for everyone if she had said “Hey Billy, I’m fucking your mom. Hope that’s chill with you buddy” instead of choosing that moment to remember that English is her second language, and struggling to form a coherent sentence.

Midway through the lecture her phone buzzed in her pocket. She slowly took it out, careful to not alert Agatha to the fact that she was using her phone. A habit she had kept from her undergrad days. Of course it didn’t matter now if she was on her phone during a lecture as she didn’t actually have to attend them. She still hid it under the desk that was attached to the seat all the same and read the message.

Wanda: Can we talk in my office later?

As much as Rio wanted to remind Wanda of the ‘no talking on a personal level’ rule, she knew that she had to break it on this occasion.

Rio: What time?

Wanda: 1ish?

Rio checked the time, one o’clock was when this lecture finished so that worked out pretty well.

Rio: Sure

Wanda didn’t reply again so Rio slipped her phone back into her pocket and watched the rest of the lecture.

Rio was standing outside Wanda’s office waiting to knock on the door. She suddenly felt very nervous about how this conversation was going to go.
She knocked gently and waited for Wanda’s “come in” before entering.
Wanda was sitting at her desk, but there was no work in front of her and her laptop was closed.
“Thank you for coming.” She said with a small smile.
Rio just nodded and walked further into the room. Her eyes scanned Wanda’s desk, once again taking in the differences between her and Agatha’s offices. She found the picture frame that she had seen the first time that she had been in Wanda’s office, except now it was facing outwards. The picture in it there for everyone to see.

It was a picture of three people. One was obviously Wanda, a happy smile on her face and her hair being carried by the wind. Beside her stood a tall man with the sleeves of his shirt rolled up to his elbows and one of his arms around Wanda’s shoulders, his smile just as happy. In the middle of them was a boy, no older than eight, with a wide, toothy grin and the red hue of sunburn colouring his nose. His hair was the same colour as Wanda’s.
