And while Rio didn’t know the nature of Wanda’s relationship with her ex-husband, or the relationship that came after that, Billy was probably pretty young when it ended and he didn’t need to see his mom bringing random people back to his house – especially people that he had built a completely separate friendship with.

Rio had watched her cousins go through a similar thing and she saw how it had affected them. They were only a few years older than her so they were very close and when their parents were having problems, they basically moved in with her and her parents. Then when her tía and tío finally got divorced nearly a year later, her cousins moved back in with their mom only to have to see whoever her flavour of the month was every time it changed. And those men were not the type to care about someone else's kids.
Her tía had mellowed out in the last decade, but the damage had already been done and Rio didn’t want to be the reason that someone else went through that.

Wanda, who was still picking at her fingers, now looked down at her hands. “I know. You’re right. I should have thought about Billy more and I didn’t. He usually doesn’t come home during the week so I really wasn’t expecting him that day. I could have handled it better instead of putting it all on you in that moment. I’m sorry.” Her voice got quieter as she spoke and her shoulders sank.
Rio still wasn’t happy with everything but the rising anger that she had felt had simmered down as Wanda talked. “We both need to talk to him and then discuss from there. He’s the most important person in this.”
Wanda looked back up at Rio and nodded. “I agree. Let me know when you’re ready to talk to me again.”
“I will.” 

And with that Rio left.
She was about to exit the building when she remembered Agatha asking her to mark essays again. She definitely wasn’t in the right headspace for it right now so she emailed her a quick apology and said that she’d be there tomorrow instead. Right now she needed to go home and figure out how she was even going to begin to approach Billy.

When she had kicked off her shoes, she threw herself down on the couch. She had predicted things with Wanda ending badly, they always did, but she hadn’t planned for something like this. She found herself suddenly feeling sorry for Billy. Was it a common occurrence for Wanda to not factor him in? Maybe the things that her cousins experienced were making her overthink this, but she couldn’t shake the feeling.

She remembered her revelation from a couple of months ago about Agatha being Wanda’s ex – it still wasn’t confirmed, but the evidence spoke for itself. Especially when she thought about the fact that Agatha never took the lift. She had told Rio that it was because the stairs took her past the café, but Rio had her suspicions that it was actually because going to the lift meant that she had to walk past Wanda’s office.
She had no idea how long Agatha and Wanda had been together but since it was an actual real relationship, there was no way that Agatha hadn’t known about Billy.
Was that why they broke up? Because of the way that Wanda treated him?

Rio cast her mind back to the first few lectures of the semester. Billy had been terrified to speak up, to answer questions. Was it because he’d had to witness a messy break-up between his mom and Agatha?
That poor kid. Rio definitely needed to make this right with him.

__________

The decision to buy pastries for her and Agatha to share on Friday afternoon wasn’t one that required much thinking. In fact, Rio didn’t think anything of it until Agatha seemed confused when she put them on the table.
This was something that Rio had done with her supervisors during her masters. If they were going to be working through lunch, it was a normal thing for her to do. She should have guessed that Agatha wouldn’t have received this treatment from any of her students – the persona that she had crafted wasn’t very welcoming of things like this – but the way that Agatha looked so stunned by the mere prospect of Rio providing them with food was so cute to her.
She was slowly but surely thawing out the cold-hearted front that Agatha presented to the world.

Rio didn’t do much on Saturday. She tended to her plants, clipping back the ones that needed it and making sure they had enough water and light. She gently stroked the long thin leaves of the dragon plant that she had put in the corner next to the doors to the balconette. “Don’t tell the others, but you’re my favourite.” She said in a hushed voice.
Her friends often made fun of her for being a ‘crazy plant lady’ and the first time they had caught her talking to the plants that she kept in her house in Virginia, they had laid into her about it for days.
All of her plants back home had names and the ones in England were no exception.

She thought about messaging Billy to see if he wanted to talk but was unsure if she should let him come to her first. She had no idea when Wanda was planning on talking to him and what she would say when she did. Would he want to talk to her, or would he rather just pretend like he didn’t know anything?
She decided to message him anyway and give him the option.

Rio: Hey, would you like to meet me before practise tomorrow to talk?

She wasn’t expecting a quick reply, if anything she thought that it would be a few hours before Billy texted her back, but her phone buzzed just a few minutes later.

Billy: Sure wanna get there an hour early?

Rio: Sounds good!

His quick compliance put Rio at ease a bit. Maybe he wouldn’t be mad. Maybe he really hadn’t noticed her inside out and backwards shirt. Maybe he just didn’t care.

__________

Rio took a breath as she scanned her student card on the door to the music room – she had finally gotten the access added and the others no longer needed to prop the door open for her.
Billy was already there, plugging in his amp and pedal board and tuning his guitar so that he was ready to go when the others got there.
He looked up at the sound of the door opening. “Hi!” He greeted Rio with his usual bright smile.
“Hey.” She greeted him back as she walked further into the room.
Billy put his guitar on the stand and turned to fully face her. “What did you want to talk about?”
Did he really not know? Or was he just playing it cool?

Rio sat down on the drum stool and tapped lightly on the snare with her fingertips, not knowing where to begin. “The other night. At your mom’s house.”
“Ahh.” He nodded like he’d just caught on. “Yes, the night you came over to borrow a book.” He pulled one of the chairs that were at the edge of the room into the centre so that he could sit facing her. “What about it?”
Rio sighed. He was going to make her say it. He wanted to hear it from her. “I wasn’t there to borrow a book.” She stated plainly.
His mouth fell open and his eyes went wide. “No! Really?” His tone was drenched in sarcasm and he dramatically put his hand on his chest for extra effect.

Rio rolled her eyes at his dramatics. “Oh okay, dickhead. I’m trying to have a serious moment here.” She wasn’t mad, she actually preferred that he was being his usual self about this. It made her feel more relaxed.

He smiled. “I’m sorry, but the fact that your shirt was inside out kinda gave you away. Also the fact that you’d come from upstairs. I know my mum keeps some books in her office, but I’m willing to bet that you don’t know what that room looks like, or that it even existed in the first place.”
She did know that Wanda had a home office actually, she had bent Wanda over the mahogany desk quite a few times. But he didn’t need to know that.

Rio rubbed the back of her neck. “Are you mad about it?”
He looked at the ground briefly before he replied. “I was, but I got over it pretty quickly. You didn’t know that she was my mum and you’re both consenting adults. There’s not much that I can be mad at really.”
For an eighteen year old boy, he was surprisingly emotionally mature.
Rio blew out a breath. “Well I’m glad. Is there anything that you want to ask me about?”
He screwed his face up in disgust. “Ew, no thank you. Keep that between you and my mum please.”
“No, I didn’t mean about… I meant in general you twat.”
“I know, I just like messing with you.” Rio rolled her eyes and he continued. “I spoke to my mum about it a couple of days ago and she pretty much covered everything.” Rio braced slightly, not knowing what Wanda had told him. “She said you ran into each other in a bar and went home together. Then you kept going home together. It’s a love story for the ages, actually. People will write songs about it.”

She picked up one of the drumsticks that was laying across the floor tom and gently threw it in his direction. “I wouldn’t have…” She trailed off, not wanting to actually say it to him. “If I knew that she was your mom. I don’t make a habit of doing that with my friend’s moms.”
He picked the drumstick up and tossed it back to her. “I know you wouldn’t have. That’s why I’m not mad at you, or her.”
She twirled the stick around her fingers a couple of times. “Would you be mad if we didn’t stop?” She asked gingerly, testing his response.

He thought for a moment and Rio waited, letting him take his time. “I mean, if you two both want to then I can’t stop you. I just don’t want to know about it.”
It was the best response he could have given and Rio was once again in awe of how emotionally mature he was. “And you said that I wasn’t her type. Guess you’re not as smart as you think.” She smirked.
“You’re not her type based on the two people that I know she’s been in relationships with.” He said as he stood up and picked up his guitar. “One is my dad who is a blonde, soft spoken golden retriever and also a man. The other is a sharp-tongued woman who commands every room that she walks into. From what I know about you, you don’t fit into either of those categories.” He gave her a cheeky grin and tapped some stomp boxes on his pedal board. “Do you wanna jam until the others get here? I just learned Crazy Train.”
Rio picked up the other stick. “Ready when you are.”

__________

Billy had saved Rio a seat again when she walked into the lecture on Monday morning. She shimmied her way down the aisle and slid into the chair next to him. He pointed to her iced coffee. “How have you not developed diabetes from those things yet?”
“I’m just built different.” Rio shrugged.
Agatha walked in and started setting up her laptop and Rio noticed that she only had an iced coffee this time. She’d fully changed her order because Rio had annoyed her into trying a different one.

Rio raised her coffee slightly in a silent acknowledgement and Agatha returned the gesture. Billy leaned over to her and said, “So you bin my mum off and move on to Agatha? That’s cold, Vidal.”
“Don’t talk to me that way, young man. I have access to your essays.”
Alice leaned over to join in. “You’ve read our essays? How? What mark did we get?”
Rio put her hands up. “I can’t divulge that information kids, I’m sworn to secrecy.”
“Oh come on.” Billy begged. “Put us out of our misery, please.” He drew the vowel out.
Rio put her hand on her chest in feigned offense. “You want me to betray the trust that the great Professor Harkness has placed in me? I’m ashamed of you both.”
They were about to plead their cases when Agatha dimmed the lights and started the lecture.

Agatha was teaching about the weapons used in various Greek myths and Billy and Rio exchanged a very excited look when a picture of Percy Jackson’s sword flashed up on screen and got a special mention.
They had bonded over their shared love of the Percy Jackson books in the pub and had a very in-depth conversation comparing the show and the musical to the book, and also spent a good portion of that time shit-talking the movies.

Rio had checked Agatha’s schedule before she left her flat that morning and knew that she had some time free now to mark more essays.
Rio enjoyed spending time with Agatha again, especially since Agatha had removed the stick that she used to keep tightly shoved up her ass.
Rio bought them both another drink and some more pastries and they made their way up to Agatha’s office.
The essay pile had dwindled since they’d marked all of the ones from the first years, but they still had all of the second and final years to do.

Rio had worked through her first chunk and leant forwards to pull another into her lap. “Do you usually do all of these by yourself?” She asked in disbelief.
“Yeah, at the end of every semester.” Agatha replenished her own pile of papers. “Having you here is making it so much easier though, so thank you.” She smiled at Rio. A genuine, thankful smile.
“Well, not all heroes wear capes, as they say.”
Agatha hummed. “That’s true. Some wear leather jackets and converse." She looked at Rio over the frame of her glasses for a second before looking back down at the essay in her hands.

Towards the end of the day Rio messaged Wanda.

Rio: I spoke to Billy yesterday, when do you want to talk?

Wanda: Does tonight work for you? He definitely won’t be making a surprise visit

Rio: Sounds good, what time?

Wanda: 6ish?

Rio: See you then

Rio holed up in the library until she had to set off walking to Wanda’s house. She could see her breath in the crisp November air as she was trying to plan for all of the avenues that this conversation could go down.
Billy had been fine with her but he might not have been as fine with Wanda and she needed to know exactly what they said to each other. She wasn’t going to let Wanda keep anything important from her.

She knocked on Wanda’s door and walked in when it was opened.
“Hi.” Wanda greeted her.
It was probably the most gentle way that she had ever been welcomed into Wanda’s home. Usually they were half way up the stairs by now or one of them would be pinned against a wall or the door with their clothes already being removed.
“Do you want a drink or anything?” Wanda continued. “I’ve got water, juice, and tea. Or I have some alcohol if you'd prefer that?”
Rio shrugged her jacket off and hung it on a free hook by the door and toed off her shoes as Wanda walked into the kitchen. “I’ve not had a proper British tea yet, so I’ll take that.”
Wanda’s head popped round the door frame. “I’m sorry, you’ve been here how long and you’ve not had a proper cuppa yet? I’m glad I can fix that now.” She went back into the kitchen and Rio heard the kettle start to boil. “Make yourself comfortable in the living room, I won’t be long.” Wanda called to her.

Rio walked into the living room and took the space in. She had walked – or been dragged – past this room so many times, but she had never been in it.
There were bookcases lining the wall opposite the door, but they weren’t full. There were random gaps on every shelf, some bigger than others, some had picture frames or ornaments in them to fill the space and some were left empty. Maybe the missing books were ones that Billy had taken into his accommodation with him, or ones that her husband had taken when they got divorced.

There was a deep blue three-seater couch and coffee table in the centre of the room opposite a TV that was mounted on the wall with a set top box and some games consoles beneath it. In the space behind the couch was a wooden table and matching set of chairs tucked neatly under it that looked like they were made from oak.
Rio moved towards one of the bookshelves and looked at the photographs that were displayed there.

Most of them were of Wanda, Billy and her ex-husband on various holidays and day trips – a few were more recent because Billy’s hair was black in them. There were some photographs that didn’t feature Billy or his dad. A couple of them were just Wanda by herself and a couple more were of a group in different restaurants. There was one picture of an incredibly young Wanda, she couldn’t have been older than five or six, standing next to a boy of the same age. They had the same features, the same big smile on their faces and the boy was missing a front tooth. Behind them stood two older people, also wearing big smiles, with one arm wrapped around the other's waist and the other hand on the shoulder of the child they stood behind.
The picture was discoloured and worn with age, an old family photo Rio assumed.

There was one frame that particularly caught her eye, though. It was smaller and tucked at the back of one of the gaps between the books. The reason it was so interesting was because it was turned around so that the picture was facing the back of the bookshelf. Rio cast a glance over her shoulder to make sure that Wanda wasn’t going to walk in and picked it up, turning it around to look at the picture. It was of Wanda and another person, a woman with chestnut hair that had her back to the camera, at a party of some kind. Wanda was wearing a maroon dress and the woman was wearing an eggplant halter style dress. They were on a dance floor and the song they were dancing to must have been a slow one because Wanda’s arms were loosely wrapped around the woman's neck and the woman's hands were on Wanda’s waist.
Wanda was looking at the women with a big, sappy smile on her face and so much love in her eyes.
Rio noticed something on Wanda’s hand so she leant in a little to get a closer look. On the fourth finger of her left hand was a ring. The picture was too small to make out any details of the ring but it was definitely an engagement ring.

She heard the sound of a tea spoon clinking against the ceramic of a mug and put the picture back as she’d found it, stepping away from the bookcase suddenly feeling like she had seen a part of Wanda’s life that she wasn’t supposed to see. She sat at one end of the end of the couch and Wanda sat down at the other end after handing Rio her tea.
“That’s a proper builders brew, nice and strong.” Wanda said before sipping her own tea.
Rio gently blew across the cup to cool the liquid down before gingerly having her first taste. It was sweeter than she thought it would be, though it was nowhere near the sweetness she was used to in her coffee. She swallowed the tea and gave an approving hum. “That’s not bad actually.” She went in for another sip.

Wanda watched her with a slight look of amusement ghosting across her features. “I’ll let the people of Yorkshire know that their tea has the American seal of approval.”
“Forgive my American ignorance but where is Yorkshire? Is it near Cambridge?”

Wanda laughed, but it wasn’t mocking. “It’s about a hundred and thirty miles north of Cambridge. The tea discourse was one of the most confusing things for me when I moved to England, but I learned quickly that Yorkshire Tea was the best tea no matter where in the country you are.”

Rio’s brows dipped slightly as she took in what Wanda had said. She’d had no idea that Wanda wasn’t from England. Her accent didn’t betray any hint of being from another country, nor did the way she spoke. Rio had fully believed that Wanda had been born and raised in this country, but then again, she really didn’t know much about Wanda courtesy of her own rules.

She had another drink of her tea before asking, “Where did you move from?”
Wanda gave a sad smile and her eyes took on the emotion as well. “I’m originally from Romania and had to move when I was ten.” She shifted on the couch, tucking her legs underneath herself and pressing herself into the corner.

Rio didn’t speak, she wanted to let Wanda share the information freely and on her own terms. Wanda looked down at her cup. “Our city was bombed and my brother and I had to crawl over our parents bodies to get out of the rubble of our apartment.”
Rio thought back to the picture she had seen of a young Wanda and her brother with their parents. They had looked so happy and they were torn apart by tragedy.
Wanda continued. “Anyway Pietro and I were taken from country to country to try and find a place to stay and when we were twelve, we were sent to London. A family took us in. They didn’t really have space for two growing pre-teens but they didn’t want to separate us, so they made it work. Our parents had helped us practise our English by watching American sitcoms with us so there wasn’t really a language barrier to battle with but we were bullied for our accents.” She looked back up from her cup and back to Rio, but she didn’t focus anywhere in particular. “Pietro refused to change his accent because it was all we had left of our home, but I was desperate to fit in so I forced myself to speak with the accent the other kids had. I still spoke Romanian with Pietro so that I didn’t lose it, but when I spoke English I sounded, for lack of a better word, normal.” She smiled again, but it was still filled with sadness.

Rio vaguely remembered Billy mentioning in passing that he had an uncle but she hadn’t heard anything else of him. “Does Pietro live in Cambridge too?” She asked tentatively.
Wanda sighed and looked back down at her tea. “He did. When I met Vision and we decided to move out of London to Cambridge, he came with us. Even as we got older, we were still inseparable. We needed each other. He was present in Billy’s life and happily looked after him when Vision and I wanted time to ourselves. He even started teaching him Romanian.” She laughed lightly at the memory, but it was quickly replaced by sadness again. “But one night, when he was walking home from work, he was attacked by muggers. They stabbed him and left him to bleed out in an alley. It took me weeks to fully process that he was gone. My last piece of home. I eventually stopped crying and learned to navigate the world without him, though I still struggle sometimes.”

A silence settled over them as Rio processed the information. Wanda had already been through so much at such a young age, and then to lose her brother when she had finally built a life and family for herself? Rio couldn’t begin to fathom what that would be like.
She thought about her own parents and family. She didn’t have any siblings, but she was so close with her cousins that they were practically her siblings and she had no idea what she would do if she lost any of them. She made a mental note to call them as soon as she could.

“Wanda, I’m so sorry you had to go through all of that.” It was a pathetic thing to say, but what does one say after hearing a story like that?
Wanda sniffed and looked back up at her, focussing on her face now. “It’s okay, I’ve come to terms with it all.” She took another drink. “You should feel honoured, though. You are now one of only three people who know that full story. Even Billy doesn’t know everything.” He doesn’t need to know. The unspoken words sat between them and Rio understood why. He knew the basics of his heritage and didn’t need to be weighed down with the full details.
“I kinda want to hear your true accent now though.” Rio said, trying to add some lightness back in.
Wanda gave a short laugh. “Get me drunk enough and it’ll slip out.” She gave Rio a pointed look. “Piss me off enough and I’ll start to speak Romanian.” Her smile started to lose the sadness beneath it.
Rio quirked an eyebrow. “See, now you’ve given me a challenge. And I don’t back down from a challenge.” A smirk settled on her lips and Wanda rolled her eyes, though there was no annoyance fuelling it.

They finished their tea and Rio made a few attempts to annoy Wanda into speaking Romanian but Wanda refused to give her the satisfaction. When they had both put their empty cups on the coffee table, Wanda said, “You didn’t come here to listen to my tragic backstory, we have something that we should talk about. How did you chat with Billy go?”
Rio crossed her legs underneath her and leaned into the corner of the settee. “It went well actually. He didn’t seem to mind all that much. He did mention that my excuses need some work though.”
Wanda snorted. “I have to agree with him.”
“Right, I was put on the spot and you were zero help at all.”
Wanda held her hands up. “Okay, I can admit that I was just as useless. You have my sincerest apologies.”
Rio narrowed her eyes. “The jury’s still out on whether I accept them or not. What did he say to you?”
Wanda shifted slightly but she didn’t take her eyes off of Rio. “He was surprisingly accepting of it. He said that he wasn’t happy that we’d kept it from him and he also warned me that you might not be ‘as into me as I am you.’” She curled her fingers in air quotes. “He didn’t elaborate on what that meant but I assured him that there were no feelings involved so he didn’t have to worry about that.”
Rio couldn’t be mad at Billy for saying that, he knew about her sleeping with Taylor and was just looking out for his mom. He was a good kid. “I did tell him that I wouldn’t have slept with you if I’d have known that you were his mom and he said he knew that so that’s why he wasn’t angry about it.”
Wanda’s eyes softened. “And now that you do know, how do you feel about it?”
Rio sighed and ran her hand through her hair. “Truthfully? I don’t know.”
Wanda nodded, accepting her answer.

How did Rio feel about it? Obviously being as close with Billy as she was injected awkwardness into the situation. But did that mean that she wanted to stop sleeping with Wanda? The sex was good, great even, even if it did leave her with a strange feeling every time she left Wanda’s house. It wasn’t like she had girls queueing up to sleep with her but she knew that if she and Wanda did put a stop to it that she wouldn’t be without sex.
If they did continue would she need to tell Billy? Would he feel betrayed if he found out that they hadn’t stopped now that Rio knew that Wanda was his mom?

She didn’t want to be the one making the decision, so she asked, “How do you feel about it?”
Wanda lifted her shoulders in a shrug. “I’m not sure either. We’re not in a relationship, and never will be, it’s just sex. But now that Billy knows…”
“It’s different.” Rio finished for her.
“It’s different.” Wanda confirmed. “Did he tell you that he wanted us to stop?”
Rio thought for a minute, casting her mind back to the conversation with Billy. “I actually asked him if he’d mind if we didn’t stop and he said that if we wanted to keep sleeping together, there wasn’t anything he could do about it. He just doesn’t want to know about it.”
Wanda laughed. “Yeah that sounds about right, actually. I’ll leave it up to you to let me know as and when.”
Rio nodded and stood to leave. “He's a really good kid, Wanda. You, his dad and your brother all did a really good job raising him.”
“Multumesc.” Wanda said with a smile and when Rio raised her eyebrows inquisitively she said, “It's Romanian for thank you.”

Rio walked home. She was still confused about how to feel, but she felt better for having spoken to both Wanda and Billy and was glad that this hadn’t blown up in any anybody’s face. 

__________

Of all the things that Agatha Harkness could do, Rio had never anticipated that one of them would be giving her her number.
It caught her completely off guard and took her a few minutes to rally. Once she had, they texted back and forth for a little while. Nothing exciting, just Agatha complaining about her students and Rio saying something like “Well, they can’t all be as good as me now can they?” which of course Agatha refuted.

“Who do we think could have made our Rio smile at her phone like that?” Maddy’s voice came from the tablet that was propped up on Rio’s coffee table.
“Well we definitely know that it’s not a man.” Chloe added on.
“She smiles when I message her.” Jesse, a friend Rio had made in her gap year between her undergrad and her masters, said matter-of-factly. He had only hung out with the full group a handful of times, but they had adopted him in all the same. He was their token straight white man.
Rio put her phone down and pointed at Jesse’s square on her screen. “You have no evidence of that, sir.”
Her phone buzzed next to her on the couch and she picked it up immediately.

Jesse: Fuckwad

She snorted and laughed when she read it.
Jesse punched the air. “Caught in 4k, Vidal!”
Chloe made a face. “Did you guys see the speed she grabbed her phone at? Spill it, Rio. Who is she?”
The three of them began to chant. “Tell us, tell us, tell us…”
Rio took off her sock and threw it at the camera. “You guys are fucking ridiculous. If you must know, I was texting my supervisor.”
Naturally, her friends took that and ran with it.
“You’re sleeping with your supervisor? Remind me to hi-five you when you’re home.” Maddy said.
Chloe had a wide-mouthed grin on her face. “Is she hot?”
“Is she straight?” Jesse quickly asked.
Rio pointed at each of their squares as she answered. “No, yes and no.”

“So she’s hot but you're not sleeping with her?” Chloe asked, raising her eyebrow.
Rio rolled her eyes. “I can think that a woman is hot and not want to sleep with her, you know.”
Maddy laughed loudly. “No you absolutely can’t!”
“It’s why you’re the worst wing woman!” Jessie exclaimed whilst pointing at the camera.
Rio smiled smugly and leaned back into her settee, crossing her arms. “Hey, it’s not my fault that you always try to pull queer women. That’s just poor judgment on your part my guy.”
She watched Jessie open and close his mouth a couple of times trying to find a rebuttal, but he eventually conceded. “Shut up.”
“That’s what I thought.” Rio pressed her tongue against her cheek and smiled.

The four friends continued to talk for a while longer, mostly catching Rio up on the home news and making plans for when Rio went home over the Christmas holidays.

__________

Just before she left her apartment in the morning, Rio sent a text to Agatha.

Rio: Am I getting the drinks today?

Agatha: I think it’s my turn. There’ll be one ready for you when you get here

Sure enough when Rio walked into Agatha’s office, a coffee was there waiting for her. Agatha was sitting in her usual chair and Rio lowered herself into the one opposite her. She picked up the drink and unwrapped the straw, sliding it into the cup and taking a sip. “Have I mentioned that it tastes better when it’s free?” She asked, the corner of her mouth ticking upwards.
Agatha hummed. “You might have said it before, yes.” She took a drink of her own coffee.
“It’s still not a diamond necklace, but I guess it’s a close second.” Rio’s smirk was full now and Agatha scoffed. “You’re never getting a diamond necklace from me, Rio. You should let that pipe dream go.”
Rio tried her best to emulate puppy dog eyes. “What if I asked really nicely?”
Agatha rolled her eyes. “Looking at me like that will get you nowhere. It’s having the opposite effect to the one you intended.” Rio stuck out her bottom lip for good measure but Agatha just made a gagging sound. “Oh that’s gonna make me bring my breakfast up if you carry on.”
Rio snorted and it turned into a laugh. “Well I’ve never had a woman tell me that my face could induce vomiting before.”
“Maybe I’m just immune to your charms then.” Agatha smirked.
“We’ll see.” Rio said, pushing her tongue against her cheek.

They marked the remaining essays in a comfortable silence, making light work of them. Rio had gotten confident with her marking skills and didn’t need to use the guide anymore. She felt a small sense of pride at this because she liked mastering new skills. Even if this was something as simple as marking undergraduate essays, it was now something that she could say that could confidently do.

As they returned the final essays to the table, Agatha checked her watch. “We still have just over an hour and unfortunately, we have no more essays to mark. Is there anything you want to do with this time?”
Rio thought for a second before she said, “Can I ask you a question?”
Agatha leaned back in her chair and crossed her legs. “Go for it.”
Rio’s eyes dipped to Agatha’s right foot, the blue ink in her skin just visible over the top of her heeled shoe. “What’s your tattoo?”
Agatha lifted a brow. “How long have you spent staring at my ankle to notice that?” She asked, but she started bending down to slip her shoe off regardless.
Without the shoe in the way Rio could see that the tattoo was a small blue circle. The way that it had faded and the ink had spread meant that it had to be an old one, but she was still none the wiser about what it actually was.

She looked back up at Agatha’s face. “I ask again, what is it?”
“It’s a full moon, obviously.” Agatha said with a slight smile. “I have two others as well. A half moon on my left shoulder blade, and a crescent moon in a place that you will never see.”
Rio had a retort ready. “I’m sure I could convince you to show me.” It was right on the tip of her tongue, but she didn’t say it. She couldn’t say that to Agatha, could she?
Instead she settled for asking, “Why moon phases?”
Agatha put her shoe back on and leaned back in her chair again. “My girlfriend at the time suggested it and I was twenty one, thinking that I was in love. So I did it.” She said it so casually, so nonchalantly, like she wouldn’t have bitten Rio’s head off just a month ago if she had asked for that information.

Rio took a moment to process the fact that Agatha had just freely offered up information about herself and Agatha filled the gap in conversation. “Do you have any tattoos?”
Rio nodded. “I have four. One on my back, just a few vines and leaves. One on the outside of my left leg, it's a Lord Of The Rings inspired one.” She rolled up the sleeve of her jacket to show Agatha the black and white striped tent that was just below her elbow ditch with ‘Le Cirque des Rêves’ written below it in cursive font. “This one is inspired by a book called The Night Circus. It’s an amazing book and I really recommend it if you haven’t read it already.” She rolled her sleeve back down. “And the last one is on my thigh,” she traced the area to indicate the size of the piece. “That one’s a watercolour Spyro The Dragon.”

Agatha, who had been quietly listening up to that point clearly couldn’t resist making a comment about the last tattoo. “You have a Spyro tattoo? And women still sleep with you?”
Rio scoffed in mock offense. “The women love him, I'll have you know.”
Agatha pursed her lips to hide her smile. “I guess it has to be seen to be believed.”
Rio smirked, unable to resist making her next quip. “Is Agatha Harkness asking me to take my jeans off in her office? Do you think just because you gave me your number that you can get into my pants now? Scandalous!”
Agatha took her glasses off and pinched the bridge of her nose. “You're infuriating”

Rio laughed. “Have you met you?”
Agatha rolled her eyes and put her glasses back on. “Given how tight your jeans are, it seems like it would be way too much effort to try and ‘get in them.’”
“And Spyro would be your reward for said effort.” Rio leaned back and clasped her hands behind her head, resting her right ankle on her left knee.

Agatha raised her eyebrows questioningly. “Seriously, are they painted on? There’s no way those are comfortable.”
It was Rio’s turn to roll her eyes now. She had never heard someone talk about her choice of jeans so much. Even when she wore ripped jeans for the first time and her dad made non-stop comments about how she looked like she’d lost a fight with a pair of scissors. “I promise you, they are real. I could run a marathon in these if I wanted to, not that I ever would want to but still.”
Agatha opened her mouth to say something else but was interrupted by the alarm on her phone going off. She stood up and started to gather her things, and Rio followed suit. Or at least she tried to. She brought the foot that had been resting on her knee back to the floor and tried to stand up in one fluid motion but her knee had other ideas. She felt a blinding pain for a few seconds when she tried to put weight on it and immediately collapsed back into the chair muttering, “Motherfucking piece of shit holy fuck.” She screwed her eyes shut as she waited for the pain to pass.

After what felt like hours – but in reality was a couple of minutes –  the pain finally dulled to a sharp ache, still not great but more manageable and Rio slowly opened her eyes again. She blinked a few times to readjust to the light and Agatha came into focus crouched at her side looking very worried. “Rio what’s wrong?” She asked, concern lacing her voice.
“Just an old knee injury that likes to remind me that it still exists every so often.” Rio said as she began to root around in her bag for the painkillers she kept in there for occasions such as this. “And before you say it, no it wasn’t due to lack of circulation from how tight my jeans are, or whatever bullshit you’re thinking of.” She tried to say it jokingly but the pain made that difficult.

“Because you fell back into the chair and started speaking only in profanities. I had no idea what was going on.” Her eyes were searching Rio’s face and her eyebrows were dipped in worry.
“Aww, I never knew you cared so much. I’m touched, really.” Rio managed a smile and was able to inflect sarcasm again.
Agatha started to stand up. “Okay, well you’re clearly feeling better now. Do you need help getting up?”
The urge to make an inappropriate joke was once again on the tip of Rio’s tongue, but once again she decided against it. She just shook her head and began to try and push herself out of the chair, putting all of her weight on her left leg and her arms.

Agatha stood and watched her struggle with a look of slight amusement on her face. She crossed her arms and said, “It’s okay to ask for help, you know.”
Rio flopped back down into the chair, defeated. “Okay fine. Can you help me stand up please?”
Agatha stepped towards her. “Well, since you asked so nicely.” She bent down and put her arm around Rio’s waist as Rio wrapped her arm around Agatha’s shoulders.
Rio leaned all of her weight against Agatha as Agatha pushed her forward and lifted her upwards at the same time.

When Rio was finally upright, Agatha handed her her bag and shouldered her own. “How are you getting home?” She asked and she reassumed her position at Rio’s side, arm wrapped tightly around her middle.
Rio began slowly limping towards the door. “I usually walk.” She huffed as she focussed on the effort of the simple task of putting one foot in front of the other.
Agatha propped Rio up against the wall as she opened the door and repeated the action on the other side when she locked the door.
When they were back on the move towards the lift Agatha said, “Well that’s not happening so what’s the alternative?”
Rio gave a pained laugh as her right heel hit the floor, jarring her knee. “Crawling?”
Agatha sighed in exasperation. “If you can survive until the end of the lecture, I can take you home.”
“You don’t have to do that.”
“I know. That’s what makes me so nice.” Agatha said in a high-pitched, airy voice.

Rio scoffed as they stepped into the lift. “Did you just get possessed by Glinda?”
Agatha glanced at her, as she settled herself into the corner of the lift, the corners of her mouth curved upwards slightly. “Does that make you my Elphaba?”
Rio breathed out a laugh as the jerk of the lift jolted her. “That depends. How much do you loath me?”
The smile was fully formed on Agatha’s lips now. “C’mon Rio. We both know that ‘loathing’ is not the feeling those two had towards each other.”
“Ahh, so you’re a fellow Gelphie truther then?”
The lift arrived at their floor and Agatha waited until she had gotten Rio out of the lift to reply. “I have no idea what those words mean, but if you’re asking if I think those witches are gay, then the answer is yes.”

They didn’t talk much more as they focussed on getting Rio to the lecture hall. The painkillers were starting to kick in now and Rio could put a bit more weight on her right leg, but Agatha didn’t remove her arm from Rio’s waist, nor did Rio unwrap her arm from Agatha’s shoulders. If anything Rio found herself leaning more into Agatha. She felt a sense of comfort from Agatha holding her, Agatha’s grip was strong but gentle and it felt grounding.

The two of them walking through the corridors like this earnt them a plethora of looks and hushed comments from passing students and faculty alike, but Rio didn’t particularly hear what they were saying, she just noticed them staring.
When they arrived at the lecture hall they were ten minutes late, which was very unlike Agatha.
Just before they got to the door, Rio removed her arm from Agatha’s shoulders and Agatha unwrapped her arm from Rio’s middle. An unspoken agreement passed between them that they shouldn’t walk in wrapped in each other’s arms.
The students that were diligently seated watched them walk into the lecture hall with a mixture of expressions on their faces.

Rio limped her way over to the seating bank fully prepared to struggle with the steps and awkwardly shuffle into her seat next to Billy, but Agatha announced, “Rio has a knee injury and needs to sit at the front today.” When she was just met with confused stares, including Rio, she continued. “So if a space could be made for her, I’m sure she would be very appreciative.”
A boy who was sitting in the seat nearest the door silently stood up and moved himself to the row behind. Rio gave him a quiet “thank you” and settled herself into the chair.

She was glad that Agatha had made sure she could sit at the front because she wouldn’t have been able to keep her leg stretched out if she was sitting in the middle like usual. The painkillers had done their job and the pain had mostly subsided, it was just the embarrassment that remained. Her injury hadn’t flared up like that in years, and when it flared up in the past it was due to putting strain on her knee. She tried to think of what she could have done to cause it, but was coming up blank.
She was pulled out of her thoughts by Agatha apologising for her lateness and dimming the lights to get straight on with the lecture.

Rio felt her phone vibrate in her pocket so she pulled it out to check it.

Billy: What the fuck happened to you?

Rio: Old knee injury came back to haunt me

Billy: Why was Agatha late too?

Rio: Said knee injury attacked me in her office so she helped me get here. She’s a hero

Billy: Never knew she cared about you so much 😜

Rio: I’m a very likable person, you little shit. Now get off your phone, you’re in a lecture!

He didn’t reply so Rio slid her phone back into her pocket and focussed on the lecture, or at least she tried to. The phantom feeling of Agatha’s arm around her sat in her mind and she absentmindedly rubbed the spot on her stomach where Agatha’s hand had been. She hadn’t held Rio tight enough to leave a mark yet the feeling would be etched into her skin for the rest of the day.

__________

Rio barely noticed the time passing and the end of the lecture sneaked up on her, the lights coming back to full brightness momentarily dazing her. The students moved around her, packing their laptops and notepads away and leaving the room.
Billy and Alice appeared in front of her, neither one of them looking concerned. Alice spoke first. “I know you’re old, but I didn’t think knee problems started at thirty.”
Rio flipped her off. “My knee problems started at sixteen actually. I was a promising basketball star who had it all ripped away from her in a fatal accident. It’s a tragedy and I can’t believe you don’t care.” She forced a crack into her voice and faked a quivering lip.

Billy rolled his eyes. “You’ve been through so much, you truly are an inspiration to us all.” He offered her a hand as she started to stand up, which she took. “For real though, are you good?”
Rio tested her knee by gently putting weight on it. It was still painful, but she no longer needed to be held up. “Yeah I’m good, I just need to rest for a few days so I won’t be at practise tonight.”
Alice nodded. “Understandable. After all, we’re only as good as our drummer.”
They told her to let them know when she was home and to take it easy before they left the lecture hall.

Rio slowly made her way over to Agatha who was leaning against the table, patiently waiting for her to finish talking to Alice and Billy.
“Are you ready to go?” Agatha asked.
“Yep. I will warn you though, you might struggle to keep up with me.”
Agatha laughed. “I shall keep that in mind.” She offered Rio her arm but Rio shook her head saying that the painkillers were doing their job and she could manage on her own.

The two of them walked to Agatha’s car, Agatha making sure to stay directly at Rio’s side – and then insisting that they link arms when Rio got a bit too confident and tried to walk with a normal gait, only to immediately regret it. They made small talk about the lecture and when they got to the car, Agatha made sure to push the passenger seat as far back as it could go so that Rio didn’t have to bend her knee too much.

The small talk continued in the car and Agatha apologised profusely when Rio hissed in pain after she ran over a pothole a little too fast.
The car ride was short and when she pulled up outside of Rio’s building, Agatha asked, “Do you want me to help you up the steps?”
Rio looked at the steps, sizing them up. There were only five of them, she could manage five steps, and Agatha had helped her enough. “No thanks, I should be good.” She replied, undoing her seatbelt and slowly getting out of the car.
She had just managed to stand up and shut the door when Agatha was in front of her again. “Rio, I used to live here. I know how difficult these steps were after I’d had a bit to drink, never mind with an actual leg injury. Let me help you.”
Rio wanted to protest, but the look Agatha was giving her told her that it would be futile so she begrudgingly accepted the help.

When they had made it up the steps – which Rio definitely could not have done alone – and Rio was searching for her keys in her bag, she asked, “When did you live here?”
Agatha leaned against the wall. “I moved here when I was offered a permanent lecturing position at the university, which was twelve years ago.” She blew out a breath and chuckled. “God I’m old.”
Rio found her keys and unlocked the door, pushing it slightly ajar. “Nah, I’d say you’ve got at least another year before you’re officially considered old.” She said with a half smile.
Agatha shook her head. “Of course you would.” She started walking back down the steps towards her car but turned to face Rio again as she said, “Promise me you’ll use the lift.”
Rio rolled her eyes but promised anyway, walking into the building and letting the door shut behind her.
She sent Agatha a selfie in the mirror of the lift for good measure and let Billy and Alice know that she’d made it home.

She got straight in the shower – which was entirely more effort than it was worth – and put on her pyjamas, resigning herself to spending the rest of the day rotting on the couch with her knee brace on and her painkillers within reach.

__________

The following morning her knee felt a lot better, though she knew that she still shouldn’t be walking around too much and that she needed to give it at least three days of proper rest.
She sat on the sofa with her toast and fired up her Switch, another day of being a couch potato ahead of her.
Before she started her game, she messaged Agatha.

Rio: Hi, I know we don’t have any more essays to mark but I thought I’d let you know that I won’t be coming in anyway

She wondered if there would be any reason for them to spend time together now that all of the essays were done. She didn’t want to stop spending time with Agatha, she enjoyed it. They had found a rhythm now that Agatha was more chilled and Rio liked talking to her. She liked being around her because they were quite similar in a lot of ways.

She thought back to the previous day, the way that Agatha had looked at her with such worry and concern. She remembered the look in Agatha’s eyes when she was crouched down beside her and she hadn’t thought about it at the time due to the amount of pain she was in, but now she was retroactively surprised. She didn't think that Agatha was heartless by any means, but she hadn’t expected her to care so much. And as much as Rio protested the help, she liked that Agatha had looked after her and made sure she made it home.

Agatha: I was going to tell you not to come in today so I’m glad you’re not, you need to rest. Also, I was going to ask you this in person but, how would you feel about giving a lecture?

Rio giving a lecture? She had honestly never thought about it. Did Agatha think she was capable of giving a lecture? She must do otherwise she wouldn’t have asked, right?
Professor Agatha Harkness had just asked PhD student Rio Vidal to give a lecture in her place.

Rio: Me? Really?

Agatha: Yes, really! I think you’d be good at it. You like talking and everyone would have to listen to you. Also it would give you a different angle for your research

Rio: Okay, sure! What on? Also when?

Agatha: I can email you the topics I still need to cover and you can choose from that if you want. I was thinking Monday, but if that’s too short notice then you can pick another day.

Rio hadn’t thought of a reply when she got the email notification. She opened it and browsed the list that Agatha had sent her. It wasn’t super long since the semester was nearly over but there were still a few to choose from.

Rio: Could I do it on Medusa? Also Monday should be fine, which time slot?

Agatha: I had a feeling you’d pick Medusa, of course you can. I thought about the early lecture on Monday since it would be the first years, less pressure. But if you’d prefer a later time then you can do that instead

Rio took a moment to think about it. If she did the early lecture then, like Agatha said, it would be less pressure because it would be for the first years. Also Billy and Alice would be there and that would make her feel less nervous. If this one went well then Agatha might let her give another lecture which she could do for the second years. The idea was starting to seem exciting.

Rio: I’m good for the early lecture! Would I be doing both hours?

Agatha: That’s up to you. If you want to do one hour and I do the other, we can. Or you can do both. It’s entirely your decision

Rio: Pencil me in for both hours and I’ll see what I come up with. If I don’t think it’ll be enough for two, I’ll let you know by Sunday so that you can handle the other hour?

Agatha: Sounds like a plan. You can send me your slides to look over if you want, but I trust that you’ll be fine

Rio: Will do

She retrieved her laptop from her bedroom and returned to the sofa, turning off her Switch in favour of the new task she now had.
She immediately dove into the research, making sure she had as many sources as possible to properly do Medusa justice. Her story had been twisted and told in so many different ways but Rio wanted to be as accurate as she possibly could be whilst still keeping it appropriate for a university lecture.

She lost track of how long she worked on the lecture for, creating slide after slide and finding pictures to go with them, truly getting lost in the research.

Chapter Notes

TW: I've written about Medusa in this chapter so there are some mentions of sexual assault.

Agatha and Rio had agreed to meet at the café before the Monday morning lecture to get their drinks, before making their way to the lecture hall together.
Rio had sent Agatha her lecture slides to look over on Friday night and Agatha had been impressed at how quickly Rio pulled the lecture together. The slides were concise but covered all of the main points and Agatha had no doubts that Rio had plenty of notes to expand on the bullet points that she had put on each slide. She was looking forward to seeing Rio give the lecture, especially because Rio had clearly made her presentation to last the full two hours.

When Agatha got to the café Rio was already waiting in line. She sidled up to Rio, casually standing next to her in the queue. “Have I not taught you that you don’t need to wait for drinks?” 
 Rio turned her head to look at her, a small smile playing on her lips. “Unlike you, I choose not to abuse that power. I thought you British people enjoyed queueing anyway. Isn’t it an integral part of your culture?”
“Yes actually. When I applied for citizenship, one of the tests they gave me was seeing how long I could stand patiently in a line of other people.” Agatha spread her arms. “Clearly I passed with flying colours.” She grabbed Rio by the wrist and started pulling her towards the collection counter. “However, I no longer need to prove that I can do it.”
Rio rolled her eyes but ordered her drink all the same and paid for both coffees.

They got their drinks and their accompanying straws, and started walking towards the lecture hall, being close enough that their shoulders brushed as they were walking.
“Are you nervous?” Agatha asked, regarding Rio out of the corner of her eye.
Rio shrugged. “Not really. I’m basically just info-dumping for two hours, and that’s a skill I already excel at.”
Agatha turned her head fully to look at Rio, the corner of her mouth curving upwards slightly. “Well, you do like hearing yourself speak.”
Rio scoffed. “Oh yeah, like you got into this profession for the satisfaction of a job well done.”
Agatha made a noise of mock annoyance. “I have no idea what you could possibly be implying, Rio.”

They arrived at the lecture hall early, no students in sight, and Rio started setting up her laptop on the desk in the centre of the room. Agatha watched Rio get prepared, loading up her PowerPoint and flicking through it to check that everything worked properly before moving on to the controls for the lights.
She continued to watch as Rio went through the different settings and took notice of the way her face lit up when she realised that she could change the colours of the lights.
Rio turned to her, open mouthed, with excitement on her features. “You’ve been able to change the colours this whole time and you’ve never done it?”
Agatha smiled, breathing out a laugh. “I never saw a reason to, but if you want to do it then feel free. This is your lecture after all.”
“I’m starting to see the appeal of this.” Rio said as she continued to figure out the lighting controls.

Agatha checked her watch, they only had a few minutes before the students started to arrive and she began to feel nervous on Rio’s behalf. She remembered the first time she had given a lecture. She had gone into it so confident and so sure of herself that she didn’t think she could possibly fumble it. But when the students were all seated and staring at her, her throat closed up and she couldn’t speak. The senior lecturer that she was shadowing had to do the introduction for her and it was one of the most embarrassing moments of her life.

She started scanning the room for a place to sit. She didn’t want Rio to feel like she was watching her, but didn’t want to be so far away that she couldn’t jump in should Rio need her to. She also didn’t feel like the students would feel comfortable with her sitting on the seating bank with them. She decided to leave the decision up to Rio, asking, “Where would you like me to sit?”
Rio turned and leant back against the desk. “Wherever you want.”
Helpful.
“It’s your lecture so you decide.”
Rio looked around the room for a moment before saying, “I assume you’re gonna be taking notes so that you can give me feedback, so would the corner give you a good enough vantage point?”
Agatha suppressed a smile. She had thought about treating this similarly to the teaching demonstrations that she’d had to give when she applied to be a lecturer at Cambridge, but she didn’t want to add that pressure. Since Rio had assumed that it was going to happen anyway, what harm could it do?
Agatha nodded. “The corner sounds good. I’ll introduce you then go sit down.” She pulled a notebook and pen from her bag.

The students started to file in and take their seats, Billy and Alice sitting in their usual spot with an extra space left for Rio, clearly unaware that she wouldn’t be taking it this time.
Agatha waited for all of the students to get settled before she stepped in front of the desk and addressed them.
“Good morning everyone. The lecture this morning is going to be a little bit different. I’m sure by now that you’ll all have seen Miss Vidal,” she gestured behind herself to where Rio was standing, “usually sitting up there with you. Well this morning, Miss Vidal will be the one giving the lecture so please afford her the same respect that you would myself. I’ll still be watching you so don’t think that you can get away with being on your phone and not paying attention.” She gave a sweeping gaze over the students, narrowing her eyes slightly to drive the point home and having to hide the smile that was tugging at the corners of her lips when she saw the shocked looks on Billy and Alice’s faces. “I will now leave you in the capable hands of Miss Vidal.”
She went back around the desk to pick up the chair and her notebook to take them to the back corner of the room, whispering “You'll be great,” to Rio before she went.

She got settled in her seat as Rio dimmed the lights and fired up the presentation onto the blank slide that would soon have text and a picture filling it. She watched Rio take a deep breath before she started speaking, exhaling out the nerves that Agatha knew she was trying to hide.
“Thank you Professor Harkness for the introduction, I will try my best to instil fear into the hearts of these students the same way that you do.” Rio began, eliciting a chuckle from the crowd of students before her. “Speaking of women that instil fear, today we’ll be covering Medusa.” She tapped on the remote that was linked to her laptop and a picture of one of the many stone statues of Medusa popped onto the slide.

“Okay so, I want you guys to tell me what you know about Medusa and I’ll add it to the slide.” Rio drew a text box ready for people to shout things out.
“She’s a baddie!” One boy shouted from the back, much to the joy of his peers. Agatha wouldn’t have entertained something like that but Rio took it in her stride, laughing and saying, “She’s a baddie? Okay I can get behind that. Someone clearly has a type”, as she typed it into the text box. She looked back at the students waiting for the next person to offer a suggestion. A girl in the front row spoke up next. “Athena turned her into the monster we know her as.”
Rio added it to the slide as Billy jumped in “Only because Poseidon assaulted her in Athena’s temple. It wasn’t Medusa’s fault.”
Rio looked up at him, her smile evidence of how proud she was of him for knowing that and having the courage to say it.

Before long the empty space around the picture of Medusa was filled by the information that the students had shouted out, and Rio was looking extremely happy that they had engaged and joined in.
Agatha was happy that Rio was getting to experience this. Trying to save yourself after you’re met with blank stares is something even she hadn’t quite learned how to do properly, even with all of her years of experience.

Rio’s next slides were on points that the students had mentioned and she effortlessly delivered the information, walking in front of the desk and standing to the side to talk about what was on each slide. She covered various versions of the myth of Medusa and Agatha couldn’t take her eyes off of Rio. The way she moved with ease and adjusted the tone of her voice to keep people’s attention. The way that she gave large amounts of knowledge in easy to understand chunks and managed to add humour in, making jokes that were typical Rio things to say whilst still keeping it appropriate for a lecture. The way that she was using her thesis research to talk about different ways that Medusa has been portrayed in various mediums over the years.
Agatha was captivated by all of it.

As Rio was starting to segue into the solemn side of Medusa’s myth she cast a glance back towards Agatha. Their gazes met and Agatha could tell that Rio was looking for reassurance. Reassurance that she could do justice to this interpretation of Medusa and that it was okay to talk about it in a lecture. Agatha gave a small smile and gentle nod letting Rio know that she had Agatha’s full support.

Rio returned the smile and changed the slide. “Okay so this has been quite light so far, but there is a darker side to Medusa’s story. Billy touched on it at the start, but I want to go a little deeper into it. During this part I will be talking about sexual assault. I won’t be going into detail but if anybody needs to leave please do. I’d rather you look after yourself than force yourself to sit through this. I also will not be tolerating any jokes made during this section, is that understood?” The students mumbled their agreements.
Agatha respected the fact that Rio added the disclaimer before going into this section of the lecture; it was mostly the reason why she hadn’t covered Medusa yet herself. It was always a sticking point for her every year – how to broach this topic, and if she should include it at all.

Rio stood in front of the desk, leaning against it. “In some versions of the myth, Medusa was the only mortal one of the three Gorgon sisters. She was a beautiful, alluring young woman who was a priestess of Athena. Medusa devoted herself to a life of celibacy in the name of Athena. However, despite her origins of beauty, Medusa’s name quickly became synonymous with malevolence, hatred, and monstrosity.” Rio clicked the remote and a painting of an olive skinned, brown-haired young woman appeared on screen next to one of the stereotypical Medusa with snakes for hair. “One of the requirements for being a priestess of Athena was that the women should remain virgins and devote their lives to the goddess, which Medusa did. One day Poseidon, a rival to Athena, caught sight of Medusa and was enthralled by her. He tried to seduce Medusa but, being a loyal priestess of Athena, she rejected him. Poseidon didn’t take that too well and I’m sure that I don’t need to say what happened next.”

Rio pushed herself off of the desk and slowly walked around the other side. “Poseidon decided that the best place to do that to Medusa would be in Athena’s temple. Afterwards he disappeared, leaving Medusa vulnerable and weak. The perfect way to let Athena know that he hated her, and Athena directed all of her anger at Medusa despite Medusa praying for guidance and forgiveness. Athena looked down on Medusa with nothing but feelings of betrayal because she had broken the biggest rule that came with being a priestess of the goddess. Whether consensual or not, Medusa was no longer a virgin. So Athena cursed her to become the snake haired, insane monster that we know of today.” Having completed a lap around the desk, Rio settled against it once more.

Agatha figured that discussing a topic like this made Rio feel restless, unsure of how to hold herself, what to do with her hands, where to direct her gaze. Those would be the things that Agatha was feeling if it was her giving this lecture. Rio was doing a fantastic job and Agatha was proud of her.

“Having been exiled to an island, the only contact Medusa had with any other living being was the men that were sent to kill her. At first, Medusa was angry with the gods for cursing her and she was scared of her ability to turn people to stone – who wouldn’t be? But soon enough anybody who took one step on her island was now marked for death at the hands of the Gorgon Medusa. The more research that I’ve done into Medusa, the more Athena’s reaction to her being sexually assaulted troubled me.”

This meeting would be cutting into her office hours so it better be fucking worth it.

She savoured the food and drink that Rio had bought her, making them last as long as she could. The beauty of the iced coffee, as Rio had once pointed out, was that she didn’t have to worry about it going cold, so she was able to make it last a good couple of hours before she finished it.
