She dried herself off and put her pyjamas on before going back downstairs to order some food. She would usually cook something, but she was too exhausted to fathom standing in the kitchen for half an hour physically making food, and then having to wash up afterwards. So ordering pizza it was.
After some deliberation, she also bought her ticket to the ball, scoffing at the limited menu choices. It might have been a few years since she attended one of these events but she swore the options used to be better.

When she had eaten, she went upstairs and started her nightly skin care routine – all products that Jen had picked out for her over the years.
When she was done she crawled into bed and picked up the book that was on her nightstand, The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern.
She had bought it a few days after Rio told her about it and was thoroughly enjoying it. She hoped that reading it tonight would quiet her mind, and it did to some extent. The fact that the book jumped around both in place and time meant that she had to concentrate on it more than she usually would if she wanted to follow it, and that gave her something else to focus her mind on.

Rio hadn’t responded to her text from earlier but she wasn’t reading into it, Rio was probably just giving her space – and she was actually thankful for it.
After reading a few chapters, she set the book back down and laid on her side to attempt sleep.
She tossed and turned for a while before her brain finally slowed down and she drifted off.

__________

The next month passed pretty easily. Rio gave another lecture, this time about the Underworld and the different layers it had. She used her PhD research to highlight a few different depictions of it, pulling information from books, TV shows, films and even games. She was good at keeping the attention of the first year students and continued to impress Agatha with how well she delivered the lecture.

Rio continued to go to Agatha’s office whenever she had downtime and they traded who would be buying the food and drinks each time. Since there were no essays to mark, they just talked. Getting to know each other and deepening their friendship.
Rio had started referring to these meetings as dates which absolutely did not make Agatha panic whatsoever. She had a completely normal reaction the first time Rio had said it and definitely didn’t nearly choke on her pastry.
“Damn, you really know how to bruise my ego.” Rio had joked.
“Well I can’t in good conscience let your head get too big. You’re insufferable enough as it is.” Agatha had replied once she could breathe again.
They still walked to and from lectures together, but they maintained a distance so as not to invoke more rumours and visits to Herb’s office.

Rio didn’t bring up their run-in with Wanda, and Agatha started to push it to the back of her mind. She did avoid the lifts for a week before remembering what Lilia and Jen had said about not living in the past. If she was to truly move on from it, then she needed to accept that these things would happen and she couldn’t hide from them forever.

Agatha invited Billy and Alice over for dinner another couple of times, she was tempted to ask about Rio’s involvement with Wanda but decided against it. She could ask Rio herself, it wasn’t fair to use Billy like that. If she did then she would be no better than Wanda, and if there's one thing that kept Agatha going, it was knowing that she was better than Wanda.

Her weekly dinners with Lilia and Jen were spent fielding questions about Rio, and telling them that she did not need a ‘game plan’ for the ball. She did mention the fact that she and Rio had bumped into Wanda on their way to a lecture and that Rio and Wanda seemed to know each other, but Lilia and Jen just confirmed what the rational part of her brain already knew. Rio and Wanda were both adults who frequented the same areas of the university, they were allowed to meet and even become friends. And should anything start with Agatha and Rio, then she should tell her about her relationship with Wanda and why it ended. But until that point, she would just have to deal with it and continue as normal.

Throughout December decorations went up around the department and the university as a whole, and Agatha added the obligatory singular rope of tinsel around her television that Jen and Lilia insisted that she put up.
Her Christmases as a child after her dad had died had never been happy ones. Her mother always went on a religious tirade, blaming Agatha for all of the bad things that had happened to her that year, saying that her evil nature had made god angry and he was punishing her for not killing Agatha when she was born.
When her step-father came on the scene he only strengthened the tirades, joining in with them and supporting Evanora’s delusions.

When she had been with Wanda she began to find ways to enjoy Christmas. Decorating the tree with Billy, baking mince pies with Wanda even though she couldn’t stand them, and getting to see and experience the joy that both Wanda and Billy felt at the season as a whole.
But since all of that had been taken from her, she had no reason to feel the Christmas spirit anymore, and this December came with a new memory. The 3rd marked one year since the car accident that nearly killed Billy. One full year since Agatha got that call from Wanda and she raced to the hospital. One full year since she was reminded that through all of the heartbreak, sadness and rage she had felt at Wanda cheating on her, the worst, hardest to face part of it was losing Billy.

December was Agatha’s least favourite month of the year, and she had plenty of reasons for it, but as the night of the end of year ball approached, she hoped that that would no longer be the case.

Chapter End Notes

Peep the time jump... WE'RE GETTING THESE BITCHES TO THE BALL!

Rio

Chapter Notes

Sorry this one is so short, it's just to give Rio's POV on some things

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Getting called into the Dean’s office was not on Rio’s bingo card for the year. Yet there she was sitting across from him with Agatha beside her, listening to him tell them that rumours were spreading about their involvement with each other.
The amusing thing was that she was, in fact, sleeping with a member of staff. Just not the member of staff that everyone apparently assumed she was sleeping with.
The less amusing part was the Dean’s tone when he spoke to Agatha, the way that he spoke down to her and clearly had no respect for her.

Agatha was clearly used to this, clearly used to being pulled into his office for stupid things that had no weight to them, but Rio wasn’t.
Rio had never been in a Dean’s office in any capacity, good or bad. This was entirely new to her but she would be damned if she let him sit there with a smug grin on his face while he tried to frame them for having an inappropriate relationship and asked for evidence of an injury.
Thank god Rio was cautious and kept her brace on even after her knee was fine again, because the satisfaction she got from watching his face drop when he saw it was a high she would be riding for some time.

He was obviously unhappy that he had to dismiss them and couldn’t take any action in favour of the baseless chatter that had made its way to him, but dismiss them he did.
Again, it was clear that Agatha was used to this. But the way that she stalked out of his office and into the hall showed Rio that it affected her more than she would ever let on.
Rio knew that Agatha wouldn’t be open to questions, especially not mere seconds after the fact, so she followed Agatha’s lead in terms of conversation. It stayed light and small – mostly about her jeans, which she was happy to comply with – until they got to Agatha’s office.

Watching the way Agatha deflated and dropped some of the ‘Professor Harkness’ persona that she upheld where people could see her let Rio know that Agatha viewed her office as a safe space. A place on campus where she could go after meetings like that to decompress and just take a few minutes to herself where she didn’t have to be switched on. And the fact that she was letting Rio witness it meant that she trusted Rio to some degree. Trusted that she wouldn’t judge or make fun of her in this small moment of vulnerability that she was experiencing.

Once again Rio let Agatha lead the conversation, only asking a question when Agatha mentioned the Dean.
Hearing Agatha say that the Dean is just looking for any excuse to fire her and that her fellow staff members aid in this, made Rio feel equal parts sad and angry. Did Agatha have any friends among her colleagues? Did she have anyone that she could go to when something like this happened?
Suddenly Agatha’s need for control, her demand for respect, started to make sense. Her peers had written her off and treated her as less than – all because of a relationship that went wrong. She had lost their respect so she took it back from her students. She wasn’t in control of how her colleagues saw her so she took control of how her students saw her. The Dean looked at her as someone who was beneath him and treated her as nothing other than an inconvenience, so she took that feeling and projected it onto the people that were beneath her .
It was a vicious cycle.

Rio wasn’t expecting Agatha to mention the ball, it didn’t seem like her thing – especially after realising that pretty much the whole department had something against her – but she spoke about it like she regularly attended the event. And she seemed almost sad when Rio told her that she was the fifth person to mention it. Was Agatha trying to ask her to go with her? As her date? No, that couldn’t be right.
Agatha had asked her the other day if she assumed everyone was flirting with her and maybe there was some truth to it because there was no way that Professor Agatha Harkness was asking her on a date. Either way, Rio felt the need to point out that the other people weren’t a threat.

They talked about the upcoming lecture whilst they walked the familiar path to the lifts, when Rio suddenly felt the wind being knocked out of her.
A body crashed into hers and sent her sideways, but she didn’t fall. She reached out and grabbed the other person to try and steady herself, and also keep them upright as she felt Agatha’s arm wrap around her waist, squeezing gently to stop her from tumbling to the floor.
Once her brain caught up, she registered the red hair and green eyes that belonged to Wanda and felt Agatha pushing her fully back onto her feet.

“Oh my god I am so sorry!” Wanda said before she realised that it was Rio that she had just very nearly knocked to the floor. She laughed lightly. “I thought we were done meeting like this, Rio.”
Rio smiled, recalling the two times that this had happened previously. It felt so long ago now. “Well I’m just lucky that Agatha was here to stop me from hitting the deck.” She said as she stepped to the side.
The smile Wanda was wearing was immediately erased when she saw Agatha and Rio watched as Wanda floundered, trying to find something to say. “I didn’t realise that you were- you don’t usually- Where are you going?”
Rio immediately felt the tension settle between the three of them. The panic on Wanda’s face, the tightness of Agatha’s smile. It all furthered Rio’s suspicion that they were each the ex that the other had referenced – and if that was true then that meant that Wanda was the reason that Agatha was a target for the Dean.

Rio cast her mind all the way back to the time she and Wanda had eaten Chinese food in her apartment, and tried to recall what Wanda had said about the ex that wasn’t her husband. She couldn’t remember the conversation fully as it was months ago, but she swore Wanda had mentioned something about being scared and that it made her do something she regretted.

Rio had zoned out and only came back to the corridor when Agatha mentioned her name.
“Rio has a bad leg, stairs aren’t an option.”
Wanda turned to her, looking worried, and started to reach towards her. Rio took a small step back, not enough to be out of Wanda’s reach – not even enough that it was noticeable – but enough that it had been an involuntary reaction to seeing Wanda trying to touch her.
“What happened to your leg? Are you okay?” Wanda asked, stopping her hands before they made contact.
“An old injury got aggravated again, but I’m fine. Just taking it easy.” Rio briefly flicked her eyes towards Agatha and noticed the subtle shake of her hand as she checked her watch.

As if having to face the Dean this morning wasn’t bad enough, Agatha had now been forced into an interaction with the person who was potentially responsible for it – albeit indirectly responsible, but if what Agatha said about everyone taking Wanda’s side was true, then she was still implicated.
Rio truly didn’t know how to feel as she watched Agatha walk away. She had no real hard evidence that supported her theory and therefore couldn’t react properly. There was a high likelihood that she would never know the full story, at the end of the day it wasn’t any of her business. She had no loyalties to either of these women, she had known them both for the same amount of time.
Sure she knew them in different ways – very different ways – but still, she knew each of them minimally.

Wanda’s voice pulled her from her thoughts. “Are you sure your leg is okay?”
Rio blinked a couple of times, her mind still not fully back. “Yeah it’s nothing, really." She started walking towards the lifts again, following Agatha. “See you later,” she threw over her shoulder, picking up her pace as much as the slight limp she still had would allow.
She got to the lift just in time to throw her arm out and stop the doors from closing. When the doors opened again, she settled herself into the corner across from Agatha.
Agatha huffed out a tired sigh and said, “I’m not answering any questions.”
Rio expected as much. She hadn’t planned on asking any questions, she didn’t even know what she would ask. She didn’t know how to begin to broach this subject right now, so instead she said, “I’m not gonna ask any. Except one.”

She watched Agatha lean back into the corner of the lift and take a deep breath.
“Are you okay?”
Judging by the speed that Agatha turned to look at her and her tone when she asked, “What?” she hadn’t been expecting Rio to ask that. She had definitely been expecting something more invasive.
“I don’t need details, but that didn’t look like a normal conversation between co-workers. So, are you okay?” Rio wasn’t lying, she really didn’t care for the details right now. All she cared about in that moment was making sure Agatha was alright.
“It’s nothing I can’t handle.”
Rio blew a breath out of her nose. “That’s not an answer.”
“Well it’s the one you’re getting so you’ll have to live with it.”
That was fair enough, Rio supposed. She said that she wasn’t going to ask questions and she stuck to her word.

On the way to the lecture hall, Rio made a decision and told Agatha that she would catch up. She made her way to the café and picked up the two pastries that she noticed Agatha favoured along with the iced coffee. Whilst she was waiting for the coffee to be made she scribbled ‘I know you have back to back lectures until the end of the day, so I hope the coffee and pastries make it a little easier for you - R’ on a napkin and tucked it into the bag with the food. When she received the coffee she carried on to the lecture hall, arriving ten minutes late thanks to the queue. She had hoped that it would only take a few minutes, but once again she was without Agatha’s privileges so she had to wait with the commoners.

To her credit Agatha didn’t let Rio’s late arrival interrupt her flow, she kept on teaching whilst Rio placed the food and drink on the table and then took her seat next to Billy.
Billy looked at her with raised eyebrows, his question evident on his face, but she shook her head. He could ask later.

When the lecture was over Rio left with Billy and Alice, she didn’t want to add anything on top of what Agatha was already feeling about the morning. As soon as they rounded the first corner away from the lecture hall Billy asked, “Please tell me that you didn’t make yourself late just so you could butter Agatha up with food.”
Rio smiled and shrugged. “I didn’t intentionally arrive late. The queue was just long.”
“I’m hearing no denial of an attempt to become the teacher's pet.” Alice joined in.
Rio stepped in front of them and turned so that she was walking backwards. “I don’t need to try to be the teacher’s pet, it just naturally happens.” She turned back around and fell back into step with them. “Besides with the marks you two got on your essays, you might want to try giving gifts to your lecturers once in a while.”
“What?” Billy and Alice asked in unison.
Billy grabbed Rio’s arm. “Did we really do that badly?”
Rio looked at him and shrugged.
“Dude!” Alice moved in front of her, making her stop walking. “Don’t fuck with us.”
“You’ll just have to wait for your grades to see if I was lying or not.” Rio said nonchalantly as she moved around Alice.
“Dick.” She heard Billy mutter behind her. 

__________

The next month passed with more of the same.
Rio still went to Agatha’s office and she enjoyed watching Agatha panic when she started to call the meetings dates, but since there was no real work to do they just talked. Sometimes they would just keep each other company whilst they read in comfortable silence, trading books and opinions.

At the start of December, Rio gave her second lecture to the first years.
“Okay so as I’m sure you’re all aware, religions tend to have their own version of the afterlife. For Greek mythology it was the underworld – a kingdom that Hades and Persephone ruled over. The earliest idea of the afterlife in Greek myth is that, when a person dies, that person's essence – or psyche –  is separated from the corpse and transported to the underworld.” She changed the slide so that the bullet points matched what she was going to say next. “In the earliest works like Homer's The Iliad and The Odyssey, the dead were kinda just lumped together to live a post-existence as shadowy figures. However in later versions of the mythology, the forms of judgement started to make an appearance. It was then believed that there were sections within the underworld where someone's psyche would be sent depending on how they lived their life on top.” She changed the slides again to one that had pictures of the three sections with their names underneath.

“The most unpleasant one is Tartarus. This is where the wicked received divine punishment. Most famously, it’s where the Titans went after they were defeated by Zeus. It also happens to be the easiest part of the game Hades, which seems backwards to me.” That last part got the laugh that she was hoping it would.
“Next is Asphodel, the meadows where the vast majority of the dead go. It’s believed to be the place where the normal people went. The people who hadn’t committed any atrocious crimes, but also hadn’t done any outstanding good deeds. And then we have Elysium, the good place. Elysium is a utopian afterlife reserved for specially distinguished individuals where life is easiest, a paradise that heroes could go to as a reward for all the good work they did on earth. So why it’s also the hardest level on Hades, I have no idea.” Once again, the reference to the game got a laugh from the students.

After giving an overview of the different sections she spoke about the rivers that were contained within the underworld, giving their names and functions. She also touched on the story of Orpheus and Eurydice, which was just an excuse to talk about Hadestown for a few minutes – something Agatha mentioned when giving feedback.
She ended the lecture by talking about the different notable residents of the underworld. Namely Hecate, Charon, Thanatos, and finally, Cerberus.
“The ultimate guard dog and overall goodest boy. He’s depicted as having three heads and is often shown as a Rottweiler, Doberman and sometimes a Molossian hound. But if you ask me, a three-headed Chihuahua would be the most terrifying dog to have chasing you down.”
The students laughed as she brought the lights back up, signalling the end of the lecture.

Band practise was focussed on running the setlist until they could all play and sing it in their sleep. There were a few last minute changes in terms of the order of the songs, and one song was swapped out for a different one that they thought would be more of a crowd pleaser, but they were all confident that they were going to absolutely smash the gig.
 Taylor joined them in the pub a couple of times, and Rio went home with her. Always leaving instead of staying the night.

Billy made a joke about not wanting to see her when he went home for dinner one weekend and she laughed it off. Rio saw Wanda a handful of times throughout the month and only because getting herself off wasn’t satisfying enough. Wanda was good at it, so why wouldn’t she use what she had at her disposal?

Rio was a big fan of Christmas and found herself getting more and more homesick as the holiday approached. She bought herself a small tabletop tree and strung some Christmas lights around her apartment to celebrate the season as much as she could by herself. Her friends and family had sent their Christmas cards to her so she put them on her bookcase and windowsills to add to the decorations.

Her flight home was the morning after the ball so she made sure that she had her bags packed and ready to go to avoid rushing around too much. She had a few calls with her family and friends to make arrangements for her being picked up from the airport and to make sure that her time at home was filled with seeing as many of the people that she missed as possible.

As the night of the ball drew closer she started to feel more nervous. She hadn’t played an actual gig since high school, and playing in a practise room was vastly different to playing in front of an audience. If the other guys fucked up they could catch back on pretty quickly, but if she fucked up then it was a lot more noticeable and that’s what she was worried about the most.

The night before the ball she struggled to sleep. She hadn’t had any more issues with her knee, but it was in the back of her mind. What if she hurt it again before or during? She had no idea how she would recover. She made sure to put her painkillers in the bag she was taking just in case and eventually drifted off to sleep.
